# Portuguese Curriculum - Micro-Sequence Syllabus
## Zero-Knowledge to Functional Portuguese

**Curriculum Scope:** 90 Units (Beginner A1 ‚Üí Upper-Intermediate B2)

**Teaching Philosophy:** eu-first approach (first person singular only until specified)

---

## PHASE 1: Foundation (Absolute Beginners)
### Unit 1: Identity Statements (Eu sou)
**First words/concepts taught:**
1. Eu (I)
2. sou (am)
3. Articles: o (masculine), a (feminine)
4. Nationalities: brasileiro/brasileira, americano/americana, portugu√™s/portuguesa
5. Professions: professor/professora, estudante, m√©dico/m√©dica, engenheiro/engenheira
6. Marital status: casado/casada, solteiro/solteira, divorciado/divorciada, vi√∫vo/vi√∫va

**Grammar introduced:**
- First person singular: Eu sou
- Gender agreement for adjectives (o/a endings)
- Definite articles with names: o [masculine name], a [feminine name]

**Practice format:**
- Recognition: "What does 'Eu sou brasileiro' mean?"
- Production: "Eu sou o/a [name]", "Eu sou [nationality]", "Eu sou [profession]", "Eu sou [marital status]"

**Student can now:**
- Introduce themselves by name
- State their nationality
- State their profession
- State their marital status
- Understand gender agreement basics

**Typical sentences:**
- Eu sou o Jo√£o / Eu sou a Maria (name)
- Eu sou brasileiro / Eu sou brasileira (nationality)
- Eu sou americano / Eu sou americana
- Eu sou professor / Eu sou professora (profession)
- Eu sou estudante
- Eu sou casado / Eu sou casada (marital status)
- Eu sou solteiro / Eu sou solteira
- Eu sou divorciado / Eu sou divorciada

---

### Unit 2: Origin with Contractions (Eu sou de)
**New vocabulary:**
- de (from/of)
- Country/city names: Brasil, Estados Unidos, Portugal, S√£o Paulo, Rio, etc.
- Articles: o, a, os, as (for contractions)

**Grammar introduced:**
- Preposition "de" + origin
- Contractions: de + o = do, de + a = da, de + os = dos, de + as = das
- When to use contractions vs. plain "de"

**Practice format:**
- "Eu sou de S√£o Paulo" (no article)
- "Eu sou do Brasil" (de + o = do)
- "Eu sou da Bahia" (de + a = da)
- "Eu sou dos Estados Unidos" (de + os = dos)

**Student can now:**
- State where they're from using correct contractions
- Understand when articles are needed with place names
- Combine Units 1 & 2: "Eu sou brasileiro. Eu sou de S√£o Paulo."

**Typical sentences:**
- Eu sou de S√£o Paulo
- Eu sou do Brasil
- Eu sou do Rio de Janeiro
- Eu sou da Bahia
- Eu sou dos Estados Unidos
- Eu sou da Inglaterra

---

### Unit 3: Location/Residence (Eu moro em)
**New vocabulary:**
- moro (I live) - first regular -AR verb introduced
- em (in/at/on)
- Place names: S√£o Paulo, Rio, Brasil, Estados Unidos, etc.
- Articles: o, a, os, as (for contractions with em)

**Grammar introduced:**
- First regular -AR verb: moro (I live)
- Preposition "em" + location
- Contractions: em + o = no, em + a = na, em + os = nos, em + as = nas
- When to use contractions vs. plain "em"

**Practice format:**
- "Eu moro em S√£o Paulo" (no article)
- "Eu moro no Brasil" (em + o = no)
- "Eu moro na Bahia" (em + a = na)
- "Eu moro nos Estados Unidos" (em + os = nos)
- "Eu moro em casa" (fixed expression, no article)

**Student can now:**
- State where they live using correct contractions
- Combine with previous units for full introduction
- Understand difference between "sou de" (origin) and "moro em" (residence)

**Typical sentences:**
- Eu moro em S√£o Paulo
- Eu moro no Brasil
- Eu moro no Rio de Janeiro
- Eu moro na Bahia
- Eu moro nos Estados Unidos
- Eu moro na Inglaterra

**Full introduction possible:**
- Eu sou o Jo√£o.
- Eu sou brasileiro.
- Eu sou professor.
- Eu sou de Belo Horizonte.
- Eu moro em S√£o Paulo.

---

### Unit 4: Street Address (Eu moro na rua/avenida)
**New vocabulary:**
- rua (street) - feminine
- avenida (avenue) - feminine
- Street names: Paulista, Ipiranga, Copacabana, etc.

**Grammar introduced:**
- Specific address with "na" (em + a = na)
- Both "rua" and "avenida" are feminine ‚Üí always "na"
- No article before street names (na Rua Paulista, not na Rua da Paulista)

**Practice format:**
- "Eu moro na Rua Paulista"
- "Eu moro na Avenida Ipiranga"
- Combining city + street: "Eu moro em S√£o Paulo, na Rua Augusta"

**Student can now:**
- Give a complete address (city + street)
- Understand that street/avenue names don't take articles
- Provide increasingly specific location information

**Typical sentences:**
- Eu moro na Rua Paulista
- Eu moro na Avenida Copacabana
- Eu moro na Rua Augusta
- Eu moro em S√£o Paulo, na Rua Consola√ß√£o

**Full introduction now includes:**
- Eu sou o Jo√£o.
- Eu sou brasileiro.
- Eu sou professor.
- Eu sou de Belo Horizonte.
- Eu moro em S√£o Paulo, na Rua Paulista.

---

### Unit 5: Workplace (Eu trabalho em/no/na)
**New vocabulary:**
- trabalho (I work) - second regular -AR verb
- Workplace locations:
  - hospital (masculine) ‚Üí no hospital
  - escola (feminine) ‚Üí na escola
  - universidade (feminine) ‚Üí na universidade
  - banco (masculine) ‚Üí no banco
  - restaurante (masculine) ‚Üí no restaurante
  - loja (feminine) ‚Üí na loja
  - empresa (feminine) ‚Üí na empresa
  - escrit√≥rio (masculine) ‚Üí no escrit√≥rio

**Grammar introduced:**
- Second regular -AR verb: trabalho (I work)
- Reusing "em" contractions from Unit 3 (no/na/nos/nas)
- Gender awareness: which workplaces are masculine/feminine

**Practice format:**
- "Eu trabalho em um hospital"
- "Eu trabalho no hospital" (specific hospital)
- "Eu trabalho na escola"
- "Eu trabalho em casa" (work from home - no article)

**Student can now:**
- State where they work using correct contractions
- Distinguish between indefinite (em um/uma) and definite (no/na)
- Recognize gender of workplace nouns

**Typical sentences:**
- Eu trabalho em um hospital
- Eu trabalho no hospital S√£o Lucas
- Eu trabalho na universidade
- Eu trabalho em um banco
- Eu trabalho na escola
- Eu trabalho em casa

**Full introduction now includes:**
- Eu sou o Jo√£o.
- Eu sou brasileiro.
- Eu sou professor.
- Eu sou de Belo Horizonte.
- Eu moro em S√£o Paulo, na Rua Paulista.
- Eu trabalho na universidade.

---

### Unit 6: Languages (Eu falo) + Conjunction "e"
**New vocabulary:**
- falo (I speak) - third regular -AR verb
- **e (and)** - KEY CONJUNCTION
- Languages:
  - portugu√™s (Portuguese) - masculine
  - ingl√™s (English) - masculine
  - espanhol (Spanish) - masculine
  - franc√™s (French) - masculine
  - alem√£o (German) - masculine
  - italiano (Italian) - masculine
  - chin√™s (Chinese) - masculine
- um pouco de (a little bit of)
- bem (well)

**Grammar introduced:**
- Third regular -AR verb: falo (I speak)
- Direct object (no preposition needed): "Eu falo portugu√™s" (not "em portugu√™s")
- **Conjunction "e" (and)** - combining items in a list
- Adverbs of degree: bem, um pouco
- Multiple uses of "e": languages, combining previous units

**Practice format:**
- "Eu falo portugu√™s"
- "Eu falo ingl√™s"
- "Eu falo portugu√™s e ingl√™s"
- "Eu falo um pouco de espanhol"
- "Eu falo portugu√™s bem"
- **Using "e" across units:**
  - "Eu sou brasileiro e professor"
  - "Eu moro e trabalho em S√£o Paulo"
  - "Eu falo portugu√™s e ingl√™s"

**Student can now:**
- State which languages they speak
- Use "um pouco de" for limited proficiency
- **Combine multiple items with "e"** - works across all previous units
- Add adverbs to describe proficiency level
- Create more natural, flowing sentences by combining information

**Typical sentences:**
- Eu falo portugu√™s
- Eu falo ingl√™s
- Eu falo portugu√™s e ingl√™s
- Eu falo um pouco de espanhol
- Eu falo franc√™s bem
- Eu sou brasileiro e professor (combining Unit 1)
- Eu moro e trabalho em S√£o Paulo (combining Units 3 & 5)

**Full introduction now includes:**
- Eu sou o Jo√£o.
- Eu sou brasileiro e professor.
- Eu sou casado.
- Eu sou de Belo Horizonte.
- Eu moro em S√£o Paulo, na Rua Paulista.
- Eu trabalho na universidade.
- Eu falo portugu√™s e ingl√™s.

---

### Unit 7: Transportation (Eu ando de/a p√©)
**New vocabulary:**
- ando (I walk/ride) - fourth regular -AR verb
- de (by/of) - used with transport
- a p√© (on foot) - fixed expression
- Example transports:
  - √¥nibus (bus)
  - bicicleta (bicycle)
  - carro (car)

**Grammar introduced:**
- Fourth regular -AR verb: ando (I walk/ride)
- "Ando de" + transport = ride/go by [transport]
- "Ando a p√©" = walk (on foot) - fixed expression
- No articles with transport in "ando de" construction

**Practice format:**
- "Eu ando de √¥nibus" (I take the bus / I go by bus)
- "Eu ando de bicicleta" (I ride a bicycle)
- "Eu ando de carro" (I go by car)
- "Eu ando a p√©" (I walk)

**Student can now:**
- Express how they get around
- Use fourth -AR verb (reinforcing the -o pattern)
- Distinguish "andar de" + transport vs "andar a p√©"
- Talk about daily transportation

**Typical sentences:**
- Eu ando de √¥nibus
- Eu ando de bicicleta
- Eu ando de carro
- Eu ando a p√©
- Eu ando de √¥nibus todo dia (I take the bus every day)

**Full introduction now includes:**
- Eu sou o Jo√£o.
- Eu sou brasileiro e professor.
- Eu sou casado.
- Eu sou de Belo Horizonte.
- Eu moro em S√£o Paulo, na Rua Paulista.
- Eu trabalho na universidade.
- Eu falo portugu√™s e ingl√™s.
- Eu ando de √¥nibus.

---

### Unit 8: Going by Transport (Eu vou de)
**New vocabulary:**
- vou (I go) - **IRREGULAR** verb
- Same transports from Unit 7: √¥nibus, bicicleta, carro

**Grammar introduced:**
- First irregular motion verb: vou (I go)
- "Vou de" + transport (I go by [transport])
- Parallel structure to Unit 7's "ando de"

**Practice format:**
- "Eu vou de √¥nibus" (I go by bus)
- "Eu vou de bicicleta" (I go by bicycle)
- "Eu vou de carro" (I go by car)
- "Eu vou a p√©" (I go on foot)

**Student can now:**
- Express going by a method of transport
- Use the irregular verb vou
- Distinguish between "ando de" and "vou de"

**Typical sentences:**
- Eu vou de √¥nibus (I go by bus)
- Eu vou de bicicleta (I go by bicycle)
- Eu vou de carro (I go by car)
- Eu vou a p√© (I go on foot)

**Key Distinction:**
- **ando de √¥nibus** = I ride/take the bus (the act of riding)
- **vou de √¥nibus** = I go by bus (using bus as the method)
- Both are valid and commonly used

**Full introduction now includes:**
- Eu sou o Jo√£o.
- Eu sou brasileiro e professor.
- Eu sou casado.
- Eu sou de Belo Horizonte.
- Eu moro em S√£o Paulo, na Rua Paulista.
- Eu trabalho na universidade.
- Eu falo portugu√™s e ingl√™s.
- Eu ando de √¥nibus.
- Eu vou de √¥nibus.

**Note:**
- Future tense "vou + infinitive" will be introduced after infinitives are taught

### Unit 9: Going to Places (Eu vou a/para)
**New vocabulary:**
- a (to - direction)
- para (to/for - destination)
- Contractions: ao (a + o), √† (a + a)
- Example destinations:
  - trabalho (work)
  - escola (school)
  - casa (home)

**Grammar introduced:**
- "Vou a/ao/√†" + place (going to a specific place)
- "Vou para" + place (going toward - often used with casa)
- Contractions: a + o = ao, a + a = √†
- No contraction with para (always "para casa", never *paro)

**Practice format:**
- "Eu vou ao trabalho" (I go to work)
- "Eu vou √† escola" (I go to school)
- "Eu vou para casa" (I go home)
- "Eu vou ao supermercado" (I go to the supermarket)

**Student can now:**
- Express WHERE they go (destinations)
- Combine with Unit 7: "Eu vou ao trabalho de √¥nibus" (where + how)
- Use contractions with "a" (ao/√†)
- Distinguish between "a" and "para"

**Typical sentences:**
- Eu vou ao trabalho (I go to work)
- Eu vou √† escola (I go to school)
- Eu vou para casa (I go home)
- Eu vou ao banco (I go to the bank)
- Eu vou √† universidade (I go to the university)
- Eu vou ao trabalho de √¥nibus (combining Units 7+8)

**Contractions with "a":**
- a + o = ao: "Vou ao banco" (masculine)
- a + a = √†: "Vou √† escola" (feminine)
- para has NO contraction: "Vou para casa"

**"A" vs "Para":**
- Generally use "a" for most destinations: ao trabalho, √† escola, ao cinema
- Use "para" for casa (home): para casa (idiomatic)
- "Para" can emphasize direction/destination: "Vou para S√£o Paulo" (going to SP)

**Full introduction now includes:**
- Eu sou o Jo√£o.
- Eu sou brasileiro e professor.
- Eu sou casado.
- Eu sou de Belo Horizonte.
- Eu moro em S√£o Paulo, na Rua Paulista.
- Eu trabalho na universidade.
- Eu falo portugu√™s e ingl√™s.
- Eu ando de √¥nibus.
- Eu vou de √¥nibus.
- Eu vou ao trabalho de √¥nibus.

### Unit 10: Multiple Languages with Varying Proficiency (e um pouco de)
**New vocabulary:**
- More languages (if needed)
- tamb√©m (also)
- mas (but)

**Grammar introduced:**
- Complex combinations: fluent language + "e" + partial language
- "e um pouco de" construction for adding languages with limited proficiency
- Natural sentence flow with multiple proficiency levels

**Practice format:**
- "Eu falo portugu√™s e ingl√™s" (both fluent)
- "Eu falo portugu√™s e um pouco de ingl√™s" (one fluent, one partial)
- "Eu falo portugu√™s, ingl√™s e um pouco de espanhol" (multiple + partial)
- "Eu falo portugu√™s bem, e um pouco de espanhol"
- "Eu falo ingl√™s, mas eu falo portugu√™s melhor" (but + better)

**Student can now:**
- Express multiple languages with different proficiency levels
- Combine fluent and partial language knowledge naturally
- Use comma + "e" for lists of three or more items
- Add nuance with "bem", "um pouco", "tamb√©m"

**Typical sentences:**
- Eu falo portugu√™s e ingl√™s, e um pouco de espanhol
- Eu falo ingl√™s bem, e um pouco de franc√™s
- Eu falo portugu√™s, ingl√™s e um pouco de alem√£o
- Eu falo espanhol, e um pouco de italiano tamb√©m
- Eu falo portugu√™s, mas eu falo um pouco de ingl√™s

**Full introduction now includes:**
- Eu sou o Jo√£o.
- Eu sou brasileiro e professor.
- Eu sou casado.
- Eu sou de Belo Horizonte.
- Eu moro em S√£o Paulo, na Rua Paulista.
- Eu trabalho na universidade.
- Eu falo portugu√™s e ingl√™s, e um pouco de espanhol.
- Eu ando de √¥nibus.
- Eu vou ao trabalho de √¥nibus.

**Key Pattern:**
This unit solidifies natural language listing before introducing new verbs.
Students master: [fluent] e [fluent], e um pouco de [partial]

### Unit 11: Dropping the Pronoun "Eu" (Pro-drop)
**New concept:**
- **Pro-drop**: Portuguese allows (and prefers) dropping subject pronouns when context is clear
- The verb ending "-o" already indicates "I" (first person singular)
- This is how native speakers actually talk

**Grammar introduced:**
- Optional subject pronouns in Portuguese
- Verb endings carry the person/number information
- "-o" ending = I (eu), so "eu" becomes redundant
- More natural, flowing speech

**Practice format - Before vs. After:**
- **Before:** "Eu sou brasileiro"
- **After:** "Sou brasileiro"
- **Before:** "Eu moro em S√£o Paulo"
- **After:** "Moro em S√£o Paulo"
- **Before:** "Eu trabalho na universidade"
- **After:** "Trabalho na universidade"
- **Before:** "Eu falo portugu√™s"
- **After:** "Falo portugu√™s"

**Student can now:**
- Speak more naturally like native speakers
- Understand that verb endings indicate the subject
- Recognize both forms (with and without "eu")
- Choose when to include "eu" for emphasis

**When to keep "Eu":**
- For emphasis: "**Eu** sou brasileiro!" (I am Brazilian - emphasizing me specifically)
- For contrast: "Eu sou professor, mas voc√™ √© estudante"
- When starting a conversation with no prior context

**Typical sentences (natural style):**
- Sou o Jo√£o
- Sou brasileiro e professor
- Sou casado
- Sou de Belo Horizonte
- Moro em S√£o Paulo, na Rua Paulista
- Trabalho na universidade
- Falo portugu√™s e ingl√™s, e um pouco de espanhol
- Ando de √¥nibus
- Vou ao trabalho de √¥nibus

**Full introduction (natural style):**
- Sou o Jo√£o.
- Sou brasileiro e professor.
- Sou casado.
- Sou de Belo Horizonte.
- Moro em S√£o Paulo, na Rua Paulista.
- Trabalho na universidade.
- Falo portugu√™s e ingl√™s, e um pouco de espanhol.
- Ando de √¥nibus.
- Vou ao trabalho de √¥nibus.

**Key Learning:**
This simplifies speech dramatically and makes students sound much more natural. The "-o" ending becomes their identity marker.

---

### Unit 12: Temporary States and Current Location (estou - irregular)
**New vocabulary:**
- estou (I am) - **IRREGULAR** verb, second "to be" verb
- Temporary states/feelings:
  - cansado/cansada (tired)
  - feliz (happy)
  - triste (sad)
  - doente (sick)
  - ocupado/ocupada (busy)
  - com fome (hungry)
  - com sede (thirsty)
- Current location:
  - em casa (at home)
  - no trabalho (at work)
  - na escola (at school)
- agora (now), hoje (today)

**Grammar introduced:**
- Second irregular verb: estou (I am - temporary/location)
- **Critical distinction: ser vs estar**
  - **ser (sou)** = permanent/inherent qualities, identity
  - **estar (estou)** = temporary states, current location, conditions
- Temporary states require estar, not ser
- Current location uses estar

**Practice format:**
- States: "Estou cansado", "Estou feliz", "Estou com fome"
- Location: "Estou em casa", "Estou no trabalho"
- Time context: "Estou cansado agora", "Hoje estou feliz"
- Natural style (no "eu"): "Estou ocupado"

**Student can now:**
- Express how they feel right now (temporary)
- Say where they are currently (not where they live - that's moro)
- Understand the ser vs estar distinction
- Distinguish permanent (sou) from temporary (estou)

**Typical sentences:**
- Estou cansado (I'm tired right now)
- Estou feliz hoje (I'm happy today)
- Estou em casa (I'm at home now)
- Estou no trabalho (I'm at work)
- Estou com fome (I'm hungry)
- Estou doente (I'm sick)

**üó£Ô∏è Spoken Brazilian Portuguese:**
In casual conversation, Brazilians almost always use **"t√°"** instead of **"est√°"** (and **"t√¥"** instead of **"estou"**):
- Formal/Writing: "Eu estou em casa" / "Voc√™ est√° cansado?"
- Casual Speech: "T√¥ em casa" / "C√™ t√° cansado?"
- Very common: "T√° bom?" (Is that okay?), "T√° tudo bem?" (Is everything okay?)

**Note:** This is universal in Brazilian Portuguese speech. Learn the formal conjugation (estou, est√°, est√°, estamos, est√£o) for writing and formal contexts, but recognize "t√°/t√¥" for listening comprehension. European Portuguese maintains the full forms more strictly.

**Critical Distinctions:**
- Sou brasileiro (permanent nationality) vs Estou no Brasil (current location)
- Sou feliz (happy person by nature) vs Estou feliz (happy right now)
- Sou professor (identity) vs Estou no trabalho (current location)
- Moro em S√£o Paulo (where I live) vs Estou em S√£o Paulo (where I am now)

**Full introduction now includes:**
- Sou o Jo√£o.
- Sou brasileiro e professor.
- Sou casado.
- Sou de Belo Horizonte.
- Moro em S√£o Paulo, na Rua Paulista.
- Trabalho na universidade.
- Ando de √¥nibus.
- Vou de √¥nibus.
- Falo portugu√™s e ingl√™s, e um pouco de espanhol.
- Agora estou em casa. (current situation)
- Estou um pouco cansado. (current feeling)

---

### Unit 13: Location at Someone's House (na casa de)
**New vocabulary:**
- casa de (house of)
- People's names: Jo√£o, Maria, Pedro, Ana
- Family members: pai (father), m√£e (mother), irm√£o (brother), irm√£ (sister), amigo/amiga (friend)
- Revisit: de + articles = do/da/dos/das

**Grammar introduced:**
- Fixed expression: "em casa" (at home - NO article) = at MY home
- Location at someone else's house: "na casa de [person]"
- Triple contraction: **na casa do/da/dos/das**
- Combining contractions:
  - em + a = na (from Unit 3)
  - de + o/a/os/as = do/da/dos/das (from Unit 2)
  - Together: na casa + de + article = **na casa do/da/dos/das**
- Possessive with "de": na casa do Jo√£o (Jo√£o's house), na casa da Maria (Maria's house)

**Practice format:**
- "Estou em casa" (at MY home - fixed expression, no article)
- "Estou na casa do Jo√£o" (at Jo√£o's house)
- "Estou na casa da Maria" (at Maria's house)
- "Estou na casa do Pedro" (at Pedro's house)
- "Estou na casa da Ana" (at Ana's house)
- "Estou na casa do meu irm√£o" (at my brother's house)
- "Estou na casa da minha m√£e" (at my mother's house)

**Student can now:**
- Distinguish "em casa" (my home) from "na casa de" (someone else's home)
- Express whose house they're at using correct contractions
- Combine multiple contraction rules naturally
- Use possessive "de" with people's names
- Master the triple contraction pattern

**Typical sentences:**
- Estou em casa (at my home)
- Estou na casa do Jo√£o (at Jo√£o's house)
- Estou na casa da Maria (at Maria's house)
- Estou na casa do Pedro (at Pedro's house)
- Estou na casa da Ana (at Ana's house)
- Vou √† casa do meu amigo (I'm going to my friend's house)
- Ele est√° na casa da irm√£ (He's at his sister's house)

**Critical Distinctions:**
- ‚ùå "Estou na minha casa" (unnatural - just say "em casa")
- ‚úÖ "Estou em casa" (at my own home)
- ‚úÖ "Estou na casa do Pedro" (at Pedro's house)
- ‚ùå "Estou na casa de o Jo√£o" (wrong - must contract)
- ‚úÖ "Estou na casa do Jo√£o" (correct - with contraction)

**Common Patterns:**
- em casa (at my/our home - no article, fixed expression)
- na casa do + masculine name (do Jo√£o, do Pedro)
- na casa da + feminine name (da Maria, da Ana)
- Triple contraction: na (em+a) + casa + do/da (de+o/a)

**Full introduction with current location:**
- Sou o Jo√£o.
- Sou brasileiro e professor.
- Sou casado.
- Sou de Belo Horizonte.
- Moro em S√£o Paulo, na Rua Paulista.
- Trabalho na universidade.
- Falo portugu√™s e ingl√™s, e um pouco de espanhol.
- Ando de √¥nibus.
- Vou de √¥nibus.
- Agora estou na casa do Pedro.
- Estou um pouco cansado.

**Key Learning:**
- Students master the triple contraction: na (em + a) + casa + do/da/dos/das (de + article)
- "Em casa" is ALWAYS used without article for "at my/our home"
- "Na casa de" + name/person requires contraction (do/da/dos/das)
- This pattern works with any person: na casa do professor, na casa da Ana
- Essential skill for expressing location at someone's residence

**Why This Unit:**
- Natural progression: extends "em casa" (from Units 12-13) to other people's houses
- Ultra-granular: focuses only on location construction with triple contraction
- Essential for social communication - where are you? I'm at Jo√£o's house
- Prepares for possessive adjectives in next unit (meu irm√£o, minha m√£e)

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 2: de contractions (do/da)
- Unit 3: em contractions (no/na)
- Unit 12: estar location
- Unit 13: Combines all these contraction rules in one complex pattern

### Unit 14: Possessive Adjectives: Meu/Minha (My)
**New vocabulary:**
- **meu/minha** (my - masculine/feminine singular) - **FIRST POSSESSIVE ADJECTIVES**
- Family members:
  - pai (father) - masculine
  - m√£e (mother) - feminine
  - irm√£o (brother) - masculine
  - irm√£ (sister) - feminine
  - filho/filha (son/daughter)
  - av√¥/av√≥ (grandfather/grandmother)
- amigo/amiga (friend - masculine/feminine)
- fam√≠lia (family) - feminine

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Possessive adjectives: meu/minha (my) - FOUNDATIONAL CONCEPT**
  - **meu** = my (masculine singular): meu irm√£o, meu amigo, meu pai
  - **minha** = my (feminine singular): minha irm√£, minha amiga, minha m√£e
  - **CRITICAL RULE: possessive agrees with the THING POSSESSED, not the speaker**
- Position: possessive + noun (no article needed)
- Used primarily with people (family members, friends) and relationships
- Can combine with estar location: "Estou na casa do meu irm√£o"

**Practice format:**
- "Meu pai mora em S√£o Paulo" (My father lives in S√£o Paulo)
- "Minha m√£e trabalha no hospital" (My mother works at the hospital)
- "Meu irm√£o fala ingl√™s" (My brother speaks English)
- "Minha irm√£ √© professora" (My sister is a teacher)
- "Estou na casa do meu amigo" (I'm at my friend's house)
- "Minha fam√≠lia √© grande" (My family is big)

**Student can now:**
- **Talk about family members using meu/minha**
- **Understand gender agreement with possessives**
- Express relationships (my brother, my sister, my friend)
- Combine possessives with location (na casa do meu pai)
- Use possessives with verbs learned so far (meu pai mora, minha m√£e trabalha)

**Typical sentences:**
- Meu pai mora no Rio (My father lives in Rio)
- Minha m√£e trabalha na escola (My mother works at the school)
- Meu irm√£o fala portugu√™s e ingl√™s (My brother speaks Portuguese and English)
- Minha irm√£ √© m√©dica (My sister is a doctor)
- Meu amigo trabalha aqui (My friend works here)
- Minha amiga mora em S√£o Paulo (My friend (f) lives in S√£o Paulo)
- Minha fam√≠lia √© brasileira (My family is Brazilian)
- Estou na casa do meu pai (I'm at my father's house)

**Possessive Agreement - CRITICAL RULE:**
- **The possessive agrees with the NOUN (what you possess), NOT with you!**
- **Masculine nouns** ‚Üí **meu**:
  - ‚ùå "minha pai" (wrong)
  - ‚úÖ "meu pai" (correct - pai is masculine)
  - Examples: meu irm√£o, meu amigo, meu filho, meu av√¥
- **Feminine nouns** ‚Üí **minha**:
  - ‚ùå "meu m√£e" (wrong)
  - ‚úÖ "minha m√£e" (correct - m√£e is feminine)
  - Examples: minha irm√£, minha amiga, minha filha, minha av√≥, minha fam√≠lia

**Common Patterns:**
- meu + masculine family member: meu pai, meu irm√£o, meu filho
- minha + feminine family member: minha m√£e, minha irm√£, minha filha
- Combining with verbs: Meu pai trabalha..., Minha m√£e mora...
- With location (from Unit 13): na casa do meu irm√£o, na casa da minha m√£e

**Sample Conversation:**
- A: Onde sua fam√≠lia mora? (Where does your family live?)
- B: Meu pai mora no Rio, mas minha m√£e mora em S√£o Paulo. (My father lives in Rio, but my mother lives in S√£o Paulo.)
- A: E seu irm√£o? (And your brother?)
- B: Meu irm√£o mora comigo em S√£o Paulo. (My brother lives with me in S√£o Paulo.)

**Combining with Previous Units:**
- Unit 13: "Estou na casa do meu irm√£o" (location + possessive)
- Verbs: "Meu pai trabalha no banco" (possessive + Unit 5 verb)
- Ser: "Minha m√£e √© professora" (possessive + Unit 1)
- Estar: "Minha irm√£ est√° em casa" (possessive + Unit 12)

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ‚ùå "Minha pai" (wrong - pai is masculine)
- ‚úÖ "Meu pai" (correct)
- ‚ùå "Meu m√£e" (wrong - m√£e is feminine)
- ‚úÖ "Minha m√£e" (correct)
- ‚ùå "O meu pai" (unnatural in most contexts - just say "meu pai")
- ‚úÖ "Meu pai" (natural Brazilian Portuguese)

**Full introduction with family:**
- Sou o Jo√£o.
- Sou brasileiro e professor.
- Sou casado.
- Sou de Belo Horizonte.
- Moro em S√£o Paulo, na Rua Paulista.
- Trabalho na universidade.
- Falo portugu√™s e ingl√™s.
- **Meu pai mora no Rio.**
- **Minha m√£e trabalha na escola.**
- **Meu irm√£o √© engenheiro.**

**Key Learning:**
- **FIRST POSSESSIVE ADJECTIVES:** meu/minha (my - singular only)
- Possessives agree with the THING POSSESSED, not the speaker
- Gender agreement is MANDATORY: meu pai (masc), minha m√£e (fem)
- This is foundational for all future possessive work
- Essential for talking about family and relationships

**Why This Unit:**
- Natural progression: after learning "na casa do Jo√£o", students need "na casa do MEU irm√£o"
- Ultra-granular: introduces ONLY the first-person singular possessive (my)
- Essential skill for personal communication - family is immediate need
- Foundational concept for future possessives (plural, your, his, her, our)
- Students can now express family relationships clearly

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 13: location at someone's house ‚Üí now can say "meu irm√£o's house"
- Unit 1: ser + professions ‚Üí "meu pai √© professor"
- Unit 3: moro em ‚Üí "minha m√£e mora em S√£o Paulo"
- Unit 5: trabalho em ‚Üí "meu irm√£o trabalha no banco"
- Possessives work naturally with all verbs learned so far

### Unit 15: Numbers 0-20 (Cardinal Numbers - Foundation)
**New vocabulary:**
- **Numbers 0-20:**
  - 0: zero
  - 1: um/uma (masculine/feminine)
  - 2: dois/duas (masculine/feminine)
  - 3: tr√™s
  - 4: quatro
  - 5: cinco
  - 6: seis
  - 7: sete
  - 8: oito
  - 9: nove
  - 10: dez
  - 11: onze
  - 12: doze
  - 13: treze
  - 14: quatorze
  - 15: quinze
  - 16: dezesseis
  - 17: dezessete
  - 18: dezoito
  - 19: dezenove
  - 20: vinte

**Grammar introduced:**
- Cardinal numbers 0-20 (foundational counting)
- **Gender agreement for 1 and 2 ONLY:**
  - **um** livro (one book - masculine) vs **uma** casa (one house - feminine)
  - **dois** livros (two books - masculine) vs **duas** casas (two houses - feminine)
- **Numbers 3-20:** no gender agreement (tr√™s, quatro, cinco... same for all nouns)
- Position: number + noun (um livro, dois carros, tr√™s casas)
- Numbers can stand alone: "Quantos? Tr√™s." (How many? Three.)

**Practice format:**
- Counting 0-20 orally
- "Tenho um cachorro" (I have one dog)
- "Tenho duas bicicletas" (I have two bicycles)
- "H√° tr√™s pessoas aqui" (There are three people here)
- "Quantos irm√£os voc√™ tem?" "Tenho dois irm√£os" (How many brothers do you have? I have two brothers)
- "Quantas irm√£s?" "Uma irm√£" (How many sisters? One sister)

**Student can now:**
- Count from 0 to 20
- Express quantities up to 20
- Use correct gender agreement for um/uma and dois/duas
- Answer "quantos/quantas?" (how many?) questions
- Talk about quantities of family members, belongings, etc.

**Typical sentences:**
- Tenho um irm√£o (I have one brother)
- Tenho duas irm√£s (I have two sisters)
- H√° cinco pessoas na minha fam√≠lia (There are five people in my family)
- Tenho tr√™s amigos brasileiros (I have three Brazilian friends)
- Moro na Rua Paulista n√∫mero dez (I live on Paulista Street number 10)
- Trabalho oito horas por dia (I work eight hours per day)
- Tenho quinze livros (I have fifteen books)

**Gender Agreement - Critical Examples:**
- **Masculine:** um carro, dois carros (one car, two cars)
- **Feminine:** uma casa, duas casas (one house, two houses)
- **No agreement:** tr√™s carros, tr√™s casas (three cars, three houses)
- **Mixed:** um irm√£o e uma irm√£ (one brother and one sister)

**Common Patterns:**
- Tenho + number + noun: "Tenho tr√™s irm√£os"
- H√° + number + noun: "H√° cinco pessoas"
- Number + noun + adjective: "dois livros novos" (two new books)
- Quantos/quantas + noun: "Quantos anos?" "Quantas pessoas?"

**Numbers in Context:**
- Address: "n√∫mero tr√™s" (number 3)
- Quantity: "dois caf√©s, por favor" (two coffees, please)
- Family: "tr√™s irm√£os" (three siblings)
- Age (preview): "dez anos" (ten years old - full expression in Unit 17)

**Sample Conversation:**
- A: Quantos irm√£os voc√™ tem? (How many siblings do you have?)
- B: Tenho dois irm√£os e uma irm√£. (I have two brothers and one sister.)
- A: E quantas pessoas h√° na sua fam√≠lia? (And how many people are in your family?)
- B: H√° seis pessoas: meus pais, meus irm√£os, minha irm√£ e eu. (There are six people: my parents, my brothers, my sister, and me.)

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ‚ùå "um casa" (wrong - casa is feminine)
- ‚úÖ "uma casa" (correct)
- ‚ùå "dois irm√£s" (wrong - irm√£s is feminine)
- ‚úÖ "duas irm√£s" (correct)
- ‚ùå "tr√™s cachorro" (wrong - missing plural)
- ‚úÖ "tr√™s cachorros" (correct - noun must be plural)

**Pronunciation Notes:**
- "dois" = [doys] - diphthong
- "seis" = [says] - diphthong
- "dez" = [dez] - closed e
- Watch out for: seis (6) vs sete (7) - very different!

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 16: "Tenho um cachorro" ‚Üí now can say "Tenho tr√™s cachorros"
- Unit 14: "Meu irm√£o" ‚Üí now "Meus dois irm√£os"
- Unit 27: "Meus irm√£os" ‚Üí now "Meus tr√™s irm√£os"
- All possession + counting combined!

**Key Learning:**
- First 20 numbers are foundational for all counting
- Only um/uma and dois/duas show gender
- All other numbers (3-20) are invariable
- Numbers always come BEFORE the noun (unlike some Romance languages)
- Essential for expressing quantities, addresses, basic math

**Why This Unit:**
- **CRITICAL FOUNDATION:** Numbers unlock age, time, dates, prices, phone numbers
- Natural progression: students can talk about possessions, now can quantify them
- Ultra-granular: teaches ONLY numbers 0-20 (foundation before expanding)
- Immediate practical value: counting family members, belongings
- Essential before Unit 17 (age) and Unit 49 (time)

### Unit 16: Numbers 21-100 (Extending the System)
**New vocabulary:**
- **Tens:**
  - 30: trinta
  - 40: quarenta
  - 50: cinquenta
  - 60: sessenta
  - 70: setenta
  - 80: oitenta
  - 90: noventa
  - 100: cem (when alone) / cento (when in 101, 102, etc.)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Compound numbers:** tens + **e** + units
  - 21: vinte **e** um
  - 32: trinta **e** dois
  - 45: quarenta **e** cinco
  - 99: noventa **e** nove
- **"E" is REQUIRED** between tens and units (unlike Spanish)
- **Gender agreement still applies to um/dois:**
  - vinte e um anos (21 years - masculine)
  - vinte e uma pessoas (21 people - feminine)
  - trinta e dois livros (32 books - masculine)
  - trinta e duas chaves (32 keys - feminine)
- **Even tens:** 30, 40, 50... stand alone (no "e")

**Practice format:**
- Counting by tens: 10, 20, 30, 40...
- Random numbers: 23, 47, 68, 91
- "Tenho vinte e cinco anos" (I'm 25 years old - preview)
- "H√° trinta pessoas" (There are 30 people)
- "Moro na Rua Augusta, n√∫mero quarenta e sete" (I live on Augusta Street, number 47)

**Student can now:**
- Count from 0 to 100
- Express any quantity up to 100
- Combine tens and units correctly with "e"
- Use correct gender for compound numbers ending in um/dois
- Give street addresses with larger numbers
- Express ages up to 100 (full structure in Unit 17)

**Typical sentences:**
- Tenho trinta anos (I'm 30 years old)
- Moro no n√∫mero cinquenta e tr√™s (I live at number 53)
- H√° quarenta alunos na classe (There are 40 students in the class)
- Trabalho cinquenta horas por semana (I work 50 hours per week)
- Meu pai tem sessenta anos (My father is 60 years old)
- Custa noventa reais (It costs 90 reais - currency in next units)
- O √¥nibus √© o n√∫mero oitenta e sete (The bus is number 87)

**Number Patterns:**
| Range | Pattern | Examples |
|-------|---------|----------|
| 20-29 | vinte e... | vinte e um, vinte e cinco, vinte e nove |
| 30-39 | trinta e... | trinta e dois, trinta e sete, trinta e oito |
| 40-49 | quarenta e... | quarenta e tr√™s, quarenta e seis |
| 50-59 | cinquenta e... | cinquenta e um, cinquenta e quatro |
| 60-69 | sessenta e... | sessenta e cinco, sessenta e nove |
| 70-79 | setenta e... | setenta e dois, setenta e oito |
| 80-89 | oitenta e... | oitenta e um, oitenta e sete |
| 90-99 | noventa e... | noventa e tr√™s, noventa e nove |
| 100 | cem | cem pessoas |

**Gender Agreement Examples:**
- vinte e **um** livro (21 books - masc) ‚Üí vinte e **uma** casa (21 houses - fem)
- trinta e **dois** carros (32 cars - masc) ‚Üí trinta e **duas** pessoas (32 people - fem)
- cinquenta e **um** ano (51 years - masc) ‚Üí cinquenta e **uma** semana (51 weeks - fem)
- **All other numbers:** no agreement (vinte e tr√™s, quarenta e cinco, etc.)

**Special Note on 100:**
- **cem** = 100 (alone): "H√° cem pessoas" (There are 100 people)
- **cento** = 100 (in compounds): "cento e um" (101), "cento e dois" (102)
- This distinction will be covered more in higher numbers unit

**Sample Conversation:**
- A: Quantos anos voc√™ tem? (How old are you?)
- B: Tenho vinte e oito anos. E voc√™? (I'm 28 years old. And you?)
- A: Tenho trinta e cinco. (I'm 35.)
- B: Onde voc√™ mora? (Where do you live?)
- A: Moro na Avenida Paulista, n√∫mero setenta e quatro. (I live on Paulista Avenue, number 74.)

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ‚ùå "vinte um" (wrong - missing "e")
- ‚úÖ "vinte e um" (correct)
- ‚ùå "trinta dois" (wrong - missing "e")
- ‚úÖ "trinta e dois" (correct)
- ‚ùå "quarenta e uma livros" (wrong - livros is masculine)
- ‚úÖ "quarenta e um livros" (correct)
- ‚ùå "cinquenta e dois pessoas" (wrong - pessoas is feminine)
- ‚úÖ "cinquenta e duas pessoas" (correct)

**Math Operations (preview for later):**
- vinte mais trinta √© cinquenta (20 + 30 = 50)
- cem menos quarenta √© sessenta (100 - 40 = 60)
- (Full math vocabulary in future units)

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 15: Numbers 0-20 ‚Üí extending to 100
- Unit 19: "Tenho um cachorro" ‚Üí "Tenho vinte e tr√™s anos"
- Unit 4: Address ‚Üí "Moro na Rua Paulista n√∫mero cinquenta e dois"
- Past tense: "Tinha trinta anos" (I was 30 years old)

**Key Learning:**
- **"E" is MANDATORY** between tens and units
- Gender agreement only for compounds ending in um/dois
- Pattern is regular and predictable (trinta e..., quarenta e...)
- Essential for age, addresses, quantities, prices
- Prepares for age expression in Unit 17

**Why This Unit:**
- Natural extension of Unit 15
- Ultra-granular: focuses ONLY on 21-100 range
- Essential before formal age expression (Unit 17)
- Practical: most everyday numbers fall in this range (ages, addresses, prices)
- Systematic pattern makes learning easier

### Unit 17: Age Expression (Tenho X anos)
**New vocabulary:**
- **anos** (years)
- **idade** (age)
- **quantos anos** (how many years - how old)
- **anivers√°rio** (birthday)
- **fazer anos** (to have a birthday - literally "to make years")
- **jovem** (young)
- **velho/velha** (old - for people)
- **novo/nova** (young, new)
- **mais velho/mais novo** (older/younger)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Age in Portuguese uses TER (to have), NOT SER (to be):**
  - ‚úÖ **Tenho** 25 anos (I am 25 years old - literally "I have 25 years")
  - ‚ùå **Sou** 25 anos (WRONG - never use ser for age!)
- **Question:** Quantos anos voc√™ tem? (How old are you? - literally "How many years do you have?")
- **Pattern:** subject + ter (conjugated) + number + anos
- **Past age:** Tinha X anos (I was X years old)
- **Future age:** Vou ter X anos (I'm going to be X years old)

**Practice format:**
- "Tenho vinte e cinco anos" (I'm 25 years old)
- "Quantos anos voc√™ tem?" (How old are you?)
- "Meu pai tem sessenta anos" (My father is 60 years old)
- "Tinha dez anos quando morava no Rio" (I was 10 years old when I lived in Rio)
- "Vou fazer vinte anos em junho" (I'm going to turn 20 in June)

**Student can now:**
- Ask and state age correctly using TER
- Express age in present, past, and future
- Ask others' ages politely
- Talk about birthdays (fazer anos)
- Compare ages (older/younger)
- Avoid the critical mistake of using SER for age

**Typical sentences:**
- Tenho trinta anos (I'm 30 years old)
- Quantos anos voc√™ tem? (How old are you?)
- Meu irm√£o tem vinte e dois anos (My brother is 22 years old)
- Minha av√≥ tem oitenta anos (My grandmother is 80 years old)
- Tinha quinze anos quando aprendi portugu√™s (I was 15 years old when I learned Portuguese)
- Vou fazer trinta anos em dezembro (I'm going to turn 30 in December)
- Meu filho tem cinco anos (My son is 5 years old)
- Ele √© mais velho que eu (He's older than me)

**Age Conjugation - All Persons:**
| Subject | Present | Past (Preterite) | Past (Imperfect) | Future |
|---------|---------|------------------|------------------|--------|
| eu | tenho 25 anos | tive 25 anos | tinha 25 anos | vou ter 25 anos |
| voc√™/ele/ela | tem 30 anos | teve 30 anos | tinha 30 anos | vai ter 30 anos |
| n√≥s | temos 28 anos | tivemos 28 anos | t√≠nhamos 28 anos | vamos ter 28 anos |
| eles/elas | t√™m 35 anos | tiveram 35 anos | tinham 35 anos | v√£o ter 35 anos |

**Critical Grammar Point - WHY "ter" not "ser":**
- **Portuguese concept:** You POSSESS years (voc√™ TEM anos)
- **English concept:** You ARE an age
- This is a MAJOR difference from English - students must internalize TER!

**Common Age Expressions:**
- Quantos anos voc√™ tem? (How old are you? - formal/informal)
- Que idade voc√™ tem? (What age do you have? - more formal)
- Voc√™ tem quantos anos? (You have how many years? - colloquial word order)
- Fazer anos = to have a birthday: "Vou fazer 30 anos" (I'm going to turn 30)
- Completar anos = to complete years: "Completei 25 anos ontem" (I turned 25 yesterday)

**Sample Conversations:**

**Conversation 1:**
- A: Quantos anos voc√™ tem? (How old are you?)
- B: Tenho vinte e sete anos. E voc√™? (I'm 27. And you?)
- A: Tenho trinta e dois. (I'm 32.)
- B: Quando √© seu anivers√°rio? (When is your birthday?)
- A: √â em maio. Vou fazer trinta e tr√™s. (It's in May. I'm going to turn 33.)

**Conversation 2:**
- A: Sua irm√£ tem quantos anos? (How old is your sister?)
- B: Ela tem dezoito anos. (She's 18.)
- A: E seus pais? (And your parents?)
- B: Meu pai tem cinquenta e cinco e minha m√£e tem cinquenta e dois. (My father is 55 and my mother is 52.)

**Conversation 3 - Past tense:**
- A: Quantos anos voc√™ tinha quando come√ßou a trabalhar? (How old were you when you started working?)
- B: Tinha dezesseis anos. Era muito jovem. (I was 16. I was very young.)

**Comparing Ages:**
- Sou mais velho que meu irm√£o (I'm older than my brother)
- Ela √© mais nova que eu (She's younger than me)
- Tenho a mesma idade que voc√™ (I'm the same age as you)
- Ele √© dois anos mais velho (He's two years older)
- Sou cinco anos mais nova (I'm five years younger)

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ‚ùå "Sou 25 anos" (WRONG - never use ser!)
- ‚úÖ "Tenho 25 anos" (CORRECT)
- ‚ùå "Tenho 25 ano" (wrong - missing plural)
- ‚úÖ "Tenho 25 anos" (correct - always plural except "um ano")
- ‚ùå "Tenho vinte cinco anos" (wrong - missing "e")
- ‚úÖ "Tenho vinte e cinco anos" (correct)
- ‚ùå "Quantos voc√™ tem anos?" (wrong word order)
- ‚úÖ "Quantos anos voc√™ tem?" (correct)

**Special Cases:**
- **One year old:** "Tenho um ano" (singular!) or "Meu filho tem um ano"
- **Zero years (baby):** "Tem seis meses" (has six months) - months will be taught later

**With Different Tenses:**
- **Present:** Tenho 30 anos (I'm 30)
- **Preterite (specific past moment):** "Tive 25 anos em 2020" (I was 25 in 2020 - specific year)
- **Imperfect (habitual/ongoing past):** "Tinha 10 anos quando morava l√°" (I was 10 when I lived there)
- **Future:** "Vou ter 40 anos em junho" (I'm going to be 40 in June)

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 15-45: Numbers ‚Üí now used for age
- Unit 16: "Tenho um cachorro" ‚Üí "Tenho vinte anos" (same verb TER!)
- Unit 14, 27-29: Possessives ‚Üí "Meu pai tem 60 anos"
- Unit 42: Imperfect ‚Üí "Tinha 15 anos" (I was 15)
- Unit 43: Comparatives ‚Üí "Sou mais velho que ele"

**Key Learning:**
- **CRITICAL:** Use TER for age, NEVER SER
- Pattern: tenho/tem/tinha + number + anos
- "Anos" is always plural (except "um ano")
- This is one of the most common expressions in Portuguese
- Essential for introductions and conversations

**Why This Unit:**
- **FOUNDATIONAL:** Age is asked in nearly every introduction
- Natural progression: learned numbers, now apply to age
- Ultra-granular: focuses ONLY on age expression (one concept)
- Addresses critical mistake (ser vs ter for age)
- Essential before telling time (similar TER usage)
- Practical: immediate use in conversations

### Unit 18: Negation (N√£o + verb)
**New vocabulary:**
- **n√£o** (not/no) - **CRITICAL UNIVERSAL CONCEPT**
- Review all verbs learned so far to apply negation

**Grammar introduced:**
- **NEGATION: "N√£o" + verb** - UNIVERSAL PATTERN for negative sentences!
  - Pattern: **n√£o + verb = negative**
  - Works with ALL verbs learned so far
  - Simple placement: n√£o comes directly before the verb
- This is a FOUNDATIONAL concept that applies to EVERY verb in Portuguese

**Practice format - Applying negation to all known verbs:**

**From Unit 1 (ser):**
- Affirmative: "Sou brasileiro" ‚Üí Negative: "**N√£o** sou brasileiro"
- Affirmative: "Sou professor" ‚Üí Negative: "**N√£o** sou professor"

**From Unit 3 (morar):**
- Affirmative: "Moro em S√£o Paulo" ‚Üí Negative: "**N√£o** moro em S√£o Paulo"
- Affirmative: "Moro no Brasil" ‚Üí Negative: "**N√£o** moro no Brasil"

**From Unit 5 (trabalhar):**
- Affirmative: "Trabalho na universidade" ‚Üí Negative: "**N√£o** trabalho na universidade"
- Affirmative: "Trabalho em casa" ‚Üí Negative: "**N√£o** trabalho em casa"

**From Unit 6 (falar):**
- Affirmative: "Falo ingl√™s" ‚Üí Negative: "**N√£o** falo ingl√™s"
- Affirmative: "Falo portugu√™s" ‚Üí Negative: "**N√£o** falo portugu√™s"

**From Unit 7 (andar de):**
- Affirmative: "Ando de carro" ‚Üí Negative: "**N√£o** ando de carro"
- Affirmative: "Ando de √¥nibus" ‚Üí Negative: "**N√£o** ando de √¥nibus"

**From Unit 10 (ir):**
- Affirmative: "Vou de carro" ‚Üí Negative: "**N√£o** vou de carro"

**From Unit 12 (estar):**
- Affirmative: "Estou em casa" ‚Üí Negative: "**N√£o** estou em casa"
- Affirmative: "Estou cansado" ‚Üí Negative: "**N√£o** estou cansado"

**Student can now:**
- **Create negative sentences with ANY verb** - major milestone!
- Express what they DON'T do, DON'T have, AREN'T, etc.
- Understand that negation is universal across all verbs
- Use "n√£o" as the PRIMARY negation word in Portuguese
- Apply this pattern to all future verbs automatically

**Typical sentences:**
- N√£o sou americano (I'm not American)
- N√£o moro no Rio (I don't live in Rio)
- N√£o trabalho no banco (I don't work at the bank)
- N√£o falo espanhol (I don't speak Spanish)
- N√£o ando de carro (I don't go by car)
- N√£o vou de √¥nibus (I don't go by bus)
- N√£o estou cansado (I'm not tired)
- N√£o estou em casa (I'm not at home)

**üó£Ô∏è Spoken Brazilian Portuguese:**
In casual speech, "n√£o" before verbs is often pronounced as **"num"**:
- Formal/Writing: "Eu n√£o sei" / "N√£o moro no Rio"
- Casual Speech: "Num sei" / "Num moro no Rio"
- Very common: "Num √©?" (Isn't it?), "Num tem" (There isn't/doesn't have)

**Important:**
- **Always write "n√£o"** - "num" is only a pronunciation
- This is extremely common in spoken Brazilian Portuguese
- European Portuguese typically pronounces "n√£o" more fully
- Recognize this in speech, but use "n√£o" in your own production until very comfortable

**Combining affirmative + negative (very common):**
- Falo portugu√™s, mas **n√£o** falo espanhol (I speak Portuguese, but I don't speak Spanish)
- Moro em S√£o Paulo, mas **n√£o** trabalho em S√£o Paulo (I live in S√£o Paulo, but I don't work in S√£o Paulo)
- Sou brasileiro, mas **n√£o** moro no Brasil (I'm Brazilian, but I don't live in Brazil)
- Estou cansado, mas **n√£o** estou doente (I'm tired, but I'm not sick)

**Double negatives (not in this unit):**
- Portuguese uses "nada" (nothing), "ningu√©m" (nobody), "nunca" (never) WITH "n√£o"
- This will be taught later

**Word Order:**
- Subject + **n√£o** + verb: Eu **n√£o** falo ingl√™s
- Can drop subject (pro-drop): **N√£o** falo ingl√™s
- **n√£o** ALWAYS comes before the verb

**Common Patterns:**
- N√£o + -AR verb: n√£o moro, n√£o trabalho, n√£o falo, n√£o ando
- N√£o + irregular verbs: n√£o sou, n√£o vou, n√£o estou
- Mas (but) connecting opposites: "Falo X, mas n√£o falo Y"

**Full introduction with negations:**
- Sou o Jo√£o.
- Sou brasileiro, mas **n√£o** sou do Rio - sou de Belo Horizonte.
- Sou professor, mas **n√£o** trabalho na escola - trabalho na universidade.
- Moro em S√£o Paulo, mas meu pai **n√£o** mora em S√£o Paulo.
- Falo portugu√™s e ingl√™s, mas **n√£o** falo espanhol.
- Ando de √¥nibus. **N√£o** ando de carro.
- Meu irm√£o mora no Rio, mas **n√£o** fala ingl√™s.

**Key Learning:**
- **"N√£o" + verb = universal negation pattern**
- Works with EVERY verb in Portuguese
- Simple placement: n√£o comes directly before verb
- This is ONE OF THE MOST IMPORTANT patterns in Portuguese
- Students can now express both what they DO and what they DON'T DO

**Why This Unit:**
- **CRITICAL STANDALONE CONCEPT**: Negation deserves dedicated focus
- Universal pattern that applies to ALL verbs (not just one verb)
- Natural progression: students have learned ~10 verbs, now can negate all of them
- Ultra-granular: teaches one universal grammar pattern
- Foundational for all future communication - negation is essential
- Students immediately double their expressive power (yes + no)

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Applies to ALL verbs learned in Units 1-14
- Works with ser (Unit 1), morar (Unit 3), trabalhar (Unit 5), falar (Unit 6), andar (Unit 7), ir (Unit 10), estar (Unit 12)
- Combines naturally with "mas" (but) from Unit 6
- Will apply to all future verbs automatically

### Unit 19: Possession (Tenho - Pets & Vehicles)
**New vocabulary:**
- **tenho** (I have) - **THIRD IRREGULAR VERB** (not *tero)
- Pets:
  - cachorro (dog) - masculine
  - gato (cat) - masculine
  - p√°ssaro (bird) - masculine
- Vehicles:
  - carro (car) - masculine
  - bicicleta (bicycle) - feminine
  - moto / motocicleta (motorcycle) - feminine
- Indefinite articles: **um** (masculine), **uma** (feminine)

**Grammar introduced:**
- Third irregular verb: **tenho** (I have) - from "ter"
  - NOT regular: would be *tero (wrong)
  - Correct: tenho
- Possession: "Tenho um/uma [thing]"
- **Applying negation from Unit 15:** "N√£o tenho" (I don't have)
- Indefinite articles for expressing "a" or "one"
- Article omission in negative: "N√£o tenho carro" (no article after negative)

**Practice format:**
- "Tenho um cachorro" (I have a dog)
- "Tenho uma bicicleta" (I have a bicycle)
- **"N√£o tenho carro"** (I don't have a car - using negation from Unit 18!)
- "Tenho um gato e um cachorro" (I have a cat and a dog)
- "Tenho uma moto" (I have a motorcycle)
- Natural style: "Tenho um cachorro, mas n√£o tenho gato"

**Student can now:**
- Express what they own/possess (pets, vehicles, belongings)
- Use third irregular verb (tenho)
- Distinguish um (masculine) vs uma (feminine)
- **Apply negation to tenho:** "N√£o tenho" (building on Unit 18)
- Talk about pets and vehicles
- Combine with "e" and "mas" for complex statements
- Connect possessions with possessive adjectives: "Meu cachorro" (from Unit 14)

**Typical sentences:**
- Tenho um cachorro (I have a dog)
- Tenho um gato (I have a cat)
- Tenho um carro (I have a car)
- Tenho uma bicicleta (I have a bicycle)
- Tenho uma moto (I have a motorcycle)
- **N√£o tenho carro** (I don't have a car)
- **N√£o tenho cachorro** (I don't have a dog)
- Tenho uma bicicleta, mas n√£o tenho carro (I have a bicycle, but I don't have a car)
- Tenho um gato e um cachorro (I have a cat and a dog)

**Combining with Unit 14 (possessives):**
- Tenho um cachorro. **Meu cachorro** √© grande. (I have a dog. My dog is big.)
- Tenho uma bicicleta. **Minha bicicleta** √© nova. (I have a bicycle. My bicycle is new.)
- **Meu pai** tem um carro. (**My father** has a car - voc√™ form will be taught later)

**Gender Awareness:**
- **Masculine:** cachorro, gato, carro, p√°ssaro ‚Üí **um**
- **Feminine:** bicicleta, moto ‚Üí **uma**

**Article Usage:**
- **Affirmative:** Tenho **um/uma** + noun
  - Tenho **um** cachorro
  - Tenho **uma** bicicleta
- **Negative:** N√£o tenho + noun (NO ARTICLE typical in BP)
  - N√£o tenho carro (not: N√£o tenho um carro)
  - N√£o tenho cachorro (not: N√£o tenho um cachorro)

**Common Patterns:**
- Tenho + um/uma: "Tenho um cachorro"
- **N√£o tenho + noun (no article):** "N√£o tenho carro"
- Tenho + multiple items: "Tenho um gato e uma bicicleta"
- Contrast with "mas": "Tenho bicicleta, mas n√£o tenho moto"

**Sample Conversation:**
- A: Voc√™ tem carro? (Do you have a car? - voc√™ form preview)
- B: N√£o, n√£o tenho carro. Tenho uma bicicleta. (No, I don't have a car. I have a bicycle.)
- A: E cachorro? (And a dog?)
- B: Sim, tenho um cachorro. Meu cachorro √© grande. (Yes, I have a dog. My dog is big.)

**Full introduction with possessions:**
- Sou o Jo√£o.
- Sou brasileiro e professor.
- Sou casado.
- Sou de Belo Horizonte.
- Moro em S√£o Paulo, na Rua Paulista.
- Trabalho na universidade.
- Falo portugu√™s e ingl√™s.
- Meu pai mora no Rio.
- **Tenho um cachorro e uma bicicleta.**
- **N√£o tenho carro.**
- Meu cachorro √© grande e minha bicicleta √© nova.

**Key Learning:**
- **tenho** is irregular (third irregular verb after ser, estar)
- Use um/uma in affirmative, often omit article in negative
- Can combine possessions with possessive adjectives from Unit 14
- Negation works naturally: n√£o tenho (from Unit 18)

**Why This Unit:**
- Natural progression: after negation (Unit 18), apply it to a new verb
- Ultra-granular: introduces ONE irregular verb focused on possession
- Essential skill for personal communication - expressing what you own
- Pets and vehicles are immediate, concrete vocabulary
- Builds on possessives from Unit 14: "Tenho um cachorro. Meu cachorro..."

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 14: possessives ‚Üí "Tenho um cachorro. Meu cachorro √© grande"
- Unit 15: negation ‚Üí "N√£o tenho carro"
- Unit 1: ser ‚Üí "Meu cachorro √© grande"
- Students can now express ownership and describe what they own

**Note:** Age expression ("Tenho X anos" = I am X years old) will be introduced later when numbers are taught.

### Unit 22: -ER Verbs (como, bebo, corro)

**Student can now:**
- Express eating, drinking, and running habits

- Apply negation to -ER verbs

**Typical sentences:**

- Bebo caf√© de manh√£

### Unit 23: Voc√™ (You) - Questions and Answers
**New vocabulary:**
- voc√™ (you - formal/neutral singular)
- Question words:
  - onde (where)
  - como (how - not the verb!)
  - o que (what)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **MAJOR MILESTONE**: First pronoun other than "eu"
- **voc√™** = you (singular, formal/neutral)
- **Question formation**: Voc√™ + verb + ?
- **Different verb endings for voc√™**:
  - -AR verbs: voc√™ mora, trabalha, anda, fala, gosta (ending in -a)
  - -ER verbs: voc√™ come, bebe, corre (ending in -e)
  - **Irregular verbs (with accents!)**: voc√™ **√©**, **est√°**, tem
    - Note the accent marks: √© (from ser), est√° (from estar)
    - eu sou ‚Üí voc√™ **√©** (not *voc√™ sou)
    - eu estou ‚Üí voc√™ **est√°** (not *voc√™ estou)
- Pattern recognition: voc√™ uses **third person singular** (not the -o ending)

**Practice format:**
- Questions to ask someone: "Voc√™ mora em S√£o Paulo?", "Voc√™ fala ingl√™s?"
- Answering questions about yourself: "Sim, moro" / "N√£o, n√£o moro"
- Question words: "Onde voc√™ mora?", "Voc√™ √© de onde?"

**Student can now:**
- Ask questions using "voc√™"
- Understand the difference between eu (-o) and voc√™ (-a/-e) verb forms
- Conduct basic conversations (asking and answering)
- Use question intonation and structure

**Typical sentences:**
- Voc√™ √© brasileiro? (Are you Brazilian?)
- Voc√™ mora em S√£o Paulo? (Do you live in S√£o Paulo?)
- Onde voc√™ trabalha? (Where do you work?)
- Voc√™ fala portugu√™s? (Do you speak Portuguese?)
- Voc√™ gosta de caf√©? (Do you like coffee?)
- Voc√™ tem cachorro? (Do you have a dog?)
- Voc√™ est√° cansado? (Are you tired?)

**üó£Ô∏è Spoken Brazilian Portuguese:**
In casual speech, "voc√™" is often reduced to **"c√™"** (pronounced like "seh"):
- Formal/Writing: "Voc√™ est√° em casa?" / "Voc√™ √© brasileiro?"
- Casual Speech: "C√™ t√° em casa?" / "C√™ √© brasileiro?"
- Very common: "C√™ vai?" (Are you going?), "C√™ quer?" (Do you want?)

**Important:**
- This reduction happens **before verbs** in casual speech
- Write "voc√™" but recognize "c√™" in conversation
- Often combined with other reductions: "C√™ t√°" = Voc√™ est√°
- European Portuguese uses "tu" instead of "voc√™" with different verb forms

**üí¨ Natural Answers to Yes/No Questions:**
Brazilians typically **repeat the verb** rather than just saying "sim/n√£o":
- Q: "Voc√™ fala portugu√™s?"
- Natural A: "**Falo.**" (not just "Sim")
- Emphatic: "Falo, sim!" or "N√£o, n√£o falo."

**Verb Form Comparison:**
- **eu moro** / voc√™ mora
- **eu trabalho** / voc√™ trabalha
- **eu ando** / voc√™ anda
- **eu falo** / voc√™ fala
- **eu gosto** / voc√™ gosta
- **eu como** / voc√™ come
- **eu bebo** / voc√™ bebe
- **eu corro** / voc√™ corre
- **eu sou** / voc√™ √©
- **eu estou** / voc√™ est√°
- **eu tenho** / voc√™ tem

**Sample Conversation:**
- A: Oi! Voc√™ √© brasileiro?
- B: N√£o, sou americano. E voc√™?
- A: Sou brasileiro. Voc√™ mora em S√£o Paulo?
- B: Sim, moro. E voc√™?
- A: Tamb√©m moro em S√£o Paulo. Onde voc√™ trabalha?
- B: Trabalho na universidade. Voc√™ fala ingl√™s?
- A: Sim, falo um pouco.

**Key Learning:**
- This is a **major cognitive shift** - students must now track WHO is doing the action
- The -o ending means "I" (eu)
- The -a (for -AR) and -e (for -ER) endings mean "you" (voc√™) or "he/she" (ele/ela)
- Question formation is simple: statement ‚Üí add question intonation
- voc√™ is used for both formal and informal contexts in Brazilian Portuguese (unlike European Portuguese)

### Unit 24: Ele/Ela (He/She) - Talking About Others
**New vocabulary:**
- ele (he)
- ela (she)
- o nome (the name)
- Common names and relationships (for practice examples)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **ele** = he / **ela** = she (third person singular)
- **KEY INSIGHT: ele/ela use the SAME verb forms as voc√™!**
- Gender distinction: ele (masculine) vs ela (feminine)
- Verb forms (identical to voc√™):
  - -AR verbs: ele/ela mora, trabalha, anda, fala, gosta (ending in -a)
  - -ER verbs: ele/ela come, bebe, corre (ending in -e)
  - Irregular: ele/ela **√©**, **est√°**, tem
- Talking about a third person (not present in the conversation)

**Practice format:**
- Describing others: "Ele mora em S√£o Paulo", "Ela trabalha na escola"

- Ele est√° cansado. (He is tired.)

| Verb | eu | voc√™ | ele/ela | n√≥s | voc√™s |
|------|-----|------|---------|-----|-------|

**Pattern Recognition:**
- -AR verbs: infinitive stem + **-am** (falar ‚Üí falam)
- -ER verbs: infinitive stem + **-em** (comer ‚Üí comem)
- Irregular: s√£o, est√£o, t√™m (but all end in -m or nasal sound)
- **The -am/-em ending signals plural "you"**

**üí¨ Natural Answers to "Voc√™s...?" Questions:**

- Emphatic answers add "sim": "Falamos, sim!" or double negation: "N√£o, n√£o falamos, n√£o."

**Key Learning:**
- voc√™s = plural of voc√™ (you ‚Üí you all)

### Unit 27: Eles/Elas (They) - Talking About Groups

  - -AR verbs: eles/elas moram, trabalham, andam, falam, gostam (ending in **-am**)

**Typical sentences:**
- Eles s√£o brasileiros. (They [masc/mixed] are Brazilian.)

- Elas falam portugu√™s e ingl√™s. (They speak Portuguese and English.)
- Eles est√£o cansados. (They are tired.)
- Elas t√™m um cachorro. (They have a dog.)
- Eles gostam de caf√©. (They like coffee.)

| Verb | eu | voc√™ | ele/ela | n√≥s | voc√™s | eles/elas |
|------|-----|------|---------|-----|-------|-----------|
| morar | moro | mora | mora | moramos | moram | moram |
| trabalhar | trabalho | trabalha | trabalha | trabalhamos | trabalham | trabalham |
| falar | falo | fala | fala | falamos | falam | falam |

| comer | como | come | come | comemos | comem | comem |
| beber | bebo | bebe | bebe | bebemos | bebem | bebem |
| ser | sou | √© | √© | somos | s√£o | s√£o |
| estar | estou | est√° | est√° | estamos | est√£o | est√£o |

**Gender Rules for Eles/Elas:**
- **eles**: all masculine group (Jo√£o e Pedro)
- **eles**: mixed gender group (Jo√£o e Maria) - masculine "wins"
- **elas**: all feminine group ONLY (Maria e Ana)

**Sample Conversation:**

- voc√™s/eles/elas all use the **same verb forms** (third person plural)
- The only differences are the pronouns themselves and context:
  - **voc√™s** = addressing people directly (you all)
  - **eles/elas** = talking about people not present (they)
- eles = masculine/mixed, elas = all feminine
- **COMPLETE PRONOUN SYSTEM ACHIEVED:**
  - Singular: eu (I), voc√™ (you), ele/ela (he/she)
  - Plural: n√≥s (we), voc√™s (you all), eles/elas (they)

**Pattern Summary - All Six Persons:**
- **eu**: -o ending (moro, como)
- **voc√™/ele/ela**: -a (AR) / -e (ER) endings (mora, come)
- **n√≥s**: -amos (AR) / -emos (ER) endings (moramos, comemos)
- **voc√™s/eles/elas**: -am (AR) / -em (ER) endings (moram, comem)

**Why This Unit:**
- Natural progression: ele/ela (Unit 22) ‚Üí eles/elas (Unit 25)
- Completes the entire pronoun paradigm
- Shows the parallelism: voc√™‚Üívoc√™s / ele/ela‚Üíeles/elas (same verb forms)
- Students can now express ANYTHING with ANY subject in Portuguese present tense
- **This is a MAJOR MILESTONE** - full conjugation competence!

### Unit 28: -IR Verbs (abro, parto, assisto)
**New vocabulary:**
- abro (I open) - first -IR verb
- parto (I leave/depart) - second -IR verb
- assisto (I watch) - third -IR verb (infinitive already known from Unit 19)
- Common vocabulary:
  - a porta (the door)
  - a janela (the window)
  - a loja (the store)
  - cedo (early)
  - tarde (late)
  - filmes (movies/films)
  - s√©ries (TV series)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **-IR verb pattern: -IR ‚Üí -o** (same ending as -AR and -ER verbs!)
- abrir ‚Üí abro
- partir ‚Üí parto
- assistir ‚Üí assisto
- **REVELATION: "-o = I" works for ALL THREE verb types!**
- Complete regular verb system: -AR, -ER, -IR all use -o
- Negation with -IR verbs: n√£o abro, n√£o parto, n√£o assisto

**Practice format - All forms:**
- **Affirmative:** "Abro a porta", "Parto cedo", "Assisto filmes brasileiros"
- **Negative:** "N√£o abro a janela", "N√£o parto tarde", "N√£o assisto s√©ries"
- Combined: "Abro a loja, mas n√£o parto cedo"
- Natural style: "Assisto filmes todo dia"

**Student can now:**
- Conjugate -IR verbs in present tense
- Recognize all three regular verb patterns (-AR, -ER, -IR)
- See that "-o" is truly universal for "I" across all verb types
- Apply negation to -IR verbs
- Connect back to Unit 16: "Gosto de assistir" + "Assisto filmes"

**Typical sentences:**
- Abro a porta (I open the door)
- Abro a janela de manh√£ (I open the window in the morning)
- Parto cedo (I leave early)
- N√£o parto tarde (I don't leave late)
- Assisto filmes brasileiros (I watch Brazilian films)
- Assisto s√©ries em portugu√™s (I watch series in Portuguese)
- N√£o assisto televis√£o (I don't watch television)

**Connecting to Unit 16:**
- Unit 16: "Gosto de assistir filmes brasileiros" (I like to watch Brazilian films)
- Unit 23: "Assisto filmes brasileiros todo dia" (I watch Brazilian films every day)
- Students see: infinitive in preferences ‚Üí conjugated in actual actions

**Complete -o Pattern Recognition:**
- **-AR verbs:** morar ‚Üí moro, trabalhar ‚Üí trabalho, andar ‚Üí ando, falar ‚Üí falo, gostar ‚Üí gosto
- **-ER verbs:** comer ‚Üí como, beber ‚Üí bebo, correr ‚Üí corro
- **-IR verbs:** abrir ‚Üí abro, partir ‚Üí parto, assistir ‚Üí assisto
- **ALL THREE use -o for "I"!** This is the universal first person singular ending

**Full Conjugation for -IR Verbs (All Pronouns):**
| Pronoun | abrir | partir | assistir |
|---------|-------|--------|----------|
| eu | abro | parto | assisto |
| voc√™/ele/ela | abre | parte | assiste |
| n√≥s | abrimos | partimos | assistimos |
| voc√™s/eles/elas | abrem | partem | assistem |

**Pattern for All Pronouns (-IR verbs):**
- eu: abro, parto, assisto (-o)
- voc√™/ele/ela: abre, parte, assiste (-e)
- n√≥s: abrimos, partimos, assistimos (-imos)
- voc√™s/eles/elas: abrem, partem, assistem (-em)

**Key Learning:**
- This completes the **three regular verb types** in Portuguese
- Students now know: -AR (5 verbs), -ER (3 verbs), -IR (3 verbs)
- **The -o ending is truly universal** across all regular verbs
- Students can now conjugate hundreds of regular verbs by recognizing the infinitive ending
- Only need to memorize irregular verbs (sou, estou, tenho, vou)

**Why This Unit:**
- Natural progression: -AR verbs ‚Üí -ER verbs ‚Üí -IR verbs
- Completes the regular verb conjugation system
- Still in present tense (not jumping to new tenses)
- **MAJOR MILESTONE**: All regular verb patterns complete!
- Students can now handle any regular verb in Portuguese present tense
- Sets foundation for future tense work (all three patterns will extend to other tenses)

### Unit 29: Future with "Vou + Infinitive" (Going to...)
**New vocabulary:**
- amanh√£ (tomorrow)
- depois (later, after)
- hoje √† noite (tonight)
- no fim de semana (on the weekend)
- na pr√≥xima semana (next week)
- no pr√≥ximo m√™s (next month)
- Time expressions already known: agora (now), hoje (today), cedo (early), tarde (late)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Future construction: vou + infinitive** = "going to" (immediate/planned future)
- This combines two concepts students already know:
  - **vou** from Unit 8 (irregular verb "ir")
  - **infinitives** from Unit 19 (gosto de + infinitive)
- Pattern: subject + vou/vai/vamos/v√£o + infinitive verb
- Expressing future plans and intentions
- Time expressions to indicate when actions will happen

**Practice format:**
- "Vou estudar portugu√™s amanh√£" (I'm going to study Portuguese tomorrow)
- "Vou trabalhar no fim de semana" (I'm going to work on the weekend)
- "Vou viajar na pr√≥xima semana" (I'm going to travel next week)
- With negation: "N√£o vou trabalhar amanh√£" (I'm not going to work tomorrow)

**Student can now:**
- Express future plans and intentions
- Talk about what they're going to do (later today, tomorrow, next week, etc.)
- Use the full conjugation of "ir" + infinitive for all pronouns
- Apply time expressions to indicate when
- Distinguish between present actions (Unit 23: "Estudo") and future plans (Unit 24: "Vou estudar")

**Typical sentences:**
- Vou estudar portugu√™s amanh√£ (I'm going to study Portuguese tomorrow)
- Vou trabalhar hoje √† noite (I'm going to work tonight)
- Vou viajar no fim de semana (I'm going to travel on the weekend)
- Vou comer no restaurante depois (I'm going to eat at the restaurant later)
- N√£o vou assistir filmes hoje (I'm not going to watch movies today)
- Vou dormir cedo (I'm going to sleep early)

**üó£Ô∏è Spoken Brazilian Portuguese:**
In casual speech, "vou" is often pronounced as **"v√¥"** (sounds like "voh"):
- Formal/Writing: "Eu vou fazer" / "Vou trabalhar amanh√£"
- Casual Speech: "V√¥ faz√™" / "V√¥ trabalh√° amanh√£"
- Very common: "V√¥ l√°" (I'm going there), "V√¥ indo" (I'm going/leaving)

**Important:**
- Always write "vou" - "v√¥" is only pronunciation
- In fast speech, infinitive endings may also reduce: fazer ‚Üí faz√™, trabalhar ‚Üí trabalh√°
- This is extremely common in spontaneous Brazilian Portuguese
- Recognize in speech, but use full forms in your own production initially

**Full Conjugation - "Ir + Infinitive" (All Pronouns):**
| Pronoun | ir (to go) | + infinitive | Example |
|---------|------------|--------------|---------|
| eu | vou | + estudar | Vou estudar |
| voc√™/ele/ela | vai | + estudar | Vai estudar |
| n√≥s | vamos | + estudar | Vamos estudar |
| voc√™s/eles/elas | v√£o | + estudar | V√£o estudar |

**Examples with All Pronouns:**
- Eu vou trabalhar amanh√£ (I'm going to work tomorrow)
- Voc√™ vai estudar hoje? (Are you going to study today?)
- Ele vai viajar na pr√≥xima semana (He's going to travel next week)
- N√≥s vamos comer no restaurante (We're going to eat at the restaurant)
- Voc√™s v√£o assistir o filme? (Are you all going to watch the movie?)
- Eles v√£o partir cedo (They're going to leave early)

**Connecting Previous Units:**
- Unit 8: "Vou de √¥nibus" (method of transport - present habitual)
- Unit 24: "Vou trabalhar de √¥nibus amanh√£" (future action + method)
- Unit 16: "Gosto de viajar" (I like to travel - preference)
- Unit 24: "Vou viajar amanh√£" (I'm going to travel - future plan)

**With Negation (from Unit 14):**
- N√£o vou trabalhar amanh√£ (I'm not going to work tomorrow)
- N√£o vou estudar hoje √† noite (I'm not going to study tonight)
- Ele n√£o vai viajar (He's not going to travel)
- N√≥s n√£o vamos comer carne (We're not going to eat meat)

**Sample Conversation:**
- A: O que voc√™ vai fazer amanh√£? (What are you going to do tomorrow?)
- B: Vou trabalhar de manh√£, e depois vou estudar portugu√™s. (I'm going to work in the morning, and then I'm going to study Portuguese.)
- A: Voc√™ vai viajar no fim de semana? (Are you going to travel on the weekend?)
- B: N√£o, n√£o vou viajar. Vou ficar em casa. (No, I'm not going to travel. I'm going to stay home.)

**Key Learning:**
- This is the **most common way to express future in Brazilian Portuguese**
- More natural and conversational than the formal future tense (estudarei, trabalharei)
- Students already know both pieces: "ir" verb + infinitives
- Works with ALL verb types: -AR, -ER, -IR
- Can use any infinitive learned so far or new ones

**Distinction from Unit 8:**
- **Unit 8:** "Vou ao trabalho" (I go to work - location/destination)
- **Unit 24:** "Vou trabalhar" (I'm going to work - future action)
- Both use "vou" but with different constructions

**Why This Unit:**
- Natural progression after completing present tense verb system
- Builds on existing knowledge (vou + infinitives already taught separately)
- Immediate practical value - talking about plans
- Easier than past tense conjugations
- Ultra-granular approach: taught the pieces first, now combine them
- **MAJOR MILESTONE**: First non-present tense introduced!

### Unit 30: Progressive Tenses - Estar + Gerund (Estou Fazendo)

**New vocabulary:**
- **Progressive expressions:**
  - agora (now)
  - neste momento (at this moment)
  - agora mesmo (right now)
  - atualmente (currently)
  - no momento (at the moment)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Progressive tense: ESTAR + GERUND:**
  - Expresses actions in progress (ongoing right now)
  - "I am doing", "You are working", "We are eating"
  - Very common in Brazilian Portuguese

**Forming the gerund:**

**-AR verbs: remove -ar, add -ando:**
- falar ‚Üí fal**ando** (speaking)
- trabalhar ‚Üí trabalh**ando** (working)
- estudar ‚Üí estud**ando** (studying)
- cozinhar ‚Üí cozinh**ando** (cooking)

**-ER verbs: remove -er, add -endo:**
- comer ‚Üí com**endo** (eating)
- beber ‚Üí beb**endo** (drinking)
- fazer ‚Üí faz**endo** (doing/making)
- escrever ‚Üí escrev**endo** (writing)

**-IR verbs: remove -ir, add -indo:**
- abrir ‚Üí abr**indo** (opening)
- dormir ‚Üí dorm**indo** (sleeping)
- assistir ‚Üí assist**indo** (watching)
- sair ‚Üí sa**indo** (leaving/going out)

**Structure: ESTAR (conjugated) + GERUND**
- Eu **estou** trabalhando. (I am working.)
- Voc√™ **est√°** comendo. (You are eating.)
- Ele **est√°** dormindo. (He is sleeping.)
- N√≥s **estamos** estudando. (We are studying.)
- Voc√™s **est√£o** assistindo TV. (You all are watching TV.)
- Eles **est√£o** falando. (They are talking.)

**When to use progressive:**
- Actions happening RIGHT NOW: "O que voc√™ est√° fazendo?" (What are you doing?)
- Temporary situations: "Estou morando em S√£o Paulo." (I'm living in S√£o Paulo - temporarily)
- Emphasis on ongoing action: "Estou trabalhando!" (I'm working! - can't be interrupted)

**Practice format:**
- Form gerunds from infinitives: falar ‚Üí falando
- Conjugate estar + gerund: "Eu estou comendo"
- Answer "O que voc√™ est√° fazendo?"
- Describe what others are doing
- Use with "agora" and time expressions

**Student can now:**
- Form the gerund for all verb types (-ando, -endo, -indo)
- Use progressive tense for actions in progress
- Ask "O que voc√™ est√° fazendo?" (What are you doing?)
- Describe ongoing actions
- Distinguish simple present from progressive

**Typical sentences:**
- Eu estou trabalhando. (I am working.)
- O que voc√™ est√° fazendo? (What are you doing?)
- Ela est√° cozinhando. (She is cooking.)
- N√≥s estamos estudando portugu√™s. (We are studying Portuguese.)
- Eles est√£o assistindo TV. (They are watching TV.)
- Estou falando no telefone. (I'm talking on the phone.)
- Ele est√° dormindo agora. (He is sleeping now.)

**Sample conversation:**
```
A: Al√¥? Oi! O que voc√™ est√° fazendo?
   (Hello? Hi! What are you doing?)
B: Estou cozinhando o jantar. E voc√™?
   (I'm cooking dinner. And you?)

A: Eu estou assistindo um filme.
   (I'm watching a movie.)
B: Qual filme?
   (Which movie?)

A: Um filme brasileiro. √â muito bom!
   (A Brazilian movie. It's very good!)
B: Legal! Bom, eu preciso ir. Ainda estou cozinhando.
   (Cool! Well, I need to go. I'm still cooking.)
```

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ‚ùå "Eu estou falar" (wrong - missing gerund ending)
- ‚úÖ "Eu estou falando" (correct)
- ‚ùå "Eu sou trabalhando" (wrong - use ESTAR not SER)
- ‚úÖ "Eu estou trabalhando" (correct)
- ‚ùå "falendo" (wrong ending for -AR verb)
- ‚úÖ "falando" (correct - -AR verbs use -ando)

**Gerund Formation - Summary:**

**-AR verbs ‚Üí -ANDO:**
- falar ‚Üí fal**ando**
- trabalhar ‚Üí trabalh**ando**
- estudar ‚Üí estud**ando**
- jogar ‚Üí jog**ando**
- comprar ‚Üí compr**ando**

**-ER verbs ‚Üí -ENDO:**
- comer ‚Üí com**endo**
- beber ‚Üí beb**endo**
- fazer ‚Üí faz**endo**
- vender ‚Üí vend**endo**
- escrever ‚Üí escrev**endo**

**-IR verbs ‚Üí -INDO:**
- abrir ‚Üí abr**indo**
- dormir ‚Üí dorm**indo**
- assistir ‚Üí assist**indo**
- partir ‚Üí part**indo**
- sair ‚Üí sa**indo**

**Progressive Tense Conjugation:**

Using "trabalhar" (to work) as example:

- Eu **estou trabalhando** (I am working)
- Voc√™ **est√° trabalhando** (You are working)
- Ele/Ela **est√° trabalhando** (He/She is working)
- N√≥s **estamos trabalhando** (We are working)
- Voc√™s **est√£o trabalhando** (You all are working)
- Eles/Elas **est√£o trabalhando** (They are working)

**Simple Present vs Progressive:**

**Simple Present (habitual):**
- Eu trabalho todos os dias. (I work every day.)
- General habit, routine

**Progressive (right now):**
- Eu estou trabalhando agora. (I am working now.)
- Action happening at this moment

**Both are correct but different meanings!**

**Common Questions with Progressive:**
- O que voc√™ est√° fazendo? (What are you doing?)
- Onde voc√™ est√° indo? (Where are you going?)
- Com quem voc√™ est√° falando? (Who are you talking to?)
- Por que voc√™ est√° chorando? (Why are you crying?)

**Progressive in Past (preview for later unit):**
- Eu estava trabalhando. (I was working.)
- Uses imperfect of ESTAR + gerund
- Will be covered in future unit

**Negative Progressive:**
- Eu n√£o estou trabalhando. (I am not working.)
- Structure: N√ÉO + estar + gerund

**Emphasis and Style:**
Progressive emphasizes the ongoing nature:
- "Eu trabalho" (neutral: I work)
- "Eu estou trabalhando" (emphasis: I'm working - busy, can't be interrupted)

**Brazilian vs European Portuguese:**
- **Brazilian:** Uses progressive VERY commonly
- **European:** Uses simple present more often
- This course teaches Brazilian Portuguese

**Alternative Structure (less common in Brazilian):**
- Estar **a** + infinitive (European Portuguese)
- Estou **a** trabalhar. (I am working - European)
- Brazilian: Estou trabalhando. (more common)

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 12: ESTAR ‚Üí now using with gerund
- All verb units ‚Üí forming gerunds from these verbs
- Unit 62: Daily activities ‚Üí "Estou tomando banho" (I'm showering)
- Unit 38: Questions ‚Üí "O que voc√™ est√° fazendo?"

**Key Learning:**
- Progressive tense: ESTAR + gerund (-ando, -endo, -indo)
- Expresses actions in progress RIGHT NOW
- Very common in Brazilian Portuguese
- -AR ‚Üí -ando, -ER ‚Üí -endo, -IR ‚Üí -indo
- Essential for describing what's happening now

**Why This Unit:**
- **FOUNDATIONAL:** Progressive is extremely common in Brazilian Portuguese
- Natural progression: know present tense, now add progressive
- Ultra-granular: focuses ONLY on progressive formation
- Practical: immediate use for describing current actions
- Grammar milestone: important tense not yet covered

### Unit 31: Plural Possessives: Meus/Minhas (My - Plural)
**New vocabulary:**
- **meus/minhas** (my - masculine/feminine PLURAL) - extending Unit 14's meu/minha
- Plural family/friends:
  - irm√£os/irm√£s (brothers/sisters)
  - filhos/filhas (sons/daughters)
  - amigos/amigas (friends)
  - pais (parents - always masculine plural)
- Personal items (plural):
  - livros (books) - masculine plural
  - chaves (keys) - feminine plural
  - documentos (documents) - masculine plural
  - sapatos (shoes) - masculine plural

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Extending Unit 14:** Adding PLURAL forms meus/minhas to complete "my" system
- **Four forms total for "my":**
  - Masculine singular: **meu** pai (from Unit 14)
  - Feminine singular: **minha** m√£e (from Unit 14)
  - Masculine plural: **meus** irm√£os (NEW!)
  - Feminine plural: **minhas** irm√£s (NEW!)
- **Agreement rule (review from Unit 14):** Possessive agrees with the THING POSSESSED
- Position: possessive + noun (no article needed)

**Practice format:**
- Review from Unit 14: "Meu pai mora em S√£o Paulo", "Minha m√£e trabalha na escola"
- **NEW - Masculine plural:** "Meus irm√£os moram aqui" (My brothers live here)
- **NEW - Feminine plural:** "Minhas irm√£s falam ingl√™s" (My sisters speak English)
- **NEW - Parents:** "Meus pais moram no Rio" (My parents live in Rio)
- **NEW - Things (fem plural):** "Minhas chaves est√£o na mesa" (My keys are on the table)
- **NEW - Things (masc plural):** "Meus livros s√£o novos" (My books are new)

**Student can now:**
- **Complete the "my" possessive system:** meu/minha/meus/minhas
- Talk about family members in plural (meus irm√£os, minhas irm√£s, meus pais)
- Express possession of multiple items (meus livros, minhas chaves)
- Understand full gender AND number agreement for possessives
- Apply all four forms correctly based on the noun

**Typical sentences:**
- Review: Meu pai √© brasileiro (My father is Brazilian - from Unit 14)
- Review: Minha m√£e trabalha no hospital (My mother works at the hospital - from Unit 14)
- **NEW:** Meus irm√£os moram em S√£o Paulo (My brothers live in S√£o Paulo)
- **NEW:** Minhas irm√£s falam ingl√™s (My sisters speak English)
- **NEW:** Meus pais moram no Rio (My parents live in Rio)
- **NEW:** Meus amigos s√£o brasileiros (My friends are Brazilian)
- **NEW:** Minhas chaves est√£o aqui (My keys are here)
- **NEW:** Meus livros s√£o novos (My books are new)

**Complete "My" Possessive System:**
| Gender/Number | Form | Example | Translation |
|---------------|------|---------|-------------|
| Masc. Singular | meu | meu pai | my father |
| Fem. Singular | minha | minha m√£e | my mother |
| Masc. Plural | meus | meus irm√£os | my brothers |
| Fem. Plural | minhas | minhas irm√£s | my sisters |

**Agreement Examples:**
- o livro ‚Üí **meu** livro (masculine singular noun ‚Üí masculine singular possessive)
- a casa ‚Üí **minha** casa (feminine singular noun ‚Üí feminine singular possessive)
- os livros ‚Üí **meus** livros (masculine plural noun ‚Üí masculine plural possessive)
- as casas ‚Üí **minhas** casas (feminine plural noun ‚Üí feminine plural possessive)

**Common Patterns:**
- Singular (from Unit 14): meu pai, minha m√£e, meu amigo, minha amiga
- **Plural (NEW):** meus pais, minhas irm√£s, meus amigos, minhas chaves

**Sample Conversation:**
- A: Onde moram seus pais? (Where do your parents live? - voc√™ form preview)
- B: Meus pais moram no Rio. (My parents live in Rio.)
- A: E seus irm√£os? (And your brothers?)
- B: Meus irm√£os moram comigo em S√£o Paulo. (My brothers live with me in S√£o Paulo.)
- A: Voc√™ tem muitos amigos? (Do you have many friends?)
- B: Sim, meus amigos s√£o de S√£o Paulo. (Yes, my friends are from S√£o Paulo.)

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ‚ùå "Meu irm√£s" (wrong - irm√£s is feminine plural)
- ‚úÖ "Minhas irm√£s" (correct)
- ‚ùå "Minhas pais" (wrong - pais is masculine plural)
- ‚úÖ "Meus pais" (correct)
- ‚ùå "Minha livros" (wrong - livros is masculine plural)
- ‚úÖ "Meus livros" (correct)

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- **Unit 14:** Introduced meu/minha (singular) - now adding plural forms
- **Unit 16:** Used with possessions - "Tenho um cachorro. Meu cachorro..." ‚Üí Now: "Meus cachorros..."
- **Unit 13:** Used with location - "na casa do meu irm√£o" ‚Üí Now: "na casa dos meus pais"

**Key Learning:**
- **Four forms for "my":** meu/minha/meus/minhas
- Possessives agree with BOTH gender AND number of the thing possessed
- This completes the "my" possessive system
- Essential for talking about family in plural and multiple belongings

**Why This Unit:**
- Natural progression: extends Unit 14's singular possessives to plural
- Ultra-granular: adds ONLY plural forms of "my" (one concept)
- Essential before introducing other persons' possessives (your, his, her, our)
- Students master ONE person's complete system before moving to others
- Practical: enables richer conversation about family, friends, and belongings
