### Unit 32: Your/His/Her Possessives: Seu/Sua + Dele/Dela Construction
**New vocabulary:**
- **seu/sua/seus/suas** (your/his/her - masculine/feminine, singular/plural) - **AMBIGUOUS!**
- **dele** (his - literally "of-him")
- **dela** (her - literally "of-her")
- **deles** (their - masculine/mixed group)
- **delas** (their - feminine group only)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Seu/sua/seus/suas possessives** - can mean YOUR, HIS, HER, or THEIR!
  - Four forms: seu (masc sing), sua (fem sing), seus (masc pl), suas (fem pl)
  - **CRITICAL PROBLEM:** Extremely ambiguous in Brazilian Portuguese
- **SOLUTION: Dele/Dela construction** (PREFERRED in colloquial BP!)
  - Structure: **article + noun + dele/dela/deles/delas**
  - o irm√£o dele (his brother), a casa dela (her house)
  - **REQUIRES article:** Cannot say just "irm√£o dele"
- Position:
  - Seu/sua: possessive + noun (like meu/minha)
  - Dele/dela: article + noun + dele/dela

**The Ambiguity Problem:**

‚ö†Ô∏è **MAJOR ISSUE:** "Seu irm√£o" can mean 5 different things!
- **Your** brother (voc√™)
- **His** brother (ele)
- **Her** brother (ela)
- **Your (plural)** brother (voc√™s)
- **Their** brother (eles/elas)

**In conversation, this creates constant confusion!**

**Practice format - Seu/Sua (ambiguous):**
- "Seu pai mora aqui?" (Does your/his/her father live here?) - **AMBIGUOUS!**
- "Sua m√£e trabalha?" (Does your/his/her mother work?) - **AMBIGUOUS!**
- "Seus irm√£os falam ingl√™s?" (Do your/his/her brothers speak English?) - **AMBIGUOUS!**

**Practice format - Dele/Dela (CLEAR):**
- "O pai dele mora aqui?" (Does HIS father live here?) - **CLEAR!**
- "A m√£e dela trabalha?" (Does HER mother work?) - **CLEAR!**
- "Os irm√£os dele falam ingl√™s?" (Do HIS brothers speak English?) - **CLEAR!**

**Student can now:**
- Use seu/sua/seus/suas possessives (but understand the ambiguity)
- **Use dele/dela/deles/delas construction for clarity** (PREFERRED in BP!)
- Distinguish "your" from "his/her" using context or dele/dela
- Understand why Brazilians prefer the dele/dela construction
- Express third-person possession clearly

**Typical sentences with seu/sua:**
- Seu irm√£o mora aqui? (Does your/his/her brother live here?)
- Sua casa √© grande? (Is your/his/her house big?)
- Seus amigos s√£o brasileiros? (Are your/his/her friends Brazilian?)
- Suas chaves est√£o na mesa (Your/His/Her keys are on the table)

**Typical sentences with dele/dela (PREFERRED):**
- O irm√£o dele mora no Rio (HIS brother lives in Rio) - **CLEAR!**
- A casa dela √© grande (HER house is big) - **CLEAR!**
- Os amigos dele s√£o brasileiros (HIS friends are Brazilian) - **CLEAR!**
- As amigas delas trabalham aqui (THEIR (fem) friends work here) - **CLEAR!**

**Comparison - Ambiguous vs Clear:**
| Ambiguous (seu/sua) | Clear (dele/dela) | Meaning |
|---------------------|-------------------|---------|
| Seu carro √© novo | O carro dele √© novo | HIS car is new |
| Seu carro √© novo | O carro dela √© novo | HER car is new |
| Sua casa √© grande | A casa dele √© grande | HIS house is big |
| Sua casa √© grande | A casa dela √© grande | HER house is big |

**When to use which:**
- **Use meu/minha/meus/minhas** for "my" - always clear (from Units 14 & 27)
- **Use dele/dela/deles/delas** for "his/her/their" - clearest option! **PREFERRED in BP!**
- **Use seu/sua/seus/suas** for "your" (voc√™/voc√™s) - but can still be ambiguous

**CRITICAL: Dele/Dela REQUIRES article:**
- ‚ùå "irm√£o dele" (WRONG - missing article)
- ‚úÖ "o irm√£o dele" (CORRECT - with article)
- ‚ùå "casa dela" (WRONG - missing article)
- ‚úÖ "a casa dela" (CORRECT - with article)

**Full Possessive System So Far:**
| Person | Masc. Sing. | Fem. Sing. | Masc. Plural | Fem. Plural |
|--------|-------------|------------|--------------|-------------|
| eu (my) | meu pai | minha m√£e | meus irm√£os | minhas irm√£s |
| voc√™/ele/ela (your/his/her) - AMBIGUOUS | seu pai | sua m√£e | seus irm√£os | suas irm√£s |
| ele (his) - CLEAR | o pai dele | a m√£e dele | os irm√£os dele | as irm√£s dele |
| ela (her) - CLEAR | o pai dela | a m√£e dela | os irm√£os dela | as irm√£s dela |

**Common in BP Speech:**
- "Vi o carro dele ontem" (I saw his car yesterday) - **VERY COMMON**
- "Conhe√ßo a irm√£ dela" (I know her sister) - **VERY COMMON**
- "Gosto dos amigos deles" (I like their friends) - **VERY COMMON**
- "A m√£e dela mora no Rio" (Her mother lives in Rio) - **VERY COMMON**

**Sample Conversation:**
- A: Onde mora o irm√£o dele? (Where does his brother live?)
- B: O irm√£o dele mora em S√£o Paulo. (His brother lives in S√£o Paulo.)
- A: E a irm√£ dela? (And her sister?)
- B: A irm√£ dela mora no Rio. (Her sister lives in Rio.)
- A: Os pais deles moram juntos? (Do their parents live together?)
- B: N√£o, o pai dele mora aqui, mas a m√£e dela mora l√°. (No, his father lives here, but her mother lives there.)

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ‚ùå "irm√£o dele" (wrong - missing article)
- ‚úÖ "o irm√£o dele" (correct)
- ‚ùå "o seu irm√£o dele" (wrong - redundant: don't mix seu with dele)
- ‚úÖ "o irm√£o dele" (correct) OR "seu irm√£o" (correct but ambiguous)
- ‚ùå "dele casa" (wrong - wrong word order)
- ‚úÖ "a casa dele" (correct - article + noun + dele)

**Agreement with Dele/Dela:**
The article and noun agree with the thing possessed:
- **o** irm√£o dele (masculine singular noun ‚Üí o)
- **a** casa dela (feminine singular noun ‚Üí a)
- **os** amigos dele (masculine plural noun ‚Üí os)
- **as** chaves dela (feminine plural noun ‚Üí as)

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- **Unit 14:** meu/minha (my - singular)
- **Unit 27:** meus/minhas (my - plural)
- **Unit 28:** seu/sua + dele/dela (your/his/her) - completes third-person possession
- **Unit 33 (next):** nosso/nossa (our)

**Key Learning:**
- **Seu/sua is VERY ambiguous** - can mean your, his, her, or their
- **Dele/dela construction is PREFERRED in Brazilian Portuguese** for clarity
- Dele/dela ALWAYS requires the article before the noun
- This is essential for talking about HIS/HER family, friends, and belongings
- Students should favor dele/dela in speech to avoid confusion

**Why This Unit:**
- Critical for clear communication - ambiguity is a real problem in BP
- Ultra-granular: focuses on one possessive person (your/his/her) + the solution
- Teaches REAL Brazilian Portuguese usage, not just textbook forms
- Essential before past tense narratives (talking about "his friends," "her parents")
- Prepares for "our" possessives in next unit

### Unit 33: Our Possessives: Nosso/Nossa/Nossos/Nossas
**New vocabulary:**
- **nosso/nossa/nossos/nossas** (our - masculine/feminine, singular/plural)
- Words commonly used with "our":
  - fam√≠lia (family) - feminine
  - casa (house) - feminine
  - pa√≠s (country) - masculine
  - cidade (city) - feminine
  - trabalho (job/work) - masculine
  - projeto (project) - masculine

**Grammar introduced:**
- **"Our" possessive adjectives: nosso/nossa/nossos/nossas**
  - Four forms based on gender/number of noun:
    - **nosso** = our (masculine singular): nosso pai
    - **nossa** = our (feminine singular): nossa m√£e
    - **nossos** = our (masculine plural): nossos irm√£os
    - **nossas** = our (feminine plural): nossas irm√£s
- **Agreement rule (same as all possessives):** agrees with the THING POSSESSED
- Position: possessive + noun (no article needed)
- **No ambiguity!** - nosso/nossa ALWAYS means "our" (unlike seu/sua)

**Practice format:**
- "Nossa casa √© grande" (Our house is big)
- "Nosso pai mora em S√£o Paulo" (Our father lives in S√£o Paulo)
- "Nossos amigos s√£o brasileiros" (Our friends are Brazilian)
- "Nossas chaves est√£o na mesa" (Our keys are on the table)
- "Nossa fam√≠lia √© grande" (Our family is big)
- "Nosso trabalho √© dif√≠cil" (Our work is difficult)

**Student can now:**
- Express "our" possession with full gender/number agreement
- Use all four forms correctly (nosso/nossa/nossos/nossas)
- **Complete the possessive system:** my, your/his/her, our
- Talk about shared family, belongings, and experiences
- Combine with n√≥s (we) for complete first-person plural expression

**Typical sentences:**
- Nossa casa √© pequena (Our house is small)
- Nosso pai trabalha no banco (Our father works at the bank)
- Nossa m√£e √© professora (Our mother is a teacher)
- Nossos pais moram no Rio (Our parents live in Rio)
- Nossos irm√£os falam ingl√™s (Our brothers speak English)
- Nossas irm√£s moram aqui (Our sisters live here)
- Nossos amigos s√£o legais (Our friends are cool)
- Nossa cidade √© bonita (Our city is beautiful)

**Complete "Our" Possessive System:**
| Gender/Number | Form | Example | Translation |
|---------------|------|---------|-------------|
| Masc. Singular | nosso | nosso pai | our father |
| Fem. Singular | nossa | nossa m√£e | our mother |
| Masc. Plural | nossos | nossos irm√£os | our brothers |
| Fem. Plural | nossas | nossas irm√£s | our sisters |

**Agreement Examples:**
- o pai ‚Üí **nosso** pai (masculine singular noun ‚Üí nosso)
- a m√£e ‚Üí **nossa** m√£e (feminine singular noun ‚Üí nossa)
- os irm√£os ‚Üí **nossos** irm√£os (masculine plural noun ‚Üí nossos)
- as irm√£s ‚Üí **nossas** irm√£s (feminine plural noun ‚Üí nossas)

**Combining with N√≥s (we) from Unit 22:**
- **N√≥s moramos** em S√£o Paulo. **Nossa casa** √© grande. (We live in S√£o Paulo. Our house is big.)
- **Nossos pais** moram no Rio, mas **n√≥s moramos** aqui. (Our parents live in Rio, but we live here.)
- **Trabalhamos** juntos. **Nosso trabalho** √© dif√≠cil. (We work together. Our work is difficult.)

**Full Possessive System - COMPLETE:**
| Person | Masc. Sing. | Fem. Sing. | Masc. Plural | Fem. Plural |
|--------|-------------|------------|--------------|-------------|
| eu (my) | meu pai | minha m√£e | meus irm√£os | minhas irm√£s |
| voc√™/ele/ela (ambiguous) | seu pai | sua m√£e | seus irm√£os | suas irm√£s |
| ele (his - clear) | o pai dele | a m√£e dele | os irm√£os dele | as irm√£s dele |
| ela (her - clear) | o pai dela | a m√£e dela | os irm√£os dela | as irm√£s dela |
| n√≥s (our) | nosso pai | nossa m√£e | nossos irm√£os | nossas irm√£s |

**Sample Conversation:**
- A: Onde moram seus pais? (Where do your parents live?)
- B: Nossos pais moram no Rio, mas n√≥s moramos aqui em S√£o Paulo. (Our parents live in Rio, but we live here in S√£o Paulo.)
- A: E seus irm√£os? (And your siblings?)
- B: Nossos irm√£os moram com nossos pais no Rio. (Our siblings live with our parents in Rio.)
- A: Como √© sua casa? (What's your house like?)
- B: Nossa casa √© pequena, mas nossa cidade √© linda. (Our house is small, but our city is beautiful.)

**Common Patterns:**
- Nossa + feminine singular: nossa casa, nossa fam√≠lia, nossa cidade, nossa m√£e
- Nosso + masculine singular: nosso pai, nosso pa√≠s, nosso trabalho, nosso irm√£o
- Nossas + feminine plural: nossas irm√£s, nossas chaves, nossas amigas
- Nossos + masculine plural: nossos pais, nossos amigos, nossos irm√£os

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ‚ùå "Nosso m√£e" (wrong - m√£e is feminine)
- ‚úÖ "Nossa m√£e" (correct)
- ‚ùå "Nossa pai" (wrong - pai is masculine)
- ‚úÖ "Nosso pai" (correct)
- ‚ùå "Nosso irm√£s" (wrong - irm√£s is feminine plural)
- ‚úÖ "Nossas irm√£s" (correct)
- ‚ùå "Nossas pais" (wrong - pais is masculine plural)
- ‚úÖ "Nossos pais" (correct)

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- **Unit 14:** meu/minha (my - singular)
- **Unit 22:** n√≥s (we) - now can say "we" AND "our"
- **Unit 27:** meus/minhas (my - plural)
- **Unit 28:** seu/sua + dele/dela (your/his/her)
- **Unit 29:** nosso/nossa (our) - **COMPLETES possessive system for main persons!**

**Key Learning:**
- **Four forms for "our":** nosso/nossa/nossos/nossas
- Possessives agree with BOTH gender AND number of the thing possessed
- **No ambiguity** - nosso/nossa ALWAYS means "our" (clearer than seu/sua!)
- Essential for talking about shared family, home, and experiences
- **MILESTONE:** Complete possessive system for eu, voc√™/ele/ela, n√≥s

**Why This Unit:**
- Natural progression: completes the possessive system after my, your/his/her
- Ultra-granular: introduces ONLY "our" possessives (one concept)
- Essential for first-person plural communication - pairs perfectly with n√≥s from Unit 25
- Practical: enables talking about shared family, home, work, and experiences
- **MILESTONE:** Students now have complete possessive system for all main persons!

### Unit 34: Past Tense - Regular -AR Verbs (Preterite)
**New vocabulary:**
- **ontem** (yesterday)
- **na semana passada** (last week)
- **no m√™s passado** (last month)
- **no ano passado** (last year)
- **anteontem** (the day before yesterday)
- **h√° [time]** (ago) - h√° dois dias (two days ago)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Preterite tense for regular -AR verbs** (simple past - completed actions)
- Past tense endings for -AR verbs:
  - eu: -**ei** (morei, trabalhei, estudei)
  - voc√™/ele/ela: -**ou** (morou, trabalhou, estudou)
  - n√≥s: -**amos** (moramos, trabalhamos, estudamos) - **SAME as present!**
  - voc√™s/eles/elas: -**aram** (moraram, trabalharam, estudaram)
- Used for actions that happened at a specific time in the past and are complete
- Time expressions that signal past tense

**Practice format:**
- Present: "Moro em S√£o Paulo" ‚Üí Past: "Morei em S√£o Paulo" (I lived in S√£o Paulo)
- Present: "Trabalho no banco" ‚Üí Past: "Trabalhei no banco ontem" (I worked at the bank yesterday)
- Present: "Estudo portugu√™s" ‚Üí Past: "Estudei portugu√™s na semana passada" (I studied Portuguese last week)
- Questions: "Onde voc√™ morou?" (Where did you live?)

**Student can now:**
- Talk about completed past actions with regular -AR verbs
- Use all -AR verbs learned so far in past tense
- Distinguish present from past using time expressions
- Notice that n√≥s form is SAME in present and past (context determines meaning)
- Ask questions about past events

**Typical sentences:**
- Morei no Brasil (I lived in Brazil)
- Trabalhei ontem (I worked yesterday)
- Estudei portugu√™s na semana passada (I studied Portuguese last week)
- Ele morou em S√£o Paulo (He lived in S√£o Paulo)
- N√≥s trabalhamos ontem (We worked yesterday - same as present!)
- Eles falaram portugu√™s (They spoke Portuguese)
- Voc√™ gostou do filme? (Did you like the movie?)
- N√£o gostei (I didn't like it)

**Full Conjugation - Preterite -AR Verbs:**
| Pronoun | Present | Preterite | Example (morar) |
|---------|---------|-----------|-----------------|
| eu | moro | morei | Morei no Rio |
| voc√™/ele/ela | mora | morou | Ele morou aqui |
| n√≥s | moramos | moramos | Moramos l√° |
| voc√™s/eles/elas | moram | moraram | Eles moraram aqui |

**Pattern for All -AR Verbs in Preterite:**
- morar: morei, morou, moramos, moraram
- trabalhar: trabalhei, trabalhou, trabalhamos, trabalharam
- estudar: estudei, estudou, estudamos, estudaram
- falar: falei, falou, falamos, falaram
- gostar: gostei, gostou, gostamos, gostaram
- andar: andei, andou, andamos, andaram
- viajar: viajei, viajou, viajamos, viajaram

**Key Pattern Recognition:**
- Remove -ar, add: -ei, -ou, -amos, -aram
- **n√≥s form identical to present:** "Moramos" can mean "we live" OR "we lived" (context clarifies)
- All other forms clearly signal past tense

**With Time Expressions:**
- Morei em S√£o Paulo **no ano passado** (I lived in S√£o Paulo last year)
- Trabalhei **ontem** (I worked yesterday)
- Estudamos portugu√™s **na semana passada** (We studied Portuguese last week)
- Ele falou comigo **h√° dois dias** (He spoke with me two days ago)
- N√£o trabalhei **anteontem** (I didn't work the day before yesterday)

**Comparing Present and Past:**
- Present: Moro em S√£o Paulo agora (I live in S√£o Paulo now)
- Past: Morei em S√£o Paulo no ano passado (I lived in S√£o Paulo last year)
- Present: Trabalho no banco (I work at the bank)
- Past: Trabalhei no banco ontem (I worked at the bank yesterday)

**Sample Conversation:**
- A: Onde voc√™ morou antes? (Where did you live before?)
- B: Morei no Rio. (I lived in Rio.)
- A: Voc√™ gostou? (Did you like it?)
- B: Sim, gostei muito. (Yes, I liked it a lot.)
- A: Voc√™ trabalhou l√°? (Did you work there?)
- B: Sim, trabalhei em um banco. (Yes, I worked at a bank.)

**With Negation (from Unit 14):**
- N√£o morei no Brasil (I didn't live in Brazil)
- Ele n√£o trabalhou ontem (He didn't work yesterday)
- N√£o gostamos do filme (We didn't like the movie)
- Eles n√£o estudaram (They didn't study)

**Key Learning:**
- This is the **simple past tense** (preterite) - for completed actions
- Very regular pattern for -AR verbs (the most common verb type)
- Easy to form: just change the ending
- Students can now talk about PAST experiences with -AR verbs
- N√≥s form creates interesting ambiguity: "Moramos aqui" = "We live here" or "We lived here"

**Why This Unit:**
- Natural progression: present ‚Üí future ‚Üí past
- -AR verbs are the most common and were taught first
- Regular pattern makes it accessible
- Immediate practical value - telling stories about past events
- Ultra-granular: focusing only on regular -AR verbs (not -ER/-IR yet, not irregulars)
- Students can now describe past actions with 5+ -AR verbs they already know
- **MAJOR MILESTONE**: First true past tense introduced!

**Note:** Irregular past tense verbs (fui, foi, teve, etc.) will come in future units. This unit focuses exclusively on the regular -AR pattern.

### Unit 35: Past Tense - Regular -ER/-IR Verbs (Preterite)
**New vocabulary:**
- Time expressions (review from Unit 29): ontem, na semana passada, no m√™s passado
- Additional: de manh√£ (in the morning), √† tarde (in the afternoon), √† noite (at night)
- j√° (already), ainda n√£o (not yet)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Preterite tense for regular -ER and -IR verbs**
- **KEY INSIGHT: -ER and -IR verbs share the SAME past tense endings!**
- Past tense endings for -ER/-IR verbs:
  - eu: -**i** (comi, bebi, corri, abri, parti, assisti)
  - voc√™/ele/ela: -**eu/-iu** (comeu, bebeu, correu, abriu, partiu, assistiu)
  - n√≥s: -**emos/-imos** (comemos/abrimos - same as present!)
  - voc√™s/eles/elas: -**eram/-iram** (comeram/abriram)
- Used for completed actions in the past (same as -AR verbs in Unit 29)

**Practice format:**
- Present: "Como arroz" ‚Üí Past: "Comi arroz ontem" (I ate rice yesterday)
- Present: "Bebo caf√©" ‚Üí Past: "Bebi caf√© de manh√£" (I drank coffee in the morning)
- Present: "Assisto filmes" ‚Üí Past: "Assisti um filme ontem" (I watched a movie yesterday)
- Questions: "O que voc√™ comeu?" (What did you eat?)

**Student can now:**
- Talk about completed past actions with regular -ER and -IR verbs
- Use all -ER verbs from Unit 20 in past tense (comer, beber, correr)
- Use all -IR verbs from Unit 26 in past tense (abrir, partir, assistir)
- Recognize that -ER and -IR share past tense endings
- Notice that n√≥s form is SAME as present (like -AR verbs)
- Combine with -AR past tense from Unit 29

**Typical sentences:**
- Comi arroz e feij√£o ontem (I ate rice and beans yesterday)
- Bebi caf√© de manh√£ (I drank coffee in the morning)
- Corri no parque na semana passada (I ran in the park last week)
- Abri a porta (I opened the door)
- Ele partiu cedo (He left early)
- Assistimos um filme (We watched a movie)
- Voc√™s comeram? (Did you all eat?)
- N√£o bebi cerveja (I didn't drink beer)

**Full Conjugation - Preterite -ER/-IR Verbs:**
| Pronoun | -ER (comer) | -IR (abrir) | Pattern |
|---------|-------------|-------------|---------|
| eu | comi | abri | -i |
| voc√™/ele/ela | comeu | abriu | -eu/-iu |
| n√≥s | comemos | abrimos | -emos/-imos |
| voc√™s/eles/elas | comeram | abriram | -eram/-iram |

**Pattern for -ER Verbs in Preterite:**
- comer: comi, comeu, comemos, comeram
- beber: bebi, bebeu, bebemos, beberam
- correr: corri, correu, corremos, correram

**Pattern for -IR Verbs in Preterite:**
- abrir: abri, abriu, abrimos, abriram
- partir: parti, partiu, partimos, partiram
- assistir: assisti, assistiu, assistimos, assistiram

**Key Pattern Recognition:**
- **-ER and -IR verbs share the same past tense pattern!**
- Remove -er/-ir, add: -i, -eu/-iu, -emos/-imos, -eram/-iram
- **n√≥s form identical to present** (just like -AR verbs):
  - "Comemos" = "we eat" OR "we ate" (context clarifies)
  - "Abrimos" = "we open" OR "we opened" (context clarifies)
- Other forms clearly signal past tense

**Comparing All Three Verb Types in Past:**
| Verb Type | eu | voc√™/ele/ela | n√≥s | voc√™s/eles/elas |
|-----------|-----|--------------|-----|-----------------|
| -AR (morar) | morei | morou | moramos | moraram |
| -ER (comer) | comi | comeu | comemos | comeram |
| -IR (abrir) | abri | abriu | abrimos | abriram |

**Comparing Present and Past (-ER/-IR):**
- Present: Como arroz todo dia (I eat rice every day)
- Past: Comi arroz ontem (I ate rice yesterday)
- Present: Assisto filmes (I watch movies)
- Past: Assisti um filme na semana passada (I watched a movie last week)
- Present: Bebo caf√© de manh√£ (I drink coffee in the morning)
- Past: Bebi caf√© ontem de manh√£ (I drank coffee yesterday morning)

**Sample Conversation:**
- A: O que voc√™ comeu ontem? (What did you eat yesterday?)
- B: Comi peixe e salada. (I ate fish and salad.)
- A: Voc√™ bebeu vinho? (Did you drink wine?)
- B: N√£o, bebi √°gua. (No, I drank water.)
- A: Voc√™s assistiram o filme? (Did you all watch the movie?)
- B: Sim, assistimos ontem √† noite. (Yes, we watched it last night.)

**Combining with -AR Past (Unit 29):**
- Trabalhei ontem e depois comi no restaurante (I worked yesterday and then ate at the restaurant)
- Estudei portugu√™s de manh√£ e √† tarde corri no parque (I studied Portuguese in the morning and in the afternoon I ran in the park)
- Eles moraram no Brasil e comeram muito churrasco (They lived in Brazil and ate a lot of barbecue)

**With Negation:**
- N√£o comi carne (I didn't eat meat)
- Ele n√£o bebeu cerveja (He didn't drink beer)
- N√£o assistimos o filme (We didn't watch the movie)
- Eles n√£o abriram a loja (They didn't open the store)

**Key Learning:**
- **-ER and -IR verbs share identical past tense conjugations**
- This simplifies learning - only need to memorize one pattern for two verb types
- Regular pattern makes it accessible
- Students can now talk about eating, drinking, watching in the past
- Combined with Unit 29, students have past tense for ALL regular verb types

**Why This Unit:**
- Natural progression: -AR past (Unit 29) ‚Üí -ER/-IR past (Unit 31)
- Shows the elegance: -ER and -IR merge in past tense
- Ultra-granular: still only regular verbs (irregulars come later)
- Immediate practical value - talking about meals, activities
- Students can now use past tense with 11+ verbs they already know
- **MAJOR MILESTONE**: Complete regular verb system in past tense!

**Note:** Irregular past tense verbs (fui, foi, fiz, teve, etc.) will come in Unit 32. This unit focuses exclusively on regular -ER and -IR patterns.

### Unit 36: Past Tense - Essential Irregular Verbs (ser, ir, ter, estar)
**New vocabulary:**
- Time expressions (review): ontem, na semana passada, no ano passado
- Additional time expressions:
  - no passado (in the past)
  - quando (when)
  - antes (before)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Preterite tense for the most essential irregular verbs**
- **AMAZING FACT: ser (to be) and ir (to go) share identical past tense forms!**
- Four essential irregulars:
  - **ser/ir**: fui, foi, fomos, foram
  - **ter**: tive, teve, tivemos, tiveram
  - **estar**: estive, esteve, estivemos, estiveram
- Context determines meaning for ser vs ir (both use fui, foi, etc.)
- These verbs don't follow regular patterns - must be memorized

**Practice format:**
- Present: "Sou brasileiro" ‚Üí Past: "Fui brasileiro" (doesn't make sense - identity doesn't change!)
- Better: "Sou professor" ‚Üí Past: "Fui professor no ano passado" (I was a teacher last year)
- Present: "Vou ao trabalho" ‚Üí Past: "Fui ao trabalho ontem" (I went to work yesterday)
- Present: "Tenho um carro" ‚Üí Past: "Tive um carro" (I had a car)
- Present: "Estou em casa" ‚Üí Past: "Estive em casa ontem" (I was at home yesterday)

**Student can now:**
- Talk about past identity/professions (fui)
- Talk about where they went (fui)
- Distinguish ser/ir by context
- Talk about past possession (tive)
- Talk about past location/state (estive)
- Tell complete stories combining regular and irregular verbs

**Typical sentences:**
- Fui professor no Brasil (I was a teacher in Brazil) - ser
- Fui ao cinema ontem (I went to the movies yesterday) - ir
- Ela foi brasileira (She was Brazilian) - doesn't work! Identity doesn't change
- Ele foi ao banco (He went to the bank) - ir
- Fomos ao restaurante (We went to the restaurant) - ir
- Tive um cachorro (I had a dog)
- N√£o tive tempo (I didn't have time)
- Estive em S√£o Paulo (I was in S√£o Paulo)
- Estivemos cansados (We were tired)

**Full Conjugation - Essential Irregulars:**
| Pronoun | ser/ir | ter | estar |
|---------|---------|-----|-------|
| eu | fui | tive | estive |
| voc√™/ele/ela | foi | teve | esteve |
| n√≥s | fomos | tivemos | estivemos |
| voc√™s/eles/elas | foram | tiveram | estiveram |

**Ser vs Ir - Context is Key:**
- **Ser (was/were):**
  - Fui estudante (I was a student)
  - Ele foi professor (He was a teacher)
  - Fomos felizes (We were happy)
  - Context: identity, profession, characteristics

- **Ir (went):**
  - Fui ao trabalho (I went to work)
  - Ele foi ao Brasil (He went to Brazil)
  - Fomos de √¥nibus (We went by bus)
  - Context: movement, destinations, going somewhere

**Common Patterns:**
- **fui/foi + profession:** "Fui professor" (I was a teacher)
- **fui/foi + a/ao/√†:** "Fui ao banco" (I went to the bank) - clearly ir
- **fui/foi + de:** "Fui de carro" (I went by car) - clearly ir
- **tive + noun:** "Tive aulas" (I had classes)
- **estive + location:** "Estive em casa" (I was at home)
- **estive + state:** "Estive doente" (I was sick)

**Comparing Present and Past:**
| Verb | Present (eu) | Past (eu) | Example |
|------|--------------|-----------|---------|
| ser | sou | fui | Sou professor ‚Üí Fui professor |
| ir | vou | fui | Vou ao cinema ‚Üí Fui ao cinema |
| ter | tenho | tive | Tenho tempo ‚Üí Tive tempo |
| estar | estou | estive | Estou em casa ‚Üí Estive em casa |

**Sample Conversation:**
- A: Onde voc√™ esteve ontem? (Where were you yesterday?)
- B: Estive em casa o dia todo. (I was at home all day.)
- A: Voc√™ foi ao trabalho na semana passada? (Did you go to work last week?)
- B: N√£o, tive f√©rias. (No, I had vacation.)
- A: Voc√™ foi professor antes? (Were you a teacher before?)
- B: Sim, fui professor de ingl√™s. (Yes, I was an English teacher.)

**Combining with Regular Past (Units 26-27):**
- Fui ao restaurante e comi peixe (I went to the restaurant and ate fish)
- Estive em casa e assisti um filme (I was at home and watched a movie)
- Tive aulas de portugu√™s e estudei muito (I had Portuguese classes and studied a lot)
- Fomos ao parque e corremos (We went to the park and ran)

**With Negation:**
- N√£o fui ao trabalho (I didn't go to work)
- Ele n√£o foi brasileiro (He wasn't Brazilian - rare, identity doesn't change)
- N√£o tive tempo (I didn't have time)
- N√£o estive l√° (I wasn't there)
- Eles n√£o foram ao cinema (They didn't go to the movies)

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ‚ùå Using "fui" for current identity: "Fui brasileiro" (I was Brazilian - implies you're not anymore!)
- ‚úÖ Better: "Sou brasileiro" (I am Brazilian - present)
- ‚úÖ Or: "Fui professor" (I was a teacher - professions can change)

**Key Learning:**
- **ser and ir share identical past forms** - only context clarifies meaning
- These four verbs are the most commonly used irregular verbs in Portuguese
- They appear in almost every conversation about the past
- Must be memorized - no pattern to help
- Students already know these verbs in present tense (Units 1, 8, 12, 14)

**Why This Unit:**
- Natural progression: regular past ‚Üí irregular past
- Ultra-granular: focusing only on the 4 most essential irregulars
- Students already know these verbs in present tense
- Immediate practical value - these are THE most common verbs in past tense
- Enables much richer storytelling about the past
- **MAJOR MILESTONE**: Can now tell complete stories with both regular and irregular verbs!

**Note:** Other irregular verbs (fazer ‚Üí fiz, ver ‚Üí vi, dar ‚Üí dei, etc.) will come in future units. This unit focuses on the four most essential irregulars that students already know in present tense.

### Unit 37: Past Tense - Common Irregular Verbs (fazer, ver, dar)
**New vocabulary:**
- Vocabulary that pairs with these verbs:
  - perguntas (questions)
  - trabalho (work/task)
  - exerc√≠cios (exercises)
  - presente (gift/present)
  - dinheiro (money)
  - ajuda (help)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Three more essential irregular verbs in preterite**
- **fazer (to make/do)**: fiz, fez, fizemos, fizeram
- **ver (to see/watch)**: vi, viu, vimos, viram
- **dar (to give)**: dei, deu, demos, deram
- These verbs are extremely common in past tense conversations
- Each has its own irregular pattern - must be memorized

**Practice format:**
- Present: "Fa√ßo exerc√≠cios" ‚Üí Past: "Fiz exerc√≠cios ontem" (I did exercises yesterday)
- Present: "Vejo meus amigos" ‚Üí Past: "Vi meus amigos" (I saw my friends)
- Present: "Dou presentes" ‚Üí Past: "Dei um presente" (I gave a gift)
- Questions: "O que voc√™ fez ontem?" (What did you do yesterday?)

**Student can now:**
- Talk about what they did/made (fiz)
- Talk about what they saw/watched (vi)
- Talk about what they gave (dei)
- Answer "O que voc√™ fez?" (What did you do?) - one of the most common questions
- Combine with Units 26-28 for rich storytelling

**Typical sentences:**
- Fiz exerc√≠cios de manh√£ (I did exercises in the morning)
- Fiz o trabalho ontem (I did the work yesterday)
- Fiz uma pergunta (I asked a question)
- Vi meus amigos (I saw my friends)
- Vi um filme ontem (I saw/watched a movie yesterday)
- N√£o vi nada (I didn't see anything)
- Dei um presente para ela (I gave her a gift)
- Dei dinheiro (I gave money)
- Ele me deu ajuda (He gave me help)

**Full Conjugation - Common Irregulars:**
| Pronoun | fazer | ver | dar |
|---------|-------|-----|-----|
| eu | fiz | vi | dei |
| voc√™/ele/ela | fez | viu | deu |
| n√≥s | fizemos | vimos | demos |
| voc√™s/eles/elas | fizeram | viram | deram |

**Pattern Recognition (or lack thereof!):**
- **fazer**: fiz, fez, fizemos, fizeram
  - Note: z sound throughout
  - Stem changes completely from "faz-" to "fiz-/fez-"

- **ver**: vi, viu, vimos, viram
  - Very short forms (just 2-3 letters!)
  - Similar to regular -IR pattern but shorter

- **dar**: dei, deu, demos, deram
  - Looks somewhat like regular -ER verbs (dei/deu)
  - But it's from "dar" (ends in -ar)
  - Unique pattern

**Comparing Present and Past:**
| Verb | Present (eu) | Past (eu) | Example |
|------|--------------|-----------|---------|
| fazer | fa√ßo | fiz | Fa√ßo exerc√≠cios ‚Üí Fiz exerc√≠cios |
| ver | vejo | vi | Vejo filmes ‚Üí Vi um filme |
| dar | dou | dei | Dou presentes ‚Üí Dei um presente |

**Common Uses for "fazer":**
- Fiz o trabalho (I did the work)
- Fiz exerc√≠cios (I did exercises)
- Fiz uma pergunta (I asked a question / literally: made a question)
- Fiz comida (I made food)
- O que voc√™ fez? (What did you do?) - **THE most common past tense question!**

**Common Uses for "ver":**
- Vi meus amigos (I saw my friends)
- Vi um filme (I watched a movie)
- Vi a casa (I saw the house)
- N√£o vi nada (I didn't see anything)
- Note: "ver" can mean both "to see" and "to watch"

**Common Uses for "dar":**
- Dei um presente (I gave a gift)
- Dei aulas (I gave classes / I taught)
- Dei dinheiro (I gave money)
- Ele me deu ajuda (He gave me help)
- Demos um passeio (We took a walk / literally: gave a walk)

**Sample Conversation:**
- A: O que voc√™ fez ontem? (What did you do yesterday?)
- B: Fiz exerc√≠cios de manh√£ e depois vi meus amigos. (I did exercises in the morning and then saw my friends.)
- A: Voc√™ viu o filme novo? (Did you see the new movie?)
- B: Sim, vi na semana passada. (Yes, I saw it last week.)
- A: Voc√™ deu o presente para ela? (Did you give her the gift?)
- B: Sim, dei ontem. (Yes, I gave it yesterday.)

**Combining with Previous Past Tense Units:**
- Fui ao cinema e vi um filme (I went to the movies and saw a film)
- Estive em casa, fiz o trabalho e depois assisti TV (I was at home, did work and then watched TV)
- Tive aulas de manh√£, fiz exerc√≠cios e depois comi (I had classes in the morning, did exercises and then ate)
- Trabalhei muito, fiz todas as tarefas e n√£o vi meus amigos (I worked a lot, did all the tasks and didn't see my friends)

**With Negation:**
- N√£o fiz nada ontem (I didn't do anything yesterday)
- Ele n√£o viu o filme (He didn't see the movie)
- N√£o dei dinheiro (I didn't give money)
- Eles n√£o fizeram o trabalho (They didn't do the work)
- N√£o vimos ningu√©m (We didn't see anyone)

**Key Phrases with "O que voc√™ fez?":**
This is THE most important question in past tense conversation:
- A: O que voc√™ fez ontem? (What did you do yesterday?)
- B: Fiz exerc√≠cios. (I did exercises.)
- B: Trabalhei. (I worked.)
- B: Vi meus amigos. (I saw my friends.)
- B: N√£o fiz nada. (I didn't do anything.)

**Key Learning:**
- These three verbs are among the most commonly used in daily conversation
- "O que voc√™ fez?" is essential - students will hear this constantly
- "fazer" is versatile - covers "do," "make," and many expressions
- "ver" covers both "see" and "watch"
- "dar" is essential for talking about giving, teaching, taking walks
- Combined with Units 26-28, students now have 7 past tense irregular verbs + all regular verbs

**Why This Unit:**
- Natural progression: essential irregulars (Unit 32) ‚Üí common irregulars (Unit 33)
- Ultra-granular: only 3 new irregular verbs (manageable)
- Immediate practical value - "fazer" especially is used constantly
- "O que voc√™ fez?" is one of the most common questions students will encounter
- Enables much richer past tense conversation
- Students can now handle most basic past tense storytelling

**Note:** Additional irregular verbs (poder, querer, saber, trazer, dizer, etc.) can come in future units. This unit focuses on three that are immediately essential for basic conversation.

### Unit 38: Question Words (Interrogatives)
**New vocabulary:**
- **Question words (interrogatives):**
  - **o que / que** (what)
  - **quem** (who)
  - **onde** (where)
  - **quando** (when)
  - **como** (how)
  - **por que** (why)
  - **qual / quais** (which / which ones)
  - **quanto/a/os/as** (how much / how many)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Systematic introduction to interrogatives**
- Question formation with all tenses (present, future, past)
- Word order: interrogative + verb + subject (or just interrogative + verb with pro-drop)
- Using question words students have encountered informally since early units
- Questions can end with question mark but intonation is key

**Practice format:**
- Present: "O que voc√™ faz?" (What do you do?)
- Future: "Quando voc√™ vai viajar?" (When are you going to travel?)
- Past: "Onde voc√™ morou?" (Where did you live?)
- "Quem √© ele?" (Who is he?)
- "Como voc√™ est√°?" (How are you?)
- "Por que voc√™ estuda portugu√™s?" (Why do you study Portuguese?)

**Student can now:**
- Ask questions about any topic covered so far
- Use interrogatives with present, future, and past tenses
- Form information questions (not just yes/no questions)
- Understand that many question words they've seen informally are now systematic
- Conduct two-way conversations (not just answer, but also ask)

**Typical sentences:**
- O que voc√™ faz? (What do you do?)
- Quem √© ela? (Who is she?)
- Onde voc√™ mora? (Where do you live?)
- Quando voc√™ vai viajar? (When are you going to travel?)
- Como voc√™ est√°? (How are you?)
- Por que voc√™ gosta de portugu√™s? (Why do you like Portuguese?)
- Qual √© seu nome? (What is your name? / literally: Which is your name?)
- Quanto custa? (How much does it cost?)
- Quantos irm√£os voc√™ tem? (How many siblings do you have?)

**Full Question Word System:**
| Question Word | Meaning | Example |
|---------------|---------|---------|
| o que / que | what | O que voc√™ fez? (What did you do?) |
| quem | who | Quem √© ele? (Who is he?) |
| onde | where | Onde voc√™ mora? (Where do you live?) |
| quando | when | Quando voc√™ foi? (When did you go?) |
| como | how | Como voc√™ est√°? (How are you?) |
| por que | why | Por que voc√™ estuda? (Why do you study?) |
| qual/quais | which/which ones | Qual √© seu carro? (Which is your car?) |
| quanto/a/os/as | how much/many | Quantos filhos voc√™ tem? (How many children do you have?) |

**Detailed Usage:**

**O QUE / QUE (what):**
- O que voc√™ faz? (What do you do?)
- O que voc√™ fez ontem? (What did you do yesterday?)
- O que voc√™ vai fazer? (What are you going to do?)
- Que hora √©? (What time is it?)
- Note: "que" is shorter, "o que" is more common in questions

**QUEM (who):**
- Quem √© ele? (Who is he?)
- Quem mora aqui? (Who lives here?)
- Com quem voc√™ foi? (With whom did you go? / Who did you go with?)
- De quem √© isso? (Whose is this? / literally: Of whom is this?)

**ONDE (where):**
- Onde voc√™ mora? (Where do you live?)
- Onde voc√™ trabalha? (Where do you work?)
- Onde voc√™ foi? (Where did you go?)
- Onde est√° meu livro? (Where is my book?)

**QUANDO (when):**
- Quando voc√™ vai viajar? (When are you going to travel?)
- Quando voc√™ chegou? (When did you arrive?)
- Quando √© seu anivers√°rio? (When is your birthday?)

**COMO (how):**
- Como voc√™ est√°? (How are you?)
- Como voc√™ vai ao trabalho? (How do you go to work?)
- Como se diz isso em portugu√™s? (How do you say this in Portuguese?)
- Como √© seu nome? (What's your name? / literally: How is your name?)

**POR QUE (why):**
- Por que voc√™ estuda portugu√™s? (Why do you study Portuguese?)
- Por que voc√™ n√£o foi? (Why didn't you go?)
- Por que voc√™ gosta disso? (Why do you like this?)

**QUAL / QUAIS (which / which ones):**
- Qual √© seu nome? (What is your name?)
- Qual √© sua profiss√£o? (What is your profession?)
- Qual livro voc√™ gostou? (Which book did you like?)
- Quais s√£o seus amigos? (Which ones are your friends?)

**QUANTO/A/OS/AS (how much / how many):**
- **Agreement with noun:**
  - Quanto custa? (How much does it cost?)
  - Quanta √°gua? (How much water?)
  - Quantos irm√£os? (How many brothers?)
  - Quantas irm√£s? (How many sisters?)
- Quantos anos voc√™ tem? (How old are you? / literally: How many years do you have?)

**With All Three Tenses:**

**Present:**
- Onde voc√™ mora? (Where do you live?)
- O que voc√™ faz? (What do you do?)
- Quem √© ele? (Who is he?)

**Future:**
- Quando voc√™ vai viajar? (When are you going to travel?)
- O que voc√™ vai fazer? (What are you going to do?)
- Onde voc√™ vai morar? (Where are you going to live?)

**Past:**
- Onde voc√™ morou? (Where did you live?)
- O que voc√™ fez? (What did you do?)
- Quando voc√™ foi? (When did you go?)
- Quem voc√™ viu? (Who did you see?)

**Sample Conversation:**
- A: Onde voc√™ mora? (Where do you live?)
- B: Moro em S√£o Paulo. E voc√™? (I live in S√£o Paulo. And you?)
- A: Moro no Rio. Quando voc√™ foi a S√£o Paulo? (I live in Rio. When did you go to S√£o Paulo?)
- B: Fui h√° dois anos. Por que voc√™ pergunta? (I went two years ago. Why do you ask?)
- A: Porque vou viajar para l√°. Qual bairro voc√™ mora? (Because I'm going to travel there. Which neighborhood do you live in?)

**Common Fixed Expressions:**
- Como vai? (How are you? / literally: How goes?)
- Como √© que...? (How is it that...? - emphasis on the question)
- O que √© isso? (What is this?)
- Quem sabe? (Who knows?)
- Onde fica...? (Where is... located?)
- Quanto tempo? (How long? / literally: How much time?)

**üó£Ô∏è Emphatic Questions with "√â que" (EXTREMELY COMMON IN BP):**

The construction **"√© que"** makes questions more emphatic and conversational. This is one of the most characteristic features of Brazilian Portuguese speech:

**Pattern:** [Question word] + **√© que** + [rest of sentence]

**Examples:**
- Basic: Onde voc√™ mora?
- Emphatic: Onde **√© que** voc√™ mora? (Where do you live? - with emphasis)

- Basic: O que voc√™ quer?
- Emphatic: O que **√© que** voc√™ quer? (What do you want? - more natural)

- Basic: Quando voc√™ vai?
- Emphatic: Quando **√© que** voc√™ vai? (When are you going?)

- Basic: Como voc√™ sabe?
- Emphatic: Como **√© que** voc√™ sabe? (How do you know?)

**With all question words:**
- Onde **√© que** voc√™ trabalha? (Where do you work?)
- Quem **√© que** fez isso? (Who did this?)
- Por que **√© que** voc√™ n√£o foi? (Why didn't you go?)
- Qual **√© que** √© melhor? (Which one is better?)
- Quanto **√© que** custa? (How much does it cost?)

**Special case - "O que √© que":**
- O que **√© que** √© isso? (What is this?)
- O que **√© que** voc√™ fez? (What did you do?)
- Note: Looks strange but is grammatically correct! First "√©" is part of "√© que", second "√©" is the verb "to be"

**Important:**
- **"√â que" makes questions less abrupt** and more conversational
- Very common in spoken Brazilian Portuguese
- Optional - both forms are correct, but "√© que" sounds more natural in conversation
- In formal writing, simpler form is preferred (Onde voc√™ mora?)
- In speech, "√© que" form is much more common

**Question Word Order:**
- Simple: **Question word + verb + (subject)**
  - Onde mora voc√™? (Where do you live?)
  - But more natural: Onde voc√™ mora? (Where do you live?)
- With pro-drop (no subject): **Question word + verb**
  - Onde mora? (Where do [you] live?)
  - Common in conversation

**Key Learning:**
- Students have encountered many of these informally (onde in Unit 3, como in Unit 21, etc.)
- Now systematizing all question words in one unit
- Can form questions in present, future, and past tenses
- Essential for conducting conversations, not just answering questions
- "quanto/a/os/as" shows gender/number agreement (like possessives)

**Why This Unit:**
- Natural progression: students have been answering questions, now they can ask them
- Systematizes question words encountered informally throughout Units 1-29
- Enables two-way conversation
- Ultra-granular: focusing only on interrogatives
- Immediately practical - students can now drive conversations
- Works with ALL tenses and ALL verbs learned so far
- **MAJOR MILESTONE**: Students can now conduct complete conversations in three tenses!

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 3: "Onde voc√™ mora?" - onde was used informally
- Unit 18: "onde, como, o que" mentioned
- Unit 29: "O que voc√™ fez?" introduced informally
- Unit 30: Now making all interrogatives systematic and explicit

### Unit 39: Reflexive Verbs (me chamo, me levanto, me sinto)
**New vocabulary:**
- **Reflexive pronouns:**
  - **me** (myself)
  - **se** (yourself/himself/herself/themselves)
  - **nos** (ourselves)
- **Common reflexive verbs:**
  - chamar-se (to call oneself / to be named)
  - levantar-se (to get up)
  - sentar-se (to sit down)
  - sentir-se (to feel)
  - vestir-se (to get dressed)
  - deitar-se (to lie down / go to bed)
  - lembrar-se (to remember)
  - esquecer-se (to forget)
- **Daily routine vocabulary:**
  - de manh√£ (in the morning)
  - √† tarde (in the afternoon)
  - √† noite (at night)
  - cedo (early)
  - tarde (late)
  - bem (well)
  - mal (badly)
  - cansado/a (tired)
  - feliz (happy)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Reflexive verbs: action reflects back on the subject**
- **Reflexive pronouns in Brazilian Portuguese go BEFORE the conjugated verb**
- Pattern: subject + reflexive pronoun + conjugated verb
  - Eu **me** chamo Maria (I call myself Maria = My name is Maria)
  - Eu **me** levanto cedo (I get up early)
  - Eu **me** sinto bem (I feel well)
- Reflexive pronouns for each subject:
  - eu ‚Üí **me** (myself)
  - voc√™/ele/ela ‚Üí **se** (yourself/himself/herself)
  - n√≥s ‚Üí **nos** (ourselves)
  - voc√™s/eles/elas ‚Üí **se** (yourselves/themselves)
- Common use: **"Como voc√™ se chama?"** = "What's your name?" (literally: How do you call yourself?)
- Answer: **"Me chamo [name]"** or informal **"Meu nome √© [name]"** (Unit 13)

**Practice format:**
- "Me chamo Jo√£o" (My name is Jo√£o / I call myself Jo√£o)
- "Me levanto √†s 6h" (I get up at 6am)
- "Me sinto bem hoje" (I feel well today)
- "Como voc√™ se chama?" (What's your name?)
- "Me visto r√°pido" (I get dressed quickly)

**Student can now:**
- Introduce themselves formally: "Me chamo [name]"
- Talk about daily routine (getting up, sitting down, going to bed)
- Express how they feel (me sinto bem/mal/cansado/feliz)
- Use reflexive verbs in all three tenses (present, future, past)
- Understand difference between reflexive and non-reflexive verbs
- Ask someone's name formally: "Como voc√™ se chama?"

**Typical sentences:**
- Me chamo Maria (My name is Maria)
- Me levanto √†s 7h (I get up at 7am)
- Me sinto bem (I feel well)
- Me sinto cansado (I feel tired)
- N√£o me sinto bem (I don't feel well)
- Me visto r√°pido de manh√£ (I get dressed quickly in the morning)
- Me sento aqui (I sit here)
- Me deito tarde (I go to bed late)
- Voc√™ se lembra? (Do you remember?)
- N√£o me lembro (I don't remember)
- Como voc√™ se chama? (What's your name?)

**Full Conjugation - Reflexive Verbs (Present Tense):**
| Pronoun | Reflexive Pronoun | chamar-se | levantar-se | sentir-se |
|---------|-------------------|-----------|-------------|-----------|
| eu | me | me chamo | me levanto | me sinto |
| voc√™/ele/ela | se | se chama | se levanta | se sente |
| n√≥s | nos | nos chamamos | nos levantamos | nos sentimos |
| voc√™s/eles/elas | se | se chamam | se levantam | se sentem |

**Examples with All Pronouns:**
- Eu me chamo Jo√£o (My name is Jo√£o)
- Voc√™ se chama Maria? (Is your name Maria?)
- Ele se levanta cedo (He gets up early)
- Ela se sente feliz (She feels happy)
- N√≥s nos sentamos aqui (We sit here)
- Voc√™s se lembram? (Do you all remember?)
- Eles se vestem r√°pido (They get dressed quickly)

**Reflexive vs Non-Reflexive:**
Some verbs can be used both ways:

| Non-Reflexive | Reflexive |
|---------------|-----------|
| Chamo meu amigo (I call my friend) | Me chamo Jo√£o (I'm called Jo√£o) |
| Levanto a m√£o (I raise my hand) | Me levanto cedo (I get up early) |
| Sinto frio (I feel cold - external) | Me sinto bem (I feel well - internal state) |
| Visto meu filho (I dress my son) | Me visto (I get dressed) |
| Sento o beb√™ (I sit the baby down) | Me sento (I sit down) |

**With All Three Tenses:**

**Present:**
- Me levanto cedo (I get up early)
- Me sinto bem (I feel well)
- Como voc√™ se chama? (What's your name?)

**Future (vou + infinitive):**
- Vou me levantar cedo amanh√£ (I'm going to get up early tomorrow)
- Vou me sentir melhor depois (I'm going to feel better later)
- Ela vai se vestir agora (She's going to get dressed now)
- Note: Pronoun can go before "vou" OR after the infinitive in BP
  - Me vou levantar (less common in BP)
  - Vou me levantar (common in BP)
  - Vou levantar-me (European Portuguese style, rare in BP)

**Past:**
- Me levantei cedo ontem (I got up early yesterday)
- Me senti bem (I felt well)
- Ele se vestiu r√°pido (He got dressed quickly)
- Nos sentamos l√° (We sat there)

**Past Tense Conjugations:**
| Pronoun | chamar-se | levantar-se | sentir-se |
|---------|-----------|-------------|-----------|
| eu | me chamei | me levantei | me senti |
| voc√™/ele/ela | se chamou | se levantou | se sentiu |
| n√≥s | nos chamamos | nos levantamos | nos sentimos |
| voc√™s/eles/elas | se chamaram | se levantaram | se sentiram |

**Sample Conversation:**
- A: Como voc√™ se chama? (What's your name?)
- B: Me chamo Ana. E voc√™? (My name is Ana. And you?)
- A: Me chamo Carlos. A que horas voc√™ se levanta? (My name is Carlos. What time do you get up?)
- B: Me levanto √†s 6h. E voc√™? (I get up at 6am. And you?)
- A: Eu me levanto √†s 7h. Como voc√™ se sente hoje? (I get up at 7am. How do you feel today?)
- B: Me sinto bem, obrigada. (I feel well, thank you.)

**Common Daily Routine with Reflexive Verbs:**
- Me levanto √†s 6h (I get up at 6am)
- Me visto r√°pido (I get dressed quickly)
- Trabalho de manh√£ (I work in the morning - not reflexive)
- Me sinto cansado √† tarde (I feel tired in the afternoon)
- Me deito √†s 10h (I go to bed at 10pm)

**With Negation:**
- N√£o me levanto cedo (I don't get up early)
- N√£o me sinto bem (I don't feel well)
- Ele n√£o se lembra (He doesn't remember)
- N√£o me esqueci (I didn't forget)
- Ela n√£o se vestiu ainda (She hasn't gotten dressed yet)

**"Me chamo" vs "Meu nome √©":**
Both mean "My name is":
- **Me chamo Jo√£o** - formal, using reflexive verb (literally: I call myself Jo√£o)
- **Meu nome √© Jo√£o** (Unit 13) - informal, more common in conversation (My name is Jo√£o)
- Both are correct and commonly used
- "Como voc√™ se chama?" is the formal question form
- "Qual √© seu nome?" is also common (What is your name?)

**CRITICAL: Common Mistakes - Verbs That Are NOT Reflexive:**

‚ö†Ô∏è **FORBIDDEN - DO NOT use these verbs reflexively:**
- ‚ùå **"me acordo"** (WRONG) - acordar (to wake up) is NOT reflexive in Portuguese
- ‚ùå **"me durmo"** (WRONG) - dormir (to sleep) is NOT reflexive
- ‚ùå **"me desperto"** (WRONG) - despertar (to wake) is NOT reflexive
- ‚ùå **"me abro"** (WRONG) - abrir (to open) is NOT reflexive
- ‚ùå **"me fecho"** (WRONG) - fechar (to close) is NOT reflexive

‚úÖ **CORRECT usage:**
- **Acordo √†s 7h** (I wake up at 7am) - NO pronoun
- **Durmo cedo** (I sleep early) - NO pronoun
- **Abro a porta** (I open the door) - NO pronoun

**Why this confusion?** These verbs seem personal ("I wake myself up"), but Portuguese treats them as non-reflexive. Only use the approved reflexive verbs list above!

**Three Types of Usage:**

**1. Reflexive (action on oneself):**
- Eu **me** levanto (I get myself up)
- Eu **me** visto (I dress myself)
- Ela **se** senta (She sits herself down)

**2. Reciprocal (action on each other - plural subjects only):**
- N√≥s **nos** vemos todo dia (We see each other every day)
- Eles **se** amam (They love each other)
- Voc√™s **se** conhecem? (Do you all know each other?)
- **Note:** Reciprocal meaning requires PLURAL subjects (n√≥s, voc√™s, eles/elas)
- me/te are ALWAYS reflexive only (singular subjects can't be reciprocal)

**3. Non-Reflexive (same verb without pronoun - action on something/someone else):**
- **Reflexive:** Eu **me** lavo (I wash myself)
- **Non-Reflexive:** Eu lavo o carro (I wash the car - NO pronoun!)

- **Reflexive:** Eu **me** levanto √†s 7h (I get up at 7am)
- **Non-Reflexive:** Eu levanto pesos (I lift weights - NO pronoun!)

- **Reflexive:** Ela **se** veste (She dresses herself)
- **Non-Reflexive:** Ela veste o beb√™ (She dresses the baby - NO pronoun!)

- **Reflexive:** Eu **me** preparo (I prepare myself)
- **Non-Reflexive:** Eu preparo o jantar (I prepare dinner - NO pronoun!)

**Key Learning:**
- Reflexive verbs are essential for daily routine vocabulary
- Reflexive pronouns go BEFORE the verb in Brazilian Portuguese (not after like European Portuguese)
- "Me chamo" is the formal way to introduce yourself
- Many verbs can be used both reflexively and non-reflexively with different meanings
- Works naturally with all three tenses learned so far
- The pronoun must match the subject (eu ‚Üí me, voc√™ ‚Üí se, n√≥s ‚Üí nos)

**Why This Unit:**
- Natural progression after interrogatives - students can now ask "Como voc√™ se chama?"
- Essential for daily routine conversations
- Introduces new pronoun category (reflexive) while building on existing pronoun knowledge
- Ultra-granular: focusing only on reflexive verbs, not other pronoun types
- Immediate practical value - "me chamo" and "me sinto" are used constantly
- Builds foundation for object pronouns in future units
- **MILESTONE**: Students can now introduce themselves formally!

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 13: "Meu nome √© Jo√£o" (informal name introduction)
- Unit 31: "Me chamo Jo√£o" (formal name introduction with reflexive verb)
- Unit 18: "Como" used informally
- Unit 31: "Como voc√™ se chama?" (systematic formal question)
- Unit 1-23: Regular verbs learned
- Unit 31: Same verbs can be used reflexively (levantar ‚Üí levantar-se)

### Unit 40: Direct Object Pronouns (me, te, o/a, nos, os/as)
**New vocabulary:**
- **Direct object pronouns:**
  - **me** (me - as object)
  - **te** (you - as object, informal)
  - **o / a** (him/it / her/it - masculine/feminine)
  - **nos** (us - as object)
  - **os / as** (them - masculine/feminine plural)
- **New verbs commonly used with direct objects:**
  - ver (to see - already learned in Unit 33)
  - conhecer (to know/meet - people/places)
  - amar (to love)
  - ajudar (to help)
  - esperar (to wait for / to hope)
  - ouvir (to hear/listen)
  - entender (to understand)
  - encontrar (to find / to meet)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Direct object pronouns: replace the direct object (the thing/person receiving the action)**
- **In Brazilian Portuguese, pronouns typically go BEFORE the verb (like reflexive pronouns)**
- Pattern: subject + object pronoun + verb
  - Ele **me** v√™ (He sees me)
  - Eu **te** amo (I love you)
  - Eu **o** conhe√ßo (I know him)
  - Ela **nos** ajuda (She helps us)
- Direct object answers "what?" or "whom?"
  - Vejo Jo√£o ‚Üí Vejo quem? Jo√£o ‚Üí **O** vejo (I see him)
  - Amo Maria ‚Üí Amo quem? Maria ‚Üí **A** amo (I love her)
  - Conhecemos as pessoas ‚Üí **As** conhecemos (We know them)
- Gender and number agreement with o/a/os/as
  - **o** = him/it (masculine singular)
  - **a** = her/it (feminine singular)
  - **os** = them (masculine plural or mixed)
  - **as** = them (feminine plural)

**Practice format:**
- "Ele me v√™" (He sees me)
- "Te amo" (I love you)
- "Conhe√ßo-o bem" ‚Üí "O conhe√ßo bem" (I know him well)
- "Ela nos ajuda" (She helps us)
- "Vejo-os todos os dias" ‚Üí "Os vejo todos os dias" (I see them every day)

**Student can now:**
- Replace direct objects with pronouns to sound more natural
- Avoid repetition: "Vejo Jo√£o. Jo√£o √© meu amigo." ‚Üí "Vejo Jo√£o. O conhe√ßo bem."
- Use object pronouns with all three tenses
- Distinguish between reflexive pronouns (Unit 35) and direct object pronouns (Unit 36)
- Understand that me/nos can be reflexive OR object pronouns (context determines)
- Form more natural, fluent Portuguese sentences

**Typical sentences:**
- Ele me v√™ todos os dias (He sees me every day)
- Te amo (I love you)
- O conhe√ßo bem (I know him well)
- A vejo na escola (I see her at school)
- Ela nos ajuda (She helps us)
- Voc√™s os conhecem? (Do you all know them?)
- N√£o as vejo mais (I don't see them anymore - feminine)
- Me entendem? (Do you understand me?)
- Te espero aqui (I wait for you here / I'll wait for you here)

**Direct Object Pronouns:**
| Pronoun | Meaning | Example |
|---------|---------|---------|
| me | me | Ele me v√™ (He sees me) |
| te | you (informal) | Te amo (I love you) |
| o | him/it (masc) | O conhe√ßo (I know him) |
| a | her/it (fem) | A vejo (I see her) |
| nos | us | Ela nos ajuda (She helps us) |
| os | them (masc/mixed) | Os conhe√ßo (I know them) |
| as | them (fem) | As vejo (I see them) |

**Examples with Different Verbs:**

**Ver (to see):**
- Ele me v√™ (He sees me)
- Te vejo amanh√£ (I see you tomorrow / I'll see you tomorrow)
- O vejo todos os dias (I see him every day)
- Nos veem na escola (They see us at school)

**Conhecer (to know):**
- Voc√™ me conhece? (Do you know me?)
- Te conhe√ßo de onde? (Where do I know you from?)
- O conhe√ßo bem (I know him well)
- N√£o a conhe√ßo (I don't know her)
- Nos conhecemos h√° anos (We've known each other for years - reflexive usage)

**Amar (to love):**
- Te amo (I love you)
- O amo muito (I love him very much)
- Ela nos ama (She loves us)

**Ajudar (to help):**
- Voc√™ me ajuda? (Can you help me? / Do you help me?)
- Te ajudo sempre (I always help you)
- Ela os ajuda (She helps them)

**Entender (to understand):**
- Voc√™ me entende? (Do you understand me?)
- Te entendo perfeitamente (I understand you perfectly)
- N√£o o entendo (I don't understand him)

**Comparing Reflexive (Unit 35) vs Direct Object (Unit 36):**

| Reflexive (action on self) | Direct Object (action on other) |
|----------------------------|----------------------------------|
| Me levanto (I get myself up) | Ele me levanta (He picks me up) |
| Me visto (I dress myself) | Ela me veste (She dresses me) |
| Me chamo Jo√£o (I call myself Jo√£o) | Ele me chama (He calls me) |
| Nos sentamos (We sit ourselves) | Eles nos sentam (They sit us down - rare) |

**Note:** me/nos can be EITHER reflexive OR direct object - context determines:
- **Me levanto** cedo (reflexive - I get myself up)
- Ele **me** v√™ (direct object - he sees me)
- **Nos** sentimos bem (reflexive - we feel well)
- Ela **nos** ajuda (direct object - she helps us)

**With All Three Tenses:**

**Present:**
- Me v√™ todos os dias (He sees me every day)
- Te amo (I love you)
- O conhe√ßo (I know him)
- Nos ajudam (They help us)

**Future (vou + infinitive):**
- Vou te ver amanh√£ (I'm going to see you tomorrow)
- Ele vai me ajudar (He's going to help me)
- Vamos conhec√™-los (We're going to meet them)
- Note: In BP, pronoun typically goes before main verb, but can attach to infinitive

**Past:**
- Me viu ontem (He saw me yesterday)
- Te amei (I loved you)
- O conheci na escola (I met him at school)
- Nos ajudaram muito (They helped us a lot)
- N√£o as vi (I didn't see them)

**Position in Brazilian Portuguese:**
- **Standard (most common):** Pronoun BEFORE verb
  - Me v√™ (He sees me)
  - Te amo (I love you)
  - O conhe√ßo (I know him)

- **After infinitive (less common but correct):**
  - Quero v√™-lo (I want to see him)
  - Vou conhec√™-la (I'm going to meet her)
  - Note: Hyphen connects pronoun to verb

- **European Portuguese often puts pronoun after:** "Vejo-o" (I see him)
- **Brazilian Portuguese prefers pronoun before:** "O vejo" (I see him)

**Gender and Number Agreement with o/a/os/as:**
Must match the noun being replaced:

- Jo√£o (masculine singular) ‚Üí **o** ‚Üí O conhe√ßo
- Maria (feminine singular) ‚Üí **a** ‚Üí A conhe√ßo
- Os meninos (masculine plural) ‚Üí **os** ‚Üí Os conhe√ßo
- As meninas (feminine plural) ‚Üí **as** ‚Üí As conhe√ßo
- Mixed group (Jo√£o e Maria) ‚Üí **os** ‚Üí Os conhe√ßo (masculine plural for mixed)

**Sample Conversation:**
- A: Voc√™ conhece Jo√£o? (Do you know Jo√£o?)
- B: Sim, o conhe√ßo bem. Ele √© meu amigo. (Yes, I know him well. He's my friend.)
- A: Quando voc√™ o viu? (When did you see him?)
- B: O vi ontem. Ele me ajudou com o trabalho. (I saw him yesterday. He helped me with work.)
- A: E Maria? Voc√™ a conhece tamb√©m? (And Maria? Do you know her too?)
- B: Sim, a conhe√ßo. Vou v√™-la amanh√£. (Yes, I know her. I'm going to see her tomorrow.)

**With Negation:**
- N√£o me v√™ (He doesn't see me)
- N√£o te amo (I don't love you)
- N√£o o conhe√ßo (I don't know him)
- N√£o nos ajudam (They don't help us)
- Nunca os vejo (I never see them)

**CRITICAL: Standard vs Colloquial Brazilian Portuguese**

This unit teaches **standard/formal BP** with clitic pronouns (me, te, o/a, nos, os/as) placed BEFORE the verb. However, you MUST know that **colloquial spoken BP** is very different:

**Standard/Formal BP (taught in this unit):**
- ‚úÖ **Eu o vi** (I saw him) - clitic pronoun before verb
- ‚úÖ **Eu a conhe√ßo** (I know her) - clitic pronoun before verb
- ‚úÖ **Eu os encontrei** (I found them) - clitic pronoun before verb

**Colloquial/Spoken BP (VERY common in daily speech):**
- ‚úÖ **Eu vi ele** (I saw him) - stressed pronoun after verb, VERY COMMON
- ‚úÖ **Eu conhe√ßo ela** (I know her) - stressed pronoun after verb, VERY COMMON
- ‚úÖ **Eu encontrei eles** (I found them) - stressed pronoun after verb, VERY COMMON
- ‚úÖ **Vejo voc√™** (I see you) - stressed pronoun after verb, VERY COMMON

**Which should you use?**
- **Writing/formal contexts:** Use clitic pronouns (o/a/os/as) before the verb
- **Speaking/informal contexts:** Brazilians commonly use stressed pronouns (ele/ela/voc√™) after the verb
- **Both are correct!** But colloquial forms dominate in everyday conversation

**About "TE" (you - informal):**
‚ö†Ô∏è **IMPORTANT:** "Te" is RARE in Brazilian Portuguese!
- ‚ùå **"Te amo"** - used in songs/poetry, but uncommon in daily speech
- ‚úÖ **"Amo voc√™"** - much more common in Brazilian Portuguese
- ‚úÖ **"Te amo"** - common in European Portuguese (with "tu")

**Why is "te" rare in BP?**
- BP uses "voc√™" (not "tu") as the standard "you"
- "Voc√™" requires "o/a" pronouns, not "te"
- "Te" is associated with "tu" (uncommon in most of Brazil)

**Practical Recommendation for Students:**
1. **Learn the standard forms** (this unit) - needed for writing and formal speech
2. **Understand colloquial forms** (ele/ela after verb) - you'll hear these constantly
3. **Use "voc√™" instead of "te"** in your own speech - more natural in BP

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
1. **Wrong agreement:** "O vejo" for Maria ‚Üí Should be "**A** vejo" (feminine)
2. **Wrong position:** "Vejo-o" (European) ‚Üí BP prefers "O vejo"
3. **Confusing reflexive and object:**
   - "Me levanto" (reflexive - I get up)
   - "Ele me levanta" (object - he lifts me up)
4. **Overusing "te" in BP:**
   - Less common: "Te vejo amanh√£" (sounds formal/literary)
   - More common: "Vejo voc√™ amanh√£" (natural BP)

**Practical Usage:**
Direct object pronouns make speech more natural and avoid repetition:

**Without pronouns (repetitive):**
- Conhe√ßo Jo√£o. Vejo Jo√£o todos os dias. Gosto de Jo√£o.

**With pronouns (natural):**
- Conhe√ßo Jo√£o. **O** vejo todos os dias. Gosto dele.

**Key Learning:**
- Direct object pronouns replace nouns to avoid repetition
- me/nos can be reflexive (Unit 35) OR direct object (Unit 36) - context determines
- o/a/os/as must agree in gender and number with the noun they replace
- Brazilian Portuguese puts pronouns BEFORE the verb (unlike European Portuguese)
- Works with all three tenses
- Makes speech sound more natural and fluent
- Essential for intermediate-level fluency

**Why This Unit:**
- Natural progression after reflexive pronouns (Unit 35)
- Both use similar forms (me, nos) but different functions
- Essential for fluent, natural-sounding Portuguese
- Reduces repetition in speech
- Ultra-granular: focusing only on direct object pronouns (indirect comes later)
- Immediate practical value - used constantly in conversation
- **MILESTONE**: Students can now form more sophisticated, natural sentences!

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 31: Reflexive pronouns (me chamo, me levanto)
- Unit 32: Direct object pronouns (me v√™, me ajuda)
- Unit 29: Ver (to see) - now can use "o vejo" instead of "vejo ele"
- Unit 16: Gosto de (Unit 19 uses indirect object - "de + person")
- Unit 32: Direct object (no preposition) - "o vejo" not "vejo de ele"

**Important Distinction:**
- **Direct object (Unit 36):** NO preposition - "Vejo Jo√£o" ‚Üí "**O** vejo"
- **Indirect object (future unit):** WITH preposition - "Falo com Jo√£o" (uses "lhe" or "para ele")

### Unit 41: Past Tense - More Common Irregular Verbs (poder, querer, saber)
**New vocabulary:**
- **Three more essential irregular verbs in preterite:**
  - poder (to be able to / can)
  - querer (to want)
  - saber (to know - facts/information)
- **Additional vocabulary:**
  - nada (nothing)
  - tudo (everything)
  - a verdade (the truth)
  - a resposta (the answer)
  - a not√≠cia (the news)
  - comprar (to buy - regular verb for examples)
  - vir (to come - for context, but conjugation comes later)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Preterite tense for poder, querer, and saber**
- These three verbs often change meaning slightly in the past:
  - **poder** (present: can/am able to) ‚Üí (past: could/was able to/managed to)
  - **querer** (present: want) ‚Üí (past: wanted/tried to)
  - **saber** (present: know) ‚Üí (past: found out/learned)
- Conjugation patterns:
  - **poder**: pude, p√¥de, pudemos, puderam
  - **querer**: quis, quis, quisemos, quiseram
  - **saber**: soube, soube, soubemos, souberam
- All three are highly irregular with unique stems

**Practice format:**
- "Pude ir ao trabalho" (I was able to go to work / I managed to go to work)
- "Quis comprar, mas n√£o pude" (I wanted to buy, but couldn't)
- "Soube a verdade ontem" (I found out the truth yesterday)
- "Ele n√£o quis falar" (He didn't want to speak / He refused to speak)

**Student can now:**
- Talk about what they could or couldn't do (pude/n√£o pude)
- Express past desires and intentions (quis/n√£o quis)
- Talk about finding out information (soube)
- Understand the nuanced meaning shifts in the past tense
- Combine with other past tense verbs for richer storytelling

**Typical sentences:**
- Pude ir (I was able to go / I managed to go)
- N√£o pude trabalhar ontem (I couldn't work yesterday)
- Quis viajar, mas n√£o pude (I wanted to travel, but couldn't)
- Ele n√£o quis comer (He didn't want to eat / He refused to eat)
- Soube a not√≠cia hoje (I found out the news today)
- Quando voc√™ soube? (When did you find out?)
- N√£o soube a resposta (I didn't know the answer)
- Pudemos ver tudo (We were able to see everything)

**Full Conjugation - More Common Irregulars:**
| Pronoun | poder | querer | saber |
|---------|-------|--------|-------|
| eu | pude | quis | soube |
| voc√™/ele/ela | p√¥de | quis | soube |
| n√≥s | pudemos | quisemos | soubemos |
| voc√™s/eles/elas | puderam | quiseram | souberam |

**Pattern Recognition:**

**poder** (pude, p√¥de, pudemos, puderam):
- Stem changes from "pod-" to "pud-/p√¥d-"
- "p√¥de" has circumflex accent to distinguish from "pode" (present tense)
- Similar to "p√¥r" family of verbs (which we'll learn later)

**querer** (quis, quis, quisemos, quiseram):
- Stem changes from "quer-" to "quis-"
- eu/voc√™ forms identical: "quis"
- z sound throughout
- Very irregular pattern

**saber** (soube, soube, soubemos, souberam):
- Stem changes from "sab-" to "soub-"
- eu/voc√™ forms identical: "soube"
- Similar pattern to "ter" (tive, teve) but different vowel

**Comparing Present and Past:**
| Verb | Present (eu) | Past (eu) | Example |
|------|--------------|-----------|---------|
| poder | posso | pude | Posso ir ‚Üí Pude ir |
| querer | quero | quis | Quero viajar ‚Üí Quis viajar |
| saber | sei | soube | Sei a verdade ‚Üí Soube a verdade |

**Meaning Shifts in Past Tense:**

**PODER (to be able to / can):**
- **Present:** ability or permission
  - Posso nadar (I can swim - I know how)
  - Posso ir? (Can I go? - permission)
- **Past:** managed to or tried and succeeded
  - Pude nadar (I was able to swim / I managed to swim - specific event)
  - Pude ir (I was able to go / I managed to go)
- **Negative past:** tried but failed
  - N√£o pude ir (I couldn't go / I wasn't able to go)

**QUERER (to want):**
- **Present:** current desire
  - Quero caf√© (I want coffee)
- **Past:** wanted at that specific time, often implies attempt
  - Quis comprar caf√© (I wanted to buy coffee - and tried)
- **Negative past:** refused or didn't want
  - N√£o quis falar (He didn't want to speak / He refused to speak)
  - Strong implication of choice/decision

**SABER (to know):**
- **Present:** knowledge you have now
  - Sei portugu√™s (I know Portuguese)
  - Sei a resposta (I know the answer)
- **Past:** found out, learned, discovered
  - Soube a verdade (I found out the truth / I learned the truth)
  - Soube ontem (I found out yesterday)
- This is a KEY difference - "soube" = "found out" not just "knew"

**Common Uses for "poder" (past):**
- Pude ir ao trabalho (I was able to go to work)
- N√£o pude dormir (I couldn't sleep)
- Pude ver o filme (I was able to see the movie / I managed to see the movie)
- Por que voc√™ n√£o p√¥de vir? (Why couldn't you come? / Why weren't you able to come?)
- Pudemos comprar a casa (We were able to buy the house)

**Common Uses for "querer" (past):**
- Quis falar com voc√™ (I wanted to talk to you)
- N√£o quis comer (I didn't want to eat / I refused to eat)
- Ele quis ajudar (He wanted to help)
- Quisemos viajar (We wanted to travel)
- Por que voc√™ n√£o quis ir? (Why didn't you want to go?)
- Note: "n√£o quis" often implies deliberate refusal

**Common Uses for "saber" (past):**
- Soube a not√≠cia ontem (I found out the news yesterday)
- Quando voc√™ soube? (When did you find out?)
- Soube que ele foi ao Brasil (I found out that he went to Brazil)
- N√£o soube a resposta (I didn't know the answer - at that specific moment)
- Ela soube a verdade (She found out the truth)
- Como voc√™ soube? (How did you find out?)

**Sample Conversation:**
- A: Por que voc√™ n√£o foi √† festa? (Why didn't you go to the party?)
- B: N√£o pude ir. Tive que trabalhar. (I couldn't go. I had to work.)
- A: Mas voc√™ quis ir? (But did you want to go?)
- B: Sim, quis muito, mas n√£o pude. (Yes, I really wanted to, but I couldn't.)
- A: Voc√™ soube que Maria foi? (Did you find out that Maria went?)
- B: Sim, soube hoje de manh√£. (Yes, I found out this morning.)

**Combining with Previous Irregular Verbs:**

**Telling a story with multiple irregular verbs:**
- Quis ir ao cinema, mas n√£o pude. (I wanted to go to the movies, but couldn't.)
- Tive que trabalhar. (I had to work.) [Unit 32]
- Fui ao trabalho cedo. (I went to work early.) [Unit 32]
- Fiz muito trabalho. (I did a lot of work.) [Unit 33]
- Depois, vi meus amigos. (Afterwards, I saw my friends.) [Unit 33]
- Soube que eles tamb√©m quiseram ir ao cinema. (I found out they also wanted to go to the movies.)
- N√£o pudemos ir, mas estivemos juntos. (We couldn't go, but we were together.) [Unit 32]

**Common Combinations:**

**Poder + Infinitive:**
- Pude viajar (I was able to travel)
- N√£o pude ver (I couldn't see)
- Pudemos comprar (We were able to buy)

**Querer + Infinitive:**
- Quis estudar (I wanted to study)
- N√£o quis falar (I didn't want to speak / I refused to speak)
- Quisemos ajudar (We wanted to help)

**Saber + Noun:**
- Soube a verdade (I found out the truth)
- Soube a not√≠cia (I found out the news)
- N√£o soube nada (I didn't know anything / I didn't find out anything)

**Saber + Que-clause:**
- Soube que ele foi (I found out that he went)
- Soube que ela est√° bem (I found out that she's well)

**With Negation:**
- N√£o pude ir (I couldn't go)
- N√£o quis falar (I didn't want to speak / I refused to speak)
- N√£o soube nada (I didn't find out anything)
- Ele n√£o p√¥de vir (He couldn't come)
- Ela n√£o quis comer (She didn't want to eat)
- N√£o soubemos a verdade (We didn't find out the truth)

**Expressing "I tried but couldn't":**
- Quis comprar, mas n√£o pude (I wanted to buy, but couldn't)
- Quis ir, mas n√£o pude (I wanted to go, but couldn't)
- Quisemos ajudar, mas n√£o pudemos (We wanted to help, but couldn't)
- This combination is VERY common in conversation

**Asking Why Someone Couldn't:**
- Por que voc√™ n√£o p√¥de vir? (Why couldn't you come?)
- Por que ele n√£o p√¥de trabalhar? (Why couldn't he work?)
- Por que voc√™s n√£o puderam ir? (Why couldn't you all go?)

**Asking When Someone Found Out:**
- Quando voc√™ soube? (When did you find out?)
- Como voc√™ soube? (How did you find out?)
- Quem te disse? N√£o soube nada! (Who told you? I didn't find out anything!)

**Subtle Distinctions:**

**"N√£o pude" vs "N√£o quis":**
- **N√£o pude** = couldn't (external circumstances prevented me)
  - N√£o pude ir porque estava doente (I couldn't go because I was sick)
- **N√£o quis** = didn't want to / refused (internal decision)
  - N√£o quis ir porque estava cansado (I didn't want to go because I was tired)

**"Sabia" (imperfect - not taught yet) vs "Soube" (preterite):**
- **Soube** = found out (specific moment of discovery)
  - Soube ontem (I found out yesterday)
- **Sabia** = knew (ongoing state - will learn in imperfect tense)
  - Students will learn this distinction in the imperfect tense unit

**Present vs Past for "saber":**
- **Sei** a resposta (I know the answer - right now)
- **Soube** a resposta (I found out the answer / I learned the answer - at a specific past moment)
- Both are correct but have different implications

**Full Example Narrative:**
Ontem quis ir ao parque, mas n√£o pude porque tive que trabalhar. Fui ao trabalho de manh√£ e fiz muito trabalho. √Ä tarde, vi meu amigo Jo√£o e soube que ele tamb√©m quis ir ao parque. Ele disse: "Por que voc√™ n√£o p√¥de vir?" Respondi: "N√£o pude porque tive que trabalhar." Depois, pudemos ir ao caf√©. Estivemos l√° duas horas e foi bom.

(Yesterday I wanted to go to the park, but couldn't because I had to work. I went to work in the morning and did a lot of work. In the afternoon, I saw my friend Jo√£o and found out that he also wanted to go to the park. He said: "Why couldn't you come?" I answered: "I couldn't because I had to work." Afterwards, we were able to go to the caf√©. We were there two hours and it was good.)

**Key Learning:**
- These three verbs are among the most commonly used in past tense conversation
- "Poder" in past = managed to / was able to (specific event)
- "Querer" in past = wanted to (often implies attempt)
- "Saber" in past = found out (not just "knew")
- "Quis...mas n√£o pude" is an extremely common combination
- Negative forms have strong implications (couldn't vs refused)
- Students now have 10 irregular verbs in past tense (Units 28, 29, 33)

**Why This Unit:**
- Natural progression: continuing irregular past tense series
- These three verbs are essential for expressing ability, desire, and knowledge in the past
- Ultra-granular: only 3 new irregular verbs (manageable)
- Immediate practical value - used constantly in storytelling and explanation
- The meaning shifts in past tense are important for nuanced communication
- Students can now tell rich stories combining all irregular verbs learned
- **MILESTONE**: Students can express complex ideas like "I wanted to but couldn't"!

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 28: ser, ir, ter, estar (essential irregulars)
- Unit 29: fazer, ver, dar (common irregulars)
- Unit 33: poder, querer, saber (more common irregulars)
- Together: 10 essential irregular verbs in past tense
- All can be combined for storytelling and explaining past events
- Unit 16: "Gosto de + infinitive" ‚Üí Unit 33: "Quis + infinitive" (similar pattern)
- Unit 24: "Vou + infinitive" ‚Üí Unit 33: "Pude + infinitive" (ability vs intention)

**Note:** Additional irregular past tense verbs (trazer, dizer, p√¥r, vir, etc.) can come in future units. This unit focuses on three that are immediately essential for expressing ability, desire, and knowledge in the past.
