### Unit 42: Para vs Por (Two meanings of "for")
**New vocabulary:**
- **Prepositions:**
  - **para** (for/to - purpose, destination, recipient, deadline)
  - **por** (for/by/through - reason, duration, agent, means)
- **Vocabulary for common uses:**
  - presente (gift/present)
  - raz√£o (reason)
  - causa (cause)
  - atrav√©s de (through - alternative to por)
  - durante (during - alternative to por)
  - motivo (reason/motive)
- **Time expressions with por:**
  - por uma hora (for an hour)
  - por dois dias (for two days)
  - por muito tempo (for a long time)
  - por enquanto (for now)
- **Common expressions:**
  - por favor (please - literally: for favor)
  - por exemplo (for example)
  - por que (why - literally: for what)
  - por isso (therefore/that's why - literally: for this)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **PARA - purpose, destination, recipient, deadline:**
  1. **Purpose/goal** (in order to): Para estudar (in order to study)
  2. **Destination** (to/toward): Vou para casa (I go home/toward home)
  3. **Recipient** (for someone): √â para voc√™ (It's for you)
  4. **Deadline** (by a time): Para amanh√£ (by tomorrow)
  5. **Opinion/perspective**: Para mim (for me/in my opinion)

- **POR - reason, duration, agent, means, location:**
  1. **Reason/cause** (because of): Por amor (for love/because of love)
  2. **Duration** (for a length of time): Por duas horas (for two hours)
  3. **Agent** (by someone - passive voice): Escrito por Jo√£o (written by Jo√£o)
  4. **Means/method** (by/through): Por email (by email)
  5. **Movement through**: Por aqui (through here)
  6. **Exchange**: Paguei 50 reais por isso (I paid 50 reais for this)

- **Key distinction:**
  - **PARA** = destination, goal, purpose, future-oriented
  - **POR** = reason, cause, duration, past-oriented

**Practice format:**
- "Estudo para aprender" (I study in order to learn) - purpose
- "Isso √© para voc√™" (This is for you) - recipient
- "Trabalho por dinheiro" (I work for money) - reason/exchange
- "Morei l√° por dois anos" (I lived there for two years) - duration

**Student can now:**
- Distinguish between the two main translations of "for" in Portuguese
- Express purpose with para + infinitive
- Express duration with por + time expression
- Talk about recipients with para
- Explain reasons with por
- Use fixed expressions like "por favor," "por exemplo," "por isso"
- Understand when to use each preposition correctly

**Typical sentences:**
- Estudo para aprender portugu√™s (I study to learn Portuguese) - purpose
- Isso √© para voc√™ (This is for you) - recipient
- Vou para o Brasil (I'm going to Brazil) - destination
- Este projeto √© para amanh√£ (This project is for tomorrow) - deadline (with SER)
- Preciso terminar at√© amanh√£ (I need to finish by tomorrow) - deadline (with AT√â, not PARA)
- Trabalho por dinheiro (I work for money) - reason
- Fiz isso por amor (I did this for love) - reason
- Morei l√° por tr√™s anos (I lived there for three years) - duration
- Mandei por email (I sent by email) - means
- Obrigado por tudo (Thank you for everything) - reason
- Por favor (Please) - fixed expression

**üó£Ô∏è Spoken Brazilian Portuguese:**
In casual speech and even informal writing, **"para"** is almost always contracted to **"pra"** (and **"para o/a"** becomes **"pro/pra"**):
- Formal/Writing: "para voc√™" / "para o Brasil" / "para a escola"
- Casual Speech: "pra voc√™" / "pro Brasil" / "pra escola"
- Very common: "Vou pro trabalho" (I'm going to work), "√â pra mim?" (Is it for me?)

**Important:**
- **"Pra/pro"** are so universal in speech they're accepted in informal writing (text messages, social media)
- In formal writing, always use "para o/a" (not "pra/pro")
- **"Por"** does NOT contract in the same way - always say/write "por"
- Regional note: Some Brazilians write "pr√°" with accent, but "pra" (no accent) is more common

**PARA - Detailed Usage:**

**1. Purpose/Goal (in order to):**
- Estudo **para** aprender (I study in order to learn)
- Trabalho **para** viver (I work to live)
- Vou ao mercado **para** comprar comida (I go to the market to buy food)
- Pattern: **para + infinitive verb**
- Answers the question: "Para qu√™?" (For what purpose?)

**2. Destination (to/toward):**
- Vou **para** casa (I go home/I'm going home)
- Vou **para** o Brasil (I'm going to Brazil)
- Ela foi **para** S√£o Paulo (She went to S√£o Paulo)
- **IMPORTANT:** "para" implies permanence or intention to stay
- Contrasts with "a" (temporary/quick visit): "Vou ao banco" vs "Vou para o banco"

**3. Recipient (for someone):**
- Isso √© **para** voc√™ (This is for you)
- Comprei um presente **para** minha m√£e (I bought a gift for my mother)
- Este livro √© **para** estudantes (This book is for students)
- Fiz comida **para** voc√™s (I made food for you all)

**4. Deadline (by a certain time):**
- **IMPORTANT - Use PARA with SER (to be), NOT with PRECISAR/TER QUE:**
  - ‚úÖ **Este projeto √© para segunda-feira** (This project is for Monday - with SER)
  - ‚úÖ **A reuni√£o √© para amanh√£** (The meeting is for tomorrow - with SER)
  - ‚úÖ **O relat√≥rio √© para ter√ßa** (The report is for Tuesday - with SER)
  - ‚ùå **AVOID:** "Preciso terminar para sexta" (sounds unnatural in BP)
  - ‚úÖ **INSTEAD USE:** "Preciso terminar **at√©** sexta" (Use AT√â with PRECISAR/TER QUE)
- **Para** quando √© o projeto? (For when is the project? / When is the project due?)

**5. Opinion/Perspective (for me/in my opinion):**
- **Para** mim, isso √© importante (For me, this is important)
- **Para** ele, foi f√°cil (For him, it was easy)
- √â dif√≠cil **para** mim (It's difficult for me)

**POR - Detailed Usage:**

**1. Reason/Cause (because of):**
- Fiz isso **por** amor (I did this for love/because of love)
- **Por** voc√™, fa√ßo tudo (For you, I do everything - because of you)
- N√£o fui **por** causa da chuva (I didn't go because of the rain)
- Answers the question: "Por qu√™?" (Why? / For what reason?)

**2. Duration (for a length of time):**
- Morei l√° **por** tr√™s anos (I lived there for three years)
- Trabalhei **por** duas horas (I worked for two hours)
- Fiquei **por** muito tempo (I stayed for a long time)
- Vou viajar **por** um m√™s (I'm going to travel for a month)
- **KEY:** duration, not deadline

**3. Agent (by someone - passive voice):**
- Escrito **por** Jo√£o (Written by Jo√£o)
- Feito **por** mim (Made by me)
- O livro foi escrito **por** ele (The book was written by him)

**4. Means/Method (by/through):**
- Mandei **por** email (I sent by email)
- Paguei **por** cart√£o (I paid by card)
- Fiz **por** escrito (I did it in writing)
- **IMPORTANT - Brazilian Portuguese Note:**
  - ‚ùå **Avoid** "por avi√£o/trem/√¥nibus" (uncommon in BP)
  - ‚úÖ **Use** "de avi√£o/trem/√¥nibus" instead
  - ‚ùå **Avoid** "por telefone" (uncommon in BP)
  - ‚úÖ **Use** "de telefone" or "no telefone" instead
  - ‚úÖ **Good to use:** por email, por cart√£o, por escrito

**5. Movement Through:**
- Passei **por** S√£o Paulo (I passed through S√£o Paulo)
- Andei **por** aqui (I walked through here)
- Entramos **por** ali (We entered through there)

**6. Exchange (for a price):**
- Paguei 50 reais **por** isso (I paid 50 reais for this)
- Comprei **por** um bom pre√ßo (I bought for a good price)
- Quanto voc√™ pagou **por** isso? (How much did you pay for this?)

**Side-by-Side Comparison:**

**"For" as PURPOSE vs REASON:**
- Estudo **para** aprender (I study in order to learn - purpose/goal)
- Estudo **por** voc√™ (I study because of you - reason/motivation)

**"For" with TIME:**
- Preciso fazer **para** amanh√£ (I need to do by tomorrow - deadline)
- Trabalhei **por** duas horas (I worked for two hours - duration)

**"For" with PERSON:**
- Isso √© **para** voc√™ (This is for you - recipient/destination)
- Fiz isso **por** voc√™ (I did this for you - because of you/reason)

**"For" with PLACE:**
- Vou **para** o Brasil (I'm going to Brazil - destination/staying)
- Passei **por** o Brasil (I passed through Brazil - transit)

**Common Fixed Expressions with POR:**
- **por favor** (please)
- **por exemplo** (for example)
- **por que** (why - literally: for what)
- **por isso** (therefore/that's why)
- **por acaso** (by chance)
- **por enquanto** (for now)
- **por fim** (finally)
- **por sorte** (luckily)
- **por certo** (certainly)

**Common Fixed Expressions with PARA:**
- **para sempre** (forever)
- **para mim** (for me/in my opinion)
- **para onde?** (to where?)
- **para qu√™?** (for what purpose?)
- **para variar** (for a change)

**Sample Conversations:**

**Conversation 1 - Purpose vs Duration:**
- A: Por que voc√™ estuda portugu√™s? (Why do you study Portuguese?)
- B: Estudo **para** viajar ao Brasil. (I study to travel to Brazil.) - purpose
- A: Por quanto tempo voc√™ estuda? (For how long do you study?)
- B: Estudo **por** uma hora todos os dias. (I study for one hour every day.) - duration

**Conversation 2 - Destination vs Through:**
- A: Para onde voc√™ vai? (Where are you going to?)
- B: Vou **para** S√£o Paulo. (I'm going to S√£o Paulo.) - destination
- A: Voc√™ passa por Rio? (Do you pass through Rio?)
- B: Sim, passo **por** Rio. (Yes, I pass through Rio.) - transit

**Conversation 3 - Recipient vs Reason:**
- A: Para quem √© este presente? (For whom is this gift?)
- B: √â **para** minha m√£e. (It's for my mother.) - recipient
- A: Por que voc√™ comprou? (Why did you buy it?)
- B: Comprei **por** amor. (I bought it out of love.) - reason

**With Different Tenses:**

**Present:**
- Trabalho **para** uma empresa (I work for a company - recipient/destination)
- Passo **por** aqui todos os dias (I pass through here every day)

**Future:**
- Vou viajar **para** Portugal (I'm going to travel to Portugal)
- Vou estudar **por** duas horas (I'm going to study for two hours)

**Past:**
- Fui **para** casa (I went home)
- Morei l√° **por** cinco anos (I lived there for five years)

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**

**1. Confusing duration (por) with deadline (para):**
- ‚ùå Trabalhei para duas horas (Wrong - "para" = by/deadline)
- ‚úÖ Trabalhei **por** duas horas (Correct - duration)
- ‚úÖ Preciso terminar **para** amanh√£ (Correct - deadline)

**2. Confusing purpose (para) with reason (por):**
- ‚ùå Estudo por aprender (Wrong - "por" = because of)
- ‚úÖ Estudo **para** aprender (Correct - purpose)
- ‚úÖ Fiz isso **por** amor (Correct - reason/motivation)

**3. Mixing up recipient (para) and cause (por):**
- ‚úÖ Isso √© **para** voc√™ (This is for you - recipient)
- ‚úÖ Fiz isso **por** voc√™ (I did this for you - because of you/for your sake)
- Both are correct but mean different things!

**4. Using wrong preposition with transportation (BRAZILIAN PORTUGUESE):**
- ‚úÖ Vou **de** avi√£o (I go by plane - CORRECT and common in BP)
- ‚ùå Vou **por** avi√£o (AVOID - uncommon in BP)
- ‚úÖ Vou **de** trem (I go by train - CORRECT)
- ‚úÖ Vou **de** √¥nibus (I go by bus - CORRECT)
- **BP Rule:** Use "de" for transportation methods, NOT "por"

**Memory Tips:**

**PARA = Forward-looking:**
- **P**urpose
- **A**im
- **R**ecipient
- **A**head (deadline)
- Think: "pointing toward something"

**POR = Backward-looking/explanation:**
- **P**ast duration
- **O**rigin (reason)
- **R**oute (through)
- Think: "explaining why or how long"

**Simple Rule of Thumb:**
- **PARA** = where something is going (destination, purpose, recipient)
- **POR** = why something happened or how long (reason, duration, means)

**Confusing/Forbidden Examples - AVOID THESE:**

**1. NEVER use "correio" (post office/mail):**
- ‚ùå **AVOID:** Both "por correio" and "pelo correio" are grammatically valid but confusing
- ‚úÖ **INSTEAD USE:** "por email" or "por escrito" (clearer alternatives)
- **Why avoid:** The article changes the meaning subtly, creating confusion for learners

**2. Transportation & Communication (BP-specific):**
- ‚ùå **AVOID:** "por telefone, por avi√£o, por trem, por carta" (uncommon in BP)
- ‚úÖ **USE INSTEAD:** "de/no telefone, de avi√£o, de trem, por email"

**3. Deadline Construction:**
- ‚ùå **AVOID:** "Preciso terminar para sexta" (sounds unnatural)
- ‚úÖ **USE:** "O projeto √© para sexta" (with SER) OR "Preciso terminar at√© sexta" (with AT√â)

**Special Cases & Idioms:**

**Voting Construction:**
- ‚úÖ **Votar para + position/office:** "Votar para presidente" (vote for president - the office)
- ‚úÖ "Votar para vereador" (vote for councilor - the office)
- ‚úÖ "Votar para deputado" (vote for representative - the office)
- ‚ùå **NOT with specific candidates:** Use "votar no candidato" (with EM) for specific people

**Mandatory Contractions:**
- **por + o/a/os/as = pelo/pela/pelos/pelas** (MANDATORY, not optional!)
- You CANNOT say "por o" - Portuguese grammar REQUIRES the contraction "pelo"
- Example: "Passei pelo parque" (NOT "por o parque")
- These contractions are grammatically required, not stylistic choices

**Question Words:**
- **Para onde?** (To where?) - destination
- **Para qu√™?** (For what purpose?) - purpose
- **Para quem?** (For whom?) - recipient
- **Por que?** (Why?) - reason
- **Por quanto tempo?** (For how long?) - duration
- **Por onde?** (Through where?) - route

**Full Example Paragraph:**
Ontem fui **para** S√£o Paulo **para** ver meu amigo. Viajei **de** √¥nibus. A viagem durou tr√™s horas - viajei **por** tr√™s horas. Comprei um presente **para** ele. Paguei 100 reais **por** isso. Fiz isso **por** amor, porque ele √© meu melhor amigo. Passei **por** v√°rias cidades no caminho. Fiquei em S√£o Paulo **por** dois dias. Depois, voltei **para** casa.

(Yesterday I went to S√£o Paulo to see my friend. I traveled by bus. The trip lasted three hours - I traveled for three hours. I bought a gift for him. I paid 100 reais for it. I did this out of love, because he's my best friend. I passed through various cities on the way. I stayed in S√£o Paulo for two days. Afterwards, I returned home.)

**Key Learning:**
- Portuguese has TWO main words for "for": para and por
- **PARA** = purpose, destination, recipient, deadline (forward-looking)
- **POR** = reason, duration, means, movement through (backward-looking/explanatory)
- "Por favor" and "por isso" are fixed expressions (memorize them)
- "Para" + infinitive = "in order to"
- "Por" + time expression = duration (works with ALL tenses)
- **CRITICAL BP RULES:**
  - Use "de avi√£o/trem/√¥nibus" (NOT "por avi√£o/trem/√¥nibus")
  - Deadlines: "O projeto √© **para** sexta" (with SER) OR "Preciso terminar **at√©** sexta" (with AT√â, NOT PARA)
  - Contractions "pelo/pela" are MANDATORY, not optional
- Context often makes the meaning clear, but using the wrong one can confuse meaning

**Why This Unit:**
- Natural break from verb conjugations - provides variety
- These two prepositions are used constantly in Portuguese
- Students have encountered them informally throughout the curriculum
- Now systematizing the distinction between para and por
- Essential for intermediate fluency
- Ultra-granular: focusing only on these two prepositions
- Immediately practical - used in almost every conversation
- **MILESTONE**: Students can now express purpose, reason, duration, and destination correctly!

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 8: "Vou de √¥nibus" (method) vs Unit 34: "Vou para casa" (destination)
- Unit 16: "Gosto de viajar" vs Unit 34: "Viajo para aprender" (purpose)
- Unit 24: "Vou estudar" vs Unit 34: "Vou estudar por duas horas" (duration)
- Unit 30: "Por que" (why) vs "Para qu√™" (for what purpose)
- Throughout: "para" and "por" used informally, now systematized

**Note:** There are additional uses of "por" (multiplication: 2 por 3 = 6; distribution: 50 por cento) and "para" that can be introduced later. This unit focuses on the most common everyday uses.

### Unit 43: Past Tense - Additional Irregular Verbs (trazer, dizer, vir, p√¥r)
**New vocabulary:**
- **Four more essential irregular verbs in preterite:**
  - trazer (to bring)
  - dizer (to say/tell)
  - vir (to come)
  - p√¥r (to put/place)
- **Additional vocabulary:**
  - presente (gift/present)
  - mensagem (message)
  - not√≠cia (news)
  - verdade (truth)
  - mentira (lie)
  - aqui (here)
  - l√° (there)
  - mesa (table)
  - lugar (place)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Preterite tense for trazer, dizer, vir, and p√¥r**
- All four verbs are highly irregular with unique stems
- Conjugation patterns:
  - **trazer**: trouxe, trouxe, trouxemos, trouxeram
  - **dizer**: disse, disse, dissemos, disseram
  - **vir**: vim, veio, viemos, vieram
  - **p√¥r**: pus, p√¥s, pusemos, puseram

**Practice format:**
- "Trouxe um presente" (I brought a gift)
- "Ele disse a verdade" (He told the truth)
- "Vim aqui ontem" (I came here yesterday)
- "Pus as chaves na mesa" (I put the keys on the table)

**Student can now:**
- Talk about bringing things in the past (trouxe)
- Report what people said (disse)
- Talk about coming/arrival in the past (vim/veio)
- Talk about placing/putting things (pus/p√¥s)
- Combine with all other past tense verbs for richer storytelling
- Use 14 irregular past tense verbs total (Units 28, 29, 33, 35)

**Typical sentences:**
- Trouxe um presente para voc√™ (I brought a gift for you)
- Ela trouxe a comida (She brought the food)
- Ele disse que vai viajar (He said that he's going to travel)
- Dissemos a verdade (We told the truth)
- Vim de √¥nibus (I came by bus)
- Ele veio aqui ontem (He came here yesterday)
- Pus o livro na mesa (I put the book on the table)
- Ela p√¥s as chaves l√° (She put the keys there)

**Full Conjugation - Additional Irregular Verbs:**
| Pronoun | trazer | dizer | vir | p√¥r |
|---------|--------|-------|-----|-----|
| eu | trouxe | disse | vim | pus |
| voc√™/ele/ela | trouxe | disse | veio | p√¥s |
| n√≥s | trouxemos | dissemos | viemos | pusemos |
| voc√™s/eles/elas | trouxeram | disseram | vieram | puseram |

**Pattern Recognition:**

**trazer** (trouxe, trouxe, trouxemos, trouxeram):
- Stem changes from "traz-" to "troux-"
- eu/voc√™ forms identical: "trouxe"
- -x- appears in all forms
- Similar to "dizer" in having identical eu/voc√™ forms

**dizer** (disse, disse, dissemos, disseram):
- Stem changes from "diz-" to "diss-"
- eu/voc√™ forms identical: "disse"
- Double -ss- throughout
- Similar pattern to "trazer" (identical eu/voc√™ forms)

**vir** (vim, veio, viemos, vieram):
- Completely irregular pattern
- Each form is unique
- "vim" (eu) is very short
- "veio" (voc√™/ele/ela) changes completely
- Similar to "ir" in being highly irregular

**p√¥r** (pus, p√¥s, pusemos, puseram):
- Stem changes from "p√µ-" to "pus-/p√¥s-"
- "p√¥s" has circumflex accent (voc√™/ele/ela form)
- Very short forms throughout
- Similar to "poder" (pude, p√¥de) in having accent distinction

**Comparing Present and Past:**
| Verb | Present (eu) | Past (eu) | Example |
|------|--------------|-----------|---------|
| trazer | trago | trouxe | Trago sempre ‚Üí Trouxe ontem |
| dizer | digo | disse | Digo a verdade ‚Üí Disse a verdade |
| vir | venho | vim | Venho aqui ‚Üí Vim aqui |
| p√¥r | ponho | pus | Ponho na mesa ‚Üí Pus na mesa |

**Common Uses:**

**TRAZER (to bring):**
- Trouxe um presente (I brought a gift)
- Ela trouxe a comida (She brought the food)
- Quem trouxe isso? (Who brought this?)
- Trouxemos vinho (We brought wine)
- Eles trouxeram os documentos (They brought the documents)
- Note: "Levar" = to take (away), "Trazer" = to bring (toward speaker)

**DIZER (to say/tell):**
- Disse a verdade (I told the truth)
- Ele disse que sim (He said yes)
- O que voc√™ disse? (What did you say?)
- Dissemos tudo (We said everything)
- Eles disseram que v√£o vir (They said they're going to come)
- Very common with "que" clauses: "Disse que..." (I said that...)

**VIR (to come):**
- Vim de carro (I came by car)
- Ele veio aqui ontem (He came here yesterday)
- Quando voc√™ veio? (When did you come?)
- Viemos juntos (We came together)
- Eles vieram de S√£o Paulo (They came from S√£o Paulo)
- Opposite of "ir" (to go): "Fui l√°" (I went there) vs "Vim aqui" (I came here)

**P√îR (to put/place):**
- Pus as chaves na mesa (I put the keys on the table)
- Ela p√¥s o livro aqui (She put the book here)
- Onde voc√™ p√¥s meu telefone? (Where did you put my phone?)
- Pusemos tudo no lugar (We put everything in place)
- Eles puseram a comida na geladeira (They put the food in the fridge)
- Common with location expressions: na mesa, aqui, l√°, no lugar

**Sample Conversations:**

**Conversation 1:**
- A: Quem trouxe o vinho? (Who brought the wine?)
- B: Eu trouxe. (I brought it.)
- A: Obrigado! Voc√™ tamb√©m trouxe comida? (Thanks! Did you also bring food?)
- B: N√£o, mas a Maria disse que vai trazer. (No, but Maria said she's going to bring some.)

**Conversation 2:**
- A: Quando voc√™ veio ao Brasil? (When did you come to Brazil?)
- B: Vim em 2020. (I came in 2020.)
- A: E sua fam√≠lia? Eles vieram com voc√™? (And your family? Did they come with you?)
- B: N√£o, eles vieram depois, em 2021. (No, they came later, in 2021.)

**Conversation 3:**
- A: Onde voc√™ p√¥s minhas chaves? (Where did you put my keys?)
- B: Pus na mesa da cozinha. (I put them on the kitchen table.)
- A: Eu j√° olhei l√° e n√£o vi. (I already looked there and didn't see them.)
- B: Ah, desculpa! Depois pus no seu quarto. (Oh, sorry! Later I put them in your room.)

**Combining with Other Irregular Verbs:**

**Telling a complete story:**
- Ontem vim aqui de manh√£. (Yesterday I came here in the morning.) [Unit 39]
- Trouxe um presente para minha amiga. (I brought a gift for my friend.) [Unit 39]
- Ela disse que gostou muito. (She said she really liked it.) [Unit 39]
- Pusemos o presente na mesa. (We put the gift on the table.) [Unit 39]
- Depois, fomos ao caf√©. (Afterwards, we went to the caf√©.) [Unit 32]
- Fizemos novos planos. (We made new plans.) [Unit 33]
- Foi um dia muito bom! (It was a very good day!) [Unit 32]

**With Negation:**
- N√£o trouxe dinheiro (I didn't bring money)
- Ele n√£o disse nada (He didn't say anything)
- N√£o vim ontem (I didn't come yesterday)
- Ela n√£o p√¥s a√ß√∫car no caf√© (She didn't put sugar in the coffee)
- N√£o trouxemos nada (We didn't bring anything)

**Common Expressions:**

**With "trazer":**
- Trouxe de casa (I brought from home)
- Quem trouxe? (Who brought it?)
- N√£o trouxe nada (I didn't bring anything)

**With "dizer":**
- Disse que sim (I said yes)
- Disse que n√£o (I said no)
- O que voc√™ disse? (What did you say?)
- N√£o disse nada (I didn't say anything)
- Disse a verdade (I told the truth)

**With "vir":**
- Vim aqui (I came here)
- Veio de onde? (Where did you come from?)
- Viemos juntos (We came together)
- Vim sozinho (I came alone)

**With "p√¥r":**
- Pus na mesa (I put it on the table)
- P√¥s onde? (Where did you put it?)
- Pusemos no lugar (We put it in place)
- P√¥s de volta (Put it back)

**Comparing Similar Verbs:**

**IR (to go) vs VIR (to come):**
- **Fui l√°** (I went there) - movement away from speaker
- **Vim aqui** (I came here) - movement toward speaker
- **Foi ao Brasil** (He went to Brazil)
- **Veio ao Brasil** (He came to Brazil)

**LEVAR (to take) vs TRAZER (to bring):**
- **Levei o livro** (I took the book - away from speaker)
- **Trouxe o livro** (I brought the book - toward speaker)
- Both are regular -AR verbs in present, but trazer is irregular in past

**Accent Marks - Important!**

**p√¥r vs por:**
- **p√¥r** (verb: to put) - with circumflex
- **por** (preposition: for/by) - no accent
- **p√¥s** (he/she put - past tense) - with circumflex
- **pus** (I put - past tense) - no accent

**Key Distinctions:**
- Infinitive: **p√¥r** (to put) - has circumflex
- Past voc√™/ele/ela: **p√¥s** (put) - has circumflex
- Past eu: **pus** (I put) - no accent
- Preposition: **por** (for/by) - no accent

**Full Example Narrative:**
Ontem trouxe um presente para minha m√£e. Vim de manh√£ √† casa dela. Disse "Feliz anivers√°rio!" e pus o presente na mesa. Ela disse que adorou. Viemos ao restaurante juntos e foi muito bom. Ela disse que foi o melhor anivers√°rio. Depois, voltamos para casa e pusemos as fotos no √°lbum.

(Yesterday I brought a gift for my mother. I came in the morning to her house. I said "Happy birthday!" and put the gift on the table. She said she loved it. We came to the restaurant together and it was very good. She said it was the best birthday. Afterwards, we returned home and put the photos in the album.)

**Key Learning:**
- These four verbs are very common in everyday conversation
- All four are highly irregular - must be memorized
- "Trouxe" and "disse" have identical eu/voc√™ forms
- "Vir" is opposite of "ir" (come vs go)
- "P√¥r" uses circumflex accent to distinguish from preposition "por"
- "Dizer" is essential for reported speech: "Ele disse que..." (He said that...)
- "Trazer" vs "levar" distinction (bring toward vs take away)
- Students now have 14 irregular past tense verbs for rich storytelling

**Why This Unit:**
- Natural progression: continuing irregular past tense series (Units 28, 29, 33, 35)
- These four verbs are essential for daily conversation
- Ultra-granular: only 4 new irregular verbs (manageable)
- Immediate practical value - constantly used in conversation
- "Dizer" enables reported speech (essential for storytelling)
- "Vir" completes the ir/vir pair (go/come)
- "Trazer" enables talking about bringing things
- "P√¥r" enables talking about placing/organizing things
- **MILESTONE**: Students can now tell very complete, natural stories in past tense!

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 28: ser, ir, ter, estar (4 essential irregulars)
- Unit 29: fazer, ver, dar (3 common irregulars)
- Unit 33: poder, querer, saber (3 more common irregulars)
- Unit 35: trazer, dizer, vir, p√¥r (4 additional essential irregulars)
- **Total: 14 irregular past tense verbs learned!**
- Combined with regular past tense (Units 26-27), students have comprehensive past tense ability

**Note:** There are additional irregular past tense verbs (haver, crer, ler, etc.) but these 14 cover the vast majority of everyday conversation needs. Future units can introduce additional irregulars as needed.

### Unit 44: Indirect Object Pronouns (lhe, lhes) + Review of me/te/nos
**New vocabulary:**
- **Indirect object pronouns:**
  - **lhe** (to/for him, to/for her, to/for you - formal)
  - **lhes** (to/for them, to/for you plural)
  - Review: **me** (to/for me), **te** (to/for you - informal), **nos** (to/for us)
- **Verbs commonly used with indirect objects:**
  - dar (to give - Unit 33)
  - dizer (to say/tell - Unit 39)
  - falar (to speak - Unit 1)
  - perguntar (to ask)
  - mostrar (to show)
  - contar (to tell/count)
  - explicar (to explain)
  - enviar (to send)
  - emprestar (to lend)
  - pedir (to ask for/request)
- **Additional vocabulary:**
  - ajuda (help)
  - favor (favor)
  - dinheiro (money)
  - livro (book)
  - telefone (phone/phone number)
  - endere√ßo (address)
  - resposta (answer)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Indirect object pronouns: replace "to/for someone" (recipient of action)**
- **Key distinction from direct objects (Unit 36):**
  - **Direct object:** WHO/WHAT receives the action directly (no preposition)
  - **Indirect object:** TO/FOR WHOM the action is done (with preposition a/para)
- **In Brazilian Portuguese, pronouns go BEFORE the verb**
- Pattern: subject + indirect pronoun + verb + (direct object)
  - Eu **lhe** dei o livro (I gave the book to him/her)
  - Ele **me** disse a verdade (He told the truth to me = He told me the truth)
  - Ela **nos** mostrou as fotos (She showed the photos to us)
- Indirect object answers "to whom?" or "for whom?"
  - Dei o livro a Maria ‚Üí Dei a quem? A Maria ‚Üí **Lhe** dei o livro (I gave the book to her)
  - Falei com Jo√£o ‚Üí Falei com quem? Com Jo√£o ‚Üí **Lhe** falei (I spoke to him)

**Practice format:**
- "Lhe dei o livro" (I gave the book to him/her)
- "Ele me disse tudo" (He told everything to me = He told me everything)
- "Mostrei-lhe as fotos" ‚Üí "Lhe mostrei as fotos" (I showed the photos to him/her)
- "Ela nos explicou tudo" (She explained everything to us)

**Student can now:**
- Express to/for whom actions are directed
- Use verbs like dar, dizer, mostrar with indirect objects
- Distinguish between direct objects (Unit 36) and indirect objects (Unit 40)
- Understand that me/te/nos can be direct OR indirect (context determines)
- Form more sophisticated sentences with both direct and indirect objects

**Typical sentences:**
- Lhe dei o livro (I gave the book to him/her)
- Ele me disse a verdade (He told me the truth)
- Ela nos mostrou o caminho (She showed us the way)
- Vou lhe contar uma hist√≥ria (I'm going to tell a story to you/him/her)
- Eles me perguntaram tudo (They asked me everything)
- Lhe pedi ajuda (I asked him/her for help)
- Me empresta dinheiro? (Can you lend me money? / Will you lend money to me?)

**Indirect Object Pronouns:**
| Pronoun | Meaning | Example |
|---------|---------|---------|
| me | to/for me | Ele me deu (He gave to me) |
| te | to/for you (informal) | Te disse (I told you) |
| lhe | to/for him/her/you (formal) | Lhe falei (I spoke to him/her/you) |
| nos | to/for us | Nos mostrou (He/she showed to us) |
| lhes | to/for them/you (plural) | Lhes dei (I gave to them/you all) |

**Direct vs Indirect Object - CRITICAL DISTINCTION:**

**Direct Object (Unit 36) - WHO/WHAT:**
- Answers "whom?" or "what?" (no preposition in Portuguese)
- Eu **o** vi (I saw him) - WHO did you see? Him.
- Comprei **o** livro ‚Üí **O** comprei (I bought it) - WHAT did you buy? The book.
- Uses: me, te, **o/a**, nos, **os/as**

**Indirect Object (Unit 40) - TO/FOR WHOM:**
- Answers "to whom?" or "for whom?" (replaces a/para + person)
- Eu **lhe** dei o livro (I gave the book to him/her) - TO WHOM did you give? To him/her.
- Falei a Maria ‚Üí **Lhe** falei (I spoke to her) - TO WHOM did you speak? To her.
- Uses: me, te, **lhe**, nos, **lhes**

**Note: me/te/nos can be EITHER direct OR indirect!**
- **Direct:** Ele **me** viu (He saw me) - WHO did he see? Me.
- **Indirect:** Ele **me** disse (He told me) - TO WHOM did he tell? To me.
- Context and verb determine which one!

**Key Verbs with Indirect Objects:**

**DAR (to give) - takes indirect object:**
- Dei o livro **a ela** ‚Üí **Lhe** dei o livro (I gave the book to her)
- Voc√™ me d√° seu telefone? (Will you give me your phone number?)
- Ele nos deu um presente (He gave us a gift)
- Deram-lhe dinheiro? ‚Üí Lhe deram dinheiro? (Did they give money to him/her?)

**DIZER (to say/tell) - takes indirect object:**
- Disse a verdade **a ele** ‚Üí **Lhe** disse a verdade (I told the truth to him)
- Ele me disse tudo (He told me everything)
- O que voc√™ lhe disse? (What did you tell him/her?)
- Disseram-nos que sim (They told us yes)

**FALAR (to speak) - can take indirect object:**
- Falei **com ela** ‚Üí **Lhe** falei (I spoke to her)
- Note: "Falar com" (to speak with) ‚Üí "Lhe falar"
- Ele me falou sobre isso (He spoke to me about this)
- Vou lhe falar amanh√£ (I'm going to speak to you/him/her tomorrow)

**PERGUNTAR (to ask) - takes indirect object:**
- Perguntei **a ela** ‚Üí **Lhe** perguntei (I asked her)
- Me perguntaram onde moro (They asked me where I live)
- Vou lhe perguntar uma coisa (I'm going to ask you/him/her something)

**MOSTRAR (to show) - takes indirect object:**
- Mostrei as fotos **a eles** ‚Üí **Lhes** mostrei as fotos (I showed the photos to them)
- Ela me mostrou o caminho (She showed me the way)
- Vou lhe mostrar minha casa (I'm going to show you/him/her my house)

**EXPLICAR (to explain) - takes indirect object:**
- Expliquei tudo **a ela** ‚Üí **Lhe** expliquei tudo (I explained everything to her)
- Me explica isso? (Can you explain this to me?)
- Ele nos explicou a situa√ß√£o (He explained the situation to us)

**Sample Conversations:**

**Conversation 1:**
- A: Voc√™ deu o livro ao Jo√£o? (Did you give the book to Jo√£o?)
- B: Sim, lhe dei ontem. (Yes, I gave it to him yesterday.)
- A: E o que ele disse? (And what did he say?)
- B: Ele me disse que gostou muito. (He told me that he really liked it.)

**Conversation 2:**
- A: Voc√™ falou com a Maria? (Did you speak with Maria?)
- B: Sim, lhe falei hoje de manh√£. (Yes, I spoke to her this morning.)
- A: E voc√™ contou sobre a festa? (And did you tell her about the party?)
- B: Sim, lhe contei tudo. (Yes, I told her everything.)

**Conversation 3:**
- A: Me empresta seu telefone? (Can you lend me your phone?)
- B: Claro! Tamb√©m vou te dar meu endere√ßo. (Of course! I'm also going to give you my address.)
- A: Obrigado! Voc√™ sempre me ajuda. (Thanks! You always help me.)

**With Different Tenses:**

**Present:**
- Lhe dou presentes (I give gifts to him/her)
- Ele me diz a verdade (He tells me the truth)
- Ela nos mostra as fotos (She shows us the photos)

**Future (vou + infinitive):**
- Vou lhe dar um presente (I'm going to give a gift to you/him/her)
- Ele vai me dizer tudo (He's going to tell me everything)
- Vamos lhe mostrar a casa (We're going to show the house to you/him/her)

**Past:**
- Lhe dei um livro (I gave a book to him/her)
- Ele me disse a verdade (He told me the truth)
- Ela nos mostrou o caminho (She showed us the way)
- Perguntaram-me tudo (They asked me everything)

**Position in Brazilian Portuguese:**
- **Standard:** Pronoun BEFORE verb (like direct objects)
  - Me deu (He/she gave to me)
  - Lhe disse (I told you/him/her)
  - Nos mostrou (He/she showed to us)

**Common Patterns:**

**Dar (to give):**
- Me d√° seu telefone? (Can you give me your phone number?)
- Lhe dei dinheiro (I gave money to him/her)
- Ela nos deu um presente (She gave us a gift)
- Vou te dar um conselho (I'm going to give you advice)

**Dizer (to say/tell):**
- Me diz a verdade (Tell me the truth)
- Lhe disse que sim (I told him/her yes)
- Ele nos disse tudo (He told us everything)
- O que voc√™ me disse? (What did you tell me?)

**Pedir (to ask for/request):**
- Pedi-lhe ajuda (I asked him/her for help)
- Me pede o que quiser (Ask me for whatever you want)
- Eles nos pediram dinheiro (They asked us for money)

**Perguntar (to ask):**
- Me perguntou meu nome (He/she asked me my name)
- Vou lhe perguntar uma coisa (I'm going to ask you/him/her something)
- Eles nos perguntaram tudo (They asked us everything)

**With Negation:**
- N√£o lhe dei nada (I didn't give anything to him/her)
- Ele n√£o me disse a verdade (He didn't tell me the truth)
- N√£o nos mostraram o caminho (They didn't show us the way)
- Nunca lhe pedi dinheiro (I never asked him/her for money)

**Comparing Direct and Indirect with Same Verb:**

**VER (direct object only):**
- **O** vi ontem (I saw him yesterday) - direct object
- Cannot use indirect object with "ver"

**DAR (takes both direct AND indirect):**
- Dei **o livro** (I gave the book) - direct object = the book
- Dei o livro **a ela** ‚Üí **Lhe** dei o livro (I gave the book to her) - indirect object = to her
- Complete: **Lhe** dei **o livro** (I gave the book to her) - both indirect and direct!

**DIZER (takes both direct AND indirect):**
- Disse **a verdade** (I told the truth) - direct object = the truth
- Disse a verdade **a ele** ‚Üí **Lhe** disse a verdade (I told the truth to him) - indirect object = to him
- Complete: **Lhe** disse **a verdade** (I told him/her the truth) - both!

**Sentences with BOTH Direct and Indirect Objects:**

Pattern: subject + **indirect pronoun** + verb + **direct object noun**

- **Lhe** dei **o livro** (I gave the book to him/her)
  - Indirect: lhe (to him/her)
  - Direct: o livro (the book)

- Ele **me** mostrou **as fotos** (He showed me the photos)
  - Indirect: me (to me)
  - Direct: as fotos (the photos)

- Ela **nos** contou **a hist√≥ria** (She told us the story)
  - Indirect: nos (to us)
  - Direct: a hist√≥ria (the story)

**IMPORTANT - "Te" vs "Lhe" for "You":**

‚ö†Ô∏è **In Brazilian Portuguese:**
- **"Te"** is rare (associated with "tu" - uncommon in most of Brazil)
- **"Lhe"** is formal/standard for "you"
- **Colloquially:** Often use "para voc√™" instead
  - Less common: "Te dei o livro" (I gave the book to you)
  - More formal: "Lhe dei o livro" (I gave the book to you)
  - Most colloquial: "Dei o livro para voc√™" (I gave the book to you)

**Practical Usage:**
Indirect object pronouns avoid repetition and sound more natural:

**Without pronouns (repetitive):**
- Falei com Jo√£o. Dei um livro a Jo√£o. Expliquei tudo a Jo√£o.

**With pronouns (natural):**
- Falei com Jo√£o. **Lhe** dei um livro. **Lhe** expliquei tudo.

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**

1. **Confusing direct and indirect:**
   - ‚ùå "Eu o dei o livro" (Wrong - "dar" takes indirect "lhe", not direct "o")
   - ‚úÖ "Eu lhe dei o livro" (Correct - indirect object)

2. **Using wrong pronoun:**
   - ‚ùå "Lhe vi" (Wrong - "ver" takes direct object, not indirect)
   - ‚úÖ "O vi" (Correct - direct object with "ver")

3. **Forgetting the indirect with certain verbs:**
   - ‚ùå "Dei o livro" (Incomplete - to whom?)
   - ‚úÖ "Lhe dei o livro" (Complete - gave the book to him/her)

4. **Overusing "te" in BP:**
   - Less natural: "Te dei o livro"
   - More natural: "Lhe dei o livro" or "Dei o livro para voc√™"

**Key Learning:**
- Indirect object pronouns replace "to/for someone"
- **lhe/lhes** are the NEW forms (for him/her/you/them)
- me/te/nos can be direct OR indirect (context determines)
- Essential with verbs like dar, dizer, mostrar, perguntar, explicar
- Brazilian Portuguese puts pronouns BEFORE the verb
- "Lhe" is more formal; colloquially Brazilians often use "para voc√™"
- Can combine indirect pronoun + direct object noun in same sentence

**Why This Unit:**
- Natural progression after direct object pronouns (Unit 36)
- Essential for complete communication - expressing to/for whom
- Ultra-granular: focusing only on indirect object pronouns
- Immediate practical value - used constantly with common verbs (dar, dizer, falar)
- Completes the pronoun system started in Unit 35-32
- **MILESTONE**: Students can now express complex ideas with both direct and indirect objects!

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 31: Reflexive pronouns (me chamo, me levanto)
- Unit 32: Direct object pronouns (me v√™, o conhe√ßo)
- Unit 36: Indirect object pronouns (me d√°, lhe disse)
- Unit 29: Dar (to give) - now can use with "lhe"
- Unit 35: Dizer (to say/tell) - now can use with "lhe"
- All three use me/nos but with different functions!

**Important Note:**
In Brazilian Portuguese, the use of **lhe/lhes** is declining in colloquial speech. Many Brazilians prefer:
- "Dei o livro **para ele**" (I gave the book to him) instead of "**Lhe** dei o livro"
- "Falei **com ela**" (I spoke with her) instead of "**Lhe** falei"

However, **lhe/lhes** are still:
- Standard in writing
- Used in formal speech
- Essential to understand (you'll hear them)
- Important for intermediate-level fluency

Students should learn both forms for comprehension and flexibility.

### Unit 45: Imperfect Tense - Regular Verbs (Ongoing/Habitual Past)
**New vocabulary:**
- **Time expressions for habitual/repeated actions:**
  - sempre (always)
  - todos os dias (every day)
  - todas as semanas (every week)
  - frequentemente (frequently)
  - normalmente (normally)
  - geralmente (generally)
  - √†s vezes (sometimes)
  - nunca (never)
  - quando era crian√ßa (when I was a child)
  - naquela √©poca (at that time/back then)
  - antes (before)
- **Additional vocabulary:**
  - crian√ßa (child)
  - jovem (young)
  - pequeno/a (small/little)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Imperfect tense (pret√©rito imperfeito): for ongoing, habitual, or descriptive past actions**
- **Key distinction from preterite (Units 26-29, 33, 35):**
  - **Preterite:** completed actions (I ate, I went, I did)
  - **Imperfect:** ongoing/habitual actions (I was eating, I used to go, I would do)
- **Regular conjugation patterns for imperfect:**
  - **-AR verbs:** -ava, -ava, -√°vamos, -avam
  - **-ER verbs:** -ia, -ia, -√≠amos, -iam
  - **-IR verbs:** -ia, -ia, -√≠amos, -iam
- **Good news: -ER and -IR verbs share the SAME imperfect endings!**
- **Better news: Imperfect is VERY regular - almost no irregular verbs!**

**Practice format:**
- "Morava em S√£o Paulo" (I used to live in S√£o Paulo / I was living in S√£o Paulo)
- "Comia muito" (I used to eat a lot / I was eating a lot)
- "Quando era crian√ßa, brincava no parque" (When I was a child, I used to play in the park)

**Student can now:**
- Describe ongoing actions in the past (was doing)
- Talk about habitual actions in the past (used to do)
- Describe what things were like in the past
- Tell richer stories by combining preterite and imperfect
- Talk about childhood and past routines

**Typical sentences:**
- Morava em S√£o Paulo (I used to live in S√£o Paulo)
- Trabalhava no banco (I used to work at the bank / I was working at the bank)
- Comia muito (I used to eat a lot)
- Estudava portugu√™s todos os dias (I used to study Portuguese every day)
- Quando era crian√ßa, brincava muito (When I was a child, I used to play a lot)
- Sempre gostava de viajar (I always used to like traveling)
- Naquela √©poca, corr√≠amos no parque (At that time, we used to run in the park)

**Full Conjugation - Regular Verbs in Imperfect:**

**-AR verbs (falar, morar, trabalhar):**
| Pronoun | Ending | Example (morar) |
|---------|--------|-----------------|
| eu | -ava | morava |
| voc√™/ele/ela | -ava | morava |
| n√≥s | -√°vamos | mor√°vamos |
| voc√™s/eles/elas | -avam | moravam |

**-ER verbs (comer, beber, correr):**
| Pronoun | Ending | Example (comer) |
|---------|--------|-----------------|
| eu | -ia | comia |
| voc√™/ele/ela | -ia | comia |
| n√≥s | -√≠amos | com√≠amos |
| voc√™s/eles/elas | -iam | comiam |

**-IR verbs (abrir, partir, assistir):**
| Pronoun | Ending | Example (assistir) |
|---------|--------|--------------------|
| eu | -ia | assistia |
| voc√™/ele/ela | -ia | assistia |
| n√≥s | -√≠amos | assist√≠amos |
| voc√™s/eles/elas | -iam | assistiam |

**Pattern Recognition:**

**-AR verbs pattern:**
- Remove -ar, add -ava/-ava/-√°vamos/-avam
- falar ‚Üí falava, falava, fal√°vamos, falavam
- morar ‚Üí morava, morava, mor√°vamos, moravam
- trabalhar ‚Üí trabalhava, trabalhava, trabalh√°vamos, trabalhavam
- estudar ‚Üí estudava, estudava, estud√°vamos, estudavam

**-ER/-IR verbs pattern (SAME endings!):**
- Remove -er/-ir, add -ia/-ia/-√≠amos/-iam
- comer ‚Üí comia, comia, com√≠amos, comiam
- beber ‚Üí bebia, bebia, beb√≠amos, bebiam
- abrir ‚Üí abria, abria, abr√≠amos, abriam
- assistir ‚Üí assistia, assistia, assist√≠amos, assistiam

**Key Insight: eu and voc√™/ele/ela forms are IDENTICAL in imperfect!**
- eu morava = voc√™/ele/ela morava
- eu comia = voc√™/ele/ela comia
- Context clarifies who is being discussed

**When to Use Imperfect vs Preterite:**

**Use IMPERFECT for:**

**1. Ongoing actions (was doing):**
- Eu **estudava** quando ele chegou (I **was studying** when he arrived)
- Ela **trabalhava** no banco (She **was working** at the bank - at that time)
- **Com√≠amos** quando voc√™ ligou (We **were eating** when you called)

**2. Habitual/repeated actions (used to do):**
- Eu **morava** em S√£o Paulo (I **used to live** in S√£o Paulo - for a period)
- **Trabalhava** todos os dias (I **used to work** every day)
- Sempre **comia** l√° (I **always used to eat** there)
- Quando era crian√ßa, **brincava** muito (When I was a child, I **used to play** a lot)

**3. Descriptions of past states/conditions:**
- Ele **era** alto (He **was** tall - description)
- A casa **era** grande (The house **was** big - description)
- **Estava** cansado (I **was** tired - state)

**4. Age, time, weather in the past:**
- Eu **tinha** 20 anos (I **was** 20 years old)
- **Eram** 3 horas (It **was** 3 o'clock)
- **Fazia** calor (It **was** hot)

**Use PRETERITE for:**

**1. Completed actions (did):**
- Eu **estudei** ontem (I **studied** yesterday - completed)
- Ela **trabalhou** no banco (She **worked** at the bank - and then left)
- **Comemos** √†s 8h (We **ate** at 8 o'clock - completed)

**2. Specific events:**
- **Fui** ao Brasil em 2020 (I **went** to Brazil in 2020 - specific event)
- **Comprei** um carro (I **bought** a car - specific action)

**Comparing Side-by-Side:**

**Preterite (completed action):**
- **Morei** em S√£o Paulo (I lived in S√£o Paulo - and then left/moved)
- **Trabalhei** no banco (I worked at the bank - specific job ended)
- **Comi** muito (I ate a lot - specific occasion)

**Imperfect (ongoing/habitual):**
- **Morava** em S√£o Paulo (I used to live in S√£o Paulo / I was living in S√£o Paulo)
- **Trabalhava** no banco (I used to work at the bank / I was working at the bank)
- **Comia** muito (I used to eat a lot / I was eating a lot)

**Common Uses - Habitual Past:**

**With "sempre" (always):**
- Sempre **morava** perto do trabalho (I always used to live near work)
- Sempre **estudava** de manh√£ (I always used to study in the morning)
- Sempre **com√≠amos** juntos (We always used to eat together)

**With "todos os dias/semanas" (every day/week):**
- **Trabalhava** todos os dias (I used to work every day)
- **Corr√≠amos** todas as manh√£s (We used to run every morning)
- **Visitava** minha m√£e todas as semanas (I used to visit my mother every week)

**With "quando era crian√ßa" (when I was a child):**
- Quando era crian√ßa, **brincava** muito (When I was a child, I used to play a lot)
- Quando era crian√ßa, **morava** no Rio (When I was a child, I lived in Rio)
- Quando era jovem, **viajava** muito (When I was young, I used to travel a lot)

**Common Uses - Ongoing Past:**

**Actions in progress when something else happened:**
- Eu **estudava** quando ele chegou (I was studying when he arrived)
- **Trabalh√°vamos** quando voc√™ ligou (We were working when you called)
- Ela **comia** quando eu entrei (She was eating when I entered)
- Note: Second verb (chegou, ligou, entrei) is preterite (completed action)

**Sample Conversations:**

**Conversation 1 - Habitual past:**
- A: Onde voc√™ morava antes? (Where did you use to live before?)
- B: Eu morava em S√£o Paulo. (I used to live in S√£o Paulo.)
- A: E trabalhava l√° tamb√©m? (And did you work there too?)
- B: Sim, trabalhava no centro. (Yes, I used to work downtown.)

**Conversation 2 - Childhood:**
- A: O que voc√™ fazia quando era crian√ßa? (What did you do when you were a child?)
- B: Quando era crian√ßa, brincava no parque todos os dias. (When I was a child, I used to play in the park every day.)
- A: Com quem voc√™ brincava? (Who did you play with?)
- B: Brincava com meus irm√£os. (I used to play with my siblings.)

**Conversation 3 - Ongoing action interrupted:**
- A: O que voc√™ fazia quando eu liguei? (What were you doing when I called?)
- B: Eu estudava portugu√™s. (I was studying Portuguese.)
- A: Desculpa interromper! (Sorry to interrupt!)
- B: N√£o tem problema! (No problem!)

**Combining Preterite and Imperfect in Stories:**

**Example narrative:**
Quando eu **morava** em S√£o Paulo, **trabalhava** no banco. Todos os dias, **acordava** cedo e **ia** ao trabalho de √¥nibus. Um dia, **cheguei** tarde porque o √¥nibus **atrasou**. Meu chefe **ficou** bravo, mas eu **expliquei** o que aconteceu.

(When I **used to live** in S√£o Paulo, I **used to work** at the bank. Every day, I **would wake up** early and **would go** to work by bus. One day, I **arrived** late because the bus **was delayed**. My boss **got** angry, but I **explained** what happened.)

**Analysis:**
- **Imperfect:** morava, trabalhava, acordava, ia (habitual/background)
- **Preterite:** cheguei, atrasou, ficou, expliquei (specific events)

**With Negation:**
- N√£o morava em S√£o Paulo (I didn't use to live in S√£o Paulo)
- N√£o trabalhava l√° (I didn't use to work there)
- Nunca comia carne (I never used to eat meat)
- N√£o estud√°vamos juntos (We didn't use to study together)

**Common Expressions with Imperfect:**

**Describing past routines:**
- Sempre morava perto da escola (I always used to live near school)
- Trabalhava de segunda a sexta (I used to work Monday to Friday)
- Comia em casa todos os dias (I used to eat at home every day)
- Estud√°vamos juntos (We used to study together)

**Time markers that trigger imperfect:**
- quando era crian√ßa (when I was a child)
- naquela √©poca (at that time)
- antes (before)
- todos os dias (every day)
- sempre (always)
- frequentemente (frequently)

**Time markers that trigger preterite:**
- ontem (yesterday)
- na semana passada (last week)
- em 2020 (in 2020)
- uma vez (once)
- de repente (suddenly)

**Memory Aid - "Would" Test:**
If you can translate using "would" or "used to" in English, use imperfect:
- I **would** go (Eu ia) - imperfect
- I **used to** go (Eu ia) - imperfect
- I went (Eu fui) - preterite

**Key Learning:**
- Imperfect = ongoing/habitual past ("was doing" or "used to do")
- Preterite = completed past ("did")
- Imperfect is VERY regular - almost no exceptions
- -ER and -IR verbs share identical imperfect endings
- eu and voc√™/ele/ela forms are identical in imperfect
- Essential for telling complete stories about the past
- Common with time expressions like "sempre," "todos os dias," "quando era crian√ßa"

**Why This Unit:**
- Natural progression: completed past (preterite) ‚Üí ongoing/habitual past (imperfect)
- Essential for intermediate-level storytelling
- Ultra-granular: only regular verbs (irregulars come in Unit 42)
- Immediate practical value - talking about childhood, routines, past living situations
- Combines with preterite for rich narrative ability
- **MILESTONE**: Students can now tell complete stories with different types of past actions!

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Units 26-27: Preterite regular verbs (completed actions)
- Unit 37: Imperfect regular verbs (ongoing/habitual actions)
- Students can now choose the correct tense based on meaning
- Both tenses needed for sophisticated storytelling

**Note:** The imperfect has very few irregular verbs (only ser, ter, and vir are irregular). These will be covered in Unit 42.

### Unit 46: Imperfect Tense - Irregular Verbs (ser, ter, vir)
**New vocabulary:**
- **Time/age expressions with imperfect:**
  - anos (years - for age)
  - idade (age)
  - jovem (young)
  - velho/a (old)
- **Additional descriptive vocabulary:**
  - pequeno/a (small/little)
  - grande (big/large)
  - rico/a (rich)
  - pobre (poor)
  - feliz (happy)
  - triste (sad)
  - forte (strong)
  - fraco/a (weak)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Only THREE irregular verbs in imperfect: ser, ter, vir**
- **ser (to be) - imperfect:**
  - eu **era**, voc√™/ele/ela **era**, n√≥s **√©ramos**, voc√™s/eles/elas **eram**
- **ter (to have) - imperfect:**
  - eu **tinha**, voc√™/ele/ela **tinha**, n√≥s **t√≠nhamos**, voc√™s/eles/elas **tinham**
- **vir (to come) - imperfect:**
  - eu **vinha**, voc√™/ele/ela **vinha**, n√≥s **v√≠nhamos**, voc√™s/eles/elas **vinham**
- **These are the ONLY irregular verbs in imperfect tense!**

**Practice format:**
- "Era alto" (I/he was tall)
- "Tinha 20 anos" (I/he was 20 years old / I/he had 20 years)
- "Vinha aqui sempre" (I/he used to come here always)
- "Quando era crian√ßa, tinha um cachorro" (When I was a child, I had a dog)

**Student can now:**
- Use all three irregular imperfect verbs (ser, ter, vir)
- Describe what people/things were like in the past (era)
- Talk about age in the past (tinha X anos)
- Talk about possession in the past (tinha um carro)
- Talk about habitual coming in the past (vinha)
- Combine with regular imperfect verbs for complete past descriptions
- Tell sophisticated stories with complete imperfect tense knowledge

**Typical sentences:**
- Era alto (I/he was tall)
- Eu era jovem (I was young)
- Quando era crian√ßa, era pequeno (When I was a child, I was small)
- A casa era grande (The house was big)
- Eles eram ricos (They were rich)
- Tinha 20 anos (I was 20 years old)
- N√£o tinha dinheiro (I didn't have money)
- T√≠nhamos uma casa (We had a house)
- Vinha aqui todos os dias (I used to come here every day)
- Eles vinham sempre (They always used to come)
- V√≠nhamos de √¥nibus (We used to come by bus)

**Full Conjugation - Imperfect Irregular Verbs:**

**SER (to be) - imperfect:**
| Pronoun | Imperfect | Example |
|---------|-----------|---------|
| eu | era | Eu era jovem (I was young) |
| voc√™/ele/ela | era | Ele era alto (He was tall) |
| n√≥s | √©ramos | N√≥s √©ramos amigos (We were friends) |
| voc√™s/eles/elas | eram | Eles eram ricos (They were rich) |

**TER (to have) - imperfect:**
| Pronoun | Imperfect | Example |
|---------|-----------|---------|
| eu | tinha | Eu tinha 20 anos (I was 20 years old) |
| voc√™/ele/ela | tinha | Ela tinha dinheiro (She had money) |
| n√≥s | t√≠nhamos | N√≥s t√≠nhamos um carro (We had a car) |
| voc√™s/eles/elas | tinham | Eles tinham uma casa (They had a house) |

**VIR (to come) - imperfect:**
| Pronoun | Imperfect | Example |
|---------|-----------|---------|
| eu | vinha | Eu vinha sempre (I always used to come) |
| voc√™/ele/ela | vinha | Ele vinha de √¥nibus (He used to come by bus) |
| n√≥s | v√≠nhamos | N√≥s v√≠nhamos juntos (We used to come together) |
| voc√™s/eles/elas | vinham | Eles vinham aqui (They used to come here) |

**Common Uses - SER (imperfect):**

**Descriptions in the past:**
- Eu **era** alto (I was tall)
- Ela **era** bonita (She was beautiful)
- A casa **era** grande (The house was big)
- **Eram** ricos (They were rich)

**Age (alternative to ter):**
- Quando **era** crian√ßa (When I was a child)
- Quando voc√™ **era** jovem (When you were young)

**Time in the past:**
- **Eram** 3 horas (It was 3 o'clock)
- **Era** tarde (It was late)

**Common Uses - TER (imperfect):**

**Age (most common way):**
- **Tinha** 20 anos (I was 20 years old / I had 20 years)
- Ele **tinha** 15 anos (He was 15 years old)
- Quando **tinha** 10 anos (When I was 10 years old)

**Possession in the past:**
- **Tinha** um carro (I had a car / I used to have a car)
- N√£o **tinha** dinheiro (I didn't have money)
- **T√≠nhamos** uma casa (We had a house)

**Common Uses - VIR (imperfect):**

**Habitual coming:**
- **Vinha** aqui sempre (I always used to come here)
- Ele **vinha** de √¥nibus (He used to come by bus)
- **V√≠nhamos** juntos (We used to come together)

**Sample Conversations:**

**Conversation 1:**
- A: Quantos anos voc√™ tinha quando morava no Rio? (How old were you when you lived in Rio?)
- B: Eu tinha 20 anos. Era jovem. (I was 20 years old. I was young.)
- A: E voc√™ vinha aqui sempre? (And did you come here often?)
- B: Sim, vinha todos os fins de semana. (Yes, I used to come every weekend.)

**Conversation 2:**
- A: Como era sua casa quando voc√™ era crian√ßa? (What was your house like when you were a child?)
- B: Era pequena, mas tinha um jardim grande. (It was small, but it had a big garden.)
- A: Seus av√≥s vinham visitar? (Did your grandparents come to visit?)
- B: Sim, eles vinham todo domingo. (Yes, they used to come every Sunday.)

**Combining Imperfect Description + Preterite Action:**
- Quando **era** crian√ßa, **fui** ao Brasil (When I was a child, I went to Brazil)
- Ele **tinha** 30 anos quando **comprou** a casa (He was 30 years old when he bought the house)
- N√≥s **v√≠nhamos** sempre, mas um dia **decidimos** parar (We always used to come, but one day we decided to stop)

**Full Example Narrative:**
Quando eu **era** jovem, **morava** em uma cidade pequena. **Tinha** poucos amigos, mas eles **eram** muito legais. Meu melhor amigo **vinha** √† minha casa todos os dias. Um dia, ele **foi** embora e nunca mais **vi** ele. Naquela √©poca, eu **tinha** muito tempo livre e a vida **era** mais simples.

(When I was young, I lived in a small city. I had few friends, but they were very cool. My best friend used to come to my house every day. One day, he left and I never saw him again. At that time, I had a lot of free time and life was simpler.)

**With Negation:**
- N√£o era alto (I/he wasn't tall)
- N√£o tinha dinheiro (I didn't have money)
- N√£o vinha aqui (I/he didn't use to come here)
- N√£o √©ramos ricos (We weren't rich)
- N√£o tinham uma casa (They didn't have a house)

**Key Learning:**
- **Imperfect has only 3 irregular verbs:** ser, ter, vir
- **Era** = was (description/state)
- **Tinha** = had (possession/age)
- **Vinha** = used to come (habitual)
- Combine imperfect (background/description) with preterite (actions)
- Use imperfect for "was doing" and "used to do"
- All three verbs are VERY common in storytelling

**Why This Unit:**
- Natural progression: completing the imperfect tense system
- Ultra-granular: only 3 irregular verbs (the ONLY ones in imperfect!)
- Immediate practical value - these 3 verbs are essential for past descriptions
- **MILESTONE**: Complete imperfect tense mastery (all regular + all 3 irregulars)!
- Students can now tell complete, sophisticated stories combining imperfect and preterite

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 37: Imperfect regular verbs (all -AR, -ER, -IR)
- Unit 38: Imperfect irregular verbs (only 3: ser, ter, vir)
- Unit 28: ser, ter in preterite (now have both tenses)
- Unit 35: vir in preterite (now have both tenses)
- Students can now tell complete stories with complete past tense system

### Unit 47: Comparatives (mais...que, menos...que, t√£o...quanto)

**New vocabulary:**
- mais (more)
- menos (less)
- que / do que (than)
- t√£o...quanto (as...as)
- melhor (better - irregular)
- pior (worse - irregular)
- maior (bigger/older - irregular)
- menor (smaller/younger - irregular)

**Adjectives for comparisons:**
- alto/a (tall)
- baixo/a (short)
- gordo/a (fat)
- magro/a (thin)
- rico/a (rich)
- pobre (poor)
- r√°pido/a (fast)
- lento/a (slow)
- f√°cil (easy)
- dif√≠cil (difficult)
- bonito/a (beautiful)
- feio/a (ugly)
- caro/a (expensive)
- barato/a (cheap)
- velho/a (old)
- jovem (young)
- inteligente (intelligent)
- interessante (interesting)
- importante (important)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Structure 1: mais + adjective + que (more...than)**
- **Structure 2: menos + adjective + que (less...than)**
- **Structure 3: t√£o + adjective + quanto (as...as)**
- **Irregular comparatives:** melhor, pior, maior, menor (NEVER use mais bom, mais mau)

**Practice format:**
- "Jo√£o √© mais alto que Maria" (Jo√£o is taller than Maria)
- "Este livro √© menos caro que aquele" (This book is less expensive than that one)
- "Sou t√£o alto quanto voc√™" (I'm as tall as you)
- "Este √© melhor que aquele" (This is better than that)

**Student can now:**
- Compare two people or things using regular adjectives
- Make equality comparisons (as...as)
- Use irregular comparatives correctly (melhor, pior, maior, menor)
- Avoid common mistakes (mais bom, mais mau)
- Compare physical traits, qualities, cost, speed
- Combine comparatives with all tenses learned

**Typical sentences:**
- Jo√£o √© mais alto que Pedro (Jo√£o is taller than Pedro)
- Maria √© menos rica que Ana (Maria is less rich than Ana)
- Sou t√£o velho quanto voc√™ (I'm as old as you)
- Este livro √© melhor que aquele (This book is better than that one)
- S√£o Paulo √© maior que o Rio (S√£o Paulo is bigger than Rio)
- Este restaurante √© mais caro que aquele (This restaurant is more expensive than that one)

**COMPARATIVES - THREE STRUCTURES:**

**Structure 1: mais + adjective + que (more...than)**
- Jo√£o √© **mais alto que** Maria (Jo√£o is taller than Maria)
- Este livro √© **mais caro que** aquele (This book is more expensive than that one)
- Sou **mais velho que** voc√™ (I'm older than you)
- S√£o Paulo √© **mais grande que** Bras√≠lia (S√£o Paulo is bigger than Bras√≠lia)
- Ela √© **mais inteligente que** ele (She is more intelligent than him)

**Note:** "que" can be replaced by "do que" (same meaning):
- Jo√£o √© mais alto **que** Maria = Jo√£o √© mais alto **do que** Maria (both correct)

**Structure 2: menos + adjective + que (less...than)**
- Maria √© **menos alta que** Jo√£o (Maria is less tall than Jo√£o / Maria is shorter than Jo√£o)
- Este livro √© **menos caro que** aquele (This book is less expensive than that one)
- Sou **menos rico que** ele (I'm less rich than him / I'm poorer than him)
- Este carro √© **menos r√°pido que** aquele (This car is less fast than that one)

**Structure 3: t√£o + adjective + quanto (as...as)**
- Sou **t√£o alto quanto** voc√™ (I'm as tall as you)
- Este livro √© **t√£o bom quanto** aquele (This book is as good as that one)
- Ela √© **t√£o bonita quanto** a irm√£ (She's as beautiful as her sister)
- Somos **t√£o ricos quanto** voc√™s (We're as rich as you)

**IRREGULAR COMPARATIVES (CRITICAL):**

‚ö†Ô∏è **NEVER say these:**
- ‚ùå mais bom (more good)
- ‚ùå mais mau (more bad)
- ‚ùå mais grande (more big - for age/importance)
- ‚ùå mais pequeno (more small - for age)

‚úÖ **ALWAYS say these instead:**
- ‚úÖ **melhor** (better)
- ‚úÖ **pior** (worse)
- ‚úÖ **maior** (bigger/older)
- ‚úÖ **menor** (smaller/younger)

**Examples with irregular comparatives:**
- Este livro √© **melhor que** aquele (This book is better than that one)
  - ‚ùå NOT: Este livro √© mais bom que aquele
- Este √© **pior que** aquele (This is worse than that one)
  - ‚ùå NOT: Este √© mais mau que aquele
- Jo√£o √© **maior que** Pedro (Jo√£o is older than Pedro - for age)
  - ‚úÖ Can also say: Jo√£o √© mais velho que Pedro (Jo√£o is older - using regular form)
- S√£o Paulo √© **maior que** o Rio (S√£o Paulo is bigger than Rio - for size/importance)
- Minha casa √© **menor que** a sua (My house is smaller than yours)

**Note on maior/menor:**
- Can mean **bigger/smaller** (size)
- Can mean **older/younger** (age)
- Can mean **greater/lesser** (importance)
- Context determines meaning

**COMMON COMPARATIVE PATTERNS:**

**Physical descriptions:**
- mais alto/baixo (taller/shorter)
- mais gordo/magro (fatter/thinner)
- mais bonito/feio (more beautiful/uglier)
- mais velho/jovem (older/younger) OR maior/menor (older/younger)
- mais forte/fraco (stronger/weaker)

**Qualities:**
- mais inteligente (more intelligent)
- mais interessante (more interesting)
- mais importante (more important)
- mais dif√≠cil/f√°cil (more difficult/easier)

**Cost:**
- mais caro/barato (more expensive/cheaper)

**Speed:**
- mais r√°pido/lento (faster/slower)

**Sample Conversations:**

**Conversation 1:**
- A: Quem √© mais alto, Jo√£o ou Pedro? (Who is taller, Jo√£o or Pedro?)
- B: Jo√£o √© mais alto que Pedro. (Jo√£o is taller than Pedro.)
- A: E Maria? (And Maria?)
- B: Maria √© t√£o alta quanto Jo√£o. (Maria is as tall as Jo√£o.)

**Conversation 2:**
- A: Qual cidade √© melhor, S√£o Paulo ou Rio? (Which city is better, S√£o Paulo or Rio?)
- B: Para mim, o Rio √© melhor. (For me, Rio is better.)
- A: Por qu√™? (Why?)
- B: Porque o Rio √© mais bonito e menos frio. (Because Rio is more beautiful and less cold.)

**Conversation 3:**
- A: Este restaurante √© caro? (Is this restaurant expensive?)
- B: √â mais caro que aquele, mas √© melhor. (It's more expensive than that one, but it's better.)
- A: Ent√£o vamos neste. (Then let's go to this one.)

**With Negation:**
- N√£o √© mais alto que ela (He's not taller than her)
- N√£o sou t√£o rico quanto voc√™ (I'm not as rich as you)
- N√£o √© melhor que o outro (It's not better than the other one)

**Combining Comparatives with Past Tenses:**

**With preterite:**
- Fui mais r√°pido que ele (I was faster than him - in that race)
- Esta viagem foi melhor que a outra (This trip was better than the other one)

**With imperfect:**
- Quando era crian√ßa, era mais alto que meus amigos (When I was a child, I was taller than my friends)
- A casa antiga era maior que esta (The old house was bigger than this one)

**Full Example:**
Este apartamento √© **maior que** o outro, mas √© **mais caro**. O outro era **menor**, mas era **t√£o bonito quanto** este. Para mim, este √© **melhor** porque tem mais quartos. Mas voc√™ pode preferir o outro porque √© **menos caro**.

(This apartment is bigger than the other one, but it's more expensive. The other one was smaller, but it was as beautiful as this one. For me, this one is better because it has more rooms. But you might prefer the other one because it's less expensive.)

**Key Learning:**
- **Three structures:** mais...que (more than), menos...que (less than), t√£o...quanto (as as)
- **Irregular comparatives:** melhor, pior, maior, menor (must be memorized - never use mais bom/mau)
- Use "que" or "do que" for "than" (both correct)
- Use "quanto" for "as" in equality comparisons
- Comparatives work with all tenses (present, preterite, imperfect, future)
- Context determines meaning of maior/menor (size vs age vs importance)

**Why This Unit:**
- Natural progression: expanding descriptive abilities
- Essential for intermediate conversation - constant need to compare
- Ultra-granular: one grammar concept (comparatives only)
- Immediate practical value - comparing things is daily communication
- Works with all adjectives and tenses already learned

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Builds on adjectives learned throughout curriculum (alto, grande, bom, etc.)
- Uses all pronouns from Units 18-22
- Can combine with all tenses: present, preterite (Units 26-29, 33, 35), imperfect (Units 37-38), future (Unit 27)
- Students can now make sophisticated descriptions and comparisons in all tenses

### Unit 48: Superlatives (O mais..., O menos...)
**New vocabulary:**
- **o mais** (the most)
- **o menos** (the least)
- **de** (of/in - for scope)
- **do mundo** (in the world)
- **do Brasil** (in Brazil)
- **da cidade** (in the city)
- **da fam√≠lia** (in the family)
- **da classe** (in the class)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Superlative structure:** article + mais/menos + adjective + de + scope
  - **o mais** alto **da** classe (the tallest in the class)
  - **a mais** bonita **do** Brasil (the most beautiful in Brazil)
- **Article agrees with the noun:**
  - o mais... (masculine singular)
  - a mais... (feminine singular)
  - os mais... (masculine plural)
  - as mais... (feminine plural)
- **Irregular superlatives:**
  - o **melhor** (the best) - NOT "o mais bom"
  - o **pior** (the worst) - NOT "o mais mau"
  - o **maior** (the biggest/oldest) - NOT "o mais grande" (in most cases)
  - o **menor** (the smallest/youngest) - NOT "o mais pequeno"

**Practice format:**
- "Ele √© o mais alto da classe" (He's the tallest in the class)
- "S√£o Paulo √© a maior cidade do Brasil" (S√£o Paulo is the biggest city in Brazil)
- "Este √© o melhor livro do mundo" (This is the best book in the world)
- "Ela √© a mais inteligente da fam√≠lia" (She's the smartest in the family)

**Student can now:**
- Express superlatives (the most/least)
- Use correct article agreement
- Use irregular superlatives correctly
- Define scope with "de" (of/in)
- Make absolute comparisons within a group
- Distinguish comparative (Unit 47) from superlative

**Typical sentences:**
- Ele √© o mais alto da turma (He's the tallest in the class)
- Esta √© a mais bonita cidade do Brasil (This is the most beautiful city in Brazil)
- S√£o Paulo √© a maior cidade do pa√≠s (S√£o Paulo is the biggest city in the country)
- Este √© o melhor restaurante da cidade (This is the best restaurant in the city)
- Ela √© a mais nova da fam√≠lia (She's the youngest in the family)
- Este foi o pior dia da minha vida (This was the worst day of my life)
- Ele √© o menos simp√°tico do grupo (He's the least friendly in the group)

**Superlative Structure - Article Agreement:**
| Noun Gender/Number | Structure | Example |
|-------------------|-----------|---------|
| Masculine Singular | o mais/menos + adj + de | o mais alto da classe |
| Feminine Singular | a mais/menos + adj + de | a mais bonita do mundo |
| Masculine Plural | os mais/menos + adj + de | os mais ricos do pa√≠s |
| Feminine Plural | as mais/menos + adj + de | as mais inteligentes da escola |

**Regular Superlatives:**
- o mais alto (the tallest)
- o mais baixo (the shortest)
- o mais rico (the richest)
- o mais pobre (the poorest)
- o mais bonito (the most beautiful)
- o mais feio (the ugliest)
- o mais inteligente (the most intelligent)
- o mais importante (the most important)
- o mais dif√≠cil (the most difficult)
- o mais f√°cil (the easiest)

**Irregular Superlatives (CRITICAL):**
- ‚ùå o mais bom ‚Üí ‚úÖ **o melhor** (the best)
- ‚ùå o mais mau ‚Üí ‚úÖ **o pior** (the worst)
- ‚ùå o mais grande ‚Üí ‚úÖ **o maior** (the biggest - for importance/size)
  - Note: "o mais grande" is acceptable for physical size, but "o maior" is preferred
- ‚ùå o mais pequeno ‚Üí ‚úÖ **o menor** (the smallest)

**Scope with "de":**
- **de + article = do/da/dos/das** (from Unit 2!)
- do mundo (in the world - de + o mundo)
- da cidade (in the city - de + a cidade)
- do Brasil (in Brazil - de + o Brasil)
- da fam√≠lia (in the family - de + a fam√≠lia)
- dos meus amigos (of my friends - de + os meus amigos)

**Sample Conversations:**

**Conversation 1:**
- A: Qual √© a maior cidade do Brasil? (What's the biggest city in Brazil?)
- B: S√£o Paulo √© a maior. (S√£o Paulo is the biggest.)
- A: E a mais bonita? (And the most beautiful?)
- B: Para mim, o Rio √© a mais bonita. (For me, Rio is the most beautiful.)

**Conversation 2:**
- A: Quem √© o mais alto da sua fam√≠lia? (Who's the tallest in your family?)
- B: Meu irm√£o √© o mais alto. Ele tem 1,90m. (My brother is the tallest. He's 1.90m.)
- A: E voc√™? (And you?)
- B: Eu sou o mais baixo! (I'm the shortest!)

**Conversation 3:**
- A: Qual foi o melhor dia da sua vida? (What was the best day of your life?)
- B: O dia do meu casamento foi o melhor. (My wedding day was the best.)
- A: E o pior? (And the worst?)
- B: N√£o quero falar sobre o pior dia! (I don't want to talk about the worst day!)

**Comparing Comparative vs Superlative:**
| Type | Structure | Example |
|------|-----------|---------|
| Comparative (Unit 47) | mais/menos + adj + que | Jo√£o √© mais alto **que** Pedro |
| Superlative (Unit 48) | o mais/menos + adj + de | Jo√£o √© o mais alto **da** classe |

**With Possessives:**
- o meu melhor amigo (my best friend)
- a minha maior preocupa√ß√£o (my biggest concern)
- o nosso maior problema (our biggest problem)

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ‚ùå "mais alto da classe" (wrong - missing article)
- ‚úÖ "o mais alto da classe" (correct)
- ‚ùå "o mais bom" (wrong - irregular superlative)
- ‚úÖ "o melhor" (correct)
- ‚ùå "a mais alto da classe" (wrong - article doesn't agree)
- ‚úÖ "o mais alto da classe" (correct - alto is masculine)
- ‚ùå "o mais alto na classe" (wrong - use "de/da" not "na")
- ‚úÖ "o mais alto da classe" (correct)

**Absolute Superlatives (preview for later):**
- Portuguese also has "absolute superlatives" with -√≠ssimo:
  - alto ‚Üí alt√≠ssimo (very tall)
  - bom ‚Üí √≥timo (excellent)
- These will be taught in a future unit

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 43: Comparatives ‚Üí Superlatives (natural extension)
- Unit 2: de contractions ‚Üí "do mundo, da cidade"
- Adjectives throughout ‚Üí all can be used in superlatives
- All tenses: "Foi o melhor dia" (past), "√â o melhor" (present)

**Key Learning:**
- Superlative requires article (o/a/os/as)
- Article agrees with the NOUN, not the person
- Use "de" for scope (in/of)
- Four irregular superlatives must be memorized
- Distinguishes "one of many" (superlative) from "one vs one" (comparative)

**Why This Unit:**
- Natural progression after comparatives (Unit 47)
- Ultra-granular: focuses ONLY on superlatives (one concept)
- Essential for expressing extremes and making judgments
- Practical: very common in everyday conversation
- Completes comparative/superlative system

### Unit 49: Telling Time (Que horas s√£o?)
**New vocabulary:**
- **hora/horas** (hour/hours, o'clock)
- **meio-dia** (noon - literally "half-day")
- **meia-noite** (midnight - literally "half-night")
- **meio/meia** (half)
- **quinze** (quarter - 15 minutes)
- **menos** (minus, to - for "to the hour")
- **para** (to - alternate for "to the hour")
- **em ponto** (on the dot, exactly)
- **da manh√£** (in the morning - AM)
- **da tarde** (in the afternoon - PM)
- **da noite** (at night - PM)
- **madrugada** (early morning hours - 1-5 AM)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Question:** Que horas s√£o? (What time is it? - literally "What hours are they?")
  - Note: PLURAL "s√£o" because time is plural concept
- **Exception:** √â uma hora (It's 1 o'clock - SINGULAR for 1:00 only!)
- **Structure patterns:**
  - **On the hour:** S√£o [number] horas
  - **Past the hour:** S√£o [hour] e [minutes]
  - **Half past:** S√£o [hour] e meia (literally "and half")
  - **Quarter past:** S√£o [hour] e quinze
  - **To the hour:** S√£o [minutes] para as [next hour] OR Faltam [minutes] para as [next hour]
- **12-hour system** (Brazil uses 12-hour more commonly than 24-hour in speech)

**Practice format:**
- "Que horas s√£o?" "S√£o tr√™s horas" (What time is it? It's 3 o'clock)
- "S√£o duas e quinze" (It's 2:15)
- "S√£o quatro e meia" (It's 4:30)
- "S√£o dez para as seis" (It's 5:50 - ten to six)
- "√â meio-dia" (It's noon)
- "√â meia-noite" (It's midnight)

**Student can now:**
- Ask what time it is
- Tell time on the hour
- Tell time with minutes (past and to the hour)
- Use special expressions (meio-dia, meia-noite)
- Distinguish AM from PM (da manh√£/da tarde/da noite)
- Schedule appointments and meetings

**Time Expressions - Complete System:**

**On the hour:**
- √â uma hora (It's 1:00) - SINGULAR!
- S√£o duas horas (It's 2:00)
- S√£o tr√™s horas (It's 3:00)
- S√£o doze horas (It's 12:00)

**Special times:**
- √â meio-dia (It's noon/12:00 PM)
- √â meia-noite (It's midnight/12:00 AM)

**Minutes past (e):**
- S√£o duas e cinco (It's 2:05)
- S√£o tr√™s e dez (It's 3:10)
- S√£o quatro e quinze (It's 4:15)
- S√£o cinco e vinte (It's 5:20)
- S√£o seis e vinte e cinco (It's 6:25)
- S√£o sete e meia (It's 7:30) - "meia" means half!
- S√£o oito e quarenta (It's 8:40)

**Minutes to (para/menos):**
- S√£o dez para as nove (It's 8:50 - ten to nine)
- S√£o quinze para as dez (It's 9:45 - quarter to ten)
- S√£o vinte para as onze (It's 10:40 - twenty to eleven)
- S√£o cinco para o meio-dia (It's 11:55 - five to noon)

**Alternative with "menos":**
- S√£o nove menos dez (It's 8:50 - literally "nine minus ten")
- S√£o dez menos quinze (It's 9:45)
- This is less common in BP, but understood

**Precision expressions:**
- S√£o tr√™s horas em ponto (It's 3:00 on the dot)
- S√£o duas e meia em ponto (It's 2:30 exactly)

**Time of day (AM/PM):**
- S√£o sete da manh√£ (It's 7 AM)
- S√£o duas da tarde (It's 2 PM)
- S√£o oito da noite (It's 8 PM)
- S√£o tr√™s da madrugada (It's 3 AM - early morning)

**Sample Conversations:**

**Conversation 1:**
- A: Que horas s√£o? (What time is it?)
- B: S√£o tr√™s e meia. (It's 3:30.)
- A: Obrigado! (Thanks!)

**Conversation 2:**
- A: A que horas come√ßa o filme? (What time does the movie start?)
- B: Come√ßa √†s oito da noite. (It starts at 8 PM.)
- A: E que horas s√£o agora? (And what time is it now?)
- B: S√£o sete e quarenta e cinco. Ainda temos tempo. (It's 7:45. We still have time.)

**Conversation 3:**
- A: Voc√™ trabalha at√© que horas? (Until what time do you work?)
- B: Trabalho at√© as seis da tarde. (I work until 6 PM.)
- A: E voc√™ acorda a que horas? (And what time do you wake up?)
- B: Acordo √†s sete da manh√£. (I wake up at 7 AM.)

**Asking about time:**
- Que horas s√£o? (What time is it?)
- Voc√™ tem horas? (Do you have the time? - colloquial)
- Pode me dizer que horas s√£o? (Can you tell me what time it is?)
- A que horas...? (At what time...?)
  - A que horas voc√™ vai? (What time are you going?)
  - A que horas come√ßa? (What time does it start?)

**Telling at what time (preposition "a" / "√†s"):**
- **√†s** + time = at [time]
- Vou √†s tr√™s (I'm going at 3:00) - "a" + "as" = "√†s"
- Come√ßa √†s oito (It starts at 8:00)
- Acordo √†s sete da manh√£ (I wake up at 7 AM)
- O filme √© √† uma (The movie is at 1:00) - "a" + "a" = "√†"

**24-hour format (less common in speech, but used):**
- S√£o treze horas (It's 1:00 PM - 13:00)
- S√£o quinze horas e trinta (It's 3:30 PM - 15:30)
- S√£o vinte horas (It's 8:00 PM - 20:00)
- Common in: military, transportation, formal settings

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ‚ùå "S√£o uma hora" (wrong - 1 o'clock is singular)
- ‚úÖ "√â uma hora" (correct)
- ‚ùå "√â duas horas" (wrong - 2+ is plural)
- ‚úÖ "S√£o duas horas" (correct)
- ‚ùå "S√£o tr√™s e meio" (wrong - "meio" is masculine, "hora" is feminine)
- ‚úÖ "S√£o tr√™s e meia" (correct)
- ‚ùå "S√£o sete quarenta e cinco" (wrong - missing "e" after hour)
- ‚úÖ "S√£o sete e quarenta e cinco" (correct)

**Pronunciation Notes:**
- "horas" = [OH-ras] - don't pronounce the H
- "meia" = [MAY-a] - diphthong
- "meio-dia" = [may-oo JEE-a]

**Time Ranges:**
- **Manh√£** (morning): 6 AM - 12 PM
- **Tarde** (afternoon): 12 PM - 6 PM
- **Noite** (night): 6 PM - midnight
- **Madrugada** (early morning): midnight - 6 AM

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 15-45: Numbers ‚Üí used for time
- Unit 16: "Tenho" ‚Üí "Voc√™ tem horas?" (Do you have the time?)
- Unit 43: "Menos" (comparative) ‚Üí "Dez para as tr√™s" (ten to three)
- Prepositions: "a/√†s" for "at" with time

**Key Learning:**
- "√â uma hora" (singular) vs "S√£o X horas" (plural)
- "E" for past the hour, "para" for to the hour
- "Meia" (not "meio") for half past
- Time of day: da manh√£, da tarde, da noite, da madrugada
- Essential skill for scheduling and daily life

**Why This Unit:**
- **FOUNDATIONAL:** Telling time is essential for daily life
- Natural progression: learned numbers, now apply to time
- Ultra-granular: focuses ONLY on telling time (one concept)
- Practical: immediate use for schedules, appointments, meetings
- Prepares for dates, schedules, and more complex time expressions
