### Unit 50: Days of the Week (Dias da Semana)
**New vocabulary:**
- **semana** (week)
- **dia/dias** (day/days)
- **Days of the week:**
  - segunda-feira (Monday - literally "second fair/market day")
  - ter√ßa-feira (Tuesday - literally "third fair day")
  - quarta-feira (Wednesday - literally "fourth fair day")
  - quinta-feira (Thursday - literally "fifth fair day")
  - sexta-feira (Friday - literally "sixth fair day")
  - s√°bado (Saturday)
  - domingo (Sunday)
- **fim de semana** (weekend)
- **dia √∫til** (weekday - literally "useful day")
- **hoje** (today)
- **amanh√£** (tomorrow)
- **ontem** (yesterday)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Days are MASCULINE** (o domingo, o s√°bado)
- **Days with "feira"** can drop "-feira" in speech: segunda, ter√ßa, quarta, quinta, sexta
- **Preposition "em" for "on"** a specific day:
  - na segunda(-feira) (on Monday)
  - no s√°bado (on Saturday)
  - no domingo (on Sunday)
- **Plural for recurring days:**
  - √†s segundas (on Mondays - every Monday)
  - aos s√°bados (on Saturdays - every Saturday)
- **NO article** for "today": hoje √© segunda (today is Monday) - NOT "hoje √© a segunda"

**Practice format:**
- "Hoje √© segunda-feira" (Today is Monday)
- "Trabalho de segunda a sexta" (I work Monday to Friday)
- "Vou ao cinema no s√°bado" (I'm going to the movies on Saturday)
- "Que dia √© hoje?" "Hoje √© quarta" (What day is today? Today is Wednesday)
- "Aos domingos eu descanso" (On Sundays I rest)

**Student can now:**
- Name all seven days of the week
- Ask and answer what day it is
- Say when events happen (on Monday, on Saturday)
- Use shortened forms (segunda vs segunda-feira)
- Express recurring events (every Monday, on Saturdays)
- Talk about the weekend

**Typical sentences:**
- Hoje √© sexta-feira (Today is Friday)
- Amanh√£ √© s√°bado (Tomorrow is Saturday)
- Ontem foi quinta-feira (Yesterday was Thursday)
- Trabalho de segunda a sexta (I work Monday to Friday)
- Vou viajar no domingo (I'm going to travel on Sunday)
- Tenho aula na ter√ßa (I have class on Tuesday)
- Aos s√°bados eu acordo tarde (On Saturdays I wake up late)
- Que dia √© hoje? (What day is today?)
- O fim de semana come√ßa na sexta (The weekend starts on Friday)

**Days of the Week - Complete List:**
| Portuguese | Shortened | English | Origin |
|------------|-----------|---------|---------|
| segunda-feira | segunda | Monday | "second fair day" |
| ter√ßa-feira | ter√ßa | Tuesday | "third fair day" |
| quarta-feira | quarta | Wednesday | "fourth fair day" |
| quinta-feira | quinta | Thursday | "fifth fair day" |
| sexta-feira | sexta | Friday | "sixth fair day" |
| s√°bado | ‚Äî | Saturday | Sabbath |
| domingo | ‚Äî | Sunday | Lord's day |

**Cultural Note:**
- The "feira" days reference medieval market days
- Sunday (domingo) was the 1st day, Monday the 2nd, etc.
- S√°bado and domingo don't use "feira" because they're religious days

**Prepositions with Days:**

**Specific day (on):**
- **na/no** + day = on [day]
- Vou viajar **na** segunda (I'm going to travel on Monday)
- O jogo √© **no** domingo (The game is on Sunday)
- Tenho reuni√£o **na** quarta (I have a meeting on Wednesday)

**Recurring days (every):**
- **√†s/aos** + day (plural) = every [day]
- Trabalho **√†s** segundas (I work on Mondays - every Monday)
- Vou √† academia **√†s** ter√ßas e quintas (I go to the gym on Tuesdays and Thursdays)
- **Aos** s√°bados eu descanso (On Saturdays I rest - every Saturday)
- **Aos** domingos vou √† igreja (On Sundays I go to church)

**Time ranges:**
- de segunda a sexta (Monday to Friday)
- de ter√ßa a quinta (Tuesday to Thursday)
- no fim de semana (on the weekend)

**Sample Conversations:**

**Conversation 1:**
- A: Que dia √© hoje? (What day is today?)
- B: Hoje √© quarta-feira. (Today is Wednesday.)
- A: E amanh√£? (And tomorrow?)
- B: Amanh√£ √© quinta. (Tomorrow is Thursday.)

**Conversation 2:**
- A: Quando voc√™ trabalha? (When do you work?)
- B: Trabalho de segunda a sexta, das 9h √†s 18h. (I work Monday to Friday, from 9 AM to 6 PM.)
- A: E no fim de semana? (And on the weekend?)
- B: No fim de semana eu descanso. (On the weekend I rest.)

**Conversation 3:**
- A: Voc√™ tem aula quando? (When do you have class?)
- B: Tenho aula √†s ter√ßas e quintas. (I have class on Tuesdays and Thursdays.)
- A: A que horas? (At what time?)
- B: √Äs 14h. (At 2 PM.)

**Common Patterns:**
- Hoje √© + day: "Hoje √© segunda"
- Amanh√£ √© + day: "Amanh√£ √© s√°bado"
- Ontem foi + day: "Ontem foi domingo"
- na/no + day (specific): "Vou viajar no s√°bado"
- √†s/aos + day plural (recurring): "Trabalho √†s segundas"
- de X a Y: "de segunda a sexta"

**Asking about days:**
- Que dia √© hoje? (What day is today?)
- Que dia √© amanh√£? (What day is tomorrow?)
- Que dia foi ontem? (What day was yesterday?)
- Em que dia...? (On what day...?)
  - Em que dia voc√™ viaja? (What day do you travel?)

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ‚ùå "Hoje √© a segunda" (wrong - no article with hoje)
- ‚úÖ "Hoje √© segunda" (correct)
- ‚ùå "em segunda" (wrong - need contraction)
- ‚úÖ "na segunda" (correct)
- ‚ùå "em o s√°bado" (wrong - must contract)
- ‚úÖ "no s√°bado" (correct)
- ‚ùå "aos segunda" (wrong - missing plural)
- ‚úÖ "√†s segundas" (correct)

**With Different Tenses:**
- **Present:** Hoje √© sexta (Today is Friday)
- **Past:** Ontem foi quinta (Yesterday was Thursday)
- **Future:** Amanh√£ vai ser s√°bado (Tomorrow will be Saturday)

**Shortened Forms in Speech:**
Very common in Brazilian Portuguese:
- "Vou na segunda" (I'm going on Monday)
- "Trabalho de segunda a sexta" (I work Monday to Friday)
- "Tenho aula na ter√ßa" (I have class on Tuesday)
- Note: "-feira" is often dropped in everyday speech

**Weekend Expressions:**
- fim de semana (weekend)
- final de semana (weekend - alternative)
- no fim de semana (on/during the weekend)
- todo fim de semana (every weekend)
- este fim de semana (this weekend)
- no pr√≥ximo fim de semana (next weekend)

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 48: Time ‚Üí "Vou √†s tr√™s na segunda" (I'm going at 3 on Monday)
- Unit 26: Future ‚Üí "Vou viajar no s√°bado" (I'm going to travel on Saturday)
- Unit 34-42: Past tenses ‚Üí "Fui ao cinema no domingo" (I went to the movies on Sunday)
- Unit 15-45: Numbers ‚Üí ordinal origins (segunda = second, ter√ßa = third)

**Key Learning:**
- Days are masculine (o s√°bado, o domingo)
- "Feira" days can drop "-feira" in speech
- Use "na/no" for specific day, "√†s/aos" for recurring
- No article with "hoje" (hoje √© segunda)
- Essential for scheduling and planning

**Why This Unit:**
- **FOUNDATIONAL:** Days are essential for scheduling

### Unit 51: Months of the Year (Meses do Ano)
**New vocabulary:**
- **m√™s/meses** (month/months)
- **ano** (year)
- **Months:**
  - janeiro (January)
  - fevereiro (February)
  - mar√ßo (March)
  - abril (April)
  - maio (May)
  - junho (June)
  - julho (July)
  - agosto (August)
  - setembro (September)
  - outubro (October)
  - novembro (November)
  - dezembro (December)
- **pr√≥ximo/pr√≥xima** (next)
- **passado/passada** (last)
- **este/esta** (this)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Months are MASCULINE** (o janeiro, o maio)
- **Preposition "em" for "in"** a month:
  - em janeiro (in January)
  - em mar√ßo (in March)
- **NO article** needed: "em janeiro" NOT "no janeiro"
- **Capitalization:** Months are NOT capitalized in Portuguese (unlike English)
- **Dates use "de":** "5 de maio" (May 5th - literally "5 of May")

**Practice format:**
- "Meu anivers√°rio √© em junho" (My birthday is in June)
- "Estamos em outubro" (We are in October - literally "We are in October")
- "Vou viajar em dezembro" (I'm going to travel in December)
- "Nasci em mar√ßo" (I was born in March)
- "Em que m√™s voc√™ nasceu?" (In what month were you born?)

**Student can now:**
- Name all twelve months
- Say when birthdays occur (in which month)
- Say when events happen (in January, in July)
- Ask what month it is
- Express birth month
- Talk about past, present, and future months

**Typical sentences:**
- Meu anivers√°rio √© em maio (My birthday is in May)
- Estamos em novembro (We are in November / It is November)
- Vou viajar em julho (I'm going to travel in July)
- Nasci em mar√ßo de 1995 (I was born in March 1995)
- O ver√£o come√ßa em dezembro no Brasil (Summer starts in December in Brazil)
- Em que m√™s estamos? (What month is it?)
- Fa√ßo anivers√°rio em setembro (I have my birthday in September)
- O ano come√ßa em janeiro (The year starts in January)

**Months of the Year - Complete List:**
| Portuguese | English | Days | Season (Brazil) |
|------------|---------|------|-----------------|
| janeiro | January | 31 | Summer |
| fevereiro | February | 28/29 | Summer |
| mar√ßo | March | 31 | Autumn |
| abril | April | 30 | Autumn |
| maio | May | 31 | Autumn |
| junho | June | 30 | Winter |
| julho | July | 31 | Winter |
| agosto | August | 31 | Winter |
| setembro | September | 30 | Spring |
| outubro | October | 31 | Spring |
| novembro | November | 30 | Spring |
| dezembro | December | 31 | Summer |

**Cultural Note:**
- Brazil is in the Southern Hemisphere
- Seasons are opposite to Northern Hemisphere
- Summer: December-February
- Winter: June-August

**Prepositions with Months:**

**In a month:**
- **em** + month (NO article)
- Meu anivers√°rio √© **em** junho (My birthday is in June)
- Vou viajar **em** dezembro (I'm going to travel in December)
- Nasci **em** abril (I was born in April)

**This/next/last month:**
- este m√™s (this month)
- no m√™s que vem / no pr√≥ximo m√™s (next month)
- no m√™s passado (last month)
- em janeiro pr√≥ximo (next January)
- em mar√ßo passado (last March)

**Sample Conversations:**

**Conversation 1:**
- A: Em que m√™s voc√™ nasceu? (In what month were you born?)
- B: Nasci em agosto. E voc√™? (I was born in August. And you?)
- A: Em dezembro. Fa√ßo anivers√°rio no Natal! (In December. My birthday is at Christmas!)

**Conversation 2:**
- A: Quando voc√™ vai viajar? (When are you going to travel?)
- B: Vou viajar em julho. (I'm going to travel in July.)
- A: Para onde? (Where to?)
- B: Para a Europa. Em julho faz calor l√°. (To Europe. In July it's hot there.)

**Conversation 3:**
- A: Em que m√™s estamos? (What month is it?)
- B: Estamos em outubro. (It's October.)
- A: J√°? O ano est√° passando r√°pido! (Already? The year is passing quickly!)

**Common Patterns:**
- em + month: "em janeiro, em julho"
- Meu anivers√°rio √© em + month: "Meu anivers√°rio √© em maio"
- Nasci em + month (+ de + year): "Nasci em mar√ßo de 1990"
- Estamos em + month: "Estamos em outubro"
- Vou/Vamos em + month: "Vou viajar em dezembro"

**Asking about months:**
- Em que m√™s...? (In what month...?)
  - Em que m√™s voc√™ nasceu? (In what month were you born?)
  - Em que m√™s √© seu anivers√°rio? (In what month is your birthday?)
- Que m√™s √©? / Em que m√™s estamos? (What month is it?)

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ‚ùå "no janeiro" (wrong - no article needed)
- ‚úÖ "em janeiro" (correct)
- ‚ùå "em o mar√ßo" (wrong - no article)
- ‚úÖ "em mar√ßo" (correct)
- ‚ùå "Janeiro" (wrong - shouldn't be capitalized unless starting sentence)
- ‚úÖ "janeiro" (correct - lowercase in middle of sentence)
- ‚ùå "Nasci em o 1995" (wrong structure)
- ‚úÖ "Nasci em 1995" OR "Nasci em mar√ßo de 1995" (correct)

**Memory Aid for Months:**
Portuguese months are very similar to English:
- Janeiro = January
- Fevereiro = February
- Mar√ßo = March
- Abril = April
- Maio = May
- Junho = June
- Julho = July
- Agosto = August
- Setembro = September
- Outubro = October
- Novembro = November
- Dezembro = December

**Seasons in Brazil (opposite to Northern Hemisphere):**
- **Ver√£o** (Summer): dezembro, janeiro, fevereiro
- **Outono** (Autumn): mar√ßo, abril, maio
- **Inverno** (Winter): junho, julho, agosto
- **Primavera** (Spring): setembro, outubro, novembro

**With Different Tenses:**
- **Present:** "Estamos em outubro" (It's October)
- **Past:** "Nasci em mar√ßo" (I was born in March)
- **Future:** "Vou viajar em julho" (I'm going to travel in July)

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 17: Age ‚Üí "Nasci em maio de 1995" (I was born in May 1995)
- Unit 15-16: Numbers ‚Üí combined with months for dates
- Unit 29: Future ‚Üí "Vou viajar em dezembro"
- Unit 34-37: Past ‚Üí "Viajei em julho" (I traveled in July)

**Key Learning:**
- Months are masculine but use NO article with "em"
- Months are NOT capitalized (unless starting sentence)
- Use "em" (not "no") for months: "em janeiro"
- Essential for dates, birthdays, scheduling
- Seasons are opposite in Brazil (Southern Hemisphere)

**Why This Unit:**
- **FOUNDATIONAL:** Months are essential for dates and scheduling
- Natural progression: have days (Unit 50), now need months
- Ultra-granular: focuses ONLY on months of the year
- Practical: immediate use for birthdays, appointments, travel
- Prepares for complete dates (Unit 51: day + month + year)

### Unit 52: Dates (Calendar Dates - Dia, M√™s, Ano)
**New vocabulary:**
- **data** (date)
- **dia** (day - the number)
- **primeiro** (first - 1st of month)
- **hoje** (today)
- **amanh√£** (tomorrow)
- **ontem** (yesterday)
- **Que dia √© hoje?** (What's today's date?)
- **quando** (when)
- **nascimento** (birth)
- **data de nascimento** (date of birth)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Date format:** day + de + month + de + year
  - 5 de maio de 2024 (May 5, 2024)
- **First of month:** Use "primeiro" NOT "um"
  - 1 de janeiro (January 1st - literally "first of January")
  - primeiro de janeiro (January 1st)
- **All other days:** Use cardinal numbers (dois, tr√™s, quatro...)
  - 2 de janeiro (January 2nd)
  - 15 de mar√ßo (March 15th)
- **Question:** Que dia √© hoje? (What's today's date?)
- **Answer:** Hoje √© [day] de [month] (Today is [month] [day])
- **Written format:** dd/mm/yyyy (day/month/year - opposite of US!)
  - 05/05/2024 = May 5, 2024
  - 25/12/2024 = December 25, 2024

**Practice format:**
- "Hoje √© 15 de outubro" (Today is October 15th)
- "Meu anivers√°rio √© no dia 3 de junho" (My birthday is on June 3rd)
- "Nasci em 20 de mar√ßo de 1995" (I was born on March 20, 1995)
- "Que dia √© hoje?" "Hoje √© primeiro de maio" (What's today's date? Today is May 1st)
- "A reuni√£o √© no dia 10" (The meeting is on the 10th)

**Student can now:**
- Give today's complete date
- State their birth date
- Schedule events with full dates
- Read and write dates in Portuguese format (dd/mm/yyyy)
- Use "primeiro" for the 1st of any month
- Express dates in past, present, and future

**Typical sentences:**
- Hoje √© 25 de novembro de 2024 (Today is November 25, 2024)
- Meu anivers√°rio √© em 10 de julho (My birthday is on July 10th)
- Nasci no dia 5 de mar√ßo de 1990 (I was born on March 5, 1990)
- A reuni√£o √© no dia primeiro de dezembro (The meeting is on December 1st)
- Vou viajar no dia 20 de junho (I'm going to travel on June 20th)
- Que dia √© hoje? (What's today's date?)
- O Natal √© no dia 25 de dezembro (Christmas is on December 25th)
- O Ano Novo √© primeiro de janeiro (New Year's is January 1st)

**Date Structure - Complete Format:**
| Element | Portuguese | Example |
|---------|------------|---------|
| Day (1st only) | primeiro de | primeiro de janeiro |
| Day (2-31) | [number] de | 15 de outubro |
| Month | [month name] | maio, dezembro |
| Year | de [year] | de 2024 |
| Complete | day de month de year | 5 de maio de 2024 |

**First of the Month - SPECIAL RULE:**
- ‚úÖ primeiro de janeiro (January 1st)
- ‚úÖ 1¬∫ de janeiro (January 1st - written)
- ‚ùå um de janeiro (WRONG - don't use "um")
- ‚úÖ primeiro de maio (May 1st)
- ‚úÖ 1¬∫ de maio (May 1st)

**All Other Days:**
- 2 de janeiro (January 2nd)
- 15 de mar√ßo (March 15th)
- 30 de abril (April 30th)
- Use regular cardinal numbers (dois, tr√™s, quinze, trinta...)

**Written Formats:**
- **Numeric:** dd/mm/yyyy
  - 05/05/2024 = May 5, 2024
  - 25/12/2024 = December 25, 2024
  - 01/01/2025 = January 1, 2025
- **With words:** [day] de [month] de [year]
  - 5 de maio de 2024
  - 25 de dezembro de 2024
- **Abbreviated (common in writing):**
  - 5/5/24
  - 25/12/24

**CRITICAL: Date Format Difference:**
- **Portuguese (and most of world):** dd/mm/yyyy (day first)
- **US format:** mm/dd/yyyy (month first)
- **Example:** 05/06/2024
  - Portuguese: June 5, 2024
  - US: May 6, 2024
  - **Be careful!**

**Sample Conversations:**

**Conversation 1:**
- A: Que dia √© hoje? (What's today's date?)
- B: Hoje √© 15 de outubro. (Today is October 15th.)
- A: E amanh√£? (And tomorrow?)
- B: Amanh√£ √© 16 de outubro. (Tomorrow is October 16th.)

**Conversation 2:**
- A: Quando √© seu anivers√°rio? (When is your birthday?)
- B: √â no dia 3 de junho. (It's on June 3rd.)
- A: Em que ano voc√™ nasceu? (What year were you born?)
- B: Nasci em 1995. (I was born in 1995.)
- A: Ent√£o sua data de nascimento completa √©...? (So your complete birth date is...?)
- B: 3 de junho de 1995. (June 3, 1995.)

**Conversation 3:**
- A: Quando come√ßa o curso? (When does the course start?)
- B: Come√ßa no dia primeiro de setembro. (It starts on September 1st.)

- B: Termina no dia 20 de dezembro. (It ends on December 20th.)

**Common Patterns:**
- Hoje √© + date: "Hoje √© 15 de maio"
- Amanh√£ √© + date: "Amanh√£ √© 16 de maio"
- Ontem foi + date: "Ontem foi 14 de maio"

**Asking about dates:**
- Que dia √© hoje? (What's today's date?)
- Quando √©...? (When is...?)
  - Quando √© seu anivers√°rio? (When is your birthday?)
  - Quando √© a reuni√£o? (When is the meeting?)
- Em que dia...? (On what day...?)
  - Em que dia voc√™ viaja? (On what day do you travel?)
- Qual √© a data? (What's the date?)
- Qual √© sua data de nascimento? (What's your date of birth?)

**Important Holidays with Dates:**
- Ano Novo: primeiro de janeiro (New Year's: January 1st)
- Dia de S√£o Valentim: 12 de junho no Brasil (Valentine's Day: June 12 in Brazil - NOT February 14!)
- Dia da Independ√™ncia: 7 de setembro (Independence Day: September 7)
- Natal: 25 de dezembro (Christmas: December 25)
- Carnaval: data m√≥vel (Carnival: moveable date - Feb/March)

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ‚ùå "um de janeiro" (wrong - use "primeiro")
- ‚úÖ "primeiro de janeiro" (correct)
- ‚ùå "15 maio" (wrong - missing "de")
- ‚úÖ "15 de maio" (correct)
- ‚ùå "maio 15" (wrong - wrong order)
- ‚úÖ "15 de maio" (correct - day before month)
- ‚ùå "no 15 de maio" (wrong - use "no dia" or nothing)
- ‚úÖ "em 15 de maio" OR "no dia 15 de maio" (correct)
- ‚ùå "05/14/2024" (wrong - this is US format)
- ‚úÖ "14/05/2024" (correct - Portuguese format)

**With Different Tenses:**
- **Present:** "Hoje √© 20 de mar√ßo" (Today is March 20)
- **Past:** "Nasci em 5 de maio de 1990" (I was born on May 5, 1990)
- **Future:** "Vou viajar no dia 15 de julho" (I'm going to travel on July 15)

**Prepositions with Dates:**
- **em** + date: "em 15 de maio" (on May 15)
- **no dia** + date: "no dia 15 de maio" (on May 15 - more specific)
- **de** connecting elements: "15 **de** maio **de** 2024"

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 15-16: Numbers ‚Üí day numbers
- Unit 50: Days of week ‚Üí "segunda, 15 de maio" (Monday, May 15)

- Unit 17: Age ‚Üí "Nasci em 5 de mar√ßo de 1995"
- Unit 53 (next): Ordinal numbers ‚Üí "primeiro" is ordinal!

**Key Learning:**
- Format: day + de + month + de + year
- Use "primeiro" for 1st of month, regular numbers for 2-31
- Written format: dd/mm/yyyy (day first!)
- No article usually: "em 15 de maio"
- Essential for birthdays, appointments, official documents

**Why This Unit:**
- **FOUNDATIONAL:** Dates are essential for all scheduling
- Natural progression: have days (49) and months (50), now combine them
- Ultra-granular: focuses ONLY on calendar dates

### Unit 53: Ordinal Numbers (Primeiro, Segundo, Terceiro...)
**New vocabulary:**
- **Ordinal numbers 1st-10th:**
  - primeiro/primeira (first - 1st)
  - segundo/segunda (second - 2nd)
  - terceiro/terceira (third - 3rd)
  - quarto/quarta (fourth - 4th)
  - quinto/quinta (fifth - 5th)
  - sexto/sexta (sixth - 6th)
  - s√©timo/s√©tima (seventh - 7th)
  - oitavo/oitava (eighth - 8th)
  - nono/nona (ninth - 9th)
  - d√©cimo/d√©cima (tenth - 10th)
- **andar** (floor - in building)
- **lugar** (place, position)
- **posi√ß√£o** (position)
- **classifica√ß√£o** (ranking, classification)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Ordinal numbers have gender agreement:** primeiro/primeira, segundo/segunda
- **Used for:**
  - Floors: "primeiro andar" (first floor), "terceiro andar" (third floor)
  - Dates: "primeiro de maio" (May 1st) - ONLY for 1st of month!
  - Positions: "primeiro lugar" (first place)
  - Sequences: "a primeira vez" (the first time)
  - Royalty: "Dom Pedro Segundo" (Dom Pedro the Second)
- **Position:** ordinal + noun (like other adjectives)
- **Abbreviations:** 1¬∫ (masc), 1¬™ (fem), 2¬∫, 3¬∫, etc.
- **After 10th:** Usually use cardinal numbers instead
  - o d√©cimo primeiro andar (11th floor - formal)
  - o andar onze (floor 11 - more common)

**Practice format:**
- "Moro no terceiro andar" (I live on the third floor)
- "Primeiro de janeiro" (January 1st)
- "Esta √© minha segunda vez no Brasil" (This is my second time in Brazil)
- "Ele ficou em primeiro lugar" (He came in first place)
- "A primeira aula √© √†s 9h" (The first class is at 9 AM)

**Student can now:**
- Use ordinal numbers for floors (1st-10th)
- Use "primeiro" for 1st of any month (from Unit 52)
- Express positions and rankings
- Describe sequences (first time, second attempt, etc.)
- Understand ordinal abbreviations (1¬∫, 2¬™, 3¬∫)
- Apply correct gender agreement

**Typical sentences:**
- Moro no segundo andar (I live on the second floor)
- O escrit√≥rio fica no quinto andar (The office is on the fifth floor)
- Esta √© minha primeira vez aqui (This is my first time here)
- Ele √© o terceiro da fila (He's third in line)
- A segunda porta √† esquerda (The second door on the left)
- O primeiro dia de aula (The first day of class)
- Fiquei em quarto lugar (I came in fourth place)
- Vou pela terceira vez (I'm going for the third time)

**Ordinal Numbers - Complete List (1st-10th):**
| Number | Masculine | Feminine | Abbreviation | Example |
|--------|-----------|----------|--------------|---------|
| 1st | primeiro | primeira | 1¬∫ / 1¬™ | primeiro lugar |
| 2nd | segundo | segunda | 2¬∫ / 2¬™ | segunda vez |
| 3rd | terceiro | terceira | 3¬∫ / 3¬™ | terceiro andar |
| 4th | quarto | quarta | 4¬∫ / 4¬™ | quarta posi√ß√£o |
| 5th | quinto | quinta | 5¬∫ / 5¬™ | quinto lugar |
| 6th | sexto | sexta | 6¬∫ / 6¬™ | sexta tentativa |
| 7th | s√©timo | s√©tima | 7¬∫ / 7¬™ | s√©timo andar |
| 8th | oitavo | oitava | 8¬∫ / 8¬™ | oitava s√©rie |
| 9th | nono | nona | 9¬∫ / 9¬™ | nono m√™s |
| 10th | d√©cimo | d√©cima | 10¬∫ / 10¬™ | d√©cimo lugar |

**Gender Agreement Examples:**
- **Masculine nouns:**
  - o primeiro andar (the first floor)
  - o segundo lugar (second place)
  - o terceiro m√™s (the third month)
- **Feminine nouns:**
  - a primeira vez (the first time)
  - a segunda porta (the second door)
  - a terceira tentativa (the third attempt)

**Common Uses:**

**Floors (andares):**
- t√©rreo (ground floor - British: ground floor, US: first floor)
- primeiro andar (first floor - British: first floor, US: second floor)
- segundo andar (second floor)
- terceiro andar (third floor)
- Note: Brazil follows European convention (ground floor is t√©rreo, not primeiro)

**Dates (only 1st of month):**
- primeiro de janeiro (January 1st)
- primeiro de maio (May 1st)
- primeiro de dezembro (December 1st)
- All other days use cardinal numbers: 2, 3, 4, 5...

**Positions/Rankings:**
- primeiro lugar (first place)
- segundo lugar (second place)
- terceiro lugar (third place)
- quarto colocado (fourth place)

**Sequences:**
- a primeira vez (the first time)
- a segunda tentativa (the second attempt)
- o terceiro dia (the third day)
- a quarta semana (the fourth week)

**Sample Conversations:**

**Conversation 1:**
- A: Em que andar voc√™ mora? (What floor do you live on?)
- B: Moro no quinto andar. (I live on the fifth floor.)
- A: Tem elevador? (Is there an elevator?)
- B: Tem, sim. (Yes, there is.)

**Conversation 2:**
- A: Esta √© sua primeira vez no Brasil? (Is this your first time in Brazil?)
- B: N√£o, √© minha terceira vez. (No, it's my third time.)
- A: Voc√™ gosta? (Do you like it?)
- B: Amo! Por isso volto sempre. (I love it! That's why I always come back.)

**Conversation 3:**
- A: Em que lugar voc√™ ficou na corrida? (What place did you get in the race?)
- B: Fiquei em segundo lugar! (I came in second place!)
- A: Parab√©ns! Quase ganhou! (Congratulations! You almost won!)

**Connection to Days of the Week (Unit 50):**
Notice the pattern:
- segunda-feira = "second fair" (Monday)
- ter√ßa-feira = "third fair" (Tuesday)
- quarta-feira = "fourth fair" (Wednesday)
- quinta-feira = "fifth fair" (Thursday)
- sexta-feira = "sixth fair" (Friday)

These use feminine ordinal forms because "feira" is feminine!

**Common Patterns:**
- no + ordinal + andar: "no terceiro andar" (on the third floor)
- em + ordinal + lugar: "em primeiro lugar" (in first place)
- a/o + ordinal + vez: "a primeira vez" (the first time)
- ordinal + de + month: "primeiro de maio" (May 1st)

**After 10th (less common):**
Most Brazilians use cardinal numbers after 10th:
- ‚úÖ o andar onze (the 11th floor - more common)
- ‚úÖ o d√©cimo primeiro andar (the 11th floor - more formal)
- ‚úÖ o andar doze (the 12th floor)
- ‚úÖ o vig√©simo andar (the 20th floor - very formal, rare)

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ‚ùå "primeiro vez" (wrong - vez is feminine)
- ‚úÖ "primeira vez" (correct)
- ‚ùå "segunda lugar" (wrong - lugar is masculine)
- ‚úÖ "segundo lugar" (correct)
- ‚ùå "o andar primeiro" (wrong - ordinal before noun)
- ‚úÖ "o primeiro andar" (correct - ordinal before noun like other adjectives)
- ‚ùå "dois de janeiro" (wrong - use ordinal for 1st of month)
- ‚úÖ "primeiro de janeiro" (correct for January 1st)
- ‚úÖ "dois de fevereiro" (correct for February 2nd - cardinal OK for 2-31)

**Abbreviations in Writing:**
- 1¬∫ andar (primeiro andar - masculine)
- 1¬™ vez (primeira vez - feminine)
- 3¬∫ lugar (terceiro lugar)
- 5¬™ posi√ß√£o (quinta posi√ß√£o)

**With Different Tenses:**
- **Present:** "Moro no terceiro andar" (I live on the third floor)
- **Past:** "Foi minha primeira vez" (It was my first time)
- **Future:** "Vai ser meu segundo ano" (It's going to be my second year)

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 49: Days of the week ‚Üí segunda-feira, ter√ßa-feira use ordinals!
- Unit 51: Dates ‚Üí "primeiro de maio" (May 1st)
- Unit 15-45: Cardinal numbers ‚Üí ordinals are related forms
- Unit 43: Comparatives ‚Üí "o mais alto" vs "o primeiro" (different concepts)

**Key Learning:**
- Ordinals have gender (primeiro/primeira, segundo/segunda)
- Used for floors, 1st of month, positions, sequences
- After 10th, usually switch to cardinal numbers
- Position before noun (like other adjectives)
- Essential for addresses (floors) and sequences

**Why This Unit:**
- Natural progression: learned cardinal numbers (44-45), now ordinals
- Ultra-granular: focuses ONLY on ordinal numbers
- Practical: essential for addresses (floors), dates (1st of month), positions
- Connects to days of the week (segunda = second, ter√ßa = third)
- Completes number system (cardinal + ordinal)

### Unit 54: Weather Expressions (Tempo e Clima)
**New vocabulary:**
- **tempo** (weather)
- **clima** (climate)
- **Weather expressions with FAZER:**
  - faz calor (it's hot)
  - faz frio (it's cold)
  - faz sol (it's sunny)
  - faz vento (it's windy)
- **Weather with ESTAR:**
  - est√° quente (it's hot/warm)
  - est√° frio (it's cold)
  - est√° nublado (it's cloudy)
  - est√° ensolarado (it's sunny)
- **Weather verbs:**
  - chove / est√° chovendo (it's raining)
  - neva / est√° nevando (it's snowing - rare in Brazil!)
- **Temperature:**
  - graus (degrees)
  - calor (heat)
  - frio (cold)
  - quente (hot)
- **Adjectives:**
  - √∫mido (humid)
  - seco (dry)
  - agrad√°vel (pleasant)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **FAZER for general weather:** Faz calor (It's hot)
  - Impersonal use of fazer (3rd person singular only)
  - No subject needed
- **ESTAR for current conditions:** Est√° quente (It's warm)
  - Describes current state
- **Weather verbs (impersonal):** Chove (It rains) / Est√° chovendo (It's raining)
- **Preposition "em":** "No Brasil faz calor" (In Brazil it's hot)
- **Degrees:** "Est√° 30 graus" (It's 30 degrees)

**Practice format:**
- "Como est√° o tempo?" "Est√° quente" (How's the weather? It's warm)
- "Que tempo faz?" "Faz sol" (What's the weather like? It's sunny)
- "Hoje faz frio" (Today it's cold)
- "Est√° chovendo" (It's raining)
- "No ver√£o faz muito calor" (In summer it's very hot)

**Student can now:**
- Ask about the weather
- Describe current weather conditions
- Use FAZER vs ESTAR correctly for weather
- Talk about temperature
- Describe seasons and their typical weather
- Express weather in different tenses

**Typical sentences:**
- Faz calor hoje (It's hot today)
- Est√° chovendo (It's raining)
- Como est√° o tempo? (How's the weather?)
- Faz muito frio no inverno (It's very cold in winter)
- Est√° quente e √∫mido (It's hot and humid)
- Que tempo faz a√≠? (What's the weather like there?)
- Est√° 35 graus (It's 35 degrees)
- Faz sol o ano todo (It's sunny all year round)
- No Rio sempre faz calor (In Rio it's always hot)

**Weather Expressions - Complete System:**

**With FAZER (general, habitual):**
- Faz calor (It's hot)
- Faz frio (It's cold)
- Faz sol (It's sunny)
- Faz vento (It's windy)
- Faz bom tempo (The weather is nice)
- Faz mau tempo (The weather is bad)

**With ESTAR (current state):**
- Est√° quente (It's warm/hot)
- Est√° frio (It's cold)
- Est√° nublado (It's cloudy)
- Est√° ensolarado (It's sunny)
- Est√° √∫mido (It's humid)
- Est√° agrad√°vel (It's pleasant)

**Weather verbs:**
- Chove (It rains) - general
- Est√° chovendo (It's raining) - right now
- Choveu (It rained) - past
- Vai chover (It's going to rain) - future
- Neva (It snows) - very rare in Brazil!
- Est√° nevando (It's snowing)

**FAZER vs ESTAR - When to use which:**

**Use FAZER for:**
- General climate: "No Brasil faz calor" (In Brazil it's hot)
- Habitual weather: "No inverno faz frio" (In winter it's cold)
- Natural phenomena: "Faz sol" (It's sunny), "Faz vento" (It's windy)

**Use ESTAR for:**
- Current conditions: "Hoje est√° quente" (Today it's warm)
- Temporary state: "Est√° nublado agora" (It's cloudy now)
- Progressive: "Est√° chovendo" (It's raining - right now)

**Both can be correct!**
- Faz calor = It's hot (in general)
- Est√° quente = It's warm/hot (right now)

**Temperature:**
- Est√° [number] graus (It's [number] degrees)
- Est√° 30 graus (It's 30 degrees)
- Est√° fazendo 25 graus (It's 25 degrees - combining fazer + estar)
- Brazil uses Celsius, not Fahrenheit!

**Seasons and Weather (Brazil):**
- **Ver√£o** (Summer - Dec/Jan/Feb): Faz muito calor, est√° quente
- **Outono** (Autumn - Mar/Apr/May): Est√° agrad√°vel, faz sol
- **Inverno** (Winter - Jun/Jul/Aug): Faz frio no sul, mas calor no norte
- **Primavera** (Spring - Sep/Oct/Nov): Faz bom tempo, est√° agrad√°vel

**Sample Conversations:**

**Conversation 1:**
- A: Como est√° o tempo a√≠? (How's the weather there?)
- B: Est√° chovendo muito. (It's raining a lot.)
- A: Aqui faz sol. Est√° muito calor! (Here it's sunny. It's very hot!)

**Conversation 2:**
- A: Que tempo faz no Brasil? (What's the weather like in Brazil?)
- B: Depende. No norte faz calor o ano todo, mas no sul faz frio no inverno. (It depends. In the north it's hot all year, but in the south it's cold in winter.)
- A: E no Rio? (And in Rio?)
- B: No Rio sempre faz calor! (In Rio it's always hot!)

**Conversation 3:**
- A: Vai chover amanh√£? (Is it going to rain tomorrow?)
- B: Acho que sim. Est√° muito nublado. (I think so. It's very cloudy.)
- A: Ent√£o vou levar guarda-chuva. (Then I'll take an umbrella.)

**Common Patterns:**
- Faz + noun: "Faz calor, faz frio, faz sol, faz vento"
- Est√° + adjective: "Est√° quente, est√° frio, est√° nublado"
- Est√° + gerund: "Est√° chovendo, est√° nevando"
- Como est√° o tempo? (How's the weather?)
- Que tempo faz? (What's the weather like?)

**Asking about weather:**
- Como est√° o tempo? (How's the weather? - current)
- Que tempo faz? (What's the weather like? - general)
- Vai chover? (Is it going to rain?)
- Est√° quente a√≠? (Is it hot there?)
- Faz frio no inverno? (Is it cold in winter?)

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ‚ùå "Est√° calor" (wrong - calor is noun)
- ‚úÖ "Faz calor" OR "Est√° quente" (correct)
- ‚ùå "Faz chovendo" (wrong - can't combine fazer with gerund for rain)
- ‚úÖ "Est√° chovendo" OR "Chove" (correct)
- ‚ùå "Eu fa√ßo calor" (wrong - weather fazer is impersonal)
- ‚úÖ "Faz calor" (correct - no subject)
- ‚ùå "Tenho calor" (means "I'm hot" - about you, not weather)
- ‚úÖ "Faz calor" (correct - for weather)

**Brazilian Weather Notes:**
- Most of Brazil is tropical - hot year-round
- Only the south gets cold winters
- Snow is VERY rare (only in some southern mountains)
- Coastal cities are humid
- Amazon region is hot and rainy
- Northeast is hot and dry

**With Different Tenses:**
- **Present:** "Faz calor" (It's hot)
- **Past:** "Fez muito calor ontem" (It was very hot yesterday)
- **Future:** "Vai fazer frio amanh√£" (It's going to be cold tomorrow)
- **Imperfect:** "Fazia frio quando eu morava l√°" (It was cold when I lived there)

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 51: Months ‚Üí "Em janeiro faz calor" (In January it's hot)
- Unit 50: Days ‚Üí "Na segunda vai chover" (On Monday it's going to rain)
- Unit 45-46: Imperfect ‚Üí "Fazia frio" (It was cold - habitual past)
- Unit 29: Future ‚Üí "Vai chover" (It's going to rain)

**Key Learning:**
- FAZER for weather conditions (faz calor, faz frio, faz sol)
- ESTAR for current state (est√° quente, est√° chovendo)
- Weather expressions are impersonal (no subject)
- Temperature uses estar + degrees
- Essential for daily conversation and travel

**Why This Unit:**
- **FOUNDATIONAL:** Weather is daily conversation topic
- Natural progression: have time/dates, now discuss weather
- Ultra-granular: focuses ONLY on weather expressions
- Practical: immediate use for conversation, planning, travel
- Introduces important FAZER construction (different from possession)

### Unit 55: Colors (Cores B√°sicas)

**New vocabulary:**
- **Basic colors:**
  - branco/branca (white)
  - preto/preta (black)
  - vermelho/vermelha (red)
  - azul (blue)
  - verde (green)
  - amarelo/amarela (yellow)
  - laranja (orange - invariable)
  - rosa (pink - invariable)
  - marrom (brown - invariable)
  - cinza (gray - invariable)
  - roxo/roxa (purple)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Color adjectives agree in gender and number with the noun:**
  - o carro **vermelho** (the red car - masculine)
  - a casa **vermelha** (the red house - feminine)
  - os carros **vermelhos** (the red cars - masculine plural)
  - as casas **vermelhas** (the red houses - feminine plural)

- **EXCEPTION: Invariable colors (no gender/number change):**
  - **laranja** (orange): uma casa laranja, um carro laranja
  - **rosa** (pink): uma casa rosa, um carro rosa
  - **marrom** (brown): uma casa marrom, um carro marrom
  - **cinza** (gray): uma casa cinza, um carro cinza

- **Color placement:** Colors come AFTER the noun in Portuguese
  - ‚úÖ carro azul (blue car)
  - ‚ùå azul carro (wrong word order)

- **Asking about color:** De que cor √©? (What color is it?)
  - De que cor √© o carro? (What color is the car?)
  - √â azul. (It's blue.)

**Practice format:**
- Describe objects by color: "A casa √© branca"
- Answer color questions: "De que cor √© o livro?" ‚Üí "√â vermelho"
- Match nouns with correct color agreement
- Identify objects: "Qual √© azul?" (Which one is blue?)
- Practice with clothing: "A camisa √© verde" (The shirt is green)

**Student can now:**
- Name 11 basic colors
- Describe objects by color with correct agreement
- Ask what color something is
- Combine colors with previously learned nouns (casa, carro, livro, etc.)
- Make simple statements about color preferences

**Typical sentences:**
- A casa √© branca. (The house is white.)
- O carro √© azul. (The car is blue.)
- De que cor √© a camisa? (What color is the shirt?)
- Meu livro √© verde. (My book is green.)
- A porta √© marrom. (The door is brown.)
- Eu gosto de vermelho. (I like red.)
- As flores s√£o rosas. (The flowers are pink.)

**Sample conversation:**
```
A: De que cor √© sua casa?
   (What color is your house?)
B: √â branca com portas verdes.
   (It's white with green doors.)

A: E seu carro?
   (And your car?)
B: √â azul.
   (It's blue.)

A: Qual √© sua cor favorita?
   (What's your favorite color?)
B: Eu gosto de azul e verde.
   (I like blue and green.)
```

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ‚ùå "O vermelho carro" (wrong word order)
- ‚úÖ "O carro vermelho" (correct - color after noun)
- ‚ùå "A casa laranjo" (wrong - laranja doesn't change)
- ‚úÖ "A casa laranja" (correct - invariable)
- ‚ùå "A casas vermelha" (wrong agreement)
- ‚úÖ "As casas vermelhas" (correct - plural agreement)
- ‚ùå "√â de azul" (wrong - extra "de")
- ‚úÖ "√â azul" (correct - no preposition needed)

**Why These Colors Are Invariable:**
- **laranja, rosa, marrom, cinza** are invariable because they originated as nouns:
  - laranja = orange (the fruit)
  - rosa = rose (the flower)
  - marrom = French "marron" (chestnut)
  - cinza = ash
- When nouns are used as color adjectives, they don't change form

**Additional Color Shades (for recognition):**
- claro (light): azul claro (light blue)
- escuro (dark): azul escuro (dark blue)
- Note: claro/escuro DO agree with noun

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 6: Regular adjectives ‚Üí colors follow same agreement rules
- Unit 3: Articles ‚Üí "o carro vermelho" uses articles learned
- Unit 14: Possessives ‚Üí "meu carro √© azul"
- Unit 25: Gostar de ‚Üí "Eu gosto de vermelho"

**Key Learning:**
- 11 basic colors in Portuguese
- Colors come AFTER the noun (opposite of English sometimes)
- Most colors agree in gender/number with the noun
- Four colors are invariable: laranja, rosa, marrom, cinza
- Essential descriptive vocabulary for everyday communication

**Why This Unit:**
- **FOUNDATIONAL:** Colors are basic descriptive vocabulary
- Natural progression: can describe objects, now add color
- Ultra-granular: focuses ONLY on colors and color agreement
- Practical: immediate use for describing anything
- Reinforces adjective agreement patterns from Unit 6

### Unit 56: Clothing Basics (Roupas B√°sicas)

**New vocabulary:**
- **Essential clothing items:**
  - a camisa (shirt - feminine!)
  - a camiseta (t-shirt - feminine)
  - a cal√ßa (pants - singular in Portuguese!)
  - a saia (skirt)
  - o vestido (dress)
  - o casaco (jacket/coat)
  - o sapato (shoe)
  - a meia (sock)
  - o chap√©u (hat)
  - os √≥culos (glasses - always plural)
  - a roupa (clothing - singular means "clothes")

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Gender surprises in clothing:**
  - **camisa is FEMININE** even though it often refers to men's shirts
  - **vestido is MASCULINE** even though dresses are typically worn by women
  - Gender is about the word, not who wears it!

- **Singular/Plural differences from English:**
  - **cal√ßa** (pants) is SINGULAR in Portuguese:
    - ‚úÖ "Eu uso **uma** cal√ßa" (I'm wearing pants)
    - ‚ùå "Eu uso cal√ßas" (sounds like multiple pairs)
  - **√≥culos** (glasses) is PLURAL in both languages:
    - "Eu uso √≥culos" (I wear glasses)

- **Wearing/Using:** USAR (to wear/use)
  - Eu uso uma camisa. (I'm wearing a shirt.)
  - Voc√™ usa √≥culos? (Do you wear glasses?)
  - Ela usa vestido. (She's wearing a dress.)

- **Verbs for getting dressed:**
  - **vestir** (to dress/wear): Eu visto uma camisa. (I put on/wear a shirt.)
  - **usar** (to use/wear): Eu uso sapatos. (I wear shoes.)
  - More common: usar (simpler, more versatile)

**Practice format:**
- Name clothing items with correct articles
- Describe what someone is wearing: "Ela usa uma saia azul"
- Practice with colors: "A camisa √© verde"
- Answer questions: "O que voc√™ est√° usando?" (What are you wearing?)
- Combine possessives: "meu sapato" (my shoe)

**Student can now:**
- Name 11 essential clothing items
- Use correct gender for clothing vocabulary
- Describe what they're wearing with USAR
- Combine clothing with colors from Unit 55
- Ask what others are wearing

**Typical sentences:**
- Eu uso uma camisa branca. (I'm wearing a white shirt.)
- Ela usa um vestido vermelho. (She's wearing a red dress.)
- Voc√™ usa √≥culos? (Do you wear glasses?)
- Meu sapato √© preto. (My shoe is black.)
- Ele usa uma cal√ßa azul. (He's wearing blue pants.)
- Eu preciso de um casaco. (I need a jacket.)
- A saia √© verde. (The skirt is green.)

**Sample conversation:**
```
A: O que voc√™ est√° usando hoje?
   (What are you wearing today?)
B: Eu uso uma camiseta azul e uma cal√ßa preta.
   (I'm wearing a blue t-shirt and black pants.)

A: E sapatos?
   (And shoes?)
B: Meus sapatos s√£o brancos.
   (My shoes are white.)

A: Voc√™ precisa de um casaco?
   (Do you need a jacket?)
B: N√£o, est√° quente hoje.
   (No, it's hot today.)
```

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ‚ùå "O camisa" (wrong - camisa is feminine)
- ‚úÖ "A camisa" (correct)
- ‚ùå "A vestido" (wrong - vestido is masculine)
- ‚úÖ "O vestido" (correct)
- ‚ùå "Eu uso cal√ßas" (sounds like multiple pairs)
- ‚úÖ "Eu uso uma cal√ßa" (correct - singular)
- ‚ùå "Eu uso um √≥culos" (wrong - √≥culos is plural)
- ‚úÖ "Eu uso √≥culos" (correct - no article with plural)

**Why CAMISA is Feminine:**
- Historical linguistic reasons
- Gender is arbitrary for many words
- Don't try to guess based on who wears it!
- Must memorize gender for each clothing item

**Shopping Phrases (for recognition):**
- Quanto custa? (How much does it cost?)
- Posso experimentar? (Can I try it on?)
- Tem no tamanho M? (Do you have it in size M?)
- Fica bem. (It fits well./It looks good.)

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 54: Colors ‚Üí "uma camisa verde" (a green shirt)
- Unit 3: Articles ‚Üí correct gender for each item
- Unit 14: Possessives ‚Üí "meu sapato" (my shoe)
- Unit 16: Precisar de ‚Üí "Eu preciso de um casaco" (I need a jacket)
- Unit 53: Weather ‚Üí "Est√° frio, eu uso um casaco" (It's cold, I'm wearing a jacket)

**Key Learning:**
- 11 essential clothing vocabulary items
- CAMISA is feminine, VESTIDO is masculine (counter-intuitive!)
- CAL√áA (pants) is singular in Portuguese
- USAR (to wear/use) is the most common verb for wearing clothes
- Combine clothing + colors for rich descriptions

**Why This Unit:**
- **FOUNDATIONAL:** Clothing is everyday vocabulary
- Natural progression: have colors, now apply to clothing
- Ultra-granular: focuses ONLY on basic clothing items
- Practical: immediate use for describing appearance, shopping
- Reinforces gender agreement with concrete vocabulary

### Unit 57: Body Parts (Partes do Corpo)

**New vocabulary:**
- **Basic body parts:**
  - a cabe√ßa (head)
  - o cabelo (hair)
  - o olho (eye)
  - a orelha (ear)
  - o nariz (nose)
  - a boca (mouth)
  - o dente (tooth)
  - o bra√ßo (arm)
  - a m√£o (hand)
  - o dedo (finger/toe)
  - a perna (leg)
  - o p√© (foot)
  - a barriga (belly/stomach)
  - as costas (back - always plural)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Plural forms with body parts:**
  - **os olhos** (eyes - plural)
  - **as m√£os** (hands - irregular plural! not "maos")
  - **os p√©s** (feet - irregular plural! not "pes")
  - **as costas** (back - ALWAYS plural in Portuguese)

- **Describing pain/problems with body parts:**
  - Use DOER (to hurt) - special verb:
    - "**Meu** bra√ßo **d√≥i**" (My arm hurts)
    - "**Minha** cabe√ßa **d√≥i**" (My head hurts)
    - "**Meus** olhos **doem**" (My eyes hurt - plural verb!)
  - Structure: possessive + body part + doer (conjugated)

- **The verb DOER (to hurt):**
  - 3rd person ONLY (body part is the subject doing the hurting)
  - **Singular:** d√≥i (one thing hurts)
  - **Plural:** doem (multiple things hurt)
  - Examples:
    - O p√© d√≥i. (The foot hurts.)
    - Os p√©s doem. (The feet hurt.)

**Practice format:**
- Name body parts with correct articles
- Practice plural forms (especially m√£os, p√©s)
- Describe pain: "Minha cabe√ßa d√≥i"
- Point to body parts: "Onde est√° o nariz?" ‚Üí "Aqui!"
- Combine with colors: "Meu cabelo √© preto"

**Student can now:**
- Name 14 essential body parts
- Use correct irregular plurals (m√£os, p√©s)
- Describe pain or problems with body parts
- Use the verb DOER correctly with body parts
- Describe physical features (hair color, eye color)

**Typical sentences:**
- Minha cabe√ßa d√≥i. (My head hurts.)
- Meus olhos s√£o azuis. (My eyes are blue.)
- Meu cabelo √© preto. (My hair is black.)
- Meus p√©s doem. (My feet hurt.)
- Eu tenho dor de barriga. (I have a stomachache.)
- Minhas m√£os s√£o pequenas. (My hands are small.)
- O bra√ßo dele d√≥i. (His arm hurts.)

**Sample conversation:**
```
A: Como voc√™ est√°?
   (How are you?)
B: N√£o estou bem. Minha cabe√ßa d√≥i.
   (I'm not well. My head hurts.)

A: Voc√™ tem febre?
   (Do you have a fever?)
B: N√£o, mas minha barriga d√≥i tamb√©m.
   (No, but my stomach hurts too.)

A: Voc√™ precisa de um m√©dico.
   (You need a doctor.)
```

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ‚ùå "Minhas maos" (wrong plural)
- ‚úÖ "Minhas m√£os" (correct - irregular)
- ‚ùå "Meus pes" (wrong plural)
- ‚úÖ "Meus p√©s" (correct - irregular)
- ‚ùå "Minha costa" (wrong - back is always plural)
- ‚úÖ "Minhas costas" (correct)
- ‚ùå "Eu doi minha cabe√ßa" (wrong structure)
- ‚úÖ "Minha cabe√ßa d√≥i" (correct - body part is subject)
- ‚ùå "Meus olhos d√≥i" (wrong verb agreement)
- ‚úÖ "Meus olhos doem" (correct - plural verb for plural subject)

**Important: M√ÉO and P√â Plurals:**
- **m√£o ‚Üí m√£os** (NOT "maos")
  - The tilde (Àú) is kept in the plural
  - Pronunciation: "mow-sh" (plural)
- **p√© ‚Üí p√©s** (NOT "pes")
  - The accent (¬¥) is kept in the plural
  - Pronunciation: "peh-sh" (plural)

**Health Expressions (for recognition):**
- dor de cabe√ßa (headache)
- dor de barriga (stomachache)
- dor de dente (toothache)
- dor nas costas (back pain)
- Note: "dor de" + body part is another way to express pain

**Describing Physical Features:**
- Combining with colors (Unit 55):
  - "Meu cabelo √© preto" (My hair is black)
  - "Meus olhos s√£o verdes" (My eyes are green)
- Combining with adjectives (Unit 6):
  - "Minhas m√£os s√£o pequenas" (My hands are small)
  - "Meu nariz √© grande" (My nose is big)

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 14/27-29: Possessives ‚Üí "meu bra√ßo", "minha cabe√ßa"
- Unit 54: Colors ‚Üí "Meus olhos s√£o azuis"
- Unit 6: Adjectives ‚Üí "grande", "pequeno" with body parts
- Unit 25: Doer (special verb pattern)
- Unit 16: Ter ‚Üí "Eu tenho dor de cabe√ßa"

**Key Learning:**
- 14 essential body parts vocabulary
- Irregular plurals: m√£os (not maos), p√©s (not pes)
- COSTAS is always plural
- DOER verb: body part is the subject (minha cabe√ßa d√≥i)
- Essential for describing health, pain, physical features

**Why This Unit:**

### Unit 58: Family Members Expanded (Fam√≠lia - Detalhada)

  - o av√¥ (grandfather)
  - a av√≥ (grandmother)
  - os av√≥s (grandparents)
  - o neto (grandson)
  - a neta (granddaughter)

  - o primo (male cousin)

  - o sobrinho (nephew)
  - a sobrinha (niece)
  - o cunhado (brother-in-law)
  - a cunhada (sister-in-law)
  - o genro (son-in-law)
  - a nora (daughter-in-law)

**Review from Unit 14:**
- o pai (father)
- a m√£e (mother)
- os pais (parents)
- o irm√£o (brother)
- a irm√£ (sister)
- o filho (son)
- a filha (daughter)
- o marido (husband)
- a esposa/mulher (wife)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Collective masculine plural:**
  - **os av√≥s** (grandparents - both genders)
  - **os netos** (grandchildren - both genders)
  - **os primos** (cousins - both genders)
  - **os tios** (aunt and uncle together)
  - When mixed gender, use masculine plural

- **Possessives with family (review + expansion):**
  - meu av√¥ (my grandfather)
  - minha av√≥ (my grandmother)
  - meus av√≥s (my grandparents)
  - minhas primas (my female cousins)

- **Asking about family:**
  - Voc√™ tem irm√£os? (Do you have siblings? - literally "brothers")
  - Voc√™ tem primos? (Do you have cousins?)
  - Quantos primos voc√™ tem? (How many cousins do you have?)
  - Como √© sua fam√≠lia? (What's your family like?)

**Practice format:**
- Name family members with correct gender
- Practice plural forms (av√≥s, netos, primos)
- Describe family: "Eu tenho dois tios"
- Answer questions about family size and relationships
- Use possessives with extended family

**Student can now:**
- Name 17 family members (beyond immediate family)
- Describe extended family relationships
- Use collective masculine plurals (av√≥s, primos, etc.)
- Ask and answer questions about family
- Combine with numbers from Units 44-45

**Typical sentences:**
- Eu tenho dois av√≥s. (I have two grandparents.)
- Minha av√≥ tem 75 anos. (My grandmother is 75 years old.)
- Meu tio mora no Brasil. (My uncle lives in Brazil.)
- Eu tenho tr√™s primos. (I have three cousins.)
- Meus netos s√£o pequenos. (My grandchildren are small.)
- Minha tia √© professora. (My aunt is a teacher.)
- Eu visito meus av√≥s no domingo. (I visit my grandparents on Sunday.)

**Sample conversation:**
```
A: Voc√™ tem uma fam√≠lia grande?
   (Do you have a big family?)
B: Sim, tenho. Eu tenho quatro tios e oito primos.
   (Yes, I do. I have four uncles/aunts and eight cousins.)

A: Seus av√≥s vivem aqui?
   (Do your grandparents live here?)
B: Minha av√≥ vive aqui, mas meu av√¥ j√° morreu.
   (My grandmother lives here, but my grandfather already died.)

A: Voc√™ √© pr√≥ximo de seus primos?
   (Are you close with your cousins?)
B: Sim, muito. N√≥s nos vemos todo m√™s.
   (Yes, very. We see each other every month.)
```

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ‚ùå "Minhas av√≥s" (wrong - av√≥s is masculine plural even for two grandmothers)
- ‚úÖ "Minhas av√≥s" is only correct if explicitly referring to "minhas av√≥ maternas e paternas"
- ‚úÖ "Meus av√≥s" (correct - standard usage for grandparents)
- ‚ùå "Eu tenho dois av√≥" (wrong - missing plural)
- ‚úÖ "Eu tenho dois av√≥s" (correct)
- ‚ùå "Meus primo" (wrong - missing plural)
- ‚úÖ "Meus primos" (correct)

**Cultural Notes:**
- **Extended family is very important in Brazilian culture**
- Common for multiple generations to live together or nearby
- Sunday family gatherings are traditional
- Cousins are often as close as siblings
- Respect for elders (especially grandparents) is emphasized

**In-Law Terms:**
- **cunhado/cunhada** (brother/sister-in-law) - sibling's spouse OR spouse's sibling
- **genro** (son-in-law) - daughter's husband
- **nora** (daughter-in-law) - son's wife
- **sogro/sogra** (father/mother-in-law) - spouse's parents [from Unit 14]

**Family Gatherings Vocabulary (for recognition):**
- reuni√£o de fam√≠lia (family reunion)
- almo√ßo de fam√≠lia (family lunch)
- churrasco em fam√≠lia (family barbecue)
- festa de fam√≠lia (family party)

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 14: Immediate family ‚Üí now expanding to extended family
- Unit 31-33: Possessives ‚Üí using with all family members
- Unit 17: Age ‚Üí "Minha av√≥ tem 80 anos"
- Unit 15-16: Numbers ‚Üí counting family members
- Unit 50: Days ‚Üí "Eu visito meus av√≥s no domingo"
- Unit 3: Places ‚Üí "Meu tio mora em S√£o Paulo"

**Key Learning:**
- 17 extended family member terms
- Collective masculine plural for mixed-gender groups (av√≥s, primos, etc.)
- Extended family is culturally important in Brazil
- Combine family vocabulary with numbers, ages, and descriptions
- Essential for talking about personal life and relationships

**Why This Unit:**
- **FOUNDATIONAL:** Family vocabulary is essential for personal conversation
- Natural progression: immediate family (Unit 14) ‚Üí extended family
- Ultra-granular: focuses ONLY on extended family relationships
- Practical: immediate use for describing family, social conversation

### Unit 59: Emotions and Feelings (Emo√ß√µes e Sentimentos)

**New vocabulary:**
- **Basic emotions:**
  - feliz (happy)
  - triste (sad)
  - cansado/cansada (tired)
  - animado/animada (excited/energetic)
  - nervoso/nervosa (nervous)
  - com raiva (angry - literally "with anger")
  - preocupado/preocupada (worried)
  - assustado/assustada (scared/frightened)
  - entediado/entediada (bored)
  - com fome (hungry - literally "with hunger")
  - com sede (thirsty - literally "with thirst")
  - com sono (sleepy - literally "with sleep")

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Emotions with ESTAR (not SER):**
  - Emotions are TEMPORARY states ‚Üí use ESTAR
  - ‚úÖ "Eu **estou** feliz" (I am happy - right now)
  - ‚ùå "Eu **sou** feliz" (wrong for current feeling - would mean personality trait)

- **Emotions using TER (to have):**
  - Some emotions/physical feelings use TER + "com" construction:
    - "Eu **tenho** fome" (I'm hungry - literally "I have hunger")
    - "Eu **tenho** sede" (I'm thirsty - literally "I have thirst")
    - "Eu **tenho** sono" (I'm sleepy - literally "I have sleep")
    - "Eu **tenho** medo" (I'm afraid - literally "I have fear")
  - Alternative: Eu estou **com** fome/sede/sono (I am with hunger/thirst/sleep)

- **Asking about feelings:**
  - "Como voc√™ est√°?" (How are you? - asking about current state)
  - "Como voc√™ se sente?" (How do you feel?)
  - "Voc√™ est√° bem?" (Are you okay?)
  - "O que voc√™ tem?" (What's wrong? - literally "What do you have?")

**Practice format:**
- Describe current emotional state: "Eu estou feliz"
- Ask how someone feels: "Como voc√™ est√°?"
- Practice ESTAR vs TER with different emotions
- Combine with reasons: "Eu estou feliz porque..." (I'm happy because...)
- Use with intensity: "muito cansado" (very tired)

**Student can now:**
- Name 12 common emotions and feelings
- Use ESTAR correctly with emotion adjectives
- Use TER correctly with fome/sede/sono/medo
- Ask how someone is feeling
- Describe why they feel a certain way
- Distinguish temporary feelings (estar) from personality (ser)

**Typical sentences:**
- Eu estou feliz. (I'm happy.)
- Ela est√° triste. (She's sad.)
- Estou muito cansado. (I'm very tired.)
- Voc√™ est√° nervoso? (Are you nervous?)
- Eu tenho fome. (I'm hungry.)
- Estamos animados! (We're excited!)
- Ele est√° preocupado. (He's worried.)

**Sample conversation:**
```
A: Como voc√™ est√°?
   (How are you?)
B: Estou cansado. E voc√™?
   (I'm tired. And you?)

A: Eu estou bem, obrigado. Por que voc√™ est√° cansado?
   (I'm fine, thanks. Why are you tired?)
B: Eu trabalho muito. E agora estou com fome tamb√©m.
   (I work a lot. And now I'm hungry too.)

A: Vamos almo√ßar?
   (Shall we have lunch?)
B: Boa ideia! Estou animado.
   (Good idea! I'm excited.)
```

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ‚ùå "Eu sou cansado" (wrong - temporary state)
- ‚úÖ "Eu estou cansado" (correct)
- ‚ùå "Eu estou fome" (wrong - fome uses ter)
- ‚úÖ "Eu tenho fome" OR "Eu estou com fome" (correct)
- ‚ùå "Eu estou com feliz" (wrong - feliz uses estar alone)
- ‚úÖ "Eu estou feliz" (correct)
- ‚ùå "Eu tenho nervoso" (wrong - nervoso uses estar)
- ‚úÖ "Eu estou nervoso" (correct)

**ESTAR vs SER with Emotions:**

**Use ESTAR for temporary feelings:**
- Eu estou feliz (I'm happy now)
- Eu estou triste (I'm sad now)
- Eu estou cansado (I'm tired now)

**Use SER for permanent personality traits:**
- Eu sou feliz (I'm a happy person)
- Eu sou otimista (I'm an optimistic person)
- Eu sou calmo (I'm a calm person)

**TER vs ESTAR with Physical Feelings:**

Both are correct, slightly different nuance:

**TER (more common, direct):**
- Eu tenho fome (I'm hungry)
- Eu tenho sede (I'm thirsty)
- Eu tenho sono (I'm sleepy)
- Eu tenho medo (I'm afraid)

**ESTAR COM (more descriptive):**
- Eu estou com fome (I'm with hunger)
- Eu estou com sede (I'm with thirst)
- Eu estou com sono (I'm with sleep)
- Eu estou com medo (I'm with fear)

**Expressing Intensity:**
- muito cansado (very tired)
- um pouco triste (a little sad)
- super feliz (super happy)
- t√£o nervoso (so nervous)

**Reasons for Feelings (for recognition):**
- Estou feliz porque... (I'm happy because...)
- Estou triste porque... (I'm sad because...)
- Estou preocupado com... (I'm worried about...)
- Estou animado para... (I'm excited for...)

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 5: ESTAR ‚Üí now using with emotions
- Unit 1: SER ‚Üí contrast with estar for personality vs temporary state
- Unit 16: TER ‚Üí extended to fome/sede/sono
- Unit 56: Body parts ‚Üí "Minha cabe√ßa d√≥i, estou preocupado"
- Unit 35: Reflexive pronouns ‚Üí "Como voc√™ se sente?"

**Key Learning:**
- 12 essential emotion and feeling vocabulary words
- ESTAR for temporary emotional states (not SER)
- TER for physical feelings (fome, sede, sono, medo)
- Asking "Como voc√™ est√°?" for current feelings
- Essential for describing mood, health, and communication

**Why This Unit:**
- **FOUNDATIONAL:** Emotions are essential for personal communication
- Natural progression: can describe physical state, now emotional state
- Ultra-granular: focuses ONLY on basic emotions and feelings
- Practical: immediate use for conversation, expressing needs
- Reinforces critical ESTAR vs SER distinction with practical context

### Unit 60: Locations and Directions (Localiza√ß√µes e Dire√ß√µes)

**New vocabulary:**
- **Prepositions of place:**
  - em (in/on/at)
  - dentro de (inside of)
  - fora de (outside of)
  - em cima de (on top of)
  - embaixo de (under/below)
  - ao lado de (next to/beside)
  - perto de (near/close to)
  - longe de (far from)
  - na frente de (in front of)
  - atr√°s de (behind)
  - entre (between)
  - acima de (above)
  - abaixo de (below)

- **Direction words:**
  - √† direita (to the right)
  - √† esquerda (to the left)
  - em frente (straight ahead)
  - para cima (upward)
  - para baixo (downward)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Compound prepositions require "de":**
  - ‚úÖ em cima **de** (on top of) - requires "de"
  - ‚úÖ ao lado **de** (next to) - requires "de"
  - ‚úÖ perto **de** (near) - requires "de"
  - Must be followed by "de" before the noun

- **Contraction of "de" with articles:**
  - de + o = **do** (of the - masculine)
  - de + a = **da** (of the - feminine)
  - de + os = **dos** (of the - masculine plural)
  - de + as = **das** (of the - feminine plural)

  Examples:
  - em cima **do** carro (on top of the car)
  - perto **da** casa (near the house)
  - ao lado **dos** livros (next to the books)

- **EM contracts with articles:**
  - em + o = **no** (in/on/at the - masculine)
  - em + a = **na** (in/on/at the - feminine)
  - em + os = **nos** (in/on/at the - masculine plural)
  - em + as = **nas** (in/on/at the - feminine plural)

**Practice format:**
- Describe object locations: "O livro est√° em cima da mesa"
- Answer "Onde est√°...?" questions (Where is...?)
- Practice contractions: de+o=do, em+a=na
- Give directions: "A loja fica √† esquerda"
- Use with ESTAR for location

**Student can now:**
- Describe where objects are located
- Use 13 prepositions of place correctly
- Contract "de" and "em" with articles (do, da, no, na)
- Give and understand basic directions
- Ask and answer "Onde est√°?" (Where is?)

**Typical sentences:**
- O livro est√° em cima da mesa. (The book is on top of the table.)
- A casa fica perto do parque. (The house is near the park.)
- O gato est√° embaixo da cama. (The cat is under the bed.)
- O banco fica ao lado da farm√°cia. (The bank is next to the pharmacy.)
- Onde est√° o banheiro? - √Ä direita. (Where's the bathroom? - To the right.)
- A escola fica longe da minha casa. (The school is far from my house.)
- O carro est√° na frente da casa. (The car is in front of the house.)

**Sample conversation:**
```
A: Onde est√° o meu celular?
   (Where's my phone?)
B: Est√° em cima da mesa, ao lado do livro.
   (It's on top of the table, next to the book.)

A: E minhas chaves?
   (And my keys?)
B: Est√£o dentro da bolsa.
   (They're inside the bag.)

A: Onde fica o supermercado?
   (Where's the supermarket?)
B: Fica perto da escola, √† esquerda.
   (It's near the school, on the left.)
```

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ‚ùå "em cima o carro" (missing "de")
- ‚úÖ "em cima do carro" (correct - compound preposition needs "de")
- ‚ùå "perto a casa" (missing "de")
- ‚úÖ "perto da casa" (correct - perto de + a = perto da)
- ‚ùå "ao lado a loja" (missing "de")
- ‚úÖ "ao lado da loja" (correct)
- ‚ùå "na cima da mesa" (wrong - "em cima" not "na cima")
- ‚úÖ "em cima da mesa" (correct)

**Compound Prepositions - Must Use "DE":**

These prepositions are ALWAYS followed by "de":
- em cima de (on top of) - NOT "em cima"
- embaixo de (under) - NOT "embaixo"
- ao lado de (next to) - NOT "ao lado"
- perto de (near) - NOT "perto"
- longe de (far from) - NOT "longe"
- dentro de (inside of) - NOT "dentro"
- fora de (outside of) - NOT "fora"
- na frente de (in front of) - NOT "na frente"
- atr√°s de (behind) - NOT "atr√°s"
- acima de (above) - NOT "acima"
- abaixo de (below) - NOT "abaixo"

**ESTAR vs FICAR for Location:**

**Use ESTAR for:**
- Temporary location of movable objects:
  - "O livro **est√°** na mesa" (The book is on the table)
  - "Eu **estou** em casa" (I'm at home)

**Use FICAR for:**
- Permanent location of places/buildings:
  - "A escola **fica** perto daqui" (The school is near here)
  - "Onde **fica** o banco?" (Where is the bank located?)

**Contractions Summary:**
- de + o/a/os/as = do/da/dos/das
- em + o/a/os/as = no/na/nos/nas
- These contractions are MANDATORY, not optional

**Asking for Directions:**
- Onde fica...? (Where is... located? - for places)
- Onde est√°...? (Where is...? - for objects/people)
- Como eu chego...? (How do I get to...?)
- √â perto? (Is it close?)
- √â longe? (Is it far?)

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 5: ESTAR ‚Üí now using for location
- Unit 3: Articles ‚Üí contracting with de and em
- Unit 11: FICAR ‚Üí using for permanent location
- Unit 7: Places ‚Üí "O banco fica perto do parque"

**Key Learning:**
- 13 prepositions of place in Portuguese
- Compound prepositions MUST use "de" (em cima de, ao lado de, etc.)
- Mandatory contractions: de+o=do, em+a=na, etc.
- ESTAR for temporary location, FICAR for permanent location
- Essential for describing location and giving directions

**Why This Unit:**
- **FOUNDATIONAL:** Location vocabulary is essential for daily life
- Natural progression: can describe objects, now describe WHERE they are
- Ultra-granular: focuses ONLY on location and direction
- Practical: immediate use for finding things, giving directions, navigation
- Reinforces contraction patterns with "de" and "em"

### Unit 61: House and Rooms (Casa e C√¥modos)

**New vocabulary:**
- **Parts of a house:**
  - a casa (house)
  - o apartamento (apartment)
  - o quarto (bedroom)
  - a sala (living room)
  - a sala de estar (living room - formal)
  - a sala de jantar (dining room)
  - a cozinha (kitchen)
  - o banheiro (bathroom)
  - o quarto de banho (bathroom - European Portuguese)
  - a garagem (garage)
  - o jardim (garden/yard)
  - a varanda (balcony/porch)
  - o corredor (hallway)
  - a escada (staircase)
  - o telhado (roof)
  - a porta (door)
  - a janela (window)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Using rooms with prepositions:**
  - **no** quarto (in the bedroom - masculine)
  - **na** cozinha (in the kitchen - feminine)
  - **na** sala (in the living room - feminine)
  - Remember: em + o = no, em + a = na

- **Expressing possession of rooms:**
  - Minha casa tem tr√™s quartos. (My house has three bedrooms.)
  - Meu apartamento tem dois banheiros. (My apartment has two bathrooms.)
  - Use TER (to have) to describe what's in the house

- **MORAR vs VIVER (to live):**
  - Both mean "to live" but slightly different usage:
  - **MORAR** = to reside, live in (more common for address)
    - "Eu moro em uma casa" (I live in a house)
    - "Eu moro no apartamento" (I live in the apartment)
  - **VIVER** = to live, exist (more general/philosophical)
    - "Eu vivo no Brasil" (I live in Brazil)

**Practice format:**
- Name rooms with correct articles
- Describe house: "Minha casa tem tr√™s quartos"
- Practice location: "Eu estou na cozinha"
- Count rooms with numbers: "dois banheiros"
- Combine with furniture vocabulary (if known)

**Student can now:**
- Name 17 parts of a house/apartment
- Describe how many rooms their house has
- Say where they are in the house: "Estou no quarto"
- Use MORAR to say where they live
- Combine with numbers from Units 44-45

**Typical sentences:**
- Eu moro em uma casa. (I live in a house.)
- Minha casa tem tr√™s quartos. (My house has three bedrooms.)
- Eu estou na cozinha. (I'm in the kitchen.)
- O banheiro fica ao lado do quarto. (The bathroom is next to the bedroom.)
- Meu apartamento tem uma varanda. (My apartment has a balcony.)
- A sala √© grande. (The living room is big.)
- Onde est√° o banheiro? - No corredor, √† direita. (Where's the bathroom? - In the hallway, on the right.)

**Sample conversation:**
```
A: Voc√™ mora em casa ou apartamento?
   (Do you live in a house or apartment?)
B: Eu moro em um apartamento.
   (I live in an apartment.)

A: Quantos quartos tem?
   (How many bedrooms does it have?)
B: Tem dois quartos e um banheiro.
   (It has two bedrooms and one bathroom.)

A: Tem varanda?
   (Does it have a balcony?)
B: Sim, tem uma varanda grande.
   (Yes, it has a big balcony.)

A: Onde voc√™ est√° agora?
   (Where are you now?)
B: Estou na sala, assistindo TV.
   (I'm in the living room, watching TV.)
```

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ‚ùå "Eu moro na uma casa" (wrong - don't use article after "na" with indefinite)
- ‚úÖ "Eu moro em uma casa" (correct)
- ‚ùå "Estou em o quarto" (wrong - must contract)
- ‚úÖ "Estou no quarto" (correct - em + o = no)
- ‚ùå "Minha casa √© tr√™s quartos" (wrong - use TER not SER)
- ‚úÖ "Minha casa tem tr√™s quartos" (correct)
- ‚ùå "no cozinha" (wrong gender)
- ‚úÖ "na cozinha" (correct - cozinha is feminine)

**SALA Variations:**
- **a sala** (general living room - most common)
- **a sala de estar** (living room - literally "sitting room")
- **a sala de jantar** (dining room - literally "dining room")
- In Brazilian homes, "sala" usually refers to the main living space

**Brazilian vs European Portuguese:**
- **Brazilian:** o banheiro (bathroom)
- **European:** o quarto de banho (bathroom)
- **Brazilian:** a varanda (balcony/porch)
- **European:** a varanda (same)
- This course teaches Brazilian Portuguese

**House Types in Brazil:**
- **casa** (house) - standalone building
- **apartamento** (apartment) - unit in building
- **sobrado** (two-story house)
- **kitnet** (studio apartment)
- **cobertura** (penthouse)

**Describing House Features:**
- grande (big)
- pequeno/pequena (small)
- novo/nova (new)
- velho/velha (old)
- espa√ßoso/espa√ßosa (spacious)
- aconchegante (cozy)

**Asking About Housing:**
- Voc√™ mora em casa ou apartamento? (Do you live in a house or apartment?)
- Quantos quartos tem? (How many bedrooms does it have?)
- Tem garagem? (Does it have a garage?)
- Tem jardim? (Does it have a yard?)

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 7: MORAR ‚Üí now specifying type of dwelling
- Unit 59: Prepositions ‚Üí "O banheiro fica ao lado do quarto"
- Unit 16: TER ‚Üí "Minha casa tem tr√™s quartos"
- Unit 15-45: Numbers ‚Üí counting rooms
- Unit 6: Adjectives ‚Üí "A sala √© grande"

**Key Learning:**
- 17 parts of house/apartment vocabulary
- Use TER to describe what house has: "tem tr√™s quartos"
- Rooms with EM: no quarto, na sala, na cozinha
- MORAR for where you live (reside)
- Essential for describing home, giving directions inside house

**Why This Unit:**
- **FOUNDATIONAL:** House vocabulary is everyday language
- Natural progression: have locations (Unit 60), now apply to house
- Ultra-granular: focuses ONLY on house and rooms
- Practical: immediate use for describing home, finding things

### Unit 62: Daily Activities Verbs (Verbos de Atividades Di√°rias)

**New vocabulary:**
- **Daily routine verbs:**
  - acordar (to wake up)
  - levantar (to get up)
  - tomar banho (to take a shower/bath)
  - escovar (to brush)
  - pentear (to comb)
  - vestir (to dress/get dressed)
  - tomar caf√© (to have breakfast - literally "take coffee")
  - almo√ßar (to have lunch)
  - jantar (to have dinner)
  - estudar (to study)
  - trabalhar (to work) [review]
  - descansar (to rest)
  - assistir (to watch)
  - dormir (to sleep)
  - cozinhar (to cook)
  - limpar (to clean)
  - lavar (to wash)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **All verbs are regular except DORMIR:**
  - **DORMIR (to sleep)** is irregular (o ‚Üí ue stem change in some forms):
    - eu durmo (I sleep)
    - voc√™ dorme (you sleep)
    - ele/ela dorme (he/she sleeps)
    - n√≥s dormimos (we sleep)
    - voc√™s dormem (you all sleep)
    - eles/elas dormem (they sleep)

- **Reflexive use with daily routine:**
  - Some activities can be reflexive (doing to yourself):
  - **vestir-se** (to get dressed - literally "dress oneself")
  - **pentear-se** (to comb one's hair)
  - **levantar-se** (to get up - literally "lift oneself")
  - More common in formal speech; often dropped in casual Brazilian Portuguese

- **Time expressions with daily activities:**
  - Eu acordo **√†s** sete horas. (I wake up at 7 o'clock.)
  - Eu almo√ßo **ao meio-dia**. (I have lunch at noon.)
  - Eu durmo **√†** noite. (I sleep at night.)
  - Use **√†s** (at) with specific times

**Practice format:**
- Describe daily routine: "Eu acordo √†s sete"
- Practice present tense conjugation of daily verbs
- Special focus on DORMIR (irregular)
- Combine with time expressions: "√†s oito horas"
- Sequence activities: "Primeiro... depois... ent√£o..."

**Student can now:**
- Name 17 daily activity verbs
- Conjugate regular daily routine verbs in present tense
- Use irregular DORMIR correctly
- Describe their daily routine with times
- Sequence activities in order

**Typical sentences:**
- Eu acordo √†s sete da manh√£. (I wake up at 7 AM.)
- Eu tomo banho todos os dias. (I shower every day.)
- Ela escova os dentes. (She brushes her teeth.)
- N√≥s almo√ßamos ao meio-dia. (We have lunch at noon.)
- Eu trabalho de segunda a sexta. (I work Monday to Friday.)
- Ele dorme oito horas por noite. (He sleeps eight hours per night.)
- Eu cozinho o jantar. (I cook dinner.)

**Sample conversation:**
```
A: A que horas voc√™ acorda?
   (What time do you wake up?)
B: Eu acordo √†s seis e meia.
   (I wake up at 6:30.)

A: E o que voc√™ faz depois?
   (And what do you do after?)
B: Eu tomo banho, tomo caf√©, e vou trabalhar.
   (I shower, have breakfast, and go to work.)

A: Voc√™ almo√ßa em casa?
   (Do you have lunch at home?)
B: N√£o, eu almo√ßo no trabalho.
   (No, I have lunch at work.)

A: A que horas voc√™ dorme?
   (What time do you sleep?)
B: Eu durmo √†s onze da noite.
   (I sleep at 11 PM.)
```

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ‚ùå "Eu dormo" for "I sleep" is CORRECT
- ‚ùå "Eu duermo" (wrong - Spanish interference)
- ‚úÖ "Eu durmo" (correct - Portuguese)
- ‚ùå "Eu tomo um banho" (not wrong, but less common)
- ‚úÖ "Eu tomo banho" (more common - no article)
- ‚ùå "Eu escovo meus dentes" (not wrong, but redundant)
- ‚úÖ "Eu escovo os dentes" (more common - use "os" not "meus")
- ‚ùå "Eu acordo em sete horas" (wrong preposition)
- ‚úÖ "Eu acordo √†s sete horas" (correct - use "√†s" for clock time)

**DORMIR Conjugation (Irregular):**

Present tense:
- eu **durmo** (I sleep) - stem change o ‚Üí u
- voc√™ **dorme** (you sleep) - stem change o ‚Üí o
- ele/ela **dorme** (he/she sleeps)
- n√≥s **dormimos** (we sleep) - regular
- voc√™s **dormem** (you all sleep)
- eles/elas **dormem** (they sleep)

This is a common pattern for -IR verbs with "o" in the stem.

**Meals Vocabulary:**
- **tomar caf√© / caf√© da manh√£** (breakfast - literally "take coffee")
- **almo√ßar / almo√ßo** (lunch - verb and noun)
- **jantar / jantar** (dinner - verb and noun)
- **lanche** (snack)

Note: "tomar caf√©" can mean "drink coffee" OR "have breakfast" - context matters!

**Body Parts with Daily Activities:**
- escovar **os dentes** (brush teeth)
- lavar **as m√£os** (wash hands)
- lavar **o rosto** (wash face)
- pentear **o cabelo** (comb hair)

Use definite article (os, as, o) not possessive (meus, minhas, meu)!

**Sequencing Words:**
- primeiro (first)
- depois (after/then)
- ent√£o (then/so)
- em seguida (next)
- finalmente (finally)
- por √∫ltimo (lastly)

**Time of Day Expressions:**
- de manh√£ (in the morning)
- de tarde (in the afternoon)
- de noite / √† noite (at night)
- ao meio-dia (at noon)
- √† meia-noite (at midnight)

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 48: Time ‚Üí "Eu acordo √†s sete horas"
- Unit 49: Days ‚Üí "Eu trabalho de segunda a sexta"
- Unit 56: Body parts ‚Üí "Eu escovo os dentes"

- 17 daily activity verbs for routine description
- DORMIR is irregular (durmo, dorme, dormimos, dormem)
- Use √ÄS + time for "at" a specific hour
- Meals: tomar caf√© (breakfast), almo√ßar (lunch), jantar (dinner)
- Essential for describing daily life and routine

### Unit 63: Frequency Adverbs (Adv√©rbios de Frequ√™ncia)

**New vocabulary:**
- **Frequency adverbs:**
  - sempre (always)
  - quase sempre (almost always)
  - geralmente (generally/usually)
  - normalmente (normally)
  - √†s vezes (sometimes)
  - de vez em quando (once in a while)
  - raramente (rarely)
  - quase nunca (almost never)
  - nunca (never)

- **Time frequency expressions:**
  - todo dia (every day)
  - todos os dias (every day - plural)
  - toda semana (every week)
  - todo m√™s (every month)
  - todo ano (every year)
  - uma vez por semana (once a week)
  - duas vezes por dia (twice a day)
  - tr√™s vezes por m√™s (three times a month)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Adverb placement (flexible but patterns exist):**

  **Option 1 - Before the verb (most common):**
  - Eu **sempre** acordo √†s sete. (I always wake up at 7.)
  - Ela **nunca** come carne. (She never eats meat.)
  - N√≥s **geralmente** almo√ßamos em casa. (We usually have lunch at home.)

  **Option 2 - After the verb (emphasis or style):**
  - Eu acordo **sempre** √†s sete. (I wake up always at 7 - emphasis)
  - Less common, more emphatic

  **Option 3 - Beginning of sentence (emphasis):**
  - **Sempre** eu acordo √†s sete. (Always I wake up at 7 - rare, emphatic)

- **NUNCA with negation:**
  - Portuguese allows double negatives!
  - Eu **nunca** como carne. (I never eat meat.) - most common
  - Eu **n√£o** como carne **nunca**. (I don't eat meat never.) - also correct!
  - Both are grammatically correct in Portuguese

- **TODO/TODA agreement:**
  - **todo** (every - masculine singular): todo dia (every day)
  - **toda** (every - feminine singular): toda semana (every week)
  - **todos** (every/all - masculine plural): todos os dias (every day)
  - **todas** (every/all - feminine plural): todas as semanas (every week)

**Practice format:**
- Describe habits with frequency: "Eu sempre acordo cedo"
- Practice adverb placement before verb
- Use "nunca" in sentences
- Combine with daily activities from Unit 62
- Count frequency: "duas vezes por semana"

**Student can now:**
- Use 9 frequency adverbs correctly
- Express how often they do activities
- Use "todo/toda" with correct gender agreement
- Count frequency (once, twice, three times per...)
- Describe habits and routines precisely

**Typical sentences:**
- Eu sempre tomo caf√© da manh√£. (I always have breakfast.)
- Ela nunca chega atrasada. (She never arrives late.)
- N√≥s geralmente almo√ßamos juntos. (We usually have lunch together.)
- Eu vou ao cinema duas vezes por m√™s. (I go to the movies twice a month.)
- Ele raramente cozinha. (He rarely cooks.)
- Eu estudo todos os dias. (I study every day.)
- De vez em quando eu durmo tarde. (Once in a while I sleep late.)

**Sample conversation:**
```
A: Voc√™ sempre toma caf√© da manh√£?
   (Do you always have breakfast?)
B: Sim, sempre. Eu nunca saio sem tomar caf√©.
   (Yes, always. I never leave without having breakfast.)

A: Com que frequ√™ncia voc√™ vai √† academia?
   (How often do you go to the gym?)
B: Eu vou tr√™s vezes por semana - segunda, quarta e sexta.
   (I go three times a week - Monday, Wednesday, and Friday.)

A: Voc√™ geralmente cozinha?
   (Do you usually cook?)
B: N√£o, raramente. Eu geralmente pe√ßo comida.
   (No, rarely. I usually order food.)
```

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ‚ùå "Eu todo dia acordo" (awkward word order)
- ‚úÖ "Eu acordo todo dia" (correct - frequency expression after verb)
- ‚úÖ "Todo dia eu acordo" (also correct - frequency at beginning)
- ‚ùå "todo semana" (wrong gender)
- ‚úÖ "toda semana" (correct - semana is feminine)
- ‚ùå "todo os dias" (wrong - missing s on todo)
- ‚úÖ "todos os dias" (correct - plural)
- ‚ùå "uma vez por o dia" (wrong contraction)
- ‚úÖ "uma vez por dia" (correct - no article)

**Frequency Adverbs - Most to Least Frequent:**

**100%:** sempre (always)
**~90%:** quase sempre (almost always)
**~75%:** geralmente / normalmente (usually/normally)
**~50%:** √†s vezes (sometimes)
**~25%:** de vez em quando (once in a while)
**~10%:** raramente (rarely)
**~5%:** quase nunca (almost never)
**0%:** nunca (never)

**TODO/TODA/TODOS/TODAS Agreement:**

**Masculine singular:**
- todo dia (every day) - "dia" is masculine
- todo ano (every year) - "ano" is masculine
- todo m√™s (every month) - "m√™s" is masculine

**Feminine singular:**
- toda semana (every week) - "semana" is feminine
- toda noite (every night) - "noite" is feminine
- toda manh√£ (every morning) - "manh√£" is feminine

**Masculine plural:**
- todos os dias (every day - literally "all the days")
- todos os anos (every year)
- todos os meses (every month)

**Feminine plural:**
- todas as semanas (every week)
- todas as noites (every night)
- todas as manh√£s (every morning)

**"Por" Expressions:**
- uma vez **por** dia (once per day)
- duas vezes **por** semana (twice per week)
- tr√™s vezes **por** m√™s (three times per month)
- Use "por" (per) not "cada" (each)

**Asking About Frequency:**
- Com que frequ√™ncia...? (How often...?)
- Quantas vezes por...? (How many times per...?)
- Voc√™ sempre...? (Do you always...?)
- Com que frequ√™ncia voc√™...? (How frequently do you...?)

**Double Negative in Portuguese:**
Unlike English, Portuguese ALLOWS and ACCEPTS double negatives:
- Eu **nunca** fa√ßo isso. (I never do that.) - standard
- Eu **n√£o** fa√ßo isso **nunca**. (I don't do that never.) - also correct!
- Both are grammatically correct; first is more common

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 61: Daily activities ‚Üí now describing frequency of those activities
- Unit 49: Days ‚Üí "de segunda a sexta" (Monday to Friday)
- Unit 15-45: Numbers ‚Üí "duas vezes" (twice), "tr√™s vezes" (three times)
- Unit 15: Negation ‚Üí "nunca" is negative adverb

**Key Learning:**
- 9 frequency adverbs from "sempre" to "nunca"
- Adverbs usually come BEFORE the verb in Portuguese
- TODO/TODA must agree in gender with following noun
- "Todos os dias" (every day) vs "todo dia" (every day) - both correct
- Essential for describing habits, routines, and patterns

**Why This Unit:**
- **FOUNDATIONAL:** Frequency is essential for describing habits
- Natural progression: have daily activities (Unit 62), now describe how often
- Ultra-granular: focuses ONLY on frequency adverbs and expressions
- Practical: immediate use for describing routine, habits, schedule
- Enriches descriptions of daily life significantly
