### Unit 64: Food and Meals Expanded (Comida e Refei√ß√µes - Expandido)

**New vocabulary:**
- **Proteins:**
  - a carne (meat)
  - o frango (chicken)
  - o peixe (fish)
  - o ovo (egg)
  - o queijo (cheese)

- **Vegetables:**
  - a alface (lettuce)
  - o tomate (tomato)
  - a cenoura (carrot)
  - a batata (potato)
  - a cebola (onion)

- **Fruits:**
  - a ma√ß√£ (apple)
  - a banana (banana)
  - a laranja (orange)
  - o morango (strawberry)
  - a uva (grape)

- **Staples:**
  - o arroz (rice)
  - o feij√£o (beans)
  - o p√£o (bread)
  - a massa (pasta)
  - o a√ß√∫car (sugar)
  - o sal (salt)

- **Drinks:**
  - a √°gua (water)
  - o suco (juice)
  - o refrigerante (soda)
  - o leite (milk)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Using food with verbs:**
  - **comer** (to eat) + food: "Eu como arroz" (I eat rice)
  - **beber** (to drink) + beverage: "Eu bebo √°gua" (I drink water)
  - **gostar de** (to like) + food: "Eu gosto de frango" (I like chicken)

- **Gender surprises in food vocabulary:**
  - **o tomate** (tomato - masculine, even though ends in -e)
  - **o leite** (milk - masculine)
  - **a carne** (meat - feminine)
  - **o sal** (salt - masculine)
  - Gender is not predictable - must memorize!

- **Partitives and quantities:**
  - um peda√ßo de p√£o (a piece of bread)
  - um copo de √°gua (a glass of water)
  - uma x√≠cara de caf√© (a cup of coffee)
  - um prato de arroz (a plate of rice)
  - um pouco de sal (a little salt)

- **Brazilian staple: Arroz e feij√£o**
  - "Arroz **com** feij√£o" (rice and beans) - use COM (with)
  - This is THE staple of Brazilian cuisine, eaten daily
  - Often said as one phrase: "arroz e feij√£o"

**Practice format:**
- Name foods with correct gender/article
- Use gostar de + food: "Eu gosto de banana"
- Order meals: "Eu quero frango com arroz"
- Describe what you eat: "Eu como ovos no caf√© da manh√£"
- Practice quantities: "um copo de suco"

**Student can now:**
- Name 28 common foods and drinks
- Use correct gender for food vocabulary
- Express food preferences with gostar de
- Order food and describe meals
- Use basic quantity expressions

**Typical sentences:**
- Eu gosto de arroz e feij√£o. (I like rice and beans.)
- Eu como frango com batata. (I eat chicken with potato.)
- Eu bebo suco de laranja. (I drink orange juice.)
- Eu quero um peda√ßo de p√£o. (I want a piece of bread.)
- Ela n√£o come carne. (She doesn't eat meat.)
- Eu como frutas todos os dias. (I eat fruit every day.)
- Eu bebo √°gua, n√£o refrigerante. (I drink water, not soda.)

**Sample conversation:**
```
A: O que voc√™ gosta de comer?
   (What do you like to eat?)
B: Eu gosto de frango com arroz e feij√£o.
   (I like chicken with rice and beans.)

A: Voc√™ come carne?
   (Do you eat meat?)
B: Sim, eu como. Mas eu prefiro frango.
   (Yes, I do. But I prefer chicken.)

A: E o que voc√™ bebe?
   (And what do you drink?)
B: Eu bebo √°gua e √†s vezes suco.
   (I drink water and sometimes juice.)

A: Voc√™ gosta de frutas?
   (Do you like fruit?)
B: Sim, muito! Eu gosto de banana e morango.
   (Yes, a lot! I like banana and strawberry.)
```

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ‚ùå "Eu gosto frango" (missing "de")
- ‚úÖ "Eu gosto de frango" (correct - gostar requires "de")
- ‚ùå "a tomate" (wrong gender)
- ‚úÖ "o tomate" (correct - masculine)
- ‚ùå "Arroz com feij√µes" (wrong - feij√£o stays singular in this phrase)
- ‚úÖ "Arroz com feij√£o" (correct - Brazilian staple phrase)
- ‚ùå "Eu bebo um suco de o laranja" (wrong - must contract)
- ‚úÖ "Eu bebo um suco de laranja" (correct)

**Brazilian Food Culture:**
- **Arroz e feij√£o** is the foundation of Brazilian meals
- Eaten at lunch (main meal) almost daily
- Usually accompanied by protein (chicken, beef, fish) and salad
- Breakfast (caf√© da manh√£): bread, coffee, fruit, cheese
- Lunch (almo√ßo): main meal, rice and beans with protein
- Dinner (jantar): lighter, or leftovers from lunch

**Gender Patterns (and exceptions):**
Most foods ending in -a are feminine, -o masculine, BUT:
- **o tomate** (masculine exception)
- **o leite** (masculine)
- **a carne** (feminine)
- **o peixe** (masculine)
- Must memorize gender for each food!

**Quantity Expressions:**
- **um peda√ßo de** (a piece of): um peda√ßo de bolo (a piece of cake)
- **um copo de** (a glass of): um copo de leite (a glass of milk)
- **uma x√≠cara de** (a cup of): uma x√≠cara de caf√© (a cup of coffee)
- **um prato de** (a plate of): um prato de arroz (a plate of rice)
- **um pouco de** (a little of): um pouco de a√ß√∫car (a little sugar)
- **muito/muita** (a lot of): muita √°gua (a lot of water), muito arroz (a lot of rice)

**Food Preferences:**
- Eu gosto de... (I like...)
- Eu prefiro... (I prefer...)
- Eu adoro... (I love...)
- Eu n√£o gosto de... (I don't like...)
- Eu odeio... (I hate...)
- Eu amo... (I love...)

**Dietary Restrictions (for recognition):**
- vegetariano/vegetariana (vegetarian)
- vegano/vegana (vegan)
- Eu n√£o como carne. (I don't eat meat.)
- Eu sou al√©rgico a... (I'm allergic to...)
- sem gl√∫ten (gluten-free)
- sem lactose (lactose-free)

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 25: Gostar de ‚Üí "Eu gosto de arroz"
- Unit 20-19: Basic food ‚Üí now expanding vocabulary significantly
- Unit 61: Meals ‚Üí "Eu como ovos no caf√© da manh√£"
- Unit 62: Frequency ‚Üí "Eu como frutas todos os dias"
- Unit 15: Negation ‚Üí "Eu n√£o como carne"

**Key Learning:**
- 28 essential food and drink vocabulary items
- ARROZ COM FEIJ√ÉO is Brazilian staple (rice and beans)
- Gender must be memorized (o tomate, a carne, o leite)

### Unit 65: Transportation and Travel (Transporte e Viagem)

**New vocabulary:**
- **Modes of transportation:**
  - o carro (car)
  - o √¥nibus (bus)
  - o metr√¥ (subway/metro)
  - o trem (train)
  - o avi√£o (airplane)
  - o t√°xi (taxi)
  - o Uber (Uber)
  - a bicicleta (bicycle)
  - a moto (motorcycle)
  - o barco (boat)
  - a p√© (on foot)

- **Travel vocabulary:**
  - a viagem (trip/travel)
  - o aeroporto (airport)
  - a esta√ß√£o (station)
  - o bilhete (ticket)
  - a passagem (ticket - for travel)
  - a mala (suitcase)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Transportation prepositions - DE vs A P√â:**
  - **de** + vehicle: "Eu vou **de** carro" (I go by car)
  - **de** √¥nibus, de metr√¥, de t√°xi, de avi√£o, de trem, de bicicleta
  - **Exception: a p√©** (on foot): "Eu vou **a p√©**" (I go on foot)
  - NOT "de p√©" - this is an exception!

- **IR (to go) + means of transportation:**
  - Eu vou de √¥nibus. (I go by bus.)
  - Eu vou de carro. (I go by car.)
  - Ele vai a p√©. (He goes on foot.)
  - Structure: IR + de + transportation

- **PEGAR (to take/catch) + vehicle:**
  - Eu pego o √¥nibus. (I take/catch the bus.)
  - Eu pego o metr√¥. (I take the subway.)
  - "Pegar" means "to take/catch/get" a vehicle
  - Use definite article: pego **o** √¥nibus (not "pego √¥nibus")

- **Travel expressions with PARA:**
  - Eu vou **para** S√£o Paulo. (I'm going to S√£o Paulo.)
  - Eu viajo **para** o Brasil. (I'm traveling to Brazil.)
  - Use PARA (to/toward) for destination

**Practice format:**
- Name transportation with correct articles
- Practice "de + vehicle": "Eu vou de √¥nibus"
- Use pegar + vehicle: "Eu pego o metr√¥"
- Describe travel: "Eu viajo para S√£o Paulo de avi√£o"
- Ask/answer transportation questions

**Student can now:**
- Name 11 modes of transportation
- Use correct preposition (de) with vehicles
- Use "a p√©" correctly for walking
- Express how they get places: "Eu vou de carro"
- Talk about travel plans and destinations

**Typical sentences:**
- Eu vou de √¥nibus. (I go by bus.)
- Eu vou para o trabalho de carro. (I go to work by car.)
- Ela vai a p√©. (She goes on foot.)
- Eu pego o metr√¥ todos os dias. (I take the subway every day.)
- Eu viajo de avi√£o. (I travel by plane.)
- Eu vou para S√£o Paulo amanh√£. (I'm going to S√£o Paulo tomorrow.)
- Quanto custa a passagem de √¥nibus? (How much does the bus ticket cost?)

**Sample conversation:**
```
A: Como voc√™ vai para o trabalho?
   (How do you go to work?)
B: Eu vou de metr√¥. √â r√°pido.
   (I go by subway. It's fast.)

A: Quanto tempo leva?
   (How much time does it take?)
B: Leva 30 minutos.
   (It takes 30 minutes.)

A: E no fim de semana, como voc√™ se move?
   (And on weekends, how do you get around?)
B: Eu geralmente vou de carro ou a p√©.
   (I usually go by car or on foot.)

A: Voc√™ vai viajar nas f√©rias?
   (Are you going to travel on vacation?)
B: Sim, eu vou para a praia de √¥nibus.
   (Yes, I'm going to the beach by bus.)
```

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ‚ùå "Eu vou em carro" (wrong preposition)
- ‚úÖ "Eu vou de carro" (correct - use "de")
- ‚ùå "Eu vou de p√©" (wrong - common mistake!)
- ‚úÖ "Eu vou a p√©" (correct - exception to the rule)
- ‚ùå "Eu pego √¥nibus" (missing article)
- ‚úÖ "Eu pego o √¥nibus" (correct - need article with pegar)
- ‚ùå "Eu vou para o trabalho em metr√¥" (wrong preposition)
- ‚úÖ "Eu vou para o trabalho de metr√¥" (correct)

**Transportation Preposition Rule:**

**Use DE with all vehicles:**
- de carro (by car)
- de √¥nibus (by bus)
- de metr√¥ (by subway)
- de t√°xi (by taxi)
- de Uber (by Uber)
- de avi√£o (by plane)
- de trem (by train)
- de bicicleta (by bicycle)
- de moto (by motorcycle)
- de barco (by boat)

**EXCEPTION - Use A P√â:**
- a p√© (on foot) - NOT "de p√©"!

**PEGAR (to take/catch) - Irregular verb:**
Present tense:
- eu pego (I take)
- voc√™ pega (you take)
- ele/ela pega (he/she takes)
- n√≥s pegamos (we take)
- voc√™s pegam (you all take)
- eles/elas pegam (they take)

Common uses:
- pegar o √¥nibus (take the bus)
- pegar o metr√¥ (take the subway)
- pegar um t√°xi (catch a taxi)
- pegar o trem (catch the train)

**Brazilian Transportation Context:**
- **√înibus** is the most common public transport in most cities
- **Metr√¥** exists in major cities (S√£o Paulo, Rio, Bras√≠lia, etc.)
- **Uber** is very popular and common in Brazil
- Many people go **a p√©** in city centers
- Traffic (tr√¢nsito) can be very heavy in big cities

**Distance and Time:**
- longe (far): "O trabalho √© longe." (Work is far.)
- perto (near): "A escola √© perto." (The school is near.)
- Quanto tempo leva? (How long does it take?)
- Leva 30 minutos. (It takes 30 minutes.)

**Asking About Transportation:**
- Como voc√™ vai para...? (How do you get to...?)
- Quanto tempo leva? (How long does it take?)
- Quanto custa? (How much does it cost?)
- Onde eu pego o √¥nibus? (Where do I catch the bus?)
- Que √¥nibus vai para...? (Which bus goes to...?)

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 7: Places ‚Üí "Eu vou para o trabalho de carro"
- Unit 26: Future (IR + infinitive) ‚Üí using IR for destinations
- Unit 59: Directions ‚Üí combining with transportation
- Unit 62: Frequency ‚Üí "Eu pego o metr√¥ todos os dias"
- Unit 48: Time ‚Üí "Leva 30 minutos"

**Key Learning:**
- 11 modes of transportation vocabulary
- Use DE with all vehicles (de carro, de √¥nibus, de avi√£o)
- Exception: A P√â (on foot) - not "de p√©"!
- PEGAR + article + vehicle (pego o √¥nibus)
- Essential for daily life, describing routine, travel

**Why This Unit:**
- **FOUNDATIONAL:** Transportation is essential daily vocabulary
- Natural progression: can describe daily activities, now how you get there

### Unit 66: Hobbies and Leisure Activities (Hobbies e Atividades de Lazer)

**New vocabulary:**
- **Sports and activities:**
  - jogar futebol (to play soccer)
  - jogar v√¥lei (to play volleyball)
  - jogar basquete (to play basketball)
  - nadar (to swim)
  - correr (to run)
  - caminhar (to walk/hike)
  - dan√ßar (to dance)
  - cantar (to sing)

- **Leisure activities:**
  - ler (to read)
  - escrever (to write)
  - desenhar (to draw)
  - pintar (to paint)
  - tocar (to play instrument)
  - ouvir m√∫sica (to listen to music)
  - assistir TV (to watch TV)
  - assistir filmes (to watch movies)
  - jogar videogame (to play video games)
  - viajar (to travel)
  - cozinhar (to cook)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **JOGAR vs TOCAR - Critical distinction:**
  - **JOGAR** = play SPORTS/GAMES
    - jogar futebol (play soccer)
    - jogar v√¥lei (play volleyball)
    - jogar videogame (play video games)
    - jogar cartas (play cards)
  - **TOCAR** = play MUSICAL INSTRUMENTS
    - tocar viol√£o (play guitar)
    - tocar piano (play piano)
    - tocar bateria (play drums)
  - **Do NOT confuse these two!**

- **GOSTAR DE + infinitive (to like to...):**
  - Eu gosto de ler. (I like to read.)
  - Ela gosta de nadar. (She likes to swim.)
  - Structure: gostar de + infinitive verb

- **Frequency with hobbies:**
  - Combining frequency adverbs (Unit 63) with hobbies:
  - Eu **sempre** jogo futebol. (I always play soccer.)
  - Eu **√†s vezes** leio. (I sometimes read.)

- **No article with sports after JOGAR:**
  - ‚úÖ Eu jogo futebol. (I play soccer.) - NO article
  - ‚ùå Eu jogo o futebol. (wrong - don't use article)
  - Exception: specific game/match uses article
  - "Eu vou jogar o jogo" (I'm going to play the game - specific)

**Practice format:**
- Name hobbies and activities
- Use gostar de + infinitive: "Eu gosto de nadar"
- Practice JOGAR vs TOCAR distinction
- Describe hobbies with frequency: "Eu sempre leio"
- Ask about others' hobbies

**Student can now:**
- Name 19 common hobbies and leisure activities
- Use JOGAR correctly for sports/games
- Use TOCAR correctly for instruments
- Express hobby preferences: "Eu gosto de ler"
- Combine hobbies with frequency adverbs

**Typical sentences:**
- Eu jogo futebol todo s√°bado. (I play soccer every Saturday.)
- Eu gosto de ler livros. (I like to read books.)
- Ela toca piano. (She plays piano.)
- Eu gosto de assistir filmes. (I like to watch movies.)
- N√≥s jogamos v√¥lei na praia. (We play volleyball on the beach.)
- Eu corro todos os dias. (I run every day.)
- Eu ou√ßo m√∫sica quando estudo. (I listen to music when I study.)

**Sample conversation:**
```
A: O que voc√™ gosta de fazer no tempo livre?
   (What do you like to do in your free time?)
B: Eu gosto de jogar futebol e ler.
   (I like to play soccer and read.)

A: Voc√™ joga futebol com que frequ√™ncia?
   (How often do you play soccer?)

   (I play every Saturday with my friends.)

   (Do you play any instrument?)

   (And what do you read?)
```

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ‚ùå "Eu toco futebol" (wrong - sports use JOGAR)
- ‚úÖ "Eu jogo futebol" (correct)
- ‚ùå "Eu jogo viol√£o" (wrong - instruments use TOCAR)
- ‚úÖ "Eu toco viol√£o" (correct)
- ‚ùå "Eu jogo o futebol" (wrong - no article with sports)
- ‚úÖ "Eu jogo futebol" (correct)
- ‚ùå "Eu gosto nadar" (missing "de")
- ‚úÖ "Eu gosto de nadar" (correct - gostar requires "de")

**JOGAR vs TOCAR - Complete Guide:**

**Use JOGAR for:**
- **Sports:** futebol, v√¥lei, basquete, t√™nis
- **Games:** videogame, cartas, xadrez (chess)
- **General "play" meaning:** jogar bola (play ball)

Examples:
- Eu jogo futebol. (I play soccer.)
- Ele joga videogame. (He plays video games.)
- N√≥s jogamos cartas. (We play cards.)

**Use TOCAR for:**
- **Musical instruments:** viol√£o, piano, bateria, guitarra
- **Literally means "to touch"** but used for instruments

Examples:
- Eu toco piano. (I play piano.)
- Ela toca viol√£o. (She plays guitar.)
- Eles tocam bateria. (They play drums.)

**No Article with Sports:**
When using JOGAR with sports, NO article is needed:
- ‚úÖ jogar futebol (play soccer)
- ‚úÖ jogar t√™nis (play tennis)
- ‚úÖ jogar basquete (play basketball)
- ‚ùå jogar o futebol (wrong - no article)

**UNLESS referring to a specific game:**
- Vou jogar **o jogo** amanh√£. (I'm going to play the game tomorrow.)
- Assistimos **o jogo** ontem. (We watched the game yesterday.)

**Musical Instruments:**
Common instruments in Portuguese:
- o viol√£o (acoustic guitar)
- a guitarra (electric guitar)
- o piano (piano)
- a bateria (drums)
- o baixo (bass)
- a flauta (flute)
- o violino (violin)

**Brazilian Sports Culture:**
- **Futebol** (soccer) is THE national sport
- Almost everyone plays or watches futebol
- Beach volleyball (v√¥lei de praia) is very popular
- Capoeira is a Brazilian martial art/dance
- Surfing is popular in coastal areas

**Asking About Hobbies:**
- O que voc√™ gosta de fazer no tempo livre? (What do you like to do in your free time?)
- Quais s√£o seus hobbies? (What are your hobbies?)
- Voc√™ pratica algum esporte? (Do you practice any sport?)
- Voc√™ toca algum instrumento? (Do you play any instrument?)

**Connecting to Previous Units:**

- 19 hobby and leisure activity verbs

### Unit 67: Technology and Communication (Tecnologia e Comunica√ß√£o)

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**

**LIGAR - Two Main Meanings:**

- Eu ligo o computador. (I turn on the computer.)

**Opposite: DESLIGAR (to turn off, to hang up):**
- Eu desligo o celular. (I turn off the cell phone.)
- Eu desligo a chamada. (I hang up the call.)

- Video calls: "chamada de v√≠deo" or "videochamada"

- **Area code** (c√≥digo de √°rea): (11) for S√£o Paulo, (21) for Rio
- **Mobile numbers** start with 9
- Example: (11) 9-1234-5678

**Asking for Contact Information:**

- Qual √© a senha do WiFi? (What's the WiFi password?)
- Voc√™ tem internet? (Do you have internet?)

**Technology Verbs:**
- **usar** (to use): Eu uso o computador.
- **ligar** (to call/turn on): Eu ligo para voc√™.
- **desligar** (to turn off/hang up): Eu desligo o celular.
- **mandar** (to send): Eu mando mensagem.
- **enviar** (to send): Eu envio email.
- **receber** (to receive): Eu recebo mensagens.
- **responder** (to reply): Eu respondo r√°pido.

### Unit 68: Shopping and Money (Compras e Dinheiro)

**New vocabulary:**
- **Money:**
  - o dinheiro (money)
  - o real (Brazilian currency - singular)
  - os reais (Brazilian currency - plural)
  - a moeda (coin)
  - a nota (bill/banknote)
  - o cart√£o (card)
  - o cart√£o de cr√©dito (credit card)
  - o cart√£o de d√©bito (debit card)
  - o Pix (instant payment system)
  - o troco (change)

- **Shopping:**
  - a loja (store)
  - o mercado (market)
  - o supermercado (supermarket)
  - a farm√°cia (pharmacy)
  - comprar (to buy)
  - vender (to sell)
  - custar (to cost)
  - pagar (to pay)
  - o pre√ßo (price)
  - barato (cheap)
  - caro (expensive)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Brazilian currency: REAL/REAIS**
  - **Singular:** um real (R$ 1,00)
  - **Plural:** dois reais, tr√™s reais, cem reais
  - Written: R$ (s√≠mbolo do real)
  - R$ 10,00 = dez reais

- **CUSTAR (to cost) - special verb:**
  - **3rd person only** (like DOER in Unit 57)
  - Subject is the thing that costs, not the person!
  - **Singular:** custa (it costs)
  - **Plural:** custam (they cost)
  - Examples:
    - Quanto **custa**? (How much does it cost?)
    - **Custa** dez reais. (It costs ten reais.)
    - Os livros **custam** vinte reais. (The books cost twenty reais.)

- **PAGAR (to pay) - takes direct object OR por:**
  - Eu pago dez reais. (I pay ten reais.) - direct object
  - Eu pago **pelo** livro. (I pay for the book.) - por + o = pelo
  - Both structures are correct

- **PIX - Brazilian instant payment:**
  - Revolutionary payment system in Brazil (launched 2020)
  - Instant bank-to-bank transfer via phone
  - "Voc√™ aceita Pix?" (Do you accept Pix?)
  - "Eu fa√ßo um Pix" (I'll make a Pix payment)
  - Has largely replaced cash in Brazil!

**Practice format:**
- Name money vocabulary with correct articles
- Practice prices: "Custa dez reais"
- Use shopping verbs: comprar, vender, pagar
- Ask "Quanto custa?" (How much does it cost?)
- Describe payment methods: "Eu pago com cart√£o"

**Student can now:**
- Name 21 shopping and money terms
- Use CUSTAR correctly (3rd person only)
- Ask and understand prices in reais
- Talk about payment methods (Pix, card, cash)
- Describe shopping experiences

**Typical sentences:**
- Quanto custa? (How much does it cost?)
- Custa dez reais. (It costs ten reais.)
- Eu pago com cart√£o. (I pay with card.)
- Voc√™ aceita Pix? (Do you accept Pix?)
- Isso √© muito caro. (This is very expensive.)
- Eu compro no supermercado. (I buy at the supermarket.)
- Eu preciso de troco. (I need change.)

**Sample conversation:**
```
A: Quanto custa este livro?
   (How much does this book cost?)
B: Custa vinte e cinco reais.
   (It costs twenty-five reais.)

A: √â um pouco caro. Voc√™ tem mais barato?
   (It's a bit expensive. Do you have cheaper?)
B: Sim, esse aqui custa quinze reais.
   (Yes, this one costs fifteen reais.)

A: √ìtimo! Eu levo. Voc√™ aceita Pix?
   (Great! I'll take it. Do you accept Pix?)
B: Sim, aceitamos Pix, cart√£o, e dinheiro.
   (Yes, we accept Pix, card, and cash.)
```

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ‚ùå "Quanto eu custo?" (wrong - YOU don't cost, things cost)
- ‚úÖ "Quanto custa?" (correct - thing is subject)
- ‚ùå "Custa dois real" (missing plural)
- ‚úÖ "Custa dois reais" (correct - plural)
- ‚ùå "dez real" (wrong - use plural)
- ‚úÖ "dez reais" (correct)
- ‚ùå "Eu pago por cart√£o" (awkward)
- ‚úÖ "Eu pago com cart√£o" (correct - use "com")

**CUSTAR (to cost) - Special Verb:**

Like DOER (to hurt), CUSTAR uses 3rd person only:
- **Singular:** custa (one thing costs)
  - O livro custa dez reais. (The book costs ten reais.)
  - Quanto custa? (How much does it cost?)

- **Plural:** custam (multiple things cost)
  - Os livros custam vinte reais. (The books cost twenty reais.)
  - Quanto custam? (How much do they cost?)

**The thing that costs is the SUBJECT**, not the person buying!

**Brazilian Currency: REAL (R$)**
- **Singular:** um real (1 real)
- **Plural:** reais (multiple reais)
- **Symbol:** R$
- **Written format:** R$ 10,00 (ten reais)
- **Decimal:** comma (,) not period
  - R$ 10,50 = dez reais e cinquenta centavos
  - Period (.) separates thousands: R$ 1.000,00 (one thousand reais)

**Money denominations:**
- **Coins (moedas):** 5, 10, 25, 50 centavos, 1 real
- **Bills (notas):** R$ 2, 5, 10, 20, 50, 100, 200

**PIX - Brazilian Payment Revolution:**
- **Launched 2020** by Brazilian Central Bank
- **Instant transfers** between any banks
- **Use:** phone number, email, CPF, or QR code
- **Free for individuals**
- **Dominant payment method** in Brazil now
- "Fazer um Pix" (to make a Pix payment)
- "Mandar um Pix" (to send a Pix)
- Has revolutionized Brazilian economy!

**Payment Methods:**
- **dinheiro** (cash): Eu pago em dinheiro.
- **cart√£o de cr√©dito** (credit card): Eu pago com cart√£o de cr√©dito.
- **cart√£o de d√©bito** (debit card): Eu pago com d√©bito.
- **Pix** (instant payment): Eu fa√ßo um Pix. / Eu pago com Pix.

**Shopping Vocabulary:**
- **comprar** (to buy): Eu compro p√£o.
- **vender** (to sell): Eles vendem frutas.
- **custar** (to cost): Custa dez reais.
- **pagar** (to pay): Eu pago com Pix.

**Asking About Price:**
- Quanto custa? (How much does it cost?)
- Qual √© o pre√ßo? (What's the price?)
- Quanto √©? (How much is it?)
- Tem desconto? (Is there a discount?)

**Describing Price:**
- **caro** (expensive): Isso √© muito caro.
- **barato** (cheap): Isso √© barato.
- **em conta** (affordable): √â bem em conta.
- **bom pre√ßo** (good price): √â um bom pre√ßo.

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 15-16: Numbers ‚Üí prices in reais
- Unit 38: Questions ‚Üí "Quanto custa?"
- Unit 64: Food ‚Üí "Eu compro comida no supermercado"
- Unit 61: Places ‚Üí "loja", "mercado", "farm√°cia"
- Unit 19: Precisar de ‚Üí "Eu preciso de troco"

**Key Learning:**
- 21 shopping and money vocabulary terms
- CUSTAR is 3rd person only (custa/custam) - thing is subject
- Brazilian currency: real (singular), reais (plural)
- PIX is dominant payment method in Brazil (revolutionary!)
- Essential for shopping, transactions, daily life

### Unit 69: Professions and Work (Profiss√µes e Trabalho)

**New vocabulary:**
- **Common professions:**
  - o m√©dico / a m√©dica (doctor)
  - o professor / a professora (teacher)
  - o enfermeiro / a enfermeira (nurse)
  - o engenheiro / a engenheira (engineer)
  - o advogado / a advogada (lawyer)
  - o dentista / a dentista (dentist - same form!)
  - o jornalista / a jornalista (journalist - same form!)
  - o estudante / a estudante (student - same form!)
  - o cozinheiro / a cozinheira (cook/chef)
  - o gar√ßom / a gar√ßonete (waiter/waitress)
  - o vendedor / a vendedora (salesperson)
  - o empres√°rio / a empres√°ria (businessperson)
  - o artista / a artista (artist - same form!)
  - o policial / a policial (police officer - same form!)

- **Work vocabulary:**
  - o trabalho (work/job)
  - a empresa (company)
  - o escrit√≥rio (office)
  - o chefe / a chefe (boss)
  - o colega / a colega (colleague - same form!)
  - o sal√°rio (salary)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Gender agreement in professions:**
  - Most professions change -o to -a for feminine:
    - m√©dico ‚Üí m√©dica
    - professor ‚Üí professora
    - cozinheiro ‚Üí cozinheira

  - Professions ending in -ista, -nte stay the SAME:
    - o dentista / a dentista (same word!)
    - o estudante / a estudante (same word!)
    - o artista / a artista (same word!)
    - Only the article changes!

- **Professions with unique feminine forms:**
  - o gar√ßom / a gar√ßonete (waiter/waitress - completely different)
  - o ator / a atriz (actor/actress - different forms)

- **Talking about professions - Two structures:**

  **Structure 1: SER + profession (no article):**
  - Eu sou m√©dico. (I am a doctor.)
  - Ela √© professora. (She is a teacher.)
  - NO article needed in Portuguese!

  **Structure 2: TRABALHAR COMO (work as):**
  - Eu trabalho como m√©dico. (I work as a doctor.)
  - Ela trabalha como professora. (She works as a teacher.)

- **TRABALHAR EM (work at) vs TRABALHAR COMO (work as):**
  - **EM** = location: "Eu trabalho **em** um hospital" (I work at a hospital)
  - **COMO** = profession: "Eu trabalho **como** m√©dico" (I work as a doctor)
  - Can combine: "Eu trabalho como m√©dico em um hospital"

**Practice format:**
- Name professions with correct gender forms
- Practice "sou + profession" (no article)
- Use "trabalhar como" for professions
- Use "trabalhar em" for locations
- Describe what family members do

**Student can now:**
- Name 20+ common professions with correct gender
- Use SER + profession correctly (without article)
- Distinguish trabalhar EM (location) vs COMO (profession)
- Ask and answer about occupations
- Describe workplace and colleagues

**Typical sentences:**
- Eu sou professor. (I am a teacher.)
- Ela √© m√©dica. (She is a doctor.)
- Eu trabalho como engenheiro. (I work as an engineer.)
- Eu trabalho em um hospital. (I work at a hospital.)
- Meu pai √© advogado. (My father is a lawyer.)
- Ela trabalha como jornalista em S√£o Paulo. (She works as a journalist in S√£o Paulo.)
- O que voc√™ faz? - Eu sou dentista. (What do you do? - I'm a dentist.)

**Sample conversation:**
```
A: O que voc√™ faz?
   (What do you do?)
B: Eu sou professor. E voc√™?
   (I'm a teacher. And you?)

A: Eu trabalho como enfermeira.
   (I work as a nurse.)
B: Onde voc√™ trabalha?
   (Where do you work?)

A: Eu trabalho em um hospital no centro.
   (I work at a hospital downtown.)
B: Voc√™ gosta do seu trabalho?
   (Do you like your job?)

A: Sim, muito! √â cansativo, mas eu gosto.
   (Yes, a lot! It's tiring, but I like it.)
```

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ‚ùå "Eu sou um m√©dico" (wrong - no article needed)
- ‚úÖ "Eu sou m√©dico" (correct - no article)
- ‚ùå "Ela √© um professora" (wrong - no article + wrong article)
- ‚úÖ "Ela √© professora" (correct)
- ‚ùå "Eu trabalho como em hospital" (wrong - mixing structures)
- ‚úÖ "Eu trabalho em um hospital" (correct)
- ‚ùå "o dentisto" / "a dentisto" (wrong - doesn't change)
- ‚úÖ "o dentista" / "a dentista" (correct - same form)

**SER + Profession - NO ARTICLE:**

This is a MAJOR difference from English:
- **English:** I am **a** doctor. (uses article)
- **Portuguese:** Eu sou m√©dico. (NO article)

Examples:
- Eu sou professor. (I am a teacher.)
- Ela √© engenheira. (She is an engineer.)
- Eles s√£o estudantes. (They are students.)
- N√≥s somos advogados. (We are lawyers.)

**Exception:** When you add an adjective, USE article:
- Eu sou **um bom** m√©dico. (I am a good doctor.)
- Ela √© **uma** professora **excelente**. (She is an excellent teacher.)

**Professions That DON'T Change Form:**

These professions use the SAME word for masculine and feminine:
- **-ista endings:**
  - o/a dentista (dentist)
  - o/a jornalista (journalist)
  - o/a artista (artist)
  - o/a pianista (pianist)

- **-nte endings:**
  - o/a estudante (student)
  - o/a assistente (assistant)
  - o/a gerente (manager)

- **-al endings:**
  - o/a policial (police officer)

**Only the ARTICLE changes:**
- o dentista (male dentist)
- a dentista (female dentist)

**TRABALHAR - Three Structures:**

**1. TRABALHAR (alone) = to work:**
- Eu trabalho muito. (I work a lot.)
- Ela trabalha de segunda a sexta. (She works Monday to Friday.)

**2. TRABALHAR EM = work at/in (location):**
- Eu trabalho **em** uma empresa. (I work at a company.)
- Ela trabalha **em** S√£o Paulo. (She works in S√£o Paulo.)

**3. TRABALHAR COMO = work as (profession):**
- Eu trabalho **como** professor. (I work as a teacher.)
- Ele trabalha **como** vendedor. (He works as a salesperson.)

**Combining:**
- Eu trabalho **como** m√©dica **em** um hospital. (I work as a doctor at a hospital.)

**Asking About Professions:**
- O que voc√™ faz? (What do you do?)
- Qual √© sua profiss√£o? (What is your profession?)
- Voc√™ trabalha com o qu√™? (What do you work with?)
- Onde voc√™ trabalha? (Where do you work?)
- Em que voc√™ trabalha? (What do you work in?)

**Brazilian Work Culture:**
- Standard work week: Monday-Friday (segunda a sexta)
- Work hours often 9am-6pm (nove √†s dezoito)
- Lunch break: usually 1-2 hours
- "CLT" (Consolida√ß√£o das Leis do Trabalho) = formal employment contract
- Many people work informally ("trabalho informal")

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 1: SER ‚Üí "Eu sou professor"
- Unit 5: TRABALHAR ‚Üí now expanding with professions
- Unit 9: Places ‚Üí "Eu trabalho em S√£o Paulo"
- Unit 58: Family ‚Üí "Meu pai √© advogado"
- Unit 38: Questions ‚Üí "O que voc√™ faz?"

**Key Learning:**
- 20+ common professions with correct gender forms
- SER + profession WITHOUT article (major difference from English)
- Trabalhar EM (location) vs Trabalhar COMO (profession)
- Professions ending in -ista/-nte/-al don't change form
- Essential for introductions, describing self and others

**Why This Unit:**
- **FOUNDATIONAL:** Profession is one of first things people ask
- Natural progression: can describe activities, now describe occupation
- Ultra-granular: focuses ONLY on professions and work
- Practical: immediate use for introductions, networking, conversation
- Addresses common mistake: article with professions

### Unit 70: Health and Medical Basics (Sa√∫de e M√©dico)

**New vocabulary:**
- **Health conditions:**
  - doente (sick)
  - saud√°vel (healthy)
  - a febre (fever)
  - a tosse (cough)
  - o resfriado (cold/flu)
  - a gripe (flu)
  - a dor (pain)
  - o rem√©dio (medicine)
  - o comprimido (pill)
  - a receita (prescription)

- **Medical places:**
  - o hospital (hospital)
  - a cl√≠nica (clinic)
  - o consult√≥rio (doctor's office)
  - o posto de sa√∫de (health center)
  - a farm√°cia (pharmacy)

- **Medical professionals (review + expand):**
  - o m√©dico / a m√©dica (doctor)
  - o enfermeiro / a enfermeira (nurse)
  - o dentista / a dentista (dentist)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **ESTAR doente (to be sick) - uses ESTAR:**
  - Eu **estou** doente. (I am sick - temporary condition)
  - NOT "sou doente" - that would mean permanently sick!
  - Temporary health states always use ESTAR

- **TER (to have) with illnesses:**
  - Eu **tenho** febre. (I have a fever.)
  - Eu **tenho** tosse. (I have a cough.)
  - Eu **tenho** gripe. (I have the flu.)
  - Use TER (not ESTAR) for specific symptoms/illnesses

- **ESTAR COM (to be with) - alternative structure:**
  - Eu **estou com** febre. (I am with fever = I have a fever.)
  - Eu **estou com** dor de cabe√ßa. (I have a headache.)
  - Both TER and ESTAR COM are correct!

- **Illness expressions:**
  - estar doente (to be sick)
  - estar bem (to be well)
  - estar mal (to feel bad/unwell)
  - ficar doente (to get/become sick)
  - melhorar (to get better)
  - piorar (to get worse)

**Practice format:**
- Describe symptoms: "Eu tenho febre"
- Use ESTAR for general sick state: "Estou doente"
- Practice TER vs ESTAR COM for symptoms
- Ask how someone is: "Como voc√™ est√°?"
- Describe at doctor: "Eu tenho dor de..."

**Student can now:**
- Describe common health problems and symptoms
- Use ESTAR correctly for being sick
- Use TER for specific illnesses/symptoms
- Name medical places and professionals
- Ask for medicine and describe problems to doctor

**Typical sentences:**
- Eu estou doente. (I am sick.)
- Eu tenho febre. (I have a fever.)
- Eu estou com dor de cabe√ßa. (I have a headache.)
- Eu preciso de um m√©dico. (I need a doctor.)
- Eu vou √† farm√°cia. (I'm going to the pharmacy.)
- Ela est√° com gripe. (She has the flu.)
- Eu preciso de rem√©dio. (I need medicine.)

**Sample conversation:**
```
A: Como voc√™ est√°?
   (How are you?)
B: N√£o estou bem. Estou doente.
   (I'm not well. I'm sick.)

A: O que voc√™ tem?
   (What's wrong? / What do you have?)
B: Eu tenho febre e dor de cabe√ßa.
   (I have a fever and headache.)

A: Voc√™ foi ao m√©dico?
   (Did you go to the doctor?)
B: N√£o, eu vou hoje.
   (No, I'm going today.)

A: Melhoras!
   (Get well! / Feel better!)
B: Obrigado!
   (Thank you!)
```

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ‚ùå "Eu sou doente" (wrong - implies permanently sick)
- ‚úÖ "Eu estou doente" (correct - temporary state)
- ‚ùå "Eu estou febre" (wrong - febre is noun, needs TER)
- ‚úÖ "Eu tenho febre" (correct)
- ‚ùå "Eu tenho doente" (wrong - doente is adjective, needs ESTAR)
- ‚úÖ "Eu estou doente" (correct)

**ESTAR vs SER with Health:**

**Use ESTAR for temporary health states:**
- Eu **estou** doente. (I am sick - temporary)
- Eu **estou** bem. (I am well - temporary state)
- Eu **estou** mal. (I feel bad - temporary)

**SER would imply permanent condition:**
- Eu **sou** saud√°vel. (I am healthy - generally, as a trait)
- But NOT "Eu sou doente" (sounds like chronic/permanent illness)

**TER vs ESTAR COM - Both Correct:**

**Use TER (more direct):**
- Eu **tenho** febre. (I have a fever.)
- Eu **tenho** tosse. (I have a cough.)
- Eu **tenho** gripe. (I have the flu.)
- Eu **tenho** dor. (I have pain.)

**Use ESTAR COM (more descriptive):**
- Eu **estou com** febre. (I am with fever = I have a fever.)
- Eu **estou com** tosse. (I have a cough.)
- Eu **estou com** gripe. (I have the flu.)
- Eu **estou com** dor. (I have pain.)

Both structures mean the same thing! Choose either.

**Common Illness Expressions:**
Building on Unit 57 (body parts):
- dor de cabe√ßa (headache)
- dor de barriga (stomachache)
- dor de garganta (sore throat)
- dor de dente (toothache)
- dor nas costas (back pain)
- dor no peito (chest pain)

Structure: dor + de/em/no/na + body part

**Describing Symptoms to Doctor:**
- Eu tenho... (I have...)
- Eu sinto... (I feel...)
- Minha cabe√ßa d√≥i. (My head hurts.)
- Eu n√£o estou bem. (I'm not well.)
- Desde quando? (Since when?)
- H√° dois dias. (For two days.)

**At the Pharmacy:**
- Eu preciso de rem√©dio para... (I need medicine for...)
- Tem algo para dor de cabe√ßa? (Do you have something for headache?)
- Precisa de receita? (Does it need a prescription?)
- Quanto custa? (How much does it cost?)

**Brazilian Healthcare System:**
- **SUS** (Sistema √önico de Sa√∫de) = public healthcare (free)
- **Plano de sa√∫de** = private health insurance
- **Posto de sa√∫de** = public health center (neighborhood clinics)
- **Farm√°cia** = pharmacy (very accessible, many on every street)
- Some medicines available over-the-counter (sem receita)

**Getting Better:**
- melhorar (to get better): "Eu estou melhorando." (I'm getting better.)
- piorar (to get worse): "Eu estou piorando." (I'm getting worse.)
- recuperar (to recover): "Eu me recuperei." (I recovered.)
- curar (to cure/heal): "O rem√©dio me curou." (The medicine cured me.)

**Well Wishes:**
- Melhoras! (Get well!)
- Fique bem! (Get well! / Be well!)
- Espero que voc√™ melhore logo! (I hope you get better soon!)
- Cuide-se! (Take care!)

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 56: Body parts ‚Üí "dor de cabe√ßa", "dor nas costas"
- Unit 58: Feelings ‚Üí "Como voc√™ est√°?" "Eu estou mal"
- Unit 5: ESTAR ‚Üí "Eu estou doente"
- Unit 16: TER ‚Üí "Eu tenho febre"
- Unit 69: Professions ‚Üí "m√©dico", "enfermeiro"

**Key Learning:**
- Health vocabulary: doente, febre, tosse, resfriado, gripe, rem√©dio
- ESTAR doente (temporary sick state) - NOT "sou doente"
- TER or ESTAR COM for symptoms (both correct)
- Medical places: hospital, cl√≠nica, consult√≥rio, farm√°cia
- Essential for describing health problems, getting help

**Why This Unit:**
- **FOUNDATIONAL:** Health vocabulary is critical for safety
- Natural progression: have body parts (56), now describe problems
- Ultra-granular: focuses ONLY on basic health vocabulary
- Practical: immediate use for doctor visits, pharmacy, emergencies
- Safety: essential vocabulary for travelers and residents

### Unit 71: Commands/Imperative Mood (Imperativo)

**New vocabulary:**
- **Common command verbs:**
  - falar (to speak) ‚Üí Fale! (Speak!)
  - comer (to eat) ‚Üí Coma! (Eat!)
  - abrir (to open) ‚Üí Abra! (Open!)
  - fechar (to close) ‚Üí Feche! (Close!)
  - esperar (to wait) ‚Üí Espere! (Wait!)
  - vir (to come) ‚Üí Venha! (Come!)
  - ir (to go) ‚Üí V√°! (Go!)
  - fazer (to do) ‚Üí Fa√ßa! (Do!)
  - sentar (to sit) ‚Üí Sente-se! (Sit down!)
  - levantar (to get up) ‚Üí Levante-se! (Get up!)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Imperative mood - Commands:**
  - Used to give orders, instructions, requests
  - Different forms for voc√™, voc√™s, and n√≥s
  - This unit focuses on **voc√™** form (most common)

- **Forming voc√™ commands:**

  **For -AR verbs:** Change -a to -e
  - falar ‚Üí voc√™ fala ‚Üí **Fale!** (Speak!)
  - comprar ‚Üí voc√™ compra ‚Üí **Compre!** (Buy!)
  - fechar ‚Üí voc√™ fecha ‚Üí **Feche!** (Close!)

  **For -ER/-IR verbs:** Change -e to -a
  - comer ‚Üí voc√™ come ‚Üí **Coma!** (Eat!)
  - abrir ‚Üí voc√™ abre ‚Üí **Abra!** (Open!)
  - escrever ‚Üí voc√™ escreve ‚Üí **Escreva!** (Write!)

- **Pattern: Flip the present tense vowel!**
  - -AR verbs: -a ‚Üí -e
  - -ER/-IR verbs: -e ‚Üí -a

- **Negative commands:**
  - Add **N√ÉO** before the verb:
  - **N√£o fale!** (Don't speak!)
  - **N√£o coma!** (Don't eat!)
  - **N√£o abra!** (Don't open!)

- **Common irregular imperatives:**
  - **ir** ‚Üí **V√°!** (Go!)
  - **vir** ‚Üí **Venha!** (Come!)
  - **fazer** ‚Üí **Fa√ßa!** (Do!)
  - **ser** ‚Üí **Seja!** (Be!)
  - **ter** ‚Üí **Tenha!** (Have!)
  - **dar** ‚Üí **D√™!** (Give!)
  - **estar** ‚Üí **Esteja!** (Be!)

**Practice format:**
- Form commands from regular verbs: falar ‚Üí Fale!
- Practice irregular commands: ir ‚Üí V√°!
- Use negative commands: N√£o fale!
- Give instructions: "Abra o livro"
- Polite requests with "por favor"

**Student can now:**
- Give direct commands in Portuguese
- Form regular imperative (flip vowel rule)
- Use common irregular imperatives
- Make negative commands (n√£o + imperative)
- Give polite instructions with "por favor"

**Typical sentences:**
- Fale portugu√™s! (Speak Portuguese!)
- Coma devagar! (Eat slowly!)
- Venha aqui! (Come here!)
- V√° para casa! (Go home!)
- N√£o fale alto! (Don't speak loudly!)
- Abra a porta, por favor. (Open the door, please.)
- Espere um momento! (Wait a moment!)

**Sample conversation:**
```
Professor: Abram os livros na p√°gina 10.
           (Open the books to page 10.)
           [Note: Abram = voc√™s form, but you'll learn that later]

Student: Qual p√°gina?
         (Which page?)

Professor: P√°gina 10. Agora leiam o texto.
           (Page 10. Now read the text.)

Student: Em voz alta?
         (Out loud?)

Professor: N√£o, leiam em sil√™ncio.
           (No, read silently.)
```

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ‚ùå "Fala portugu√™s!" (wrong - that's present tense, not command)
- ‚úÖ "Fale portugu√™s!" (correct - imperative form)
- ‚ùå "Come isso!" (wrong - present tense)
- ‚úÖ "Coma isso!" (correct - imperative)
- ‚ùå "Vai aqui!" (wrong - present tense)
- ‚úÖ "V√° aqui!" or better "Venha aqui!" (correct - imperative)

**Imperative Formation - The Vowel Flip:**

**Regular -AR verbs (change -a to -e):**
- falar ‚Üí voc√™ fal**a** ‚Üí Fal**e**! (Speak!)
- comprar ‚Üí voc√™ compr**a** ‚Üí Compr**e**! (Buy!)
- estudar ‚Üí voc√™ estud**a** ‚Üí Estud**e**! (Study!)
- trabalhar ‚Üí voc√™ trabalh**a** ‚Üí Trabalh**e**! (Work!)

**Regular -ER/-IR verbs (change -e to -a):**
- comer ‚Üí voc√™ com**e** ‚Üí Com**a**! (Eat!)
- beber ‚Üí voc√™ beb**e** ‚Üí Beb**a**! (Drink!)
- abrir ‚Üí voc√™ abr**e** ‚Üí Abr**a**! (Open!)
- escrever ‚Üí voc√™ escrev**e** ‚Üí Escrev**a**! (Write!)

**Memory trick:** The vowel "flips" from the present tense voc√™ form!

**Common Irregular Imperatives:**

These DON'T follow the flip pattern:
- **ir** ‚Üí **V√°!** (Go!) - NOT "Vai"
- **vir** ‚Üí **Venha!** (Come!) - NOT "Vem"
- **fazer** ‚Üí **Fa√ßa!** (Do/Make!)
- **ser** ‚Üí **Seja!** (Be!)
- **ter** ‚Üí **Tenha!** (Have!)
- **dar** ‚Üí **D√™!** (Give!)
- **estar** ‚Üí **Esteja!** (Be!)
- **p√¥r** ‚Üí **Ponha!** (Put!)

Must memorize these!

**Negative Commands:**

Simply add **N√ÉO** before the imperative:
- **N√£o fale!** (Don't speak!)
- **N√£o coma!** (Don't eat!)
- **N√£o venha!** (Don't come!)
- **N√£o v√°!** (Don't go!)
- **N√£o fa√ßa isso!** (Don't do that!)

Same form for negative - just add n√£o!

**Polite Commands:**

Add **POR FAVOR** to soften the command:
- **Fale mais devagar, por favor.** (Speak more slowly, please.)
- **Venha aqui, por favor.** (Come here, please.)
- **Abra a janela, por favor.** (Open the window, please.)

Or use conditional (more advanced):
- **Voc√™ poderia falar mais devagar?** (Could you speak more slowly?)

**Common Command Phrases:**
- Espere! (Wait!)
- Olhe! (Look!)
- Escute! (Listen!)
- Venha! (Come!)
- V√°! (Go!)
- Pare! (Stop!)
- Siga! (Follow! / Continue!)
- Entre! (Enter! / Come in!)
- Saia! (Leave! / Get out!)
- Sente-se! (Sit down!)
- Levante-se! (Stand up!)

**Commands with Reflexive Verbs:**

Attach the pronoun to the end with hyphen:
- sentar-se ‚Üí **Sente-se!** (Sit down!)
- levantar-se ‚Üí **Levante-se!** (Get up!)
- calar-se ‚Üí **Cale-se!** (Be quiet!)

For negative, pronoun goes before verb:
- **N√£o se sente!** (Don't sit down!)
- **N√£o se levante!** (Don't get up!)

**Signs and Instructions:**

You'll see imperatives everywhere:
- **Empurre** (Push)
- **Puxe** (Pull)
- **Pare** (Stop)
- **Siga** (Go / Continue)
- **N√£o entre** (Don't enter)
- **Proibido fumar** (No smoking - literally "Prohibited to smoke")

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- All regular verbs from Units 1-2, 8-10, etc. ‚Üí now in command form
- Unit 35: Reflexive pronouns ‚Üí "Sente-se!" "Levante-se!"
- Unit 15: Negation ‚Üí "N√£o fale!"
- Commands use vocabulary from all previous units

**Key Learning:**
- Imperative mood for commands and instructions
- Regular pattern: flip the vowel (-a‚Üîe) from voc√™ present tense
- Common irregular imperatives: V√°, Venha, Fa√ßa, Seja
- Negative commands: N√£o + imperative
- Essential for instructions, directions, requests

**Why This Unit:**
- **FOUNDATIONAL:** Commands are essential grammar structure
- Natural progression: know verbs, now use them as commands
- Ultra-granular: focuses ONLY on imperative mood (voc√™ form)
- Practical: immediate use for giving/receiving instructions
- Grammar milestone: major mood not yet covered

### Unit 72: Demonstratives - This/That (Demonstrativos)

**New vocabulary:**
- **Demonstrative adjectives/pronouns:**
  - este/esta/estes/estas (this/these - near speaker)
  - esse/essa/esses/essas (that/those - near listener)
  - aquele/aquela/aqueles/aquelas (that/those - far from both)

- **Demonstrative pronouns (neuter):**
  - isto (this - abstract/general)
  - isso (that - abstract/general)
  - aquilo (that - abstract/general, far)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Three-way distinction in Portuguese:**

  Portuguese has THREE demonstratives, not two like English!

  **ESTE (this) - near the speaker:**
  - **Este** livro (this book - in my hand)
  - Near me, the person speaking
  - Equivalent to "this" in English

  **ESSE (that) - near the listener:**
  - **Esse** livro (that book - in your hand)
  - Near you, the person listening
  - Equivalent to "that" in English (near)

  **AQUELE (that) - far from both:**
  - **Aquele** livro (that book - over there)
  - Far from both speaker and listener
  - Equivalent to "that over there" in English

- **Gender and number agreement:**

  Demonstratives MUST agree with the noun:

  **Masculine singular:**
  - este livro (this book)
  - esse carro (that car)
  - aquele homem (that man over there)

  **Feminine singular:**
  - esta casa (this house)
  - essa mulher (that woman)
  - aquela loja (that store over there)

  **Masculine plural:**
  - estes livros (these books)
  - esses carros (those cars)
  - aqueles homens (those men over there)

  **Feminine plural:**
  - estas casas (these houses)
  - essas mulheres (those women)
  - aquelas lojas (those stores over there)

- **Demonstrative pronouns (replacing nouns):**
  - Eu quero **este**. (I want this one.)
  - Eu prefiro **aquele**. (I prefer that one over there.)
  - **Estas** s√£o minhas. (These are mine.)

- **Neuter demonstratives (for abstract things):**
  - **Isto** √© importante. (This is important.)
  - **Isso** √© verdade. (That is true.)
  - **Aquilo** √© estranho. (That is strange.)
  - Use when NOT referring to specific noun

**Practice format:**
- Point to objects: "Este livro", "Esse carro", "Aquele pr√©dio"
- Practice all gender/number combinations
- Use distance (near me, near you, over there)
- Replace nouns with pronouns: "Eu quero este"
- Use neuter for abstract: "Isto √© bom"

**Student can now:**
- Use three-way demonstrative system correctly
- Choose este/esse/aquele based on distance
- Make demonstratives agree in gender and number
- Use demonstrative pronouns (este, aquele)
- Use neuter demonstratives (isto, isso, aquilo)

**Typical sentences:**
- Este livro √© meu. (This book is mine - I have it)
- Esse livro √© seu? (Is that book yours? - you have it)
- Aquele livro √© caro. (That book is expensive - over there)
- Eu quero esta camisa. (I want this shirt.)
- Voc√™ gosta desses sapatos? (Do you like those shoes? - pointing to listener)
- Aquelas casas s√£o grandes. (Those houses are big - over there)
- Isto √© importante. (This is important.)

**Sample conversation:**
```
[In a store, looking at shirts]

A: Voc√™ gosta desta camisa?
   (Do you like this shirt? - speaker is holding it)
B: Qual? Essa que voc√™ est√° segurando?
   (Which one? That one you're holding? - near speaker)

A: Sim, esta aqui.
   (Yes, this one here.)
B: Eu prefiro aquela ali.
   (I prefer that one over there. - pointing to far shirt)

A: Aquela azul?
   (That blue one?)
B: Sim, aquela.
   (Yes, that one.)
```

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ‚ùå Using "ese" (Spanish) instead of "esse"
- ‚úÖ "esse" (correct - Portuguese spelling)
- ‚ùå "este casa" (wrong gender)
- ‚úÖ "esta casa" (correct - casa is feminine)
- ‚ùå Using only "este" and "aquele" (ignoring esse)
- ‚úÖ Use all three: este, esse, aquele (Portuguese has 3!)
- ‚ùå "isto livro" (wrong - isto is only for abstract)
- ‚úÖ "este livro" (correct - use este with nouns)

**The Three-Distance System:**

**ESTE/ESTA/ESTES/ESTAS (this/these):**
- **Location:** Near the SPEAKER
- **Gestures:** "this here", pointing to myself
- Examples:
  - Este √© meu livro. (This is my book - I have it)
  - Esta casa √© minha. (This house is mine - where I am)

**ESSE/ESSA/ESSES/ESSAS (that/those):**
- **Location:** Near the LISTENER
- **Gestures:** "that there", pointing to you
- Examples:
  - Esse √© seu livro? (Is that your book? - you have it)
  - Essa casa √© sua? (Is that house yours? - where you are)

**AQUELE/AQUELA/AQUELES/AQUELAS (that/those):**
- **Location:** Far from BOTH speaker and listener
- **Gestures:** "that over there", pointing away
- Examples:
  - Aquele √© o livro dele. (That is his book - over there)
  - Aquela casa √© cara. (That house is expensive - far away)

**Memory Aid:**
- **Este** = "e" = "eu" (I/me) = near ME
- **Esse** = near yoU (listener)
- **Aquele** = "ali" (over there) = FAR

**Gender/Number Agreement Chart:**

|  | Masc. Sing. | Fem. Sing. | Masc. Plural | Fem. Plural |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Near speaker | este | esta | estes | estas |
| Near listener | esse | essa | esses | essas |
| Far from both | aquele | aquela | aqueles | aquelas |

**Neuter Demonstratives (Abstract):**

Use these when referring to IDEAS, not specific nouns:

**ISTO (this - abstract, near speaker):**
- **Isto** √© verdade. (This is true.)
- **Isto** √© importante. (This is important.)
- What is "isto"? An idea, a situation, not a specific object

**ISSO (that - abstract, near listener or recent):**
- **Isso** √© interessante. (That is interesting.)
- **Isso** √© bom. (That is good.)
- Often refers to what someone just said

**AQUILO (that - abstract, far):**
- **Aquilo** √© estranho. (That is strange.)
- **Aquilo** que voc√™ disse. (That which you said.)

**Using Demonstratives as Pronouns:**

You can use demonstratives WITHOUT a noun (as pronouns):
- Eu quero **este**. (I want this one.)
- Voc√™ prefere **esse**? (Do you prefer that one?)
- **Aquele** √© melhor. (That one is better.)
- **Estas** s√£o minhas. (These are mine.)

**Common Phrases:**
- este aqui (this one here)
- esse a√≠ (that one there - near you)
- aquele ali/l√° (that one over there)
- isto aqui (this here - abstract)
- isso a√≠ (that's it / that there)

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 3: Articles ‚Üí demonstratives also show gender/number
- Unit 6: Adjectives ‚Üí demonstratives are adjectives when with nouns
- Unit 55-68: All nouns learned ‚Üí now point to them specifically
- Unit 28: Possessives ‚Üí "este livro" vs "meu livro"

**Key Learning:**
- Portuguese has THREE demonstratives (este, esse, aquele) not two!
- Este (near me), Esse (near you), Aquele (far from both)
- Must agree in gender and number with noun (4 forms each)
- Neuter forms (isto, isso, aquilo) for abstract concepts
- Essential for pointing, specifying, clarifying which one

**Why This Unit:**
- **FOUNDATIONAL:** Demonstratives are essential grammar
- Natural progression: can name nouns, now specify which one
- Ultra-granular: focuses ONLY on demonstrative system
- Practical: immediate use for shopping, pointing, specifying
- Grammar milestone: fills major gap in curriculum

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**

### Unit 76: Future Tense (Farei, Far√°)
**New vocabulary:**
- farei (I will do), far√° (he/she will do)
- viajarei (I will travel), comerei (I will eat)
- serei (I will be), estarei (I will be - location/state)
- direi (I will say - irregular)
- trarei (I will bring - irregular)
- amanh√£ (tomorrow), pr√≥xima semana (next week), no futuro (in the future)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Future tense formation:** infinitive + -ei/-√°/-emos/-√£o
- Regular pattern: falar ‚Üí falarei, falar√°s, falar√°, falaremos, falar√£o
- ONLY 3 irregulars: fazer ‚Üí farei, dizer ‚Üí direi, trazer ‚Üí trarei
- All three drop the middle syllable: fa(ze)r ‚Üí farei, di(ze)r ‚Üí direi, tra(ze)r ‚Üí trarei
- When to use future tense vs "vou + infinitive"

**Uses of Future Tense:**
1. **Formal predictions:** O Brasil ganhar√° a Copa. (Brazil will win the Cup.)
2. **Uncertain future:** Ser√° que vai chover? (I wonder if it will rain?)
3. **Formal writing:** O governo far√° mudan√ßas. (The government will make changes.)
4. **Distant future:** Em 2030, morarei em Portugal. (In 2030, I'll live in Portugal.)

**Future vs Vou + Infinitive:**
- **Vou + infinitive (Unit 29):** immediate, planned future - "Vou viajar amanh√£" (I'm going to travel tomorrow)
- **Future tense:** formal, uncertain, distant future - "Viajarei no pr√≥ximo ano" (I will travel next year)
- BP speakers heavily prefer "vou + infinitive" in speech
- Future tense more common in writing and formal contexts

**Practice format:**
- Conjugate verbs in future tense
- Choose between "vou + infinitive" vs future tense
- Transform present tense to future tense
- Translate future plans and predictions

**Student can now:**
- Make formal predictions and talk about distant future
- Use future tense in formal writing
- Understand the difference between two future constructions
- Handle the 3 irregular future verbs (fazer, dizer, trazer)

**Typical sentences:**
- Eu falarei com voc√™ amanh√£. (I will speak with you tomorrow - formal)
- Eles viajar√£o para o Brasil no pr√≥ximo ano. (They will travel to Brazil next year.)
- Voc√™ far√° isso? (Will you do this?)
- Direi a verdade. (I will tell the truth - irregular)
- No futuro, morarei em Lisboa. (In the future, I'll live in Lisbon.)

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ‚ùå "fazerei" (incorrect irregular)
- ‚úÖ "farei" (correct - fazer ‚Üí farei)
- ‚ùå "dizerei" (incorrect irregular)
- ‚úÖ "direi" (correct - dizer ‚Üí direi)
- ‚ùå Using future tense for immediate plans
- ‚úÖ Use "vou + infinitive" for immediate/planned: "Vou comer agora" (I'm going to eat now)

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 29: Vou + infinitive (informal future) ‚Üí now add formal future
- Unit 34-35: Past tense formation ‚Üí similar pattern (add endings to infinitive)
- Unit 77: Conditional ‚Üí uses same irregular stems (fazer ‚Üí faria)

**Why This Unit:**
- **ESSENTIAL:** Completes the tense system (past, present, future)
- Good news: ONLY 3 irregular verbs (fazer, dizer, trazer)!
- Understanding when to use future vs "vou + infinitive" is key
- Future tense common in formal writing, news, predictions
- Regular formation pattern is very predictable

### Unit 77: Conditional Tense (Faria, Gostaria)
**New vocabulary:**
- faria (I would do), gostaria (I would like)
- seria (I would be), estaria (I would be - location/state)
- poderia (I could), deveria (I should)
- comeria (I would eat), viajaria (I would travel)
- talvez (maybe), se eu fosse (if I were)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Conditional formation:** infinitive + -ia/-ia/-√≠amos/-iam
- Regular pattern: falar ‚Üí falaria, falarias, falaria, falar√≠amos, falariam
- Same 3 irregulars as future: fazer ‚Üí faria, dizer ‚Üí diria, trazer ‚Üí traria
- Note: All persons except n√≥s use same ending (-ia)

**Uses of Conditional:**
1. **Polite requests:** Gostaria de um caf√©. (I would like a coffee.)
2. **Hypotheticals:** Eu faria isso, mas n√£o tenho tempo. (I would do that, but I don't have time.)
3. **Advice:** Voc√™ deveria descansar. (You should rest.)
4. **Possibilities:** Seria bom viajar. (It would be good to travel.)

**Practice format:**
- Conjugate verbs in conditional
- Polite requests with "gostaria de"
- Hypothetical situations: "Eu faria... mas..."
- Advice with "deveria"

**Student can now:**
- Make polite requests (gostaria de instead of quero)
- Express hypothetical situations
- Give advice using conditional
- Sound more formal and polite in Portuguese

**Typical sentences:**
- Gostaria de uma x√≠cara de caf√©. (I would like a cup of coffee - polite)
- Eu viajaria para o Brasil, mas n√£o tenho dinheiro. (I would travel to Brazil, but I don't have money.)
- Voc√™ deveria estudar mais. (You should study more.)
- Seria interessante morar em Lisboa. (It would be interesting to live in Lisbon.)
- O que voc√™ faria? (What would you do?)

**Polite Requests with Gostaria:**
- Gostaria de um caf√©. (I would like a coffee.) ‚Üê very polite
- Quero um caf√©. (I want a coffee.) ‚Üê direct
- Poderia me ajudar? (Could you help me?) ‚Üê polite
- Voc√™ poderia abrir a janela? (Could you open the window?) ‚Üê polite request

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ‚ùå "faziria" (incorrect irregular)
- ‚úÖ "faria" (correct - fazer ‚Üí faria)
- ‚ùå Using "quero" when being polite
- ‚úÖ Use "gostaria de" for polite requests
- ‚ùå Confusing conditional with imperfect
- ‚úÖ Imperfect = did (past), Conditional = would do (hypothetical)

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 76: Future tense ‚Üí same 3 irregular stems
- Unit 45-46: Imperfect ‚Üí similar endings but different meaning
- Unit 84: Imperfect subjunctive ‚Üí used together for hypotheticals

**Why This Unit:**
- **ESSENTIAL FOR POLITENESS:** "Gostaria de" is extremely common
- Follows naturally from future tense (same irregulars)
- Key for expressing hypotheticals and advice
- Makes Portuguese sound more sophisticated and polite
- Regular formation very easy to learn

### Unit 78: √â que - Emphatic Questions
**New vocabulary:**
- √© que (emphatic marker)
- onde √© que (where...?), o que √© que (what...?)
- quando √© que (when...?), como √© que (how...?)
- por que √© que (why...?), qual √© que (which...?)
- quanto √© que (how much...?)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **√â que construction:** [Question word] + √© que + [rest of sentence]
- Makes questions more emphatic and conversational
- EXTREMELY common in Brazilian Portuguese speech
- Optional but very natural-sounding

**Pattern:**
- Basic: Onde voc√™ mora? (Where do you live?)
- Emphatic: Onde **√© que** voc√™ mora? (Where do you live? - more emphasis)
- Basic: O que voc√™ quer? (What do you want?)
- Emphatic: O que **√© que** voc√™ quer? (What do you want? - more emphasis)

**Practice format:**
- Transform basic questions into √© que questions
- Recognize √© que in conversations
- Use with all question words

**Student can now:**
- Ask questions that sound more natural and conversational
- Understand this extremely common BP construction
- Add emphasis and flow to questions
- Sound more like a native BP speaker

**Typical sentences:**
- Onde √© que voc√™ trabalha? (Where do you work?)
- O que √© que voc√™ est√° fazendo? (What are you doing?)
- Quando √© que voc√™ vai viajar? (When are you going to travel?)
- Como √© que se faz isso? (How do you do this?)
- Por que √© que voc√™ n√£o foi? (Why didn't you go?)
- Qual √© que √© o seu? (Which one is yours?)

**Special Case - O que √© que:**
- O que **√© que** √© isso? (What is this?)
- First "√©" = part of "√© que" construction
- Second "√©" = the verb "to be"
- Looks strange but grammatically correct!
- Very common in Portuguese

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ‚ùå "Onde que voc√™ mora?" (missing "√©")
- ‚úÖ "Onde **√© que** voc√™ mora?" (correct - need both words)
- ‚ùå Using √© que in formal writing
- ‚úÖ Better for conversation, use simple questions in formal writing

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 38: Question words ‚Üí now make them more emphatic
- Unit 23-27: Voc√™, ele/ela, n√≥s, etc. ‚Üí use with all subjects
- Unit 1: Ser verb ‚Üí "√©" from ser is part of "√© que"

**Why This Unit:**
- **EXTREMELY COMMON:** You'll hear this constantly in Brazilian Portuguese
- Makes questions sound more natural and conversational
- Simple to learn, big impact on fluency
- Characteristic feature of BP (less common in EP)

### Unit 79: Crase (√†, √†s)
**New vocabulary:**
- √† (to the - feminine singular)
- √†s (to the - feminine plural)
- √† esquerda (to/on the left)
- √† direita (to/on the right)
- √†s tr√™s horas (at 3 o'clock)
- ir √† praia (go to the beach)
- √† noite (at night)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Crase:** contraction of a (preposition) + a (article) = √†
- Written with grave accent: √†
- Plural form: √†s (a + as)
- ONLY occurs with feminine articles
- One of the trickiest aspects of Portuguese!

**When Crase Occurs:**
1. **Preposition a + feminine article a:**
   - Vou (a + a) praia ‚Üí Vou **√†** praia (I'm going to the beach)
   - (a + a) esquerda ‚Üí **√†** esquerda (to/on the left)

2. **With hours (time):**
   - √†s 3 horas, √†s 8 da manh√£
   - (a + as) tr√™s horas ‚Üí **√†s** tr√™s horas

3. **Fixed expressions:**
   - √† noite (at night), √† tarde (in the afternoon)
   - √† vontade (at ease), √†s vezes (sometimes)

**When Crase Does NOT Occur:**
1. **Masculine nouns:** ao (not √†)
   - Vou ao mercado (NOT √† mercado)
2. **Verbs:** a falar (NOT √† falar)
3. **Indefinite articles:** a uma praia (NOT √† uma)
4. **Before names:** a Maria (NOT √† Maria) - unless with article

**Practice format:**
- Identify when to use crase
- Fill in √† vs a vs ao
- Common expressions with crase
- Time expressions with √†s

**Student can now:**
- Use crase correctly with feminine nouns
- Tell time with √†s + hours
- Use direction expressions (√† esquerda/direita)
- Understand when crase is required

**Typical sentences:**
- Vou √† praia. (I'm going to the beach.)
- Vire √† direita. (Turn right.)
- √Äs tr√™s horas. (At 3 o'clock.)
- Vou √† escola. (I'm going to school.)
- √Ä noite, eu estudo. (At night, I study.)
- √Äs vezes, eu viajo. (Sometimes, I travel.)

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ‚ùå "Vou a praia" (missing crase)
- ‚úÖ "Vou √† praia" (correct - √† = a + a)
- ‚ùå "Vou √† mercado" (masculine - no crase)
- ‚úÖ "Vou ao mercado" (correct - ao = a + o masculine)
- ‚ùå "as 3 horas" (missing crase)
- ‚úÖ "√†s 3 horas" (correct - √†s = a + as)
- ‚ùå "√† falar" (before verb)
- ‚úÖ "a falar" (correct - no crase before verbs)

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 13: Location (em casa, na escola) ‚Üí now add "√†" for movement to
- Unit 49: Telling time ‚Üí √†s + hours
- Unit 60: Directions ‚Üí √† esquerda, √† direita

**Why This Unit:**
- **NOTORIOUSLY DIFFICULT:** Even native speakers struggle with crase
- Essential for correct written Portuguese
- Common in daily expressions (√† noite, √†s vezes, √† direita)
- Helps distinguish between: a (preposition), a (article), √† (contraction)
- Practice is key - this takes time to master!

### Unit 80: Todo vs Tudo
**New vocabulary:**
- todo/toda (all, every - adjective)
- todos/todas (all - plural)
- tudo (everything - pronoun)
- todo o/toda a (the whole)
- todos os dias (every day)
- todo mundo (everyone)
- Tudo bem? (Everything okay?)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Todo/toda:** adjective that agrees with noun (all, every, whole)
- **Tudo:** invariable pronoun meaning "everything"
- Never confuse them - different parts of speech!

**Todo/Toda (Adjective):**
- Agrees with noun: todo livro (m), toda casa (f)
- Plural: todos os livros, todas as casas
- Means "all" or "every" or "whole"
- Examples:
  - todo o dia (the whole day)
  - toda a noite (the whole night)
  - todos os dias (every day)
  - todas as pessoas (all the people)

**Tudo (Pronoun):**
- Invariable - never changes
- Means "everything"
- Stands alone, doesn't modify nouns
- Examples:
  - Tudo bem? (Everything okay?)
  - Eu sei tudo. (I know everything.)
  - Tudo est√° certo. (Everything is right.)

**Common Expressions:**
- **todo mundo:** everyone (literally "all world")
- **todos os dias:** every day
- **toda hora:** all the time
- **Tudo bem?:** Everything okay? / How are you?
- **Tudo bom?:** Everything good? (same meaning)
- **de todo:** at all (negation)

**Practice format:**
- Choose between todo/toda/todos/todas vs tudo
- Complete expressions (todo mundo, todos os dias)
- Translate sentences requiring correct form

**Student can now:**
- Distinguish between todo (adjective) and tudo (pronoun)
- Use common expressions with todo/tudo correctly
- Use "todo mundo" for "everyone"
- Greet with "Tudo bem?"

**Typical sentences:**
- Todo dia eu estudo. (Every day I study.)
- Todos os alunos est√£o aqui. (All the students are here.)
- Tudo bem? (Everything okay? / How are you?)
- Eu fiz tudo. (I did everything.)
- Todo mundo gosta de m√∫sica. (Everyone likes music.)
- Ela trabalha toda semana. (She works every week.)

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ‚ùå "Tudo dia" (tudo doesn't modify nouns)
- ‚úÖ "Todo dia" (correct - todo = every)
- ‚ùå "Eu sei todo" (todo needs a noun)
- ‚úÖ "Eu sei tudo" (correct - tudo = everything)
- ‚ùå "Todos bem?" (todos is plural adjective)
- ‚úÖ "Tudo bem?" (correct - tudo = everything)
- ‚ùå "tudo as pessoas" (tudo doesn't agree)
- ‚úÖ "todas as pessoas" (correct - todas agrees with feminine plural)

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 8: Todo o dia (whole day) vs todos os dias (every day)
- Unit 50: Days of week ‚Üí todos os dias (every day)
- Unit 23-27: Todo mundo (everyone) uses singular verb

**Why This Unit:**
- **COMMONLY CONFUSED:** Even intermediate learners mix these up
- "Todo mundo" (everyone) is extremely common
- "Tudo bem?" is one of the most common greetings
- Mastering this distinction is essential for correct Portuguese
- Different parts of speech: todo (adjective) vs tudo (pronoun)

### Unit 81: Introduction to Subjunctive Mood
**New vocabulary:**
- modo indicativo (indicative mood - facts)
- modo subjunctivo (subjunctive mood - wishes, doubts, hypotheticals)
- que (that - introduces subjunctive clauses)
- espero que (I hope that), quero que (I want that)
- duvido que (I doubt that), talvez (maybe)
- √© importante que (it's important that)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Mood concept:** indicative vs subjunctive
- **Indicative:** states facts, certainty, reality
  - Ele **fala** portugu√™s. (He speaks Portuguese - fact)
- **Subjunctive:** expresses wishes, doubts, emotions, hypotheticals, commands
  - Espero que ele **fale** portugu√™s. (I hope he speaks Portuguese - wish)
- **When subjunctive is triggered:** certain verbs and expressions require it

**Subjunctive Triggers (Preview):**

1. **Wishes/Desires:**
   - espero que (I hope that)
   - quero que (I want that)
   - desejo que (I wish that)

2. **Doubt/Uncertainty:**
   - duvido que (I doubt that)
   - talvez (maybe)
   - n√£o acho que (I don't think that)

3. **Emotions:**
   - √© bom que (it's good that)
   - √© importante que (it's important that)
   - tenho medo que (I'm afraid that)

4. **Commands/Requests:**
   - Ele sugere que... (He suggests that...)
   - Ela pede que... (She asks that...)

5. **Future conditions (Portuguese unique!):**
   - quando (when - future)
   - se (if - future hypothetical)

**Practice format:**
- Identify indicative vs subjunctive contexts
- Recognize subjunctive triggers
- Understand why subjunctive is needed
- Preview subjunctive formation (Units 82-85)

**Student can now:**
- Understand the concept of grammatical mood
- Recognize when subjunctive is needed (triggers)
- Differentiate between facts (indicative) and wishes/doubts (subjunctive)
- Prepare for learning subjunctive conjugations in Units 82-85

**Typical patterns:**
- **Indicative (fact):** Ele fala portugu√™s. (He speaks Portuguese.)
- **Subjunctive (wish):** Espero que ele fale portugu√™s. (I hope he speaks Portuguese.)
- **Indicative (fact):** Eles est√£o aqui. (They are here.)
- **Subjunctive (doubt):** Duvido que eles estejam aqui. (I doubt they are here.)

**Why Subjunctive Exists:**
Portuguese distinguishes between:
- **Reality/Facts:** indicative mood
- **Non-reality (wishes, doubts, hypotheticals):** subjunctive mood

This is grammatically required in Portuguese - you cannot omit the subjunctive when it's triggered.

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ‚ùå "Espero que ele fala" (using indicative after trigger)
- ‚úÖ "Espero que ele fale" (correct - must use subjunctive after espero que)
- ‚ùå Avoiding subjunctive because it seems hard
- ‚úÖ Embrace it - it's essential for correct Portuguese!

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- All present tense verbs (Units 1-28) ‚Üí now transform to subjunctive
- Unit 18: Negation ‚Üí "n√£o acho que" triggers subjunctive
- Units 82-85: Will learn actual subjunctive conjugations

**Why This Unit:**
- **THEORETICAL FOUNDATION:** Understand WHY subjunctive exists before learning HOW
- Subjunctive is not optional - it's grammatically required
- Portuguese has THREE subjunctive tenses (present, imperfect, future)
- This unit prepares students conceptually before conjugations
- Makes Units 82-85 easier by establishing the framework

---

### Unit 82: Present Subjunctive - Regular Verbs
**New vocabulary:**
- que eu fale (that I speak), que voc√™ coma (that you eat)
- que n√≥s falemos (that we speak), que eles partam (that they leave)
- espero que (I hope that), √© importante que (it's important that)
- talvez (maybe), antes que (before), para que (so that)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Present subjunctive formation - Regular verbs:**
  - **-AR verbs:** Change -o to -e
    - falo ‚Üí fale, fales, fale, falemos, falem
  - **-ER/-IR verbs:** Change -o to -a
    - como ‚Üí coma, comas, coma, comamos, comam
    - parto ‚Üí parta, partas, parta, partamos, partam

**Formation Pattern:**
1. Start with first person present indicative: falo, como, parto
2. Drop the -o: fal-, com-, part-
3. Add opposite vowel endings:
   - -AR verbs get E endings: -e, -es, -e, -emos, -em
   - -ER/-IR verbs get A endings: -a, -as, -a, -amos, -am

**Regular Examples:**

**Falar (to speak):**
- que eu **fale**
- que voc√™/ele/ela **fale**
- que n√≥s **falemos**
- que voc√™s/eles/elas **falem**

**Comer (to eat):**
- que eu **coma**
- que voc√™/ele/ela **coma**
- que n√≥s **comamos**
- que voc√™s/eles/elas **comam**

**Partir (to leave):**
- que eu **parta**
- que voc√™/ele/ela **parta**
- que n√≥s **partamos**
- que voc√™s/eles/elas **partam**

**Common Triggers (Review from Unit 81):**
- Espero que voc√™ **fale** com ele. (I hope you speak with him.)
- √â importante que n√≥s **comamos** bem. (It's important that we eat well.)
- Talvez eles **partam** amanh√£. (Maybe they'll leave tomorrow.)

**Practice format:**
- Conjugate regular verbs in present subjunctive
- Complete sentences with subjunctive triggers
- Transform indicative to subjunctive

**Student can now:**
- Form present subjunctive of all regular verbs
- Use subjunctive after common triggers
- Express wishes, doubts, and emotions correctly
- Apply the "opposite vowel" rule

**Typical sentences:**
- Espero que voc√™ fale portugu√™s. (I hope you speak Portuguese.)
- √â bom que n√≥s estudemos juntos. (It's good that we study together.)
- Talvez ela coma aqui. (Maybe she'll eat here.)
- Quero que eles venham. (I want them to come.) [vir is irregular - Unit 83]
- √â importante que voc√™ descanse. (It's important that you rest.)

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ‚ùå "Espero que voc√™ fala" (using indicative)
- ‚úÖ "Espero que voc√™ fale" (correct - subjunctive required)
- ‚ùå "que eu falo" (indicative form)
- ‚úÖ "que eu fale" (correct - subjunctive form)
- ‚ùå Forgetting the opposite vowel rule
- ‚úÖ AR‚ÜíE, ER/IR‚ÜíA

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 81: Subjunctive concept ‚Üí now learn the conjugations
- Units 5-7, 22, 28: Regular verbs ‚Üí now in subjunctive
- Unit 83: Irregular subjunctives ‚Üí coming next

**Why This Unit:**
- **CORE GRAMMAR:** Present subjunctive is the most common subjunctive tense
- Regular formation is very systematic (opposite vowel)
- Builds on present indicative knowledge
- Opens up expressing wishes, doubts, emotions naturally
- Most common subjunctive tense in daily speech

### Unit 83: Present Subjunctive - Irregular Verbs
**New vocabulary:**
- que eu seja (that I be), que voc√™ esteja (that you be - location)
- que ele tenha (that he has), que n√≥s vamos (that we go)
- que eles deem (that they give), que eu saiba (that I know)
- que voc√™ possa (that you can), que ele queira (that he wants)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Present subjunctive - Irregular verbs**
- Most common irregular verbs have unpredictable subjunctive forms
- Must memorize these key verbs

**Key Irregular Subjunctives:**

**Ser (to be):**
- que eu **seja**, que voc√™ **seja**, que ele/ela **seja**
- que n√≥s **sejamos**, que voc√™s **sejam**, que eles **sejam**

**Estar (to be - location/state):**
- que eu **esteja**, que voc√™ **esteja**, que ele/ela **esteja**
- que n√≥s **estejamos**, que voc√™s **estejam**, que eles **estejam**

**Ter (to have):**
- que eu **tenha**, que voc√™ **tenha**, que ele/ela **tenha**
- que n√≥s **tenhamos**, que voc√™s **tenham**, que eles **tenham**

**Ir (to go):**
- que eu **v√°**, que voc√™ **v√°**, que ele/ela **v√°**
- que n√≥s **vamos**, que voc√™s **v√£o**, que eles **v√£o**

**Dar (to give):**
- que eu **d√™**, que voc√™ **d√™**, que ele/ela **d√™**
- que n√≥s **demos**, que voc√™s **deem**, que eles **deem**

**Saber (to know):**
- que eu **saiba**, que voc√™ **saiba**, que ele/ela **saiba**
- que n√≥s **saibamos**, que voc√™s **saibam**, que eles **saibam**

**Querer (to want):**
- que eu **queira**, que voc√™ **queira**, que ele/ela **queira**
- que n√≥s **queiramos**, que voc√™s **queiram**, que eles **queiram**

**Poder (to be able):**
- que eu **possa**, que voc√™ **possa**, que ele/ela **possa**
- que n√≥s **possamos**, que voc√™s **possam**, que eles **possam**

**Haver (to have - impersonal):**
- que **haja** (only 3rd person singular used)

**Practice format:**
- Memorize irregular subjunctive forms
- Complete sentences using irregular subjunctives
- Distinguish when to use irregular vs regular forms

**Student can now:**
- Use present subjunctive of all major irregular verbs
- Express complex wishes and doubts with common verbs
- Handle ser/estar/ter/ir in subjunctive contexts
- Combine with triggers from Unit 81-82

**Typical sentences:**
- Espero que voc√™ esteja bem. (I hope you are well.)
- √â importante que n√≥s sejamos honestos. (It's important that we be honest.)
- Talvez ele tenha raz√£o. (Maybe he's right.)
- Quero que voc√™s v√£o comigo. (I want you all to go with me.)
- Duvido que ela saiba a resposta. (I doubt she knows the answer.)
- √â bom que voc√™ possa vir. (It's good that you can come.)

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ‚ùå "Espero que voc√™ √© feliz" (using indicative ser)
- ‚úÖ "Espero que voc√™ seja feliz" (correct - irregular seja)
- ‚ùå "que eu tenho" (indicative form)
- ‚úÖ "que eu tenha" (correct - irregular subjunctive)
- ‚ùå "que n√≥s vamos" when vamos is subjunctive
- ‚úÖ Context determines: "N√≥s vamos" (indicative) vs "que n√≥s vamos" (subjunctive - same form!)

**Memory Aids:**
- **Ser ‚Üí seja:** think "SEJa content"
- **Estar ‚Üí esteja:** ends in -esteja (similar pattern to seja)
- **Ter ‚Üí tenha:** TENha sounds like TEN
- **Ir ‚Üí v√°:** super short, just v√°!
- **Dar ‚Üí d√™:** give accent to d√™
- **Saber ‚Üí saiba:** SAIba has AI
- **Querer ‚Üí queira:** QUEIra has EI
- **Poder ‚Üí possa:** POSSa has double S

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 82: Regular subjunctives ‚Üí now add irregulars
- Unit 1, 12, 36: Ser/estar/ter ‚Üí now in subjunctive mood
- Unit 29: Ir (vou) ‚Üí now "que eu v√°" (subjunctive)

**Why This Unit:**
- **ESSENTIAL VERBS:** These are the most common verbs in Portuguese
- Can't express many ideas without these irregular forms
- Ser/estar/ter/ir appear constantly in subjunctive contexts
- Memorization required - no shortcuts for irregulars

### Unit 84: Imperfect Subjunctive
**New vocabulary:**
- se eu fosse (if I were), se voc√™ tivesse (if you had)
- se ele pudesse (if he could), se n√≥s soub√©ssemos (if we knew)
- seria (would be), faria (would do)
- eu gostaria que (I would like that), eu quisera (I wished)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Imperfect subjunctive formation:**
  - Take preterite 3rd person plural: eles falaram
  - Remove -ram: fala-
  - Add -sse endings: -sse, -sses, -sse, -ssemos, -ssem

**Formation Examples:**

**Falar:** eles falaram ‚Üí fala- ‚Üí falasse
- que eu **falasse**, que voc√™ **falasse**
- que n√≥s **fal√°ssemos**, que eles **falassem**

**Comer:** eles comeram ‚Üí come- ‚Üí comesse
- que eu **comesse**, que voc√™ **comesse**
- que n√≥s **com√™ssemos**, que eles **comessem**

**Ter:** eles tiveram ‚Üí tive- ‚Üí tivesse
- que eu **tivesse**, que voc√™ **tivesse**
- que n√≥s **tiv√©ssemos**, que eles **tivessem**

**Ser/Ir:** eles foram ‚Üí fo- ‚Üí fosse
- que eu **fosse**, que voc√™ **fosse**
- que n√≥s **f√¥ssemos**, que eles **fossem**

**Uses of Imperfect Subjunctive:**

1. **Se clauses (hypotheticals):**
   - Se eu **fosse** rico, eu viajaria. (If I were rich, I would travel.)
   - Se voc√™ **tivesse** tempo, voc√™ viria? (If you had time, would you come?)

2. **After past tense triggers:**
   - Eu queria que voc√™ **viesse**. (I wanted you to come.)
   - Era importante que n√≥s **estud√°ssemos**. (It was important that we studied.)

3. **Polite suggestions:**
   - Seria bom se voc√™ **descansasse**. (It would be good if you rested.)

4. **Wishes about past:**
   - Eu gostaria que ele **estivesse** aqui. (I would like him to be here.)

**Se + Imperfect Subjunctive + Conditional:**
- **Se eu tivesse** dinheiro, eu **compraria** uma casa.
  (If I had money, I would buy a house.)
- **Se voc√™ fosse**, eu **iria** tamb√©m.
  (If you went, I would go too.)

**Practice format:**
- Form imperfect subjunctive from preterite
- Complete se clauses with imperfect subjunctive + conditional
- Transform present subjunctive to imperfect subjunctive

**Student can now:**
- Express hypothetical situations in past or present
- Use "se" (if) clauses correctly
- Make polite suggestions
- Express wishes about impossible or contrary-to-fact situations

**Typical sentences:**
- Se eu fosse voc√™, eu aceitaria. (If I were you, I would accept.)
- Se ele soubesse a verdade, ele entenderia. (If he knew the truth, he would understand.)
- Eu queria que voc√™ viesse √† festa. (I wanted you to come to the party.)
- Se n√≥s tiv√©ssemos tempo, n√≥s viajar√≠amos. (If we had time, we would travel.)
- Era importante que eles estudassem. (It was important that they studied.)

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ‚ùå "Se eu seria" (using conditional in se clause)
- ‚úÖ "Se eu fosse" (correct - imperfect subjunctive in se clause)
- ‚ùå "Se ele tem" (using present in hypothetical)
- ‚úÖ "Se ele tivesse" (correct - imperfect subjunctive for hypothesis)
- ‚ùå Forgetting to use conditional in main clause
- ‚úÖ Se eu fosse rico, eu **compraria** (would buy) - conditional

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 77: Conditional ‚Üí used with imperfect subjunctive in se clauses
- Unit 34-43: Preterite ‚Üí basis for forming imperfect subjunctive
- Units 82-83: Present subjunctive ‚Üí now add imperfect subjunctive

**Why This Unit:**
- **ESSENTIAL FOR HYPOTHETICALS:** "If I were you..." constructions
- Follows logically from preterite (uses preterite stem)
- Enables expressing contrary-to-fact situations
- Common in polite suggestions and wishes
- Pairs with conditional tense naturally
